# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 19

## 7332

B”H, 3 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing and diligent in communal affairs, R’ Shalom, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 28 Elul with the enclosure, in which you write and ask how to conduct yourself regarding matters where there are differences between the nusach of the Arizal and the customs of the shul in which you daven.

It is understood that regarding your own personal conduct, there is no reason for you to change, as this does not involve the prohibition of "do not form factions" (lo tisgodedu), as is also explained in the ruling of the Tzemach Tzedek in Orach Chaim, end of section 236. However, based on what is explained in several places—that one should change from Nusach Ashkenaz to Nusach Sefard, and from Sefard to the nusach of the Arizal, which is Nusach Chabad (but not the reverse)—you should endeavor to introduce certain customs (naturally, in a pleasant manner). Regarding the Hakafos, where our custom is to circle three times, you should explain: what difference does it make to them if there are three circles? At the very least, announce that anyone who wishes to may participate in it, especially since the Hakafos take place after davening and do not "disturb" the others.

I do not know how you conducted yourself regarding the Tekios, and it is surprising that you did not clarify the matter beforehand. For it seems to me that their custom is not to blow one hundred sounds, and you could have fulfilled the count of one hundred yourself, with the aforementioned explanation. Consequently, this would have also reached the others present (as explained in Likkutei Torah, beginning of Parshas Shemini), and this is simple to understand.

With blessings for a Gmar Chasima Tova,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
My letters with blessings for the year surely arrived already.

***

## 7,233

B”H, 3 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following the longest of intervals, your letter dated 28/9 was received. At an auspicious time, I will mention you and your wife, may she live, at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

It is understood and simple that one must increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos, in accordance with the directive that we must always ascend in matters of holiness. This serves as a conduit and vessel for receiving the blessings of Hashem, may He be blessed, in all that is needed. This is all the more so when one is in a place where, for whatever reasons, those who observe Torah and mitzvos are few. Certainly, every single one of the Bnei Yisrael who is there must serve as an example of what a Jew—a child of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov—is, even in the eyes of the non-Jews. 

That is to say, every individual behavior of a Jew contains an element of Kiddush Hashem. And even though the difficulties in such places are understandable, we have been promised by Hashem that He assists everyone. Moreover, our Sages of blessed memory have informed us: "A person who sanctifies himself a little from below is sanctified greatly from above."

For several reasons, I do not wish to elaborate on this point, especially since for someone like you, no explanation is necessary. I will only reiterate the essential point: that everyone, in every place, must fulfill the Torah and the mitzvos. *Lefum tza'ara agra*—according to the effort is the reward—and we have been promised that it is possible to observe and fulfill the Torah and the mitzvos. May it be His will that you bring good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned.

With the blessing of *Chasimah v’Gmar Chasimah Tovah*.

P.S. Regarding what you wrote concerning the *pidyon*, please distribute the money to charity connected with *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*, or to an institution *al taharas hakodesh* in your country.

Enclosed is a copy of my general letter for Rosh Hashanah, which I am sure you will publicize in an appropriate manner.

#### ***7,233***

**General letter for Rosh Hashanah:** See above, Vol. 18, 7,214.

## 7,234

B"H, 3 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

Mrs. Tziporah, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter from Erev Rosh Hashanah, and in accordance with your request, this reply is being sent without waiting for its turn.

In it, you write the opinion of the specialist doctors you visited recently regarding your medical treatment.

Now, our Torah is the "Torah of life"—it is what grants the physician permission to heal, which also includes the concept of providing strength.

May it be Hashem’s will that the surgery lead to your speedy recovery, and that you return to your previous state of health. Together with your husband, may he live and be well, may you continue in the matters of our holy Torah and its mitzvos, and first and foremost—in chinuch al taharas hakodesh.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all that was mentioned, and for a *chasimah v’gmar chasimah tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7,234***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 21, p. 604, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

**Mrs. Tziporah:** Bonin, Ra’anana. Another letter to her appears above in Vol. 18, 6,505.

## 725

B.H., 4 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Elul, in which you raise several matters, I provide this response, albeit briefly:

1) The general conduct of a Jewish man and woman must be specifically through ways of pleasantness and ways of peace, for this is the way of the Torah (the word *Torah* implying *hora'ah*—instruction), as it is written: "Its ways are ways of pleasantness, and all its paths are peace."

2) It is understood that a student must listen to the voice of their teachers, as these matters are explained in many places, including in the *Shulchan Aruch*, *Hilchos Kevod Rav*.

3) It is correct what you write regarding the *nusach* of the Arizal. He established his *nusach* by compiling it from several versions in a manner that would be appropriate for all, as is explained at length in the book *Likutei Amarim* by the Maggid of Mezritch. He was the teacher of the author of the *Sefer Hafla'ah* and *Sefer HaMikneh*, luminaries of the world whose books are studied in **all** yeshivos.

4) One who davens in a shul where the *nusach* is different is permitted to daven in their own *nusach*, and there is **no concern whatsoever** in this [provided, of course, that this individual is not leading the congregation as *shaliach tzibbur*]. However, based on the above, this should be done in ways of pleasantness and without making a point of it.

5) Based on what was stated above in section 3, it is understood that one may change from *Nusach Ashkenaz* to *Nusach Sefard*, and from *Nusach Sefard* to the *nusach* of the Arizal—which is *Nusach Chabad*—but not the reverse. Therefore, it is correct that you continue with the *nusach* of davening (as you write) that you have already begun and are continuing with. You will surely do this in ways of pleasantness and peace, and you will certainly also receive the full agreement of your teacher, may she live.

It is my hope that your conduct in all your affairs is consistent with the conduct of the daughters of Yisrael, each of whom is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah. Now is the time to make good resolutions to increase in this, as the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah* are a time of *hisorerus*, as it is written: "Seek Hashem when He is found, call upon Him when He is near."

At a time of *ratzon*, I will mention all those you write about at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be Hashem's will that you bring good news regarding each and every one of them.

With the blessing of *Chasimah v'Gmar Chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
Regarding the completeness of the matter written above: that there is no concern in davening in one's own *nusach* even if the congregation is davening in a different one, this is explained in many places, including in *Piskei Dinim* of the Tzemach Tzedek, *Orach Chaim*, siman 236. It is known that this was the conduct of the author of the *Hafla'ah* and the conduct of his teacher.

That which is brought above, that one may change from *Nusach Ashkenaz* to *Sefard* (and from *Sefard* to the *nusach* of the Arizal, which is *Nusach Chabad*), but not the reverse, is explained in *Shu"t Minchas Elazar*, Part 1, siman 1, and in the *Kuntres Shiurei Minchah* there. He cites there several books that discuss this.

## 730

B"H, 5 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 28 Elul, in which you write the main points of what you have been experiencing, and regarding your davening in the Chabad nusach and the difficulties you have encountered in this regard:

I have already addressed this in a letter to your friend, which I am certain you will show her. I will emphasize here only the point I mentioned in that letter: that this is a matter of the utmost importance. The paths we are commanded to follow in our Torah—Torah of life—are "ways of pleasantness and ways of peace." Every individual must distance themselves completely from matters of controversy, Heaven forbid. On the contrary, if one truly wishes to spread the awareness of the Chabad approach, the best way to do so is by being a living example in one’s conduct, both in matters between man and Hashem and in matters between man and his fellow, in such a way that all who see them will praise them and say, "How elevated is this approach, that those who follow it conduct themselves in such a manner."

Regarding what you write in your letter—that because you daven in the Chabad nusach, you sometimes need to stand while the rest of the class is sitting—this is not understood. The difference between the Chabad nusach and other versions lies in the text of the tefillah, not in the matter of standing or sitting. You can certainly time yourself so that when you are saying Shemoneh Esrei and the like, it coincides with the time the entire class is davening Shemoneh Esrei. It is surely understood that it is not pleasant for you to isolate yourselves, and it also contradicts the order and discipline of the class. Therefore, you should make an effort to coordinate the timing, as mentioned.

May it be Hashem’s will that you, as well as your friends, conduct yourselves within the class as is fitting for daughters of Yisrael, each of whom is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah, and may you succeed in all your endeavors.

With blessings for a *chasimah v’gmar chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6237

B"H, 6 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, Adin, may he live,
Greetings and blessings!

Following the longest of intervals, your letter of 3 Tishrei was received. I mentioned it today at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for a *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah tovah* in a manner that is good, both visibly and revealed. It is understood that the true good is that which aligns with the instructions of our Torah, of which it is said, "For I have given you a good teaching"—the Torah given to us by the Creator and Guide of the world, who is the essence of good. This is especially true given that Divine Providence has endowed you with the power to influence others; therefore, any increase in yourself is multiplied many times over in those you influence. From this, it is understood that the promise of our Sages, "Whoever adds, they add to him," applies with even greater force regarding you. There is nothing that can stand before the will, provided there is effort to the point of *yegiah* (exertion), as our Sages have taught: "You have labored and found"—specifically through labor.

You write that you are currently serving as a teacher in several settlements in the Negev, but you lack any explanation regarding this—in what framework, what subjects, etc. Although my hope is strong that you are utilizing every opportunity and possibility to disseminate true, traditional Judaism, not only in speech but also in action—for the action is the essential thing—I am certain you will provide details on this in the next opportunity, as well as regarding the activities of your colleagues, may they live, in such matters. As far as I am aware, there was a group of young men and women whose goal should be the dissemination of Judaism.

My hope is strong that you have fixed times for yourself to study Torah, both in *nigleh* and *Chassidus*, and that you are meticulous in the performance of *mitzvos*. As mentioned above, this is of the utmost importance regarding you. May it be His will that you bring good news in this regard as well, and also that you are keeping the three known *shiurim* of *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*.

With blessings for a *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah tovah* and for good tidings.

#### ***6237***

**Adin, may he live:** Steinsaltz, Jerusalem.

## 7,038

7,038

B"H, 6 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Beis Medrash Beis Yisrael in the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 25 Elul, a day regarding which it is said, "In the beginning G-d created..." (Bereishis 1:1), and "In the beginning" (*Bereishis*) contains the letters of *Trei Shabbos* (see Tikkunei Zohar, beginning of Tikkun 48).

In it, you write regarding the matter of observing Shabbos, for which reason you have decided to purchase a machine, etc., which involves various expenses.

Now, although there is no special fund for matters such as these, and in general the state of the funds is such that they are burdened with expenses upon expenses,

Nevertheless, in accordance with the verse, "I am a companion to all who fear You" (Tehillim 119:63), enclosed herewith is a private check as a symbolic contribution toward the aforementioned matter.

May it be the will of Hashem that through *Trei Shabbos*, the Jewish people will be guarded, and immediately they will be redeemed by Mashiach Tzidkeinu in the true and complete redemption.

With respect and with a blessing for a *Chasimah V'Gmar Chasimah Tovah*.

***

**Beis Medrash Beis Yisrael:** Of the Karlin-Stolin Chassidim.

**To purchase a machine:** A battery/power generator. See above, Vol. 18, Letter 6,792.

## 339

B"H, 6 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your question:

1) You have until now davened in Nusach Sefard, and you are asking whether to change to Nusach Chabad—that is, the Nusach of the Arizal—since you are studying in a Chabad yeshiva.

In general, this is the correct thing to do, for several reasons. However, the instruction is well-known: one may change from Nusach Ashkenaz to Sefard, and from Nusach Sefard to the Nusach of the Arizal (which is Nusach Chabad), but not the other way around. Therefore, if you decide to change, it must be for good. It is also a well-known Chassidic tradition that our Alter Rebbe refined his Nusach from sixty siddurim.

With blessings for good tidings and for a *chasimah v’gmar chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
Regarding the inquiry on behalf of Mr. [Name], may he live, for an opinion concerning the removal of the beard, etc.: We have only the words of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek, as explained at length in his Responsa, Yoreh Deah, Siman 93—see there at length—that the matter is forbidden. See also his *Piskei Dinim* to Yoreh Deah, Siman 181-182. And in *Tehillim* on the verse *V’hu Rachum*. See also Responsa *Minchas Elazar*, Part 2, Siman 64.

It is my hope that you (the writer) are studying with consistency and diligence, and that you are also keeping the known *shiurim* of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya. It would also be appropriate to have your tefillin checked to ensure they are kosher according to law.

## 740

B"H, 6 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Rosh Hashanah, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed with it, which was read at an *eis ratzon* at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

It is understandable that I was alarmed by the calm tone in which you wrote regarding your position and employment, concluding that you know I oppose this with all my might—as if this were a private matter of mine or merely my personal opinion, and that I simply wish to oppose it, and with all my might at that. I have come only to state what I have learned in the *sefarim*, and I have explained my view openly. I have not come as one issuing a decree, *chas v’shalom*, nor have I opposed anyone personally; rather, I have sought to save the individual and the collective from a sin committed *b’farhesya*—the likes of which has not been seen for thousands of years—being done in the name of *Klal Yisrael*!

It is understood that these days are not at all appropriate for writing at length on such a matter. On the other hand, I did not see myself as permitted to pass over this in silence, especially during these days when Hashem is demanding and pleading, "Seek Hashem when He is found, call upon Him when He is near." In the language of our *Nesi’im*, the *Nesi’ei HaChassidus*, these are days of the "drawing of the *Maor* (the Luminary) to the *nitzotz* (the spark)." It is already known what is explained in Kabbalah and Chassidus, that the word *Shabbos* consists of the letters *tashuv* (you shall return)—*teshuvah ila’ah* (the higher repentance). The preparation that precedes this is *teshuvah tata’ah* (the lower repentance): complete regret for the past and a firm resolution for the future. As mentioned, it is impossible to elaborate on this during these days.

May it be the will that the drawing of the *Maor* will ignite all the sparks wherever they may be, with kindness and mercy, and immediately, *Am Yisrael* will observe *Shabbos* according to its *halachah*, and they will be redeemed immediately from the internal *galus* and the *galus* in its literal sense—a *galus* of which the verse states, "I will surely hide My face," where the darkness is great, doubled and redoubled, to the point that the concealment itself is concealed, where they claim that this is the way and this is what is desired, and as mentioned, specifically *b’farhesya* and specifically in the name of *Klal Yisrael*. If only one could bring good tidings regarding this—and there is no "good" other than the way of the Torah, of which it is said, "For I have given you a good teaching," which was given on *Shabbos* and with the prerequisite of *shmiras Shabbos*, which was given earlier at Marah (and not in pleasantness), yet they accepted it upon themselves with love, as explained in the *Rishonim* and *poskim*.

With the wish that these few lines, small in quantity, will achieve their effect, and that from here on, you will find your livelihood and the livelihood of your family, *shiy*, in accordance with Torah, with *kashrus* and with dignity.

With the blessing of *chasimah v’gmar chatimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 7th of Tishrei

B"H, 6th of Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 28th of the month of mercy (Elul).

At an auspicious time, I mentioned you and all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

Regarding your question on behalf of your brother-in-law, may he live: since he lives in a place where the residents do not conduct themselves as they should, etc., should he move to a religious and Charedi environment, even though he will have to borrow money to do so?

Based on the words of our Sages (Avos, Chapter 6, Mishnah 9) and the ruling of the Rambam in Hilchos De'os, beginning of Chapter 6, it is understood that one must strive as much as possible to live in an environment of those who are G-d-fearing and who observe Torah and mitzvos properly. Surely he will be able to repay the money he borrows under favorable terms, and may Hashem grant him success.

With blessings for good tidings, and for a *chasimah v'gmar chatimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 742

B"H, 7 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Tzom Gedaliah—may it soon be transformed into joy and gladness—after the longest of intervals. It is understood that I was extremely distressed by its content, and even more so by the coldness of spirit in your writing regarding what you have been through, more than by the events themselves.

However, since our Sages have said that there is nothing that can stand before the will, and "you have labored and found," it is certainly within your power to walk in the way of the King, the King of kings, in the fullest sense of the word. On the contrary, it is actually easier for one who has been in a military framework for a period of about two years, as you write—meaning that for many months you have been accustomed to the conduct of *kabbalas ol* (accepting the yoke) and obeying the command of a flesh-and-blood commander like yourself, even though in many details you are often superior to the commander in character, intellect, or both. Yet, the very existence of the army and the maintenance of order depend precisely upon *kabbalas ol*. If this is true regarding a flesh-and-blood person, how much more so—to make an infinite distinction—regarding the King of the kings of kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He. There is no need to elaborate on such a simple matter.

May it be the will of Hashem that these days of the proximity of the Light to the spark illuminate your path in life—that which is already within you as an inheritance through the *ahavah mesuseres* (hidden love) that exists in every Jew, and which has been further strengthened by the stock from which you were hewn, etc. From here on, may your life be a true life, consistent with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, and its *mitzvos*, of which it is said, "and he shall live by them."

With blessings for a *chasimah v'gmar chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 7443

B"H, 11 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished man of many accomplishments, R' Eliezer Lipa, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 5 Tishrei, as well as the letter and the *pidyon nefesh* delivered by the traveler arriving here from there. Many thanks, many thanks.

May it be the will of Hashem that each of us merits, in the coming year, to effectuate all matters in the manner of the mitzvah of the *Arba Minim*. These are general mitzvos [like all matters of the general new year, which is saturated with all good], yet their drawing down below into the world is accomplished by first drawing them down into the heart of man (which is why one brings the *Arba Minim* to the heart), as it is written, "He has set the world in their heart" — the heart of man. Through this, an abundance of blessing and success will be drawn down for the entire year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings for a *Chag Sameach*, the season of our rejoicing, and for good tidings.

P.S.
Regarding your question concerning my letter about your book, *Otzar Maamarim Al HaTorah*: The instruction of Admur the Tzemach Tzedek is known, in the style of our Sages, "We are the workers of the day," to create "day" (light, as it is written, "And G-d called the light 'day'") in the world. If, in your opinion, my letter will add to the matter of awakening *yiras shamayim* for His Torah and mitzvos, it is understood that you have permission to include it in the second volume of your book.

Regarding what you wrote concerning *dibbur* (speech) and *amirah* (saying): they are distinct. 
1) From the perspective of the one speaking: *amirah* is quiet/private, while *dibbur* is revealed and proclaimed (see *Zohar* Vol. III, 132b; *Likutei Torah* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, *Chukas* 57c, and references cited there). 
2) From the perspective of the listener: *amirah* is when one receives it easily and gently, while *dibbur* is harsh (*Makkos* 11a; *Likutei Torah* of the Arizal, beginning of *Parshas Haazinu*, which you cite in your letter, and elsewhere).

- Regarding what is written in *Zohar* Vol. III, 79b (see also *Mechilta* there, cited in Rashi) — it is resolved in *Or HaChama* there.

## 744

B"H, 12 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessing!

In response to your letter of [date], in which you outline the main points of your life story and note that you are currently in the year in which you must complete your studies as an engineer. You mention that you do not know in which country you will settle after finishing your studies, and you are also worried about your mother, may she live and be well, who is currently in Egypt, and that you must also consider her settlement and livelihood when the time comes for that.

Certainly, consistent with the content of your letter, it is unnecessary to elaborate on the foundation of our faith: that the Creator of the world is the Leader of the world in the present, and He oversees each and every person with Divine Providence. He, blessed be He, is the essence of good, and it is the nature of the Good to bestow good—provided that one conducts oneself in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of Life, for such conduct is the channel and the vessel for receiving the blessings of Hashem, blessed be He.

Since there are still several months until the completion of your studies—at which point you will have to decide where to settle, etc.—it is understood that you should only concern yourself with this a few months before the completion, not ten months in advance. Worrying certainly distracts from your studies and all other matters. After a few months have passed, it would be appropriate for you to correspond with your friends in the countries you mentioned, and also to clarify the situation in France, where you are currently located. Certainly then—that is, after a few months—you will be able to clarify matters better than you can now, and in accordance with that clarification, you will decide to settle in one country or another.

The same applies to the matter of a *shidduch* that you mention, for it is said, "And from Hashem comes an intelligent wife." Therefore, there is no room for worry, only for an interest in clarifying the details **when the time comes** to think about a *shidduch* **in practice**. At that time, of course, you must clarify the worldview of the person you are writing about, or anyone similar: whether she is compatible with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of Life. For only then—"a man and a woman, the *Shechinah* is between them"—when their lives are founded upon the foundations of Torah and *mitzvos*, etc. One should not be concerned by the fact that there are differences in their temperaments, as that is a common occurrence, and when the matter is suitable, the aforementioned does not pose any obstacle at all.

In connection with your state of mind, which is sometimes not as it should be, it is appropriate to have your *tefillin* checked to ensure they are kosher according to *din*. Furthermore, every weekday, before putting on *tefillin*, you should set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above, and for a happy holiday,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S. In my secretariat, we do not write in French, which is why this response is in Lashon HaKodesh. However, you may continue to write in French in the future, as I am able to read that language.

## 13 Tishrei, 5720

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your question in your letter of 11 Tishrei regarding the trip of your wife, may she live and be well, to visit England and also Sweden:

I must tell you the truth, that in general I do not see any inner substance in the aforementioned, especially during the approaching autumn and winter days. However, since it is evident from your letter that there is a strong desire and craving for this trip, it should be combined with some mission of a mitzvah [such as visiting the local Agudas N'shei Chabad or circles of observant women in general, to inspire them regarding mitzvos and a lifestyle according to the Torah, etc.]. Surely you will be able to arrange for the children, may they live, in the best possible way.

May it be the will of Hashem that the departure and return be at a good and auspicious time, and that you utilize it for matters of mitzvah, in addition to fulfilling your desire, with joy and goodness of heart.

You are surely preparing to utilize our upcoming days of rejoicing in a manner appropriate for spreading the wellsprings of Chassidus.

With blessings for good tidings and a happy holiday.

## Z'mo

B"H, 13 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc.,
R' Meir Yisrael Isser, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

...Thank you for your letter regarding the instruction you found in the Siddur *Daas Kedoshim* to recite "v'yanuchu vom" (and they shall rest in them) during the Ne'ilah prayer when Yom Kippur falls on Shabbos. This surely follows the continuation of the phrase "shabbasos" (Shabbos days).

Regarding your observation about the addition made by the Alter Rebbe in his Siddur, "b'rogez ahavah tizkor" (in anger, remember love), you ask: what is the intent, given that "rachem" (have mercy), "akedah" (the binding), and "temimus" (innocence/perfection) correspond to the Patriarchs?

This has been asked of me before, and I replied that, in my opinion, the version that only recites "rachem," "akedah," and "temimus" is what actually requires explanation. After all, the verse mentions four remembrances: "Then I will remember My covenant with Jacob, and also My covenant with Isaac, and also My covenant with Abraham will I remember, and I will remember the land" (Vayikra 26:42). Since the verse speaks of a time of Divine wrath—as in the request "and we do not know"—there must be an alignment between these two matters.

From the above, it is also understood that "b'rogez ahavah tizkor" corresponds to the fourth remembrance, "and I will remember the land." This is also understood based on what is explained in *Zohar Chadash* 196b: "'The woman whom you loved'—this is *Knesses Yisrael*, because regarding her it is written 'love,' as it is written, 'I have loved you with an everlasting love.' And *Knesses Yisrael* is the 'land' mentioned in the verse."

Based on this explanation, the precision in the Alter Rebbe’s Siddur is also understood: "Abraham, Isaac, Jacob, and the fourth foot," unlike the version in Sephardic Siddurim: "rachem, ahavah, akedah, temimus."

***

**R' Meir Yisrael Isser, may he live:** Friedman. Another letter to him appears above, Vol. 4, p. 454.

## 7047

B"H, 13 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the avreich who is occupied with many deeds, etc., Yitzchak Tzvi, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the eve of the Holy Day, along with the enclosure. Many thanks for the good news regarding the matters in Ir Ganim. Surely, the success achieved thus far will provide you, and all those involved and exerting themselves in the affairs of the Reshet, with additional and stronger powers to expand these activities as much as possible. If one who sustains a single soul in Yisrael is considered as if he sustained an entire world, how much more so when it concerns two, three, or more. It is evident to the eye that with appropriate effort, it is possible to add dozens more students to the gan and the school. It is understood that the above must be done in a manner that does not introduce a spirit of contention with the opposition, for the words and ways of our Torah are "ways of pleasantness," as is emphasized in the teachings of Chassidus.

Based on the above, it is understood that it is very appropriate—and even more so—to organize a farbrengen and Simchas Beis HaShoeivah and the like in Ir Ganim.

With blessings for success in all of the above, and may you reach the point of "spreading out to the west, east, north, and south," and to an inheritance without boundaries. Awaiting good news,

**M. Schneerson**

## 748

B"H, Eve of 14 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn

To strengthen peace, and to unite and draw the hearts of each one closer to the other, and to strengthen oneself in *bitachon*—that it is **certainly** only as it is written, "For Hashem your G-d is testing you." And when one discerns that this is only a test, it is nullified **completely**, and the inner meaning of the aforementioned is revealed—*menaseh* (and elevates) Hashem your G-d you, to a level above all concealments and hiddenness, to the point of knowing (and connecting with a very firm and strong bond) a face-to-face revelation (*Likutei Torah, Parshas Re'eh 19b* and onwards). And the good from above becomes good that is seen and revealed below as well—good for us, in a revealed and manifest way, together with our joy (in the plural).

## Geneva

Geneva

B"H, 20 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, and in continuation of the blessing for the year which you have surely already received.

1) Regarding what you wrote concerning the bicentennial year of the passing (Hillula) of the Baal Shem Tov.

The most essential point to emphasize is to remove from the minds of those who err the notion that the entire Torah of the Baal Shem Tov is merely that "the Merciful One desires the heart," and that it is not, Heaven forbid, in accordance with the ruling of the Mishnah that "the deed is the essential thing." Consequently, they arrive at conclusions [that lead to laxity], etc., as mentioned above. Therefore, it is imperative to emphasize that the Baal Shem Tov did not, Heaven forbid, make light of even a hair’s breadth of the slightest detail of the words of the Scribes. Rather, he added to the magnitude of the importance of *kavanah*, and furthermore, that to every single one of the children of Israel, the full ability was given to unite with their Creator through His Torah and mitzvos. [And this is not only for those who were created with the intellectual capacity to delve deeply into the study of Torah], but every single person is obligated in the actual performance of the mitzvos. And every person, in the language of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, according to the capacity of his comprehension and the root of his soul, is also obligated in the *Pardes* of Torah.

2) Regarding your comments about proposals to involve school students in various parades and demonstrations.

In general, I am not comfortable with such matters, for one does not interrupt the study of children even for the building of the Beis Hamikdash, and certainly not for [lesser matters], etc. The exception to this rule is only when the participation has an educational value, for the student’s learning is not only through speech, but also through actions and such matters; on the contrary, we see tangibly that these things are engraved and remembered more deeply in the soul of the student.

The practical outcome is that prior to the desired participation, there must be an explanation from the teacher or guide regarding the inner point of this participation. From the above, the necessary caution in such matters is also understood, for there is always room for the student to hear a different explanation from someone else regarding the matter in which he is participating. As you mention in your letter, a second explanation can lead to the opposite conclusion. As you also note in your letter, in a case of doubt in such matters, "sit and do not do" is preferable. And regarding your point about not separating oneself from the community: on the contrary, sometimes one must use additional emphasis regarding the importance of a method and worldview that is to such an extent that one **must** separate from the community, and not be enticed by the fact that many say the opposite.

3) Regarding what you wrote about your son, may he live, who has not completely freed himself from what is happening to him, etc., even though the situation has become much better than it was in the past.

Surely the doctor has explained to you that the aforementioned depends on his nervous background, or at least a significant part of it. When there is improvement, strengthening, and self-discipline, etc., there is also improvement in the matter. However, in order to increase the improvement and nullify the whole issue, there are several remedies that doctors prescribe, such as limiting food and, of course, drinking close to bedtime, etc.

4) Regarding what you wrote about preventing pregnancy, etc.

Our Torah—from the word *hora'ah* (instruction)—is a Torah of life (which includes life not only in the World to Come, but also in this world, and on the contrary—this is the essential thing, for "it is not in heaven"). And the matter of blood pressure, aside from the fact that it changes from time to time and depends on the state of agitation and general mood, etc., and that distraction reduces it significantly, the doctor will also explain to you that thousands upon thousands of people with blood pressure higher than normal give birth to sons and daughters in the best possible way, etc.

The main point in the above is that any interference on the part of man in such matters, which belong solely to the Creator of the world and its Guide, is the opposite of simple logic, and not only the opposite of the Torah’s perspective. I should add a few more points to this, and I will bring only two:

(a) It is the obligation of this generation, in which each person is like a brand plucked from the fire of the holocausts, may Hashem protect us, to fulfill not only what was done by those who perished for the sanctification of Hashem’s name, but the essential thing is to also fulfill the number of the children of Israel, literally.

(b) In our current era, when everyone searches for excuses and precedents, even in a strange manner, just to make their way of life easier, there is a great fear that the aforementioned conduct will influence others to do the same. For the cause of blood pressure is not publicized, and people do not ask for the reason or explanation, etc., but rather they bring proof from the actual conduct.

May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good news regarding all of the above, and regarding your success in the holy work of education on the foundation of purity, and "whoever adds, they add to him."

With blessings for good tidings and a happy holiday.

Due to the sanctity of the festival, the Rebbe shlita did not sign, and I am signing on his behalf.

The Secretary

## 7053

7053

B”H, Chol Hamoed Sukkos, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yitzchak Damiel
Greetings and blessings!

I trust you have received my letter of New Year’s blessings, as well as the keys to Likutei Torah that were sent to you.

Since you wrote that the members of your group have been engaged in a discussion regarding my two letters, I am sure you will write to me about the continuation of that discussion.

Regarding your request that I write in greater detail concerning certain points in my letters: in addition to the pressing matters that the current time brings, which also makes it difficult to concentrate on the subject mentioned, there is a further point—and this is the main one. It is much easier to write an additional explanation or a continuation of the two aforementioned letters if I receive information as to which points or matters you are finding difficult, or which do not seem reasonable to you, or were not sufficiently clarified in my letters. Then, I will endeavor to write at greater length.

Enclosed is a copy of my general letter for this year’s Rosh Hashanah. In truth, its content is also relevant to the subject matter of the aforementioned letters, and especially to the second letter, which is based on the recognition—as in the saying of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe: “A Yid neither can nor wants to be severed from Elokus.” This is certainly, and simply, true for each and every one of the inquirers, and therefore, perhaps any further explanation will be entirely unnecessary if only—as translated in Likutei Torah at the beginning of Parshas Shemini—they are “touched” in their inner essence.

Surely it has also reached you, as we have discussed several times here, that this year marks the 200th anniversary of the histalkus-hillula of the Baal Shem Tov. It is appropriate to note two primary points regarding the Baal Shem Tov’s essence and avodah, which on the face of it are opposites: a) that he connected and even united with the simple Jews, and b) that he brought before them—and, as our Sages of blessed memory precisely state, “before them” means to their inner essence—the secrets of the Torah, including even the secrets of the secrets. But in truth, these two points are one, according to the principle in Chassidus, explained in many places, that whatever is higher, higher still—and only that which is higher, higher still—can descend lower, lower still. From this also follows the result that every matter in Chassidus must reach the level of practical action, and not just a minor action, but specifically a major action—an action in physicality and matter. Through this, the higher, higher still, and the lower, lower still, are united, and by this means, one draws down that which is not in the category of “above” and “below” at all—that is to say, the Atzmus and Mahus, which is the whole of man.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above, and a happy holiday to you and your entire family.

Due to the holiness of the festival, the Rebbe shlita has not signed, and I am signing on his behalf,

The Secretary

## Zhena

B"H, 25 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a very long interval, I received your letter from 28 Elul (which apparently was sent via regular mail).

Regarding what you wrote about your schedule, it is understood that it requires a fundamental correction. My meaning is simple: you must begin to increase your actual Torah study. Our Sages have given us their assurance and definitive ruling that one who fulfills the Torah out of poverty (of time) will eventually fulfill it out of wealth (of time). This is also understood from the words of our Sages in the Mishnah, that whoever accepts upon himself the yoke of Torah, the yoke of government and the yoke of worldly affairs are removed from him. The emphasis here is specifically on the **yoke** of Torah—not only when one has plenty of time, plenty of desire, etc.—and further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

It is my hope that you are keeping up with the three daily study portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, as is well known, and that you are maintaining the set times for the study of Chassidus that you mentioned, in addition to your study on Shabbos. This is especially true in light of what is explained in the writings of the Arizal, that on Shabbos there is a necessity to study the inner dimension of the Torah (which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus).

Regarding your news about the condition of your wife, may she live and be well, may Hashem fulfill the days of her pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child, in its proper time and season, properly and with ease.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

P.S.
It is my hope, even though you did not mention it, that your wife, may she live and be well, is utilizing her talents for the dissemination of traditional Judaism and its matters, especially in the field of education, for which she has been gifted from Above with a special talent, as she has seen in practice in the past.

## 7,057

7,057

B”H, 27 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter of 17 Elul was received, and the response was delayed due to the preoccupations of the auspicious days of this month.

I was pleased that my letter reminded you of the strong bond you have with Lubavitch, and that it stirred in you memories of days gone by, as well as the memory of your father, of blessed memory, and his inner connection with Lubavitch. And since our Sages, of blessed memory, have said that the Holy One, blessed be He, did not create a single thing in vain, surely these memories will have their effect, in accordance with the motto of our people, the Children of Israel, that action is the essential thing.

Regarding what you write—that your work is not satisfying, and that at most it serves to improve the deed but not to improve the person, etc.—in this area in particular, Chassidic teaching places special emphasis on the effect of action upon the person. In truth, action sometimes influences the person more deeply than the activity of speech and thought. This is why we find in the Torah an extra emphasis on the actual performance of mitzvos, and only afterwards comes the matter of faith—in the sense of *na'aseh* (we will do) and then *nishma* (we will hear). This is true even though it is well known how much [our Sages] condemned the matter of "the commandments of men learned by rote." This is also brought in the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of our Alter Rebbe, Epistle 21, which concludes with the words of the great teacher, the physician of the soul and the physician of the body alike, the Rambam, in his commentary on the Mishnah in *Avos*: "Everything is according to the abundance of the action"—to refine the soul.

This is especially true since it is said of the Jews, "a land of desire" (*eretz chefetz*), and the Baal Shem Tov’s parable regarding this is well known: that when one looks from the outside, one cannot imagine the treasures hidden in the depths; so it is regarding the sons and daughters of Israel. There is more on this point in the content of my general letter for this year’s Rosh Hashanah, a copy of which is enclosed herewith, and I hope you will find interest in it.

With respect and blessing,

#### ***7,057***

**And the Baal Shem Tov’s parable is well known:** See also above, Vol. 18, Epistle 6,195, and the references in the notes there. Vol. 17, 6,499.

## 758

B"H, 28 Tishrei, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, man of fine character and many accomplishments,
R' Yosef Eliyahu, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

As you requested, I will mention you and all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter. May it be His will that just as you brought the request, you will also bring good news regarding this.

The merit of your activities in the manner of *tomechin d'oraysa* (supporters of Torah)—even more so than your own personal study—will surely stand for you and your family, may they live and be well, in the aforementioned matters.

As emphasized in the *maamar* of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe—the authority on the *nistar* (hidden) aspects of Torah—and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the authority on the *nigleh* (revealed) aspects of Torah—on the verse, "It is a tree of life to those who grasp it" (*Simchas Torah* 5740): These are the *baalei hasagah* (those with intellectual comprehension) who study Torah, and those who support them are "blessed" (*me'ushar*). These are the *baalei avodah* who engage in Torah; "blessed," *glicklech*. As it is stated in the *Zohar* (Vol. III, 59b), read not *me'ushar* (blessed), but *merosho* (from its head), for through their *avodah* they draw down from "its head"—that is, from the inwardness of the *Ein Sof*, may He be blessed—and this is the virtue of the foot that sustains the head specifically.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## Janet

B"H, 30 Tishrei, 1st day of Rosh Chodesh Marcheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Women’s Divisions of the Bais Rivkah Schools,
May Hashem grant you life,

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to hear about the annual undertakings of the various divisions—Crown Heights, East New York and Brownsville, West Side—which are taking place today and in the coming days of this month. It is especially satisfying that, immediately following the festive month of Tishrei, in the first "weekday" month of the year—Marcheshvan—the women’s groups have renewed their activity for the Bais Rivkah schools without any loss of time. This also gives me hope that this important and holy work will be carried out under the full influence and inspiration of the month of Tishrei, which, as the first month of the year, sets the tone for the entire year. Especially since the holy days of the month of Tishrei contain specific directives for Jewish women and mothers.

It is well known that our Sages, of blessed memory, arranged the reading of the Torah and the Haftaros so that what we read in the Torah and the Prophets reflects the content of the holy days and their directives for daily life.

In the first days of the year—the days of Rosh Hashanah—we read in the Torah about the birth of the first Jewish child born as a Jew to Jewish parents, and about the mesiras nefesh of Jewish parents for the upbringing of a child. This is also the content of the Haftarah of the first day of Rosh Hashanah, regarding another Jewish mother—Channah—and the birth of a Jewish child—Shmuel—and her mesiras nefesh in dedicating her only child to a G-dly education. Also in the Haftarah of the second day of Rosh Hashanah, where we beseech the Ribono shel Olam to take the Yidden out of galus, it is stated that what awakens the Divine compassion is "Rachel weeping for her children"—the mother Rachel mourning the fate of her children.

The lesson from this—which must serve as a foundation for the entire year—is to know that a Jewish child, from birth, belongs to the Ribono shel Olam; that Jewish parents, and mothers in particular, must have mesiras nefesh for the chinuch hakasher of their children; and that chinuch hakasher al taharas hakodesh is the foundation of the Geulah Shleimah, speedily in our days.

And this is the work of the women’s auxiliary groups for the Bais Rivkah schools, and the greatest merit for bringing true happiness to each one individually, to them and their families, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings and for success in this work.

706

B"H, 30 Tishrei, 5720

This letter is being written and the response sent during the auspicious days of the month of Tishrei, which is the seventh month. It is called "seventh" in its entirety—not only its Yomim Tovim—and as our Sages explain, it is "saturated" (*musba*) with all good. The words of our Rebbes are well known: that this month is a general month for the entire year, and we draw its influence into all the days of the year.

May it be so regarding the general and specific matters of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad: to draw down the blessing and goodness of this month upon the days to come, with joy and gladness of heart, to increase in good deeds, and to influence others to do the same.

With blessings for good tidings and success in your holy work.

## 761

B"H, 1st of Mar-Cheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 27th of Tishrei... and there is no difficulty regarding this.

It is surprising that you write about your studies in the aforementioned field, yet you make no mention of the primary study for every Jewish man and woman: the study of our holy Torah, the *Toras Chaim* (Torah of Life). The content of this name is to be taken literally—it is a guide for life, specifically for day-to-day life, to know the deeds that one should do and those that one should not do. This is especially true given that you are in a land that even the nations of the world call the Holy Land, and it is written: "A land which Hashem your G-d seeks out; the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year." From this, it is understood that the vigilance in observing the *mitzvos* must be many times greater in this land. I am certain you will elaborate on this in your next opportunity.

With blessings for success in your studies and in conduct befitting a daughter of Israel, for every one of them is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah.

With blessings for good news,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

#### ***761***

**In response to your letter from the 27th of Tishrei:** As printed above in Vol. 18, 6777; the date there is incorrect.

## 762

762

B"H, 1st of Menachem Av, 5720

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 28th of Tishrei, along with the enclosure. It is understandable that there is wonder and astonishment that he is depressed, etc., at a time when Divine Providence has granted him the merit and success to engage in holy work—the affairs of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, and, in its inner essence, the spreading of the wellsprings outward. And surely the ruling of our Torah is well-known: "Whoever takes upon himself, etc." May it be the will [of Hashem] that very soon he will bring good tidings that are visibly and revealedly good, in all the matters about which he writes.

We are currently on the morrow of the "seventh month," which is as its name implies—all the days of the month are included in this, and our Sages of blessed memory expounded that it is "satiated" (*mushba*) with all good. It is the general month, from which its matters are drawn down upon the entire year, provided that the Torah and mitzvos serve as the channel and the vessels for the drawing down and receiving of the blessings and influences of the Ribono shel Olam.

And this is easy to understand.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7,263

Brooklyn.

Regarding your question about the teachings of the Maggid of Mezritch in the books of the Mitteler Rebbe: although "what we have not seen is not proof" [that it does not exist], it is known that, in general, his books do not mention the names of the books or the individuals whose teachings he cites, unlike the books of the Tzemach Tzedek and even the books of the Alter Rebbe.

Concerning the books of the Tzemach Tzedek, such indices have not yet been compiled; for one who wishes to find something, there is no other recourse but to go through the books page by page.

Regarding what you wrote about publishing my letters to you—if there will be any benefit in this for the awakening of fear of Heaven, Torah, and mitzvos, it is understood that you have permission to do so.

With respect and with wishes that each one of us will fulfill all that depends on him to spread the wellsprings of the Baal Shem Tov until they reach the outermost reaches, and we will merit the coming of the Master, King Moshiach, speedily in our days.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 765

B"H, 3rd of Mar-Cheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the Avreich, Yaakov Emanuel, may he live,

Peace and Blessing!

After a long interval, I received your letter from Rosh Chodesh Cheshvan, in which you write of your activities in the field of education and in spiritual matters in general.

It is understandable that I was especially pleased to read about your shiurim with a group of youth that is growing in quantity, and surely in quality as well—though, naturally, this is most difficult to perceive with physical eyes. My hope is strong—even though you do not mention it—that in your explanation of the Thirteen Principles, etc., you utilize every opportunity to connect the concepts to *maaseh b'poel* (actual deed), and even more so, to daily life. Especially since, as the Mishnah rules, "the deed is the essential thing," which is not merely a separate part, but is essential for the existence of the entire matter. See also *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Epistle 21. It is also understood that the expression used above, **utilizing** every opportunity, also includes **creating** an opportunity, since the general opportunity—that is, your meeting with the group—is sufficient to establish the demand for instruction in the *halachos* required for daily life; and this is clear.

All of the above applies also to the *beis knesses* where you are continuing your involvement after having been there during the *moadim* of the month of Tishrei. Regarding all that has been said, the ruling of our Sages applies: "You have labored and you have found." Regarding the listeners, even if there are those among them who are currently fulfilling the state of "I am asleep in exile," the conclusion of the verse certainly applies to them: "but my heart is awake" (to Hashem, His Torah, and His mitzvos), and this will be found within them.

May it be the will of Hashem that you increase in all the above, in accordance with the demands of the hour and the motto of the previous year and the current one—"and you shall spread out" (*u'faratzta*), etc. Furthermore, we have the added dimension of the bicentennial year of the passing and *hillula* of the Baal Shem Tov, for when his wellsprings spread outward, the Master, King Moshiach, will come.

With blessings for success and for good tidings in all the above.

## 776

B"H, 5th of Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, involved in communal needs,
Rabbi Sh. Y. [Zevin], may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...My opinion is clear: participation in a coalition (and certainly, and all the more so, in a ministerial position that brings about the commission of a sin, etc.) is absolutely forbidden according to the Shulchan Aruch. And the matter of sin is present in most government ministries, and perhaps in all of them. And first and foremost in the Ministry of Religious Affairs—in the plural—where there are actual prohibitions of avodah zarah. And it is magnified many times over when the person signing the order is one who wears tefillin, for this is an additional declaration that one must partner, Heaven forbid, etc.

The question that will be asked is simple: after all, it is precisely upon this ministry that the funding for many matters of the Jewish religion depends. But it is obvious that one may not trade in mitzvos and sins in general, and who can say regarding one of the three [cardinal sins]—and the first of them, avodah zarah in its literal sense—that such a thing has not occurred since the Men of the Great Assembly nullified it? And especially to carry out this matter in the name of Klal Yisrael.

My intention in writing the above (which you surely suspect me of, and it is a well-founded suspicion) is that if it is in your power to prevent the aforementioned—and Eretz Yisrael is accustomed to miracles—may a blessing come upon you, and the merit of the many will assist you.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 67

B"H, 11 MarCheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn

To the Kfar Chabad Committee
May Hashem protect them and grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

Following my previous letter, which has surely been received by now, and further to your letter of 4 Tishrei:

1) It is appropriate that the areas you write about, which are beyond the train tracks, should be under the jurisdiction of the village committee for the purposes you describe. This also applies regarding the Moroccans, if the areas allocated to them are also located there.

2) Regarding what you wrote about planting an orchard in the middle of the village—it is understood that the matter requires further study as to whether it is advisable, for the reasons you mention. You should consult with the appropriate offices and also investigate whether such a thing exists in other settlements and villages in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, that are in a similar situation to yours.

3) I received the joyous news that there were already a few hundred esrogim on those citrus trees in Kfar Chabad that were brought from Calabria, even though this year they were not used, as per the statement of our Sages, for they were not yet fit for "heavenly work," etc., and also because an esrog must not be orlah (Tanya, Chapter 37). It is surprising that this happy news was not reported from the village. At the same time, it was brought to my attention that there is a lack of protection for these trees against winds, etc., by erecting a fence or planting suitable trees, etc. I am sure that those involved in this matter will attend to it in good time.

4) Regarding what you wrote about the possibilities and plans for expanding Kfar Chabad and Chabad institutions in general—as is also apparent from your letter, there is still a lack of proper foundation in the village's affairs and existing institutions, as well as in private areas. There is room for concern that if several new matters are added, the aforementioned will be further diminished.

5) Regarding the manner of utilizing the various areas in the village in connection with the mikveh that will finally be built (may it be Hashem’s will, speedily in our days) as a Chabad center—you should consult with experts in the field of village and settlement planning, together with the elders of Anash in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, in general. For as mentioned above, this is a matter that concerns all of Anash in Eretz Yisrael, and it has already been said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

6) Surely you are making plans in good time for utilizing the month of Kislev, the Month of Redemption. For apparently, despite all the requests, entreaties, and urging from here to prepare plans in advance, even regarding the Four Species campaign this year, several details were done in haste at the very last moment, and this apparently had an effect on the results. I must also point out that the pamphlet for the Four Species and the pamphlet for Simchas Torah also showed signs of haste, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above and for success in your holy work.

It is understood that the facility for artificial insemination cannot be in the middle of a village or settlement, and it must be at the greatest possible distance from educational institutions. It is a great wonder that there was even a discussion about this.

## 770

B"H, 11 MarCheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, R' Yitzchak, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, I received your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, along with the *pidyon nefesh*, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be the will of Hashem that the content of your next letter will also be joyous regarding the state of your health.

Especially since we have just emerged from the month of Tishrei—the seventh month, which is "satiated" with all goodness and serves as a general template for the entire year—may the blessing and success apply to all your affairs, both general and specific, throughout the entire year.

With blessings for good tidings, in good health, and with peace of mind,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding what you wrote concerning the doctors' instruction to eat frequently, and how this conflicts with the length of your morning *davening*, as you have hitherto been careful not to taste anything before *davening* based on the instruction—the aforementioned eating, due to the ailment you describe, is a medical matter (to prevent the accumulation of acidic juices in the stomach) and not because of hunger, nor even for the strengthening of the body. Based on this, the permission is explicit (in *Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken*, end of section 89, subsection 6; and see the words of the *Pri Chadash* cited in *Machatzis HaShekel* there). One should also note the general rule known from the *Taz*, *Yoreh Deah*, section 117. It is highly probable that the instruction [not to eat before *davening*] was certainly not intended for a case such as this. To be extra certain, you should consult with three people regarding this conduct.

Regarding what you wrote about the sum of money given to you, and that you already wrote to the donor that you would not accept it, etc.—since the act [of giving] has already been done, you should distribute it—along the lines of our Sages' statement in *Bava Basra* 133b—a third to the Lubavitch house in London, a third to the *kupah* (fund) of *Keren HaShanah* here in *Machaneh Yisrael*, and a third for your own needs, *un farnitzen freilicherheit* (and spend it with joy).

## 772

B"H, 14 MarCheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Talmud Torah Beis Yosef Yeshiva Lubavitch
in Toronto
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life

Shalom u’Bracha!

After the longest of intervals, report no. 39 was received.

Regarding its conclusion, you request instructions concerning the mikveh.

It is clear that the matter of a mikveh is of the utmost importance. Since it is located in the building of the Talmud Torah Yeshiva Lubavitch and is also known as the "Lubavitcher Mikveh," it is understood that one must strive with all necessary effort not only to ensure that everything is arranged properly—as written in the report—but that it should further develop, and the number of visitors should increase many times over.

Indeed, the initial period has long since passed; it is only the beginnings that are difficult, especially in a matter such as this, where the merit of the many assists them.

It is worth noting and illuminating how deeply our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, were involved in this. It is a wondrous thing: even those among them who, for various reasons, did not wish to issue halachic rulings—to the extent that even when it was necessary to rule, they would hand the text to a Rav so that he would be the one to state the law—made an exception for the laws of *mikveh taharah*. They concerned themselves with this with special attention, sending responsa, detailed instructions, and so on.

According to the way of *drush*, *remez*, and *sod*, there is a connection between the two matters—for the most essential element in successful *chinuch* on the purity of holiness is the birth of the child in purity and holiness. And this is understood.

May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good tidings regarding both general and specific matters, for we have just come from the month of Tishrei—the seventh month, which is sated with all good—and it is the general principle for the entire year, drawing down goodness, blessing, and success in all matters of the year.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned.

## 763

763

B"H, 14 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Enclosed are the letters that you provided for me to read... Regarding the substance of the discussion in the attached letters, I have also enclosed a clipping from a periodical published in Denver. Seemingly, all of the above are **specifically** seeking new paths. Now, it is understood and also simple that if these are new paths for an old goal, there is room to discuss and examine whether this is correct—even though our Sages said that all paths are presumed [to be valid], etc. But if, G-d forbid [and according to reports there is room for this concern], they are also seeking new "goals" specifically, or—to put it in other words—a new religion, then from the very outset of the law, there is a refutation.

Seemingly, the path, after all, is through emphasizing the ruling of the Mishnah, that the deed—the accepted [practice]—is the essential thing, and that the precedence of *na'aseh* (we will do) to *nishma* (we will hear) was a **necessary** condition for the receiving of the Torah. And this is not only in those days, but in every single day. Only now, the matter is much easier, after the experience of several thousand years, which has demonstrated the eternity of the Torah and the mitzvos.

And in matters of Torah and mitzvos, there is no room for negotiation—meaning, that they would concede on a portion of them in principle, provided that they accept upon themselves the other portion. For even though regarding actual fulfillment, the command is to strive for the fulfillment of even a minor detail of *divrei sofrim*, even by the most insignificant person or a complete *rasha*, G-d forbid, this is not a precedent or a lesson at all for establishing a new system of negotiation in religion.

Certainly, elaborating on all of this is entirely superfluous. May it be G-d’s will that you not be impressed by the fear of what the reaction will be from those with whom you are in contact if you inform them of all the above, since these are not my words nor your words, but the ruling of our holy Torah, *Toras Chaim*, in its literal sense. You can cite their sources in the Rambam, etc., in addition to what is explained in the books of the history of the Children of Israel, in the chapter regarding movements that innovate or distort the religion of Israel and its Torah. It is also understood that you have permission to quote me as well, as you know that this is my opinion, or that I have written this in one of my letters, etc. But as mentioned, the matter is agreed upon from the earliest of the early authorities down to the very last of the late authorities.

763. Received letter of 7 Menachem Av with the enclosure.

With blessings for good news in all the above.

## 7404

B.H., 14 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn

To the illustrious Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent scholar,
Rabbi Shmuel, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 9th of Menachem Av regarding the Kaddish and Yahrtzeit for an infant—to be recited by his father, may he live, etc.—it appears from the tone of your letter that the parents of the father do not object to this, etc. It should also be noted that there is no room for a discussion regarding "encroaching upon the boundaries" of other mourners*.

You have already noted the Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, section 376. See there the Pischei Teshuvah, subsection 3, regarding the law if the deceased was under twenty years of age. This matter is explained even further in the Sdei Chemed, Asifat Dinim, Maarechet Aveilut, subsections 151, 162, and 218; see also Shulchan Aruch, ibid., section 344, paragraph 4. From all of the above, it is implied that the recitation of Kaddish (and likewise the Yahrtzeit) is beneficial once thirty days have passed; see the Shach there. Regarding those who wish to distinguish between the Kaddish recited after Tzidduk HaDin and a standard Kaddish—arguing that the latter, being for the elevation of the soul, should perhaps not be recited before the age of thirteen, as the child was not yet obligated in mitzvos—this has already been refuted based on the sources cited in the aforementioned Sdei Chemed, and in the Sefer Kol Bo Al Aveilut by Rabbi Greenwald.

It is true that in the Sefer Yalkut Dat V’Din (by Rabbi David Assaf, Haifa, 5745), a letter from the illustrious Rabbi Tzvi Pesach Frank, may he live, was printed stating that before the age of thirteen, one does not observe Yahrtzeit or recite Kaddish. However, he brought no supporting evidence for his words, and in the aforementioned sefarim, the opposite is argued.

Now, the well-known difficulty regarding this matter, brought in the Noda B’Yehuda, Second Edition, Yoreh Deah, section 8, is based on what is written in Sanhedrin 104a. However, it is brought in many places that this is resolved in Tosafot, Sotah 10b, s.v. "d'aitai," that prayer saves.

This is explained at length in the Tzava'ah (Testament) of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory (printed in Kuntres Chinuch L'Naar, page 19; see there at length). From there, it is also proven that a father has a higher status regarding this than other relatives, and this is well-understood.

Regarding a different matter, to conclude your letter concerning the calculation of the Yahrtzeit day—whether it is from the day of death or the day of burial—the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is as follows: The Yahrtzeit is on the day of death, even in the first year, and even if the day of burial is far removed from the day of death (printed in Hayom Yom, 13 Shevat).

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon we merit the fulfillment of the prophecy, "And I will turn the hearts of the fathers to the children, and the hearts of the children to their fathers," for "He will swallow up death forever, and those who dwell in the dust will awaken and sing."

One may look into the wondrous hints in the phrase "He will swallow up death forever" (specifically), in the commentary Dan Yadin, page 49—on the Sefer Karnayim—by the G-dly Kabbalist Rabbi Shimshon of Ostropol. It relates to Yonah ben Amitai, who is known to have drawn down Ruach HaKodesh during the Simchat Beit HaShoeivah. May we merit its fulfillment soon, with the building of the Third Beit HaMikdash and the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and blessings for good tidings.

***

*) According to the custom in these lands, everyone recites Kaddish together.

**R' Nachman, may he live:** Sudak, who traveled on a *shlichus* to manage the Lubavitch house in London, as mentioned above in Vol. 18, letter 6,974. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 13, 4,567. Below, 778.

## 771

771

B"H, 17 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, your letter from 8 Menachem Av was received. Regarding your questions:

a) Concerning the treatment for your face.

In general, it is correct [to seek treatment], for man is commanded to do what is within his power through natural means, and the Torah has granted the physician permission to heal. However, one must find a specialist in the field, and preferably one who has extensive experience, as they will more easily be able to determine the appropriate treatment for your face.

b) Since you have two brothers older than you, etc.

Although you are correct that regarding the marriage of a sister this is not an impediment, it is nonetheless worthwhile that you speak about this matter with a Rav and *moreh hora'ah* in your vicinity. He will rule for you with the authority of his *semichah*, and then the matter becomes *daas Torah*.

c) Regarding marriage in general.

One of the known pieces of advice in this regard is that you should resolve with appropriate firmness that when you marry, you will conduct your home on the foundations of Torah and *mitzvos*—in the observance of the laws of *taharas hamishpachah*, the observance of *Shabbos*, eating *kosher*, and so on. And Hashem, who looks into the heart and sees that you have resolved this in truth and with firmness, and that you will indeed act accordingly, will provide you with your appropriate *zivug*—suitable for you both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned.

## 777

B"H, 17 MarCheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to the telegrams received, I sent a telegram today, which reads as follows:

"Telegrams received. I look forward to continued good news. Surely you are following the doctors’ instructions for rest, etc., with strong bitachon and a good heart. With blessings, [my signature]."

As mentioned, you will surely not withhold the good of informing me of the state of your health, along with your other matters, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed—in accordance with the phrasing of the prayer where we ask and elicit from the Master of Blessings that which is good for us...

Regarding what I wrote in my telegram about rest, it is meant literally. As is standard, one of the most important and beneficial matters in such situations is rest in the simple sense: rest for the body and inner rest from worries and the like. This is so even though, on the face of it, every person is commanded regarding this in the Torah—for bitachon in the Creator of the world and its Guide, and as is known from the Baal Shem Tov’s explanation of hashgacha pratis down to the most minute details, acts to negate any room for worry of any kind. Furthermore, it is a foundation of faith, and this is well understood.

Surely you have received the regards from the guests from Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, who were here during the month of Tishrei—the seventh month, which is sated with all good. May it be His will that each of them brings tidings of only good, in both material and spiritual matters—true good, good for Heaven and good for people, good that bears fruit. And in the inner point, where matters expand and spread out, the concept of "may your springs spread outward" is fulfilled. Very soon, we will merit the fulfillment of the prophecy that "in his footsteps comes the Master, King Moshiach." We have now entered the bicentennial year of the histalkus-hilula of the Baal Shem Tov, the source of the aforementioned springs.

With blessings for good news as mentioned above.

P.S.

There is no contradiction between the above and what is written regarding worry in matters of Torah and mitzvos, for it is explained in the holy Tanya that there are specific times for this, and even during times of worry, "joy is implanted in my heart from this side," and this is well understood.
