## 67

B"H, 18 MarCheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write regarding your state of health and the situation in your family, may they live: when you write the Jewish names along with the mother’s name, you will all be mentioned at the Tziyun HaKadosh of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

Regarding your question as to why such a change has come about for you in comparison to how things were before you came to Eretz Yisrael: In general, Eretz Yisrael is referred to in our holy Torah by the name Eretz HaKodesh (the Holy Land). As the verse states, "The eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year." Therefore, upon arriving in the Holy Land, one must increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos. A fortiori, when one wishes to enter a country, one requires a visa from that country, and upon arriving in that country, one must conduct oneself according to the customs of that land, even if it is a different conduct than one was accustomed to previously. So too, and to a much greater extent, upon entering Eretz Yisrael—which is called the palace of the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He—Hashem Yisbarach, who is merciful, gracious, and the essence of good, does not demand more than one’s capabilities, and He provides various opportunities to fulfill His request. If, due to certain reasons, this has not been the case for you until today, by making a firm resolution to do so, Hashem Yisbarach helps one carry out that resolution. Therefore, I hope that regardless of how things may have been until today, you will make good resolutions to increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos (for no matter how good one may be in this, there is always room to increase), and Hashem Yisbarach will fulfill what He writes in His Torah: "If you walk in My statutes..." and He will grant blessing and success in all that you need. And according to what is written to me, that your son, may he live, studies in a Charedi school, I hope that you will continue in this spirit, so that all your children will be raised in this way, which will be a good beginning in the aforementioned, and "there is nothing that can stand before the will."

Enclosed is a check from one of the funds of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which you should mix with your own money; this will bring you success in what you require.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 780

B”H, 19 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 15 Menachem Av, in which you write that you have been asked to give a lecture to a group before whom you already lectured about two years ago.

It is unclear why you are in doubt. Since you have already lectured once before a large audience, why should you not do so now, especially since the setting is smaller? Surely you can take advantage of this opportunity to speak about the perspective of our holy Torah—Torah Chaim—regarding the role of man, the manner of his avodah to the Creator, and so on. Regarding what you wrote—that it is possible they will ask you several questions—if you have an answer ready on the spot, all the better. If not, you can always say that since the question is not part of your lecture, you will provide the answer at another time, at a second gathering, or in writing, and the like.

You do not mention when the aforementioned lecture is to take place. It seems you have a transcript of the first lecture; it would be worthwhile to send it here, so that there will be a clearer understanding of the entire matter.

Regarding what you wrote concerning guidelines for the aforementioned lecture, you surely have several maamarim of Chassidus, as well as the Tanya with its subject index, and also the index for Torah Or and the index for Likutei Torah that was just published. Based on the subject indices of the aforementioned, you can find the topics in which you are most interested.

At a time of favor, mention your son, may he live, at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

It is surely superfluous to urge you to increase your efforts in general in the dissemination of the wellsprings. This aforementioned opportunity can also be utilized for this dissemination, as is understood—especially since it seems that people with influence over certain circles will participate in the gathering. This is particularly true given that we are in this year, the bicentennial year of the passing and hillula of the Baal Shem Tov—a time and period auspicious for the dissemination of the wellsprings, until they reach even the outermost reaches.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 781

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his communal work, a man of fine character, R' Chaim Shaul, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Rather, you must ensure that the technical matters are handled specifically by others—and you understand—under your supervision, in a manner of "hovering" [from above], or at most, by checking in and out.

The same applies to supervising the classes. When you arrange for all the details of the matters, in practice, to be carried out by others, while you only receive reports, etc.—it will certainly increase your enthusiasm and desire, as well as your health in the literal sense, and you will be able to dedicate all your energy to the development of the Yeshiva. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

## 752

B"H, 21 MarCheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 14 MarCheshvan, in which you outline the main points of your life’s history and conclude by describing the difficulties you are currently facing regarding establishing yourself with a livelihood, as well as regarding matters of shidduchim.

Since, according to your letter, you have various offers regarding a position in holiness as a shochet or mashgiach, and taking into account that such positions are generally in demand now in the United States—especially when combined with the skills of a mohel and baal kriah—you should make a concerted effort to establish yourself in the United States in this field. This is, of course, without compromising on matters of Shulchan Aruch. Given the current information, this can be accomplished with the proper hishtadlus, especially considering your connections. Furthermore, even when considering a shidduch from another country, it has become known recently that in those other countries, it carries weight when one can state that they have a steady livelihood in America.

Taking advantage of this opportunity—as everything is surely by Hashgacha Pratis, including your reaching out to me—I wish to draw your attention to the necessity of setting fixed times for the study of Pnimiyus HaTorah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. As explained in many places, and specifically in the Kuntres Ets Chaim by the Rebbe Rashab, especially in this generation of Ikvesa D’Meshicha (as we see according to all the signs enumerated in Maseches Sotah), this is a necessity for all those who have studied in a yeshiva (even outside of Tomchei Temimim), and truly a personal obligation for everyone to add as much light as possible. Since we see the fulfillment of "there is no day whose curse is not greater than the previous one," and the darkness is becoming ever stronger—to the point where "they call darkness light and bitter sweet"—one must add ever more in the "light and the luminary" of Torah, which is Pnimiyus HaTorah. And there is nothing that can stand before the will. This is especially relevant since you have many acquaintances and friends among the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, whom you have met during your travels, etc.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

P.S.
You mention in your letter that some of your children, may they live, are located in Chicago. Among the rabbis there are also Anash, and perhaps it would be appropriate for you to connect with them if you think your children are in need of anything regarding matters of Yiddishkeit, as they might be able to assist with that.

## 783

783

B"H, 21 Mar-Cheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing man, who is full of good deeds,
R' Yaakov Yitzchak, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the eve of Shabbos, in which you ask about what is written in the holy Tanya, Chapter 12, that the *beinoni* is one who never allows the evil to prevail to such an extent, and has never committed a sin in his life and will never do so, etc.—you ask whether *teshuvah me'ahavah* (repentance out of love) is effective in this regard, to be considered as if he had never sinned at all.

Regarding the substance of your question, it is explained in *Maseches Yoma* (86a, end) that *teshuvah me'ahavah* uproots the sin from its inception. However, regarding what is written in the Tanya, there is room for study, for it emphasizes there that the title "rasha" is not applied to him even for a single moment in his life, as is also explained there in Chapter 1. If he subsequently performs *teshuvah*, he is called a *tzaddik gamur*.

Therefore, although it is a bit of a stretch in terms of the phrasing, I interpret what is stated at the beginning of Chapter 12 of the Tanya to mean that the standing and state of the *beinoni* is such that he is not susceptible to sin, neither in the future nor in the past. Even if it is possible that in the past he was in a different state, he has since changed in the interim through his *avodah* and actions, etc.

Based on this, what is stated in the beginning of Chapter 14 of the Tanya is also resolved: **that every** person can be a *beinoni* at any time and at any hour. That is to say, even a *rasha gamur* has the capacity for all that has been mentioned, for there is nothing that can stand before *teshuvah*, and he can repent in such a way that he will no longer be susceptible to all the matters enumerated in Chapter 12.

Although I do not mention this in my hope, I trust you have utilized the matters and possibilities of the month of Tishrei, especially since it is called the "seventh month," which is "saturated with all good," as our Sages of blessed memory state in the *Midrash Rabbah* in its place regarding the verse.

May it be the will of Hashem that since it is also the general month for the entire year, the blessing will be drawn down into all matters, both private and general alike. Among these is the *hafatzas hama'ayanos* (spreading of the wellsprings) until they reach the outermost reaches—especially this year, which is the bicentennial of the *histalkus* and *hilula* of the Baal Shem Tov, for when his wellsprings spread outward, "the Master will come"—this refers to the King Moshiach.

With blessings for good tidings in all that has been mentioned.

## 784

784

B”H, 22 Marcheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-scholar, and possessor of noble character, scion of a distinguished lineage, etc.,
R’ Shazar, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I received your telegram with pleasure, and I am responding with a prompt, urgent letter rather than a telegram, so that it may be clearer. I believe that a difference of a few days is of no consequence.

You ask what should be studied following the completion of the Tanya.

In my opinion, it is appropriate that they continue with the study of the sefer **Torah Or.** Among the reasons for this is that the reader or lecturer for the group will find explanations of the maamarim in Torah Or—especially the earlier ones—in the sefer **Toras Chaim** by the Mitteler Rebbe, and for some of the maamarim, also in the sefer **Ohr HaTorah** by the Tzemach Tzedek, as noted in the footnotes and references at the end of the Torah Or, Kehot edition, which is being sent to you in a separate package.

Allow me to add, based on the well-known statement of our Sages of blessed memory, “Great is study, for it leads to action,” that may it be G-d’s will that this be fulfilled through their aforementioned study as well.

I trust you received my letters in due time, as well as the indices for Likutei Torah, and the personal regards I sent via the visitors here during the month of Tishrei. I am certain you will write to me regarding this as well.

While writing to you, I must express my regret that Kfar Chabad B and the Chabad housing project in Jerusalem have not yet even entered the first stage of practical implementation. Aside from the fact that at such a time every moment is precious, there is also the fact that in the meantime, there were those who, had the aforementioned projects at least entered their first stage, would not have dispersed to other places, and others refrained from traveling to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, from the outset. However, since we have a great rule that one does not cry over the past (even though at times it is difficult to restrain oneself), my main purpose in writing is regarding the future. It is my hope that you will utilize all your influence to ensure that these matters progress in practice, at least from this point forward, as well as in the general affairs of Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

As I have concluded in several of my letters this year, I will take this opportunity to mention that this year is the 200th anniversary of the passing-hillula of the Baal Shem Tov. The Baal Shem Tov, according to the sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which were printed in the *Kuntres Chai Elul 5703*, began his avodah even before his revelation by concerning himself with the material needs of our fellow Jews. He also influenced the hidden tzaddikim of his generation in this direction, as explained at length in the aforementioned sichos; see there [since I am in doubt as to whether you have the aforementioned booklet in your possession, it is being sent along with the sefer Torah Or].

With respect and blessing for outstanding success in all the above.

This awakens memories that are passed down from generation to generation, which are recalled and stirred especially during jubilee years. And since the motto in all Jewish matters is, as our Sages stated in their Mishnah, "the deed is the essential thing," the purpose of these memories is that they should lead to actions in his spirit. It is well known that one of the Baal Shem Tov’s first activities, even before his revelation, was to strive to strengthen Jewish settlements in the villages and inns at the crossroads—not only in spirituality, but also in physicality. From this, there is a directive for each one of us, and further elaboration is unnecessary.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

I read in the press regarding a seminary for religious teachers, and that it seems the Union of Moshavim also has a part in this. I would be interested to know the details regarding this, and thank you in advance.

## Jaffa

B"H, 22 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Yechezkel Yissachar, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh regarding the expansion of the chicken coop:

In general, it is a sound idea to expand the farm in general, and there is no reason to be afraid of the fact that one must borrow money for the time being. However, as to whether this should be done within the area of the chicken coop or on another plot, you should consult with those who can assess the prospects regarding parnassah, whether in the area of the chicken coop or another agricultural possibility.

Regarding your question about whether one should generally want to earn more—there is already an answer to this: one gives maaser from tzedakah, and the choicest way to perform the mitzvah is to give a chomesh. According to the Iggeres HaTeshuvah and the Kodesh of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, it is even more than that. It is therefore understood that when the mosdos are in need of additional funds, and the need is ever-increasing, the tzedakah—and consequently, the income—must also be ever-increasing and greater. As an addition to this matter, the fact that anash, may they live, need to be in a state of expansion in gashmius as well, will also lead to an expansion in ruchnius, and this is easy to understand.

May the merit of your work in Kfar Chabad, for Kfar Chabad—where "Hashem commanded the blessing"—and also in Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, stand by you to bring good tidings in all of the above.

With blessing.

#### ***Jaffa***

## 789

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

Mr. Asher Zelig, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have been informed of your question regarding the text of the prayers.

In general, the text of the verses in the prayer book follows, of course, the text as written in the Tanach. However, at times there are variant versions, or perhaps a printing error in the Tanach, which accounts for the variation in the Siddur. Regarding the verse in Yirmiyahu 17:7, the word *mivtacho* should be vocalized with a *patach* under the *tet*, as is printed in most editions of the Tanach (although in some it appears with a *kamatz*, and therefore there are Siddurim that follow the *kamatz* version).

On this occasion, since everything is by Divine Providence, and you have turned to me regarding this, I will take the opportunity to awaken you to the necessity of establishing a regular study of the inner dimension of Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. If this was a necessity in all times and in all places, it is certainly so in our era, and in this country in particular.

And it is especially appropriate that you observe the practice of reciting the monthly Tehillim portion—as the Tehillim is divided for the days of the month—each day after morning davening.

With blessings for good news in all the above.

***

**Mr. Asher Zelig:** Rotberg, Brooklyn.

## 607

B"H, 25 MarCheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a long interruption, your letter from the beginning of the month of Cheshvan has arrived—it was delayed in transit longer than usual.

It is understandable that there is great surprise and wonder that you do not mention your activities in holy matters in general, and regarding the month of Tishrei in particular, concerning the dissemination of Yiddishkeit and the dissemination of the wellsprings of Chassidus specifically. If all Anash are obligated in this, how much more so those who have witnessed the kindnesses of Hashem Yisbarach—even when everything is going smoothly, and especially when one is requesting additional blessings from Hashem. Even for one who calculates that he has been conducting himself in this way for many years, it is surely understood that, on the contrary, that very fact is sufficient reason to demand of oneself even more, as explained in Iggeres HaKodesh, end of Chapter 9: "He was accustomed to reading one page, let him read two pages," etc. It is certainly unnecessary to elaborate on such self-evident matters.

May it be His will that I merit to receive good news regarding all of the above, and that it proceeds in a manner of "increasing and continuing, increasing and illuminating," until "you shall spread out to the west and to the east, to the north and to the south." When one conducts oneself as Hashem Yisbarach commands, then, as the Mishnah states: "Nullify your will before His will, so that He may nullify the will of others before your will," and so on.

Regarding the question of the sums you send to your mother, tichyeh, it is understood that you must maintain and continue this; the question and doubt regarding this is surprising.

As for the question of whether you may utilize your entire tzedakah fund, or a portion of it, for this purpose—and specifically from your maaser—you must ask a Rav who rules on halachic questions and provide him with the details; he will tell you the Daas Torah on the matter.

As we approach the month of Kislev, the month of miracles and redemption, may it be so in all your aforementioned affairs.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

In response to your questions:
a) For tzedakah, you should set aside approximately [amount] of your income (after deducting business expenses).
b) Renting the spacious location for the business—this is very correct (though you should first clarify the reason why the rent is so low).
c) Purchasing the wool you wrote about—this is correct. May it be, as mentioned above, with success.

## 701

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 21 Menachem Av, in which you write about what you have experienced and that, for the time being, you have not yet become engaged.

Regarding the undesirable matters that occurred in the past, the instruction of our Torah—Torah of life—is well known: that it is within the power of every person to rectify and improve their affairs from this point forward. True regret over the past, combined with a firm resolution for the future, is effective. Regarding shidduchim in particular, there are two points to add:

1) You must decide with the appropriate firmness that when you marry, you will conduct your home as is fitting for a daughter of Israel—each of whom is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah—through the observance of taharas hamishpachah, the observance of Shabbos, eating kosher, etc., among the other mitzvos of the Torah. Hashem, who sees into the heart, knowing that you have truly decided this and will indeed conduct yourself accordingly, will provide you with your appropriate match, both materially and spiritually.

2) You must recognize reality as it is: there is no perfection in the world. Therefore, one should not search for and scrutinize the shortcomings of those with whom one is becoming acquainted. This is especially true when taking into account that the person searching is also not perfectly flawless. When one looks at fellow Jews with a favorable eye and focuses on what is essential—good character traits, conduct in the upright path, which is the path of Torah and mitzvos, etc.—then, as a matter of course, one sees that the secondary and tertiary matters need not take up more space than they are worth. When the essential is present in its fullness, that is what determines the decision to say "yes."

It is appropriate that, following all of the above, you set aside a few coins for tzedakah every weekday morning until you become engaged and marry in a good and auspicious hour.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 792

B"H, 29 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your question as to what I meant concerning the shidduch for your sister-in-law and her sister, may they live:

The intention is simple—to suggest it to her respectfully through friends and acquaintances, and not through the parents. Experience has shown that this approach is more successful. Even when it is suspected that the parents are behind it, they still overlook this, especially when care is taken not to give any room for such suspicion.

Regarding your writing about the reasons for the lack of success in the Chabad sphere in your camp:

It is well known that even though the Torah exempts one who is truly coerced (*ones*), we do not say that it is considered as if he actually performed the deed. Ultimately, the task is to spread the wellsprings outward, and this cannot be replaced by explanations and justifications. When one approaches it in such a manner—meaning, that there is no choice and the spreading of the wellsprings is an absolute necessity—then certainly, as experience has shown in many such situations, one finds several ways, and I emphasize **several**, far more than just one method of action.

With blessings for good news regarding all that was mentioned, both in general and in detail.

Your letter was received, as was your telegram—the *pidyon nefesh* was read today at the Ohel. You will surely write with details regarding this.

## 793

B"H, 29 Mar-Cheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 24 Cheshvan, in which you write about the state of mind and the matters at [the seminary]... which are not satisfactory, and therefore the thought has occurred to you to study in a different city...

It is surprising to hear such a suggestion. You were raised in a Chassidic home and in a Chassidic environment, and you have surely heard many stories regarding the conduct of our Rebbes, the Nesi’im, and their life histories. This, too, serves as a lesson, for we are commanded to follow in the ways of our Rebbes, the Nesi’im. Their *mesiras nefesh* and their dedication in general to improving the situation of the sons and daughters of Yisrael—even those who are distant from them, whether physically or spiritually—is well known. From this, we derive a great principle for the conduct of each and every one of us within the collective of Yisrael.

Regarding your situation: if, as you write, the spiritual state is not satisfactory, and one of the reasons in your opinion is that among the students there are those who come from homes that are not strictly observant of Torah and *mitzvos*, etc., it is surely simple that if the number of students coming from *chareidi* homes decreases, the situation at [the seminary] will deteriorate.

Conversely, the more the number of these *chareidi* students increases, the more the situation will improve—especially when each one of them becomes an active force, similar to what is said to the *temimim*: "candles to illuminate."

It is understood from the above that you must completely dismiss the thought of leaving this seminary. On the contrary, since you have sensed the deficiency, you should organize all the students over whom you have influence, and also influence indirectly those who are not under your direct influence, so that a change for the better will occur in this regard. The merit of the many will surely assist you.

It is understood and also simple that it is within your authority and your merit to publicize these words of mine to the students involved in this matter, and together you will act in the direction mentioned. The Ribono shel Olam will surely grant you success, especially since the seminary is from the foundation and under the leadership of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nevgum, zi"a*, Nasi of Yisrael.

Awaiting good news in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 794

29 MarCheshvan, 5720
Brooklyn

To the distinguished Rabbi, the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and involved in communal affairs, etc.,
Rabbi Sh. Y. (may he live)

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Lech Lecha, regarding your attempt to justify the matters I wrote about in my previous letter: you yourself prefaced your remarks by noting that it is difficult to provide a halachic response to these issues. As for your claim that "they give them from their own," it is understood that this has no basis in Torah, neither in terms of halacha nor in practice, unless one wishes to turn a blind eye to the reality and the actions in question, which involve no "own" resources at all. There is no need to elaborate on a matter so distressing and alarming.

Regarding your statement that the mention of the prohibition of the "D.K." [Coalition] is a novelty to you:

- The novelty does not come from my side, for it is explicitly stated in the Shulchan Aruch as a matter of practical halacha. What, then, have I innovated here?

As for the argument that there is already a *chazakah* [presumption of validity] of several years—[I heard this same argument regarding the question of traveling on Israeli ships]—I have not found any support for it among the *poskim*; in fact, the opposite is true... The "justification" for the entire situation is apparently what is stated in a Maamar of Chassidus (though for the time being it is not clear to me who said or wrote it, even though it seemingly contains matters from the Alter Rebbe) on the *dih* "And the thousand and..." [the parable], that our generations are in a state of the deepest *hitalfuyis* [fainting/unconsciousness], [and therefore, they whispered into the ears of Bnei Yisrael the name, the coming of the Baal Shem Tov, whose name is Yisrael]. And the *hitalfuyis* also has a positive side, for if there were any awareness, it would be impossible to bear the pain, etc. And a word to the wise is sufficient.

...May it be the will of Hashem that since we are approaching the month of Kislev, the month of miracles and redemption—and specifically with oil that does not mix with other liquids, and in a manner of "increasing and going forward, increasing and adding light," and rejecting even the matter of the "fruit of the holiday" [i.e., the nations of the world, as they are protected in the Beis Hamikdash—this too, no]—that we will finally merit the fulfillment of the prophecy, "They shall be for you alone, and no strangers with you." And may it be in our immediate time, and even before the beginning of the aforementioned month.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

...Regarding what was written that in Iggeres HaKodesh, end of section 10, "to cleave to her" should be "to cleave to **Him** [Hashem]": Seemingly: 1) The continuation "hers" (referring to the Sukkah of Dovid [or "his"—Dovid]) would not fit well. 2) Preceding this, the discussion is about the *avodah* of Hashem or the Sukkah of Dovid, not about cleaving to Hashem.

In the early editions of Iggeres HaKodesh, it is written as it is before us, except that the aforementioned note is missing. It appears that "to her" refers to the Sukkah of Dovid—the *Malchus*, the *Shechinah*, as our Sages say in many places, "to cleave to the *Shechinah*." (Note, for the general matter, Likutei Torah, Chukas 63d; see there 20b).

## 704

By the Grace of Hashem, Erev Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the G-d-fearing, distinguished, and learned congregants of the Nusach Ari Beis Medrash...

Peace and Blessing!

As we find ourselves on Erev Rosh Chodesh Kislev—a month of redemption, miracles, and victory, as is known to all Yidden—and as I prepare to travel to the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, as is the custom every Erev Rosh Chodesh in general, and this Erev Rosh Chodesh Kislev in particular:

I was astonished, and pained, to hear a rumor—which I hope is not true in practice—that there is a desire, Heaven forbid, to change the good custom of reciting and studying the teachings of our Rebbes, the Chassidus of Chabad, in the Beis Medrash. This has been the practice for many years and generations, and it is a custom that is even reflected in the very name of the shul, Nusach Ari.

As I said above, I want to be firm in my confidence that this is nothing more than a rumor, and that you will continue this good custom as you have until now, and even add to it, in accordance with the directive of our holy Torah to "increase in holiness," and the instruction of the mitzvah of Chanukah candles, which must be *mosif v'holech, mosif v'or*—increasing and progressing, adding more light.

I am certain that all the congregants of the Nusach Ari Beis Medrash will help maintain this custom. In truth, it is no longer merely a custom; through the *chazakah* of many years, it has already become a *din Torah*.

Furthermore, and this is also essential: it is well known that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, as well as his father and every generation back to the Alter Rebbe, demanded the *hafatzas hamaayanos*—the spreading of the wellsprings of Chassidus everywhere. It was explicitly emphasized that this is not a matter only for Chabad Chassidim, but, in the course of time, for all of Klal Yisrael. If this was a demand in the time of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and even earlier, then how much more so in our generation, the *ikvesa d'meshicha*, when we require *siyata d'shmaya* at every single step.

My astonishment was even greater to hear that it is possible that some of the Satmar Chassidim might be dissatisfied, or even interfering with this study of Chabad Chassidus. This is especially striking given that this past Sukkos, I received the sefer *Yoel Moshe* [by the Rebbe of Satmar, shlita], in which he cites, relies upon, and bases his arguments on the words of the Alter Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch. It is truly difficult to believe that one of his own Chassidim would act in opposition to this—and even more so, to interfere with others in such a matter, and in public.

As I said above, I hope that the study of Chabad Chassidus will continue without any interference. I will be brief this time and wish you peace—true peace. As our Sages ruled (Sanhedrin 99b): "Whoever occupies himself with Torah for its own sake brings peace to the heavenly retinue and the earthly retinue." This matter is explained at length in *Likutei Torah* by the Alter Rebbe in the *maamar* beginning with the words *Hechaletzu*, as well as in the *maamar* with the same opening by the Rebbe (Rashab), which is enclosed herewith.

With blessings for a joyous and Chassidishe month. Through this aforementioned study, which is a part of *hafatzas hamaayanos*—spreading the wellsprings of the Baal Shem Tov outward—may we merit, very soon, the fulfillment of the response of Melech HaMashiach: "When your wellsprings spread outward."

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the above.

## 797

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, etc.,
R' Yaakov, may he live.

...It is my hope that you are utilizing the days of this month, the month of miracles and redemption, in which falls the Rosh Hashanah of the teachings of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus. This is also included in the Rosh Chodesh itself (which is why it is called "head" [Rosh] and not "beginning" [techilah], as explained regarding the name Rosh Hashanah). This is especially true given that in your camp [the city of Bnei Brak] there is a central location for many yeshivos, and according to reports, there is a noticeable shift among the yeshivah students to hear (derheren) matters concerning the inner dimension of the Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus.

## 798

798

B"H, 1 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and cherishers of Torah and mitzvos,
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

This year marks 200 years since the histalkus-hilula of the Baal Shem Tov, the founder of the general Chassidic movement. It is well known that the Baal Shem Tov began his holy avodah as an educator of young children. He was a teacher’s aide, and he would carry the little children in his arms and bring them to cheder, teaching them the alef-beis, brachos, Krias Shema, and so on, with a love and devotion that knew no bounds.

The Nesi’ei Chabad—from the Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya, who established the Chabad Chassidic system upon the foundations laid by his "grandfather," the Baal Shem Tov, to the founder of the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Lubavitch, Admur Moharashab, and his son, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, who transplanted the yeshiva to America—have, as is well known, spread Torah, yiras shamayim, and pnimiyus haTorah with great mesiras nefesh. Thus, today, the far-reaching branches of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, with the central yeshiva in Brooklyn at the helm, are the greatest creative forces in the field of kosher chinuch, based on the purity of holiness. There, every student becomes imbued with ahavas Hashem, ahavas haTorah, and ahavas Yisrael, and becomes a source of bright and living hashpaah in his entire environment.

On this day of Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 1 Kislev—a month of bright segulah, with the Yom HaGeulah of the Alter Rebbe and the mitzvah of the Chanukah lights, which is in a manner of **mosif v’holech** (increasing and continuing)—I turn to all the friends of the Lubavitcher yeshivos, and to all lovers of Torah and mitzvos in general, with a heartfelt call to support the annual campaign of the Merkaz Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, which aims to provide tangible assistance—a rescue effort—to ensure their existence.

The zechus of this mitzvah, which is connected with zechus harabim, and the zechus of the coming days of segulah, will surely stand by each and every one, together with their families, to enjoy the Ribono shel Olam’s blessings in a manner of mosif v’holech, in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

With respect and blessing,

Menachem Schneerson

## 699

B"H, 1 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn

To the Avreich, Levi, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 28th of Mar-Cheshvan, in which you write regarding the positive change in some of the matters you mentioned.

May it be Hashem’s will that you bring good news regarding the other matters as well.

It is understood and simple that since you are a bochur, you must increase even further in the study of Torah with persistence and diligence, and in the meticulous performance of its mitzvos, for through this, you will receive an increase in the blessings of Hashem, may He be blessed, in all that you require.

Since you mention that your father follows the good custom of setting aside money for tzedakah during *Vayivarech Dovid*—a practice rooted in the writings of the Arizal and in many other places—he should certainly continue this good custom now as well. This is also included in the concept of giving tzedakah before davening, the primary time for which is during the Shemoneh Esrei (as explained in the Alter Rebbe’s introduction to his Siddur). However, one should add to this by giving tzedakah before beginning the entire davening as well. And this is easy to understand.

With blessings for good news in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

[Footnote *] In the Pri Megadim, Orach Chayim, end of siman 92, in Mishbetzos Zahav, subsection 10, it is suggested that tzedakah before davening is fulfilled by giving during the recitation of *Vayivarech Dovid*. [And seemingly, the act of giving during *Vayivarech Dovid* includes the act of giving tzedakah before davening.] However, from what the Alter Rebbe writes in his Shulchan Aruch, where he treats the two matters separately (in siman 51 and siman 92), it is implied that these are two distinct acts of giving. Especially according to the intent behind these acts (which are explained in the writings of the Arizal regarding *Vayivarech Dovid*, and in the Alter Rebbe’s Iggeres HaKodesh, section 6, and in the Tzemach Tzedek’s Tehillim, siman 17), which are opposite in nature. And even though the law regarding giving before davening is brought in the Shulchan Aruch at the end of siman 92, it can be said that its appropriate time is before the entire davening. Furthermore, it is obvious that there is no place to interrupt between *Geulah* and *Tefillah* (which is the context of siman 92) with the act of setting aside tzedakah, and this is not the place to elaborate.

## Zaka

[2 Kislev, 5720]

...My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of the Alter Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya, often reminded us that one must learn from the weekly parsha regarding all the events of the week.

Coincidentally, Parshas Vayeitzei teaches us much about the responsibility of the woman as the **akeres habayis**, not only of her own home but of the entire **Beis Yisrael**. For in this parsha, we learn how Yaakov Avinu arrived in a foreign land and endured difficult times, yet despite all this, he established the Beis Yisrael there, where **all** the children remained loyal to the tradition of the Avos—Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov. And this was made possible thanks to the fact that the Jewish mothers—Rachel, Leah, Bilhah, and Zilpah—did everything that depended on them to ensure the integrity of their home and the future of their people...

#### ***Zaka***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 18, p. 213.

## 702

B.H., 2 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a long interruption, I received your letter from Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, the month of miracles and redemption.

Thank you for the good news at the beginning of your letter, that regarding the situation, etc., one must thank Hashem Yisbarach. May Hashem Yisbarach help that, no matter how good it may be, He can certainly add even more. This will surely bring about an increase on your part and on the part of your family, *sheyichyu*, in matters of Torah and *mitzvos* for yourselves, and also in spreading Yiddishkeit, Torah, and *mitzvos* wherever one can reach, doing so with tranquility, joy, and a good heart, and increasing in this from time to time.

With blessings for good news in all the aforementioned.

Regarding your writing about a *mechitza* where the upper part is made of **transparent** glass — this is surely making a mockery of the whole thing; whom are you fooling with this?

The simple explanation of *kehotzi'am osam* (*Bereishis* 19:17) is: *kehotzi'a hem* (the angels) *osam* [as it says in verse 16: *vayotzi'ehu* — in the plural. Also, in *Targum Onkelos* — 19:17 — the version in many printings is *apiku*, not *apik*].

## 7,303

B"H, 3 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, your letter of 2 Kislev was received, in which you write about your difficult financial situation.

I have already written to several people that if they would accustom themselves to sharing good news and writing about it frequently, they would minimize, or perhaps entirely avoid, the need to correspond regarding the opposite of good tidings, and the wise will understand.

In any event, the advised counsel is to increase in tzedakah; even if it is difficult, one should increase by at least a few coins more than one has been accustomed to in the past. One of the auspicious times for this is every weekday morning before davening.

Furthermore—and this is the main point—one must strengthen one's bitachon in Hashem, who sustains and provides for all with goodness, grace, kindness, and mercy. This is especially true in light of the understanding of hashgacha pratis, which is explained in Chassidus as applying to every single person and to the most minute details of their life. The wonderful saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (printed in Hayom Yom, 28 Cheshvan), is well known—that this completes the Divine intent; see there. Strengthening one's bitachon adds even more to the aforementioned.

Especially since we are in the month of Kislev, and this year is the bicentennial of the histalkus and hillula of the Baal Shem Tov, any increase—particularly in the study of pnimiyus haTorah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus, the "tree of life" where there are no difficulties, concealments, or obstructions—will add even more.

With blessings for good news in all that has been mentioned.

## 704

B"H, 4 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters dated the 22nd and 29th of Mar-Cheshvan, and the 1st of Kislev...

2) I must point out another matter: since the work of teachers—and certainly that of administrators—cannot be based solely on *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke), as is explained in many places, including in the teachings of Chassidus, and as is tangibly evident that it can only be successful if performed with joy, a good heart, and a feeling of *taanug* (pleasure), it is essential that the administration’s relationship with each individual be conducted in ways of pleasantness, and certainly in ways of peace—even if the administration believes it is one hundred percent in the right and they are one hundred percent at fault. And who can say if there is not at least some doubt in the matter?

What leads me to write this is that I am receiving letters of grievance from several schools in the Reshet. Although the specific complaints differ, the common denominator in the vast majority is that they do not feel a sense of empathy for their concerns, nor a desire to assist them, etc., whether from the administration, the local director (in the letters from teachers), or the teachers (in the letters from directors)—though, of course, the grievances are not identical in every letter, nor of the same intensity and frequency.

Surely, with some contemplation, a way can be found to immediately rectify this. After all, the reward for one who overlooks his own nature is the drawing down of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy, as per the ruling of our Sages, which are without limit. *Kal v'chomer.*

3) It seems one of the reasons for the grievance is the occasional delay in salary. I am interested to know if you have established a fund that provides loans to teachers against the salary to be received in that same month—that is, a loan for a few days, or at most a week or two. Would there be any benefit in this? And is it possible to ensure (*ba'varenen*) that the debt will be repaid without any delay—that is, that it be secured by the check received from the offices? *Kal v'chomer*...

Since we are in the month of Kislev, the month of miracles and redemption, which contains the festivals of the 10th and 19th of Kislev, and concludes with the days of Chanukah—where the *halacha* follows Beis Hillel, to increase and go further—may you be bearers of good news in all matters of spreading Yiddishkeit and spreading the wellsprings, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed, increasing in light as you go and add.

With blessings for good tidings.

P.S. The letters from the 8th of Kislev have been received. Likewise, the *pidyon nefesh* from the 23rd and 26th of Tishrei, the 10th and 21st of Mar-Cheshvan, and the 1st of Rosh Chodesh Kislev have been received.

## 725

Brooklyn.

This will diminish the desire for it and provide clarity of mind to contemplate the undesirability of the habit. With blessings for good tidings.

## Z'ko

B"H, 7 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the New York Women’s Committee for the benefit of the vocational school for girls and the teachers’ seminary in Kfar Chabad, in our Holy Land, may it be built and established,
May Hashem grant them life.

Blessings and peace!

The report of your work, and the news regarding the installation ceremony for the new officers on Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Vayeitzei, has caused me understandable joy.

I send my greetings and blessing to the new officers, with the hope that they, together with the previous officers and all the members, will strengthen and expand the work of the Women’s Committee, and will have a successful year—especially keeping in mind that this year marks the 200th anniversary of the Histalkus-Hilula of the Baal Shem Tov.

We have often heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of the Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya, that the events of the week are reflected in the Parsha of that week, and one must learn from the Parshas Hashavua how to conduct oneself during that week.

In Parshas **Vayeitzei** we learn how Yaakov Avinu arrived in a foreign land and endured difficult times and trials. Yet, he was not deterred by any difficulties, and precisely in that foreign land, he established the Beis Yisrael, where all his children remained faithful to the tradition of the Avos—Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov. This was made possible because the Jewish mothers—Rachel, Leah, Bilhah, and Zilpah—did everything within their power to ensure the integrity of their homes and the future of their people. This is the inner meaning of the concept that the Jewish woman is the **Akeres Habayis**—not only of her own home, but of the entire **Beis Yisrael.**

As we are in the month of Chanukah, and the mitzvah and lesson of Chanukah is to spread the light of "the mitzvah candle and the Torah light" in a manner of **mosif v'holech**—increasing more and more each day—may the Ribono shel Olam grant success to your work so that it may rise and grow. This will surely also bring Hashem’s blessings to each of the participants, also in a manner of *mosif v'holech*, so that it may be bright and joyful in your homes in every respect, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success.

#### ***Z'ko***

**What the Jewish mothers:** See also above, letter Z'ka.

## 7107

B"H, 8 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the text of your davening—whether you should change from the version you were accustomed to by your parents, may they live and be well.

Since, as explained elsewhere, one should not change from the Nusach HaAri to Nusach Sefard or Ashkenaz, if you have decided to change permanently and for good, you may do so. However, if the change is only for a limited time, you should wait until you arrive at a decision to change permanently.

2) You ask, since we are commanded, "Serve Hashem with joy," through what kind of hisbonenus can one reach this joy?

The most immediate and correct hisbonenus is understood from the words of the Rambam (Hilchos Lulav, at the end), where he states: "The joy with which a person rejoices in the performance of a mitzvah and in the love of the Almighty who commanded them, is a great avodah." This is explained by the commentators there.

3) Regarding your question on the order of your studies and how to concentrate on your learning:

- It is understood that in this matter, you should consult with your teacher, who knows you and your character, and who desires your well-being.

With blessings for success in all the above.

#### ***7107***

**Do not change:** See also above, Letter 7032, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 7108

B"H, 8 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the group of participants in the study of our holy Torah
on the night of holy Shabbos,
in Jerusalem, the holy city, may it be built and established
by Moshiach Tzidkeinu,
Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the letter dated the third day of the month of Kislev—the month of miracles and redemption—written by the G-d-fearing, esteemed, and distinguished R' Naftali Tzvi Gottlieb, may he live, bringing good tidings regarding the establishment of a group study session during the aforementioned *idna d'ra'ava* (time of divine favor).

And surely, even though it is not explicitly mentioned in your letter, you are also studying the teachings of Chassidus, which is the very Torah of the Baal Shem Tov (as written in the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, may his soul be bound in the bond of life, printed in *Hayom Yom* for 19 Kislev). It is well known from the writings of the Arizal regarding the necessity of studying *pnimiyus haTorah* on the holy Shabbos.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that this study be in a manner that is "ever-increasing and adding light" in thought, speech, and ultimately in action—for this is the purpose of study, that it leads to action. And through this study, the concept of "and to Him shall you cleave" (*u'vo tidbakun*) will be fulfilled (see *Likutei Torah*, *Re'eh* 20b). This will also hasten the fulfillment of the prophecy, "And I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth," as explained there. This is especially true through the study of *pnimiyus haTorah* and the spreading of the wellsprings outward, for that is when "the Master comes"—King Moshiach.

With blessings for success in Torah study, with *yiras shamayim*, and with the light and vitality of Chassidus.

## Jacket

B"H, 8 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

Mr. Yaakov, may he live.
Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter from the eve of Friday, in which you ask regarding what you found printed in the sefer *Ginzei Nistaros*, Part 1, section 59, that they took it upon themselves to observe annually, etc., on the 26th of Tammuz, and you ask for the reason why this day is not celebrated, and not even a trace of a Yom Tov is evident.

I have not heard an explanation for this, but what appears to me is that we find in such matters regarding the establishment of a Yom Tov, that the manner of acceptance and the establishment only becomes clear after some time. A memory and hint to this can be found in the language of our Sages regarding the miracle of Chanukah: "The following year they established them" (*Shabbos 21b*). Since the aforementioned acceptance was in the year 5519—meaning, even before the aforementioned observance took place for the **first** time, the histalkus and hillula of the Baal Shem Tov occurred, and the "bundle was untied." It is known what the state of affairs was among his disciples at that time, etc., which suggests that from the outset, the acceptance did not take effect.

2) There, in section 55, the position that "there is no place void of Him," even in the lowest things, etc.—this is the position of the Ramak, of blessed memory. You raise a difficulty, for surely this is also the position of the Arizal, as is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Alter Rebbe, section 25.

One could say regarding this: It is known that the concept of Tzimtzum is not according to the Kabbalah of the Ramak, but rather according to the Kabbalah of the Arizal. The concept of Tzimtzum gave room for the error of some who consider themselves wise to understand the concept of Tzimtzum literally (see *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, chapter 7). This is not the case according to the Kabbalah of the Ramak, where from the outset there is no room for the aforementioned error. Since the letter (in the aforementioned section 55) was written to resolve difficulties with the greatest simplicity, the Kabbalah of the Ramak was mentioned, according to which everyone agrees that even in the lowest things, "there is no place void of Him."

My hope is strong that you have fixed times for **learning** the teachings of Chassidus in an expansive manner, and that only rarely do you encounter difficulties, etc. And since we are commanded to "ascend in holiness," surely the aforementioned fixed study adds to itself from time to time. May it be the will [of Hashem] that, as per the saying of our Alter Rebbe, this should be a "fixed time" not only in terms of time, but also (and this is the main thing) a "fixed time" in the soul.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
Surely you keep the three daily shiurim of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, as is known, and at the very least you will keep them from here on in.

## 7020

B”H, 9 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Shalom Levin
Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from the beginning of Cheshvan, which was delayed in transit. I, too, delayed my response, thinking you would soon be visiting Kfar Chabad. But it seems your visit was postponed, and since we have now entered the month of Kislev, I will delay my letter no longer. In particular, I wish to express my satisfaction that our conversation bore fruit, and that the message calling for teachers to volunteer for youth education found an echo, with many responding and volunteering for this cause.

It is my hope that this good beginning will draw in even more volunteers, many times over, and that the education itself will be a beginning toward a complete education, as we discussed. Every Jew possesses a point of Judaism, which is why every person has an interest in Judaism that captures their heart when the appropriate awakening is provided. I refer to the Judaism that has been traditional for thousands of years, whose true expression—as the Mishnah states—is that the deed is essential, in the practical, day-to-day life. It is just that for some, their point of Judaism is expressed openly in matters of *tzedakah*, while for others it is in a different matter, but in all of them, their hearts are sensitive to *Hashem*. Therefore, I hope that the aforementioned education will develop until it becomes an education for a full Judaism. And since you have begun with the aforementioned *mitzvah*, you will surely continue until you complete it—insofar as one can speak of completion in matters of education, for man, as man, must receive and indeed does receive education every day of his life. This is especially so according to the explanation of the Baal Shem Tov on the Mishnah, "Who is wise? One who learns from every person," adding that everything the *Ribono shel Olam* created in His world is to teach man the deed that he should do (transcribed in the memoirs of the Rebbe Rayatz, Part 1, in the appendices at the end).

I have a strong hope that you will not withhold the kindness of informing me about your visit to Kfar Chabad, and further—and this is the main thing—about the continuation of your activities in the areas we discussed, which you also brought up at the beginning of your letter, regarding the education of youth after they finish elementary school. May it be His will that in this, too, matters will develop according to the instruction of the conclusion of this month we have entered, the days of Chanukah, in a manner of "increasing and going forward," adding light, an additional candle each and every day—"The candle of *Hashem* is the soul of man," and "The *mitzvah* is a candle and the Torah is light."

With respect and blessings—and allow me to convey my regards to all those whose spirit moved them to the aforementioned cause, as written in your letter.

You also sent me a section of your article, "He will reprove and he will love," in which you publicized the content of our conversation. Thank you for bringing it to the attention of the participants at the teachers' meeting, and in general to such a circle, as this is perhaps the only channel to inform them of the matters we discussed.

Along with this, I must also express my regret regarding one matter that is inappropriate, and this is fundamental, and it is surprising that it came from you. I hope you surely understand that I am referring to the words in your article: "For the services and devotion of... will stand to his credit, and he will not be punished for his inadvertent sins."

According to my recollection, what I said is that even one who has many merits, this does not give him the license to commit any transgression whatsoever, even a small one, etc.

What increases my astonishment is that surely, even according to your own view, these things are not accurate as written, and in the style of our Sages, one could say it is a scriptural matter and one could say it is a matter of logic—and specifically in your field, the field of education.

For, behold, the entire matter of compulsory education, which was one of the first achievements of the Ministry of Education that was implemented in Eretz Yisrael, is based on the premise that even though parents brought the child into the world and feed, give drink to, clothe, and provide for all his needs, this does not give them the license **at all** to educate him **however** they see fit. Those who must care for the good of the collective and the individual together determine at least a minimum curriculum, and regarding this minimum, the parents have no say whatsoever.

And how much more so in the present case, where the "inadvertent sins," in your words, touched and affected thousands and tens of thousands of our brothers and sisters, the children of Israel. Although, in the same way, this applies also to the person himself regarding his own affairs.

And if you wish to say it is a scriptural matter, this principle is explained in many verses, and in particular in the words of the prophet Yechezkel (18:24 and onward), "But when a righteous man turns away from his righteousness," etc.

As you concluded in your letter, I too hope that we will yet have the opportunity to continue our conversation. And I cannot restrain myself from mentioning this auspicious year, the 200th year since the *histalkus-hillula* of the Baal Shem Tov.

In connection with this, I have attached a copy of one of my letters, which I hope will interest you.

## 7121

B"H, 10 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Wednesday, along with the enclosure.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the improvement of your health and for the success of the medical treatment, for a speedy recovery.

As we spoke during your visit here, the more you increase your trust in Hashem—the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, and who watches over each and every person with *hashgacha pratis*—the more you will surely increase the blessing in the aforementioned matters. This is as we request and seek from the Master of Blessings, according to the phrasing of our prayers, for that which is good for us, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed.

I have delayed speaking or writing regarding what follows until now for several reasons. However, since you conclude your letter with a request for advice on a *tikkun* (rectification) that you might undertake *bli neder*, I would respond as follows:

According to what is explained by the Tzemach Tzedek [whose halachic rulings we follow in all matters, and especially regarding *anash* and those who have merited to benefit from the light of the teachings of Chassidus] in his notes on the Psalms of the Sweet Singer of Israel, regarding the verse "And He is merciful" (Tehillim 78:38), specifically in section 4, where he discusses the thirteen *tikkunei dizkana* (rectifications of the beard) and how they draw down great mercies, and how through these *tikkunei dizkana* everything is sweetened and becomes pleasant and sweetened:

It is highly appropriate that from now on, you conduct yourself in the manner described there regarding the corners of the beard. This is especially true according to what is explained in the *Shu"t Tzemach Tzedek* based on the *nigleh* (revealed) Torah as well. May all matters become pleasant and sweetened, as mentioned above, in a way that is visible and revealed. This is particularly important so that it may also involve an element of *kiddush Hashem*, and the merit of the many will assist you.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and may the renewal of this month of Kislev and its themes be present in all your affairs—for you and your household—in a manner of "increasing and continuing, increasing and shining." This includes the dissemination of matters of Yiddishkeit everywhere your hand can reach, and even further outward, for the *mitzvah* of the month is the Chanukah candle, which increases and continues from the time the sun sets and is placed at the entrance of one's house, facing outward.

With blessings for a *Shabbos tova*.

## 722

B"H, 10 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 2 Kislev, along with the enclosure. Regarding your statement that you will fulfill the instruction out of a sense of *kabalas ol*—this matter should not be approached in the manner you described. In matters such as these—that is, where one must influence others, especially those who perhaps do not yet have any recognition of the subject, and when dealing with adults who possess broad knowledge in the field known as the spiritual sciences—it is essential that the approach be one that Chazal describe as "words that come from the heart." For the influence must come more from the side of *regesh* (feeling) than through cold intellect. Even though we have been promised by Chazal that it is a *chazakah* (presumption) that *ta'amulah* (outreach) does not return empty, true *ta'amulah* is that which is carried out with one's own *osiyos* (words/expressions), even if those *osiyos* are ones he has heard, seen, or read, etc.

The conclusion from the above is that the portion of my letter that has already been presented and received by them should be incorporated into your correspondence with them. As for the part that has not yet been recorded, it is surely a case of "a vision for the appointed time," and "He has made everything beautiful in its time."

May it be Hashem’s will that, since we are currently between the days of 10 Kislev—the *geulah* of the Mitteler Rebbe—and 19 Kislev—the *geulah* of the Alter Rebbe—the *geulah* will be drawn down into all matters, both general and particular alike.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 613

B.H., 14 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, which you begin with an explanation regarding the nature of the beginning of the letter:

It goes without saying that this is entirely unnecessary. Especially when writing a letter to another person, with the desire that the other should respond and that there should be some benefit from the correspondence, one should write as one feels.

However, I must also respond to your explanation with which you seek to justify your statement that "you are not a Chossid," while immediately thereafter you mention that your father was a Chossid, etc. This is a contradiction in terms.

For if external traits are inherited, it is surely understandable that the *tichunos hanefesh* (traits of the soul)—which were far deeper and more deeply ingrained in the parents—are transmitted to the children to a much greater and deeper extent.

Based on your letter, I imagine that you are aware of how deeply ingrained the feeling of a Chossid is, particularly in the era of your parents—in the parlance of today, "in the old country"—and how that feeling was bound up with their very soul-life. Therefore, it is certain that this is inherited by the children. Just as with other traits, some are already active and effective, while others wait for a suitable opportunity. Some of them, perhaps, one might wish to suppress or prevent from being active and effective; yet it is certain that they exist. Just as with any living thing or any existing thing in the world, one cannot make it "non-existent"—at most, one can change the form of the thing, but one cannot make it as if it never existed (i.e., before the creation of the thing)—even when one wishes to fight against it. And I am certain that this is not the case with you; at most, it is perhaps the other case, where it is not active, and perhaps there is also a feeling that it is better not to allow its influence, so that it does not demand what Chassidus requires, which would lead to restricting oneself and being different from one's entire environment—something that requires effort, which one does not always wish to exert.

This long introduction was, of course, not written for the sake of mere preaching, and certainly not, Heaven forbid, for the sake of moralizing, but rather to express my perspective on people from various circles, with the hope that they will come to the conviction that within each of them, in their depths, there lies a treasure of immense value. Consequently, every day that one does not bring it to the surface to influence and accomplish with it, even in daily life, is a waste. Surely, the satisfaction will be such that the effort required to publicly bring forth this deeply hidden treasure one possesses is incomparable.

Moving to the second paragraph of your letter: it does not require faith in another person at all, but rather faith in oneself, in one's own **Yid**, which is, as the expression of Rabbeinu HaZaken in his Sefer HaTanya, "The second soul in a Yid is a part of Elokus from above **literally.**"

I would like to take the liberty of writing, albeit briefly, regarding the conclusion of your letter, where you mention your daughter, *tichye*.

The best influence on "students," including children, is not so much through talking—even when it is repeated many times—as it is through being a living example. When one wants one hundred percent from another, one must add to that hundred percent within oneself. When one reflects that this must influence children for years and years, and that when Hashem Yisbarach blesses one with grandchildren, it has an effect on them as well—then every effort in this regard is worthy and justified. As the saying goes, it can reach until the end of the world (the generations).

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the above.

## 6,414

B"H, 14 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in the needs of the community, Rabbi Yeshaya, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

After the longest of intervals, I received your letter from Wednesday, in which you write of your holy work in lecturing each week on matters of Yiddishkeit, and you ask which points to emphasize regarding the Baal Shem Tov, especially as we are in the year of the 200th anniversary of his passing and hillula.

In general, the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov are vast indeed, and they have been explained thoroughly in the teachings of Chabad; for in the words of the Rebbe Rashab, the teachings of Chabad are the very same as the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov (see the copy of this holy letter at the beginning of **Hayom Yom**, and also in the introduction to **Kuntres U’Maayan**).

What is particularly important to emphasize is to refute and nullify the error—which some spread, whether inadvertently or even intentionally—that the Baal Shem Tov, Heaven forbid, was lenient in any matter, even the slightest detail of the words of the Sages. Heaven forbid even to mention such a thing, and given the simplicity of the matter, especially for one such as yourself, further elaboration is unnecessary.

It is also fitting to emphasize the two aspects of the Baal Shem Tov’s activities: that he began his holy work by educating the young children of Israel, alongside the revelation of a most profound approach to the foundations of Yiddishkeit and its worldview. Enclosed is a copy of my letter to those gathering for the Chag HaGeulah of 19 Kislev, which is approaching, in which I also touched upon these points.

With blessings for good tidings, including in your personal matters.

## 14 Kislev, 5720

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 8th of Kislev, in which you write regarding your bedtime and wake-up time, and ask for my opinion as to whether this schedule is appropriate or if it should be changed.

The litmus test for this should be based on what is explained in the Laws of Talmud Torah by the Alter Rebbe regarding a teacher: that he should not be awake at night in a way that would prevent him from teaching well the next morning (see Laws of Talmud Torah, Chapter 1, Section 12). It is understood that this applies equally to one’s own Torah study. Since the number of hours of sleep required is not the same for every person, and depends on the constitution of the body, habit, and so on, the guidelines provided by the poskim are by way of an average and for the majority, for the Torah speaks of the majority.

You must examine for yourself the number of hours of sleep you require so that when you wake up, you are able to study with the necessary understanding. Based on this, you should set your bedtime and wake-up time. It is understood that in any case, the time for reciting the Shema in the morning must be observed, and this is especially relevant during the summer months.

I am certain that you are increasing from time to time the hours spent in Torah study in general, and in the study of Chassidus in particular, for we are commanded to ascend in matters of holiness, and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 7116

B"H, 14 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Yehuda Leib, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 10 Kislev, the day of the redemption of our holy master, the Mitteler Rebbe, of blessed memory.

In it, you write that it appeared to you that in the beginning of the letter you received, the Name was written differently than it was corrected afterward, and this raises for you a question regarding the permissibility of the matter and a discussion of the halachic implications.

According to my recollection, the Name Havayah was not written there even initially, and consequently, there was no issue here of instruction or a precedent for elsewhere.

On this occasion, and especially since you wrote your letter on the aforementioned auspicious day—and the words of the Arizal are well-known, that these days, when they are "remembered," they are also "made" (i.e., they are re-enacted)—I will stir you regarding the necessity of establishing a daily study of Chassidus, with an increase on Shabbos. If this was a necessity in all places and at all times, how much more so in our current era, and particularly in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

Regarding what you wrote as to whether there is a distinction between handwriting and typing on a typewriter—it seems your intention is that the latter is more lenient. To my mind, on the contrary, it is more stringent, since it is in block script (even if without *tagin*), whereas handwriting is not. And it has already been ruled by the majority of the *Acharonim* that there is sanctity in printed books, as noted in *Sdei Chemed*, *Pe'as HaSadeh*, *Kelalim*, letter 4, *Kelal* 38.

#### ***7116***

**R' Yehuda Leib:** Kalpoholz, Jerusalem.

**In block script:** See above, Vol. 12, Letter 4044, and the references in the notes there. Below, 7128.

## 167

[15 Kislev, 5720]

...And as we find ourselves on the day when the moon is in its fullness in the month of Kislev—the third month from the count of the *baalei teshuvah*, corresponding to the third month from the count of the *tzaddikim*, which is the month of Sivan—

May it be His will that in all matters, both individual and collective, there be tidings of good, in a manner of "increasing and progressing, increasing and illuminating," and at the central point: the spreading of the *maayanos* outward.

And indeed, within this very month is the *yom habahir*, the 19th of Kislev, the *Rosh Hashanah* for *Chassidus*. In the words of *kudsha brich hu* Admur Moharashab, in the well-known letter (printed in *Hayom Yom*, 19 Kislev): "This day is the *Rosh Hashanah* for *Chassidus*, which our holy forefathers—may their merits protect us—bequeathed to us, and it is the very Torah of the Baal Shem Tov."

## 619

B"H, 16 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc.,
R' Eliezer Yechiel, may he live,

Shalom and blessing!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., who is involved in communal needs, R' Zalman Yaffe, may he live. The *pidyon nefesh* will be read at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, at a time of favor, for a complete and speedy recovery and for all that is needed, in both body and soul. May it be His will that you have good news to report.

Especially as we find ourselves in the auspicious days of this month of Kislev, with the *Yom HaGeulah* of the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, and the days of Chanukah with its *Al HaNissim*, etc.

Furthermore, this year is a year of *segulah* in general, marking 200 years since the *histalkus-hilula* of the Baal Shem Tov. As is stated in the *sefarim*, during the time of a *hilula*, the great light of the *baal hahilula* is revealed in an intensified measure.

It goes without saying that the concept of remembrance and memory among Jews is that it should lead to **"remembered and performed,"** meaning that everything should be translated into **action** in practice, as it ought to be carried out under the impression and influence of that matter.

It is well known that the Baal Shem Tov began his holy work as an assistant, carrying small children on his shoulders to *cheder* and teaching them *brachos*, *Krias Shema*, *Amen*, *Yehei Shmei Rabba*, and so on. Simultaneously, the Baal Shem Tov revealed and taught the deepest and most internal matters of Torah and *pnimiyus haTorah*, as they must be expressed in daily life, based on the foundation of *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael*.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant that each one of us should continue all the aforementioned matters in our daily lives to the fullest extent, for through this, one also creates the channels and vessels to draw down the blessings of Hashem in the fullest measure, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessing.

## 7220

B"H, 16 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Yechezkel Yehuda, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of request via the esteemed and distinguished, etc., who is involved in communal needs, R' Zalman Yaffe, may he live. His *pidyon nefesh* was also received, and as requested, I will mention him at a time of favor at the gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may his soul be bound in the bond of life, along with all his household members, may they live—each and every one according to their needs, in accordance with the content of his letter. May it be His will that he brings good tidings, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed, in all matters.

This is especially relevant as we find ourselves in the auspicious days of this month, which includes the day of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, as well as the days of Chanukah and the lighting of the candles in a manner of "increasing and continuing, increasing and illuminating."

Furthermore, the entire year is an auspicious year, marking four jubilees since the passing—the *hillula*—of the Baal Shem Tov. It is known that the concept of *histalkus* is that all the matters of the one celebrating the *hillula* are elevated with greater intensity and strength.

It is understood that the purpose of remembrance is to draw these matters down into actual practice, in daily life, in such a way that they are "remembered and performed." Indeed, the beginning of the holy *avodah* of the Baal Shem Tov, even before he was revealed, was as a *bahelfer* (assistant teacher), carrying holy children in his arms to teach them the *alef-beis*, blessings, and *Krias Shema*, etc.—education in pure holiness. On the other hand, he revealed the hidden lights of the *pnimiyus haTorah* by spreading the wellsprings even among those who were still in the category of "the outside," in order to hasten the footsteps of *Melech HaMoshiach*.

May it be His will that each of us fulfills our role to draw down all these matters throughout all the days of the year, in actual practice, and in the fullest measure, so that through this, the channels and vessels are opened to receive the blessings of Hashem in all that is needed, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessing.
