## 7221

B"H, 16 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, engaged in communal needs, R' Binyamin, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 25 MarCheshvan, in which you write regarding the dissemination of the wellsprings of Chabad via radio waves in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established by Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

It is my firm hope that you and your colleagues will not be satisfied with the achievements of the past, for in matters of Torah and holiness, the command is to "ascend in holiness." Naturally, there is always room for improvement and increase in matters of holiness and goodness that are connected to Hashem, who is infinite and boundless, and who desires that man and his actions be in His image and likeness.

This is especially true in this year, a year of *segulah*, marking four jubilees since the *histalkus-hillula* of the Baal Shem Tov. It is well known regarding the concept of *histalkus* that at that time, all the matters of the *baal hillula* are elevated with greater intensity and strength. The Baal Shem Tov emphasized the matter of dissemination, as he expressed in his *Iggeres HaKodesh*—the dissemination of the wellsprings (even among those who are still in the category of) "outward." And is there any dissemination greater than that which occurs through radio waves, which break through all boundaries and partitions? Happy is the portion of each and every one who does all that depends on him in disseminating the wellsprings, to fulfill the instruction mentioned in the aforementioned *Iggeres HaKodesh*, to draw near and hasten the coming of *Malka Meshicha* speedily and in reality.

Since you, as you write, studied in the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Warsaw—the internal purpose and intent of which is also the dissemination of the wellsprings, in both the revealed and the inner parts of the Torah together—you surely absorbed its spirit and the matters of the teachings of Chassidus and the teachings of Chabad, which are the very teachings of the Baal Shem Tov. Just as in physical matters the law prevails that nothing is in vain and nothing is completely lost, so too, the time you spent within the four cubits of the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva and its influence exist and continue to perform their effect; may you utilize them to their fullest. Especially since the merit of the many assists you.

With respect and regards to all those participating with you in the aforementioned activity, and with a blessing for good tidings in all that has been mentioned.

As you requested, I will mention you and your household, may they live, at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in accordance with the content of your letter.

Regarding what you write concerning the rationale of recording words of *hisorerus* in connection with the day of 19 Kislev, the Rosh Hashanah of Chassidus, in order to broadcast them on that day or close to it: It is understood that words of *hisorerus* in general, and especially in connection with this day of *segulah*, cannot be spoken "on demand," as they require a special state of soul and a special *hisorerus*. Surely for someone like you, further elaboration is unnecessary. Although the intention is desirable, it is not possible to fulfill the request. Due to the multitude of preoccupations, the response was delayed, and I ask for your forgiveness.

## 7222

B"H, 16 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 12/3, in which you write that you have met a young man from abroad who is visiting our Holy Land (may it be rebuilt speedily), and that he comes from a non-religious family and is not religious himself, and furthermore, that he intends to return to his home country to...

It is understood that you are correct: this is not a suitable match with a non-religious person. For the happiness of a Jewish home—true happiness—exists only when it is built upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos. Regarding Torah and its mitzvos, it is said that the deed is the essential thing, not merely the feelings of the heart, and this is especially true when one is conducting himself in the opposite manner.

It is understood that sometimes one can influence someone to become religious, even to the point of practicing it in daily life, but this requires prolonged effort. This is especially true when the person in question is at least within a religious environment. Furthermore, one cannot be certain of the results of such efforts in advance until they are actually seen, for not every person is equally receptive to efforts and influence from the outside. In the case you write about, none of these conditions are present at this time, especially given his desire to return to his home country.

It is difficult to imagine that you alone would be able to influence him to change in the aforementioned manner—that is, to conduct his daily life in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them."

May it be the will of Hashem, who watches over every man and woman with Divine Providence, to guide you well and lead you to a suitable arrangement in all details.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 7224

B"H, 15 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, and learned, who engages in communal needs, a man of many accomplishments, a man of distinction, of the holy seed, R' Yitzchak Meir HaKohen, may he live and be well.

Peace and blessing!

Following up on my previous letter, I am writing regarding a matter that is timely—the days leading up to 19 Kislev. In the words of the Alter Rebbe, this is the day of the great *hillula* of our holy Rebbe, of blessed memory, and the day of the redemption of the Alter Rebbe. In the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, it is the festival "which redeemed our souls in peace, and the light and vitality of our souls was given to us."

I wish to once again stir [you] regarding the *avodah* of spreading the *maayanos* outward, in the language of the Baal Shem Tov in his well-known *Iggeres HaKodesh*.

If this holy obligation (and privilege) rests upon everyone who has merited to taste the teachings of Chassidus, then all the more so for those whom Divine Providence has graced with influence over a wide circle; for them, the demand and necessity are many times greater.

Especially when a lack of activity in this area—and even when one does not act as one ought, in the style of our Sages—is interpreted as an agreement, Heaven forbid, with the opponents and those who cause confusion, etc.

Knowing his energy, if he only chooses to utilize it to its fullest, my hope is strong that his activities in the aforementioned field will succeed in spreading the *maayanos* even to the "outward."

May it be the will [of Hashem] that in our immediate future, the prophecy—fitting for the response of Melech HaMoshiach, as mentioned in the aforementioned letter of the Baal Shem Tov—that "your wellsprings will spread outward" will be fulfilled.

I hope he will forgive me for writing to him with the aforementioned note, and the main thing is that I receive good news regarding all of the above.

With respect and blessing.

## 7125

7125

B"H, 20 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 12 Kislev, I will begin with the point that I found most surprising: section 4, regarding the continuation of the institution [although there is some room to judge favorably, since this section begins with the words "improper thoughts"—meaning that from the outset he disqualified them—yet the surprise remains even regarding the initial premise]. It is surely unnecessary to elaborate on the simple fact regarding the great necessity and vitality of every educational institution that wishes to be on the foundation of purity and holiness, especially since the necessity for this is constantly increasing and growing. However, it is understood and also simple that along with this, one must strive not only to avoid shrinking the institution, but on the contrary, to increase it first and foremost in quantity. Consequently, from the quantity, there will eventually come an increase in quality as well, as is customary in Yisrael. Regarding such matters, one can apply the teaching of Chazal: "You have labored and you have found." This is especially true since the recognition of the necessity for religious education is constantly spreading.

From here, I move to section 1 of your letter, regarding the state of his speech, etc. This is also related to the aforementioned response. My intention is: surely you still have a copy of your letters to me regarding your speech and your state of mind at that time, to the point that it was as if, Heaven forbid, all was lost, etc. Even then, you put into writing thoughts similar to those mentioned. Now you see that the situation is much better than you had estimated. If only you had been **strong** in your trust at that time, the improvement would have progressed further and would have been even greater. One does not cry over the past, except regarding the future and regarding section 4 of your letter.

It would be appropriate for you to speak with Anash who also come into contact with the offices you write about; perhaps they will be able to advise you regarding efforts of *hishtadlus*.

It is my hope that with pleasant speech and enlightening words, without any intimidation whatsoever, you will explain to your wife, tichyeh, that she should completely divert her mind from the "improper thoughts" mentioned—as you phrased it in your letter—especially since these actions of hers were mentioned at the time of her request for the success of the medical treatment and her recovery.

Until now, I have refrained from commenting on what follows, but I do not see that I have the right to refrain from writing about it now. In your previous letter, you mentioned, as if in passing, that your son, shyei, is studying in a certain institution.

Although I am not familiar with the conditions of study in the institution you mention, surely, as the well-known saying goes, "For good, one can always add." There are several educational institutions for his age in Eretz Yisrael, tichyeh, where they study only *limudei kodesh* permeated with *yiras shamayim*, and among them are those that are also permeated with *ahavas Hashem*—that is, Chassidic. Seemingly, every activist in the field of education must first and foremost set an example that one should not be satisfied with a half-measure or a third-measure of education, especially when taking into account the influence of the street, etc., and *v'd"l*. This is similar to the distinction in law between "moist enough to moisten" and "merely moist."

It is my hope that on the bright day of 19 Kislev, you will *farbreng* in a suitable environment—meaning that what you write regarding the program for 19 Kislev, you will bring into actuality, and most importantly, in a way that its impression will be noticeable throughout the entire year. For this day is the Rosh Hashanah for *Chassidus* (as is known from the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of the Rebbe Rashab, printed in *Hayom Yom* for 19 Kislev). It is known that the precision is "head" (*rosh*) and not "beginning" (*techilah*), because from it, influences are drawn for all the days of the year, similar to the influence from the head to all the limbs.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all that was mentioned.

#### ***7125***

A portion is printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 21, p. 352, and a portion there, p. 385.

## 7226

B"H, 21 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, the G-d-fearing, the man of action, whose work is the work of Heaven,
Meir, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 11 Kislev. Enclosed is my letter to the seventh grade, and I am certain that if further explanation is needed, you will find the appropriate words for it.

I read with interest the account of your activities at the holy institution. I will mention you once again at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that your success may be in accordance with the will of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im—that they should be "candles to illuminate." Although this was originally said specifically regarding the students of Tomchei Temimim, the fact remains that Scripture considers one who teaches Torah to his friend's son as if he had fathered him. A son inherits from his father the qualities required to be a "candle to illuminate," as understood from the Mishnah at the end of Chapter 2 of Eduyot. From this, it is understood that the Temimim have the ability and the power to create students like themselves, provided they invest themselves in this with *mesiras nefesh*, in the manner of a father’s influence upon a son. And this is well understood.

It is my hope that you utilized the auspicious day of 19 Kislev for this work as well, and that the upcoming days of Chanukah will add to all of the above, with success.

With blessings for success in all matters and for good tidings.

***

**Meir, may he live:** Friedman, Kfar Chabad.

## 7127

B"H, 21 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to the *pidyon nefesh* received through...

At an auspicious time, I will mention him and his wife, *tichye*, at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*, in accordance with the content of his letter.

It is surprising that he does not mention whether they have attempted appropriate injections, as well as specific exercises and movements (*bavegungen*) for the fingers and the feet. For although the nature of the ailment is not clear from the letter, it appears that this also falls within the realm of blood circulation (*blut tzirkulirung*). In any event, it is worthwhile to consult the attending physician regarding the aforementioned, as when a person acts according to the ways of nature, it serves as a conduit and vessel for that which is above the ways of nature as well.

Since, in a Jewish person, physicality and spirituality walk hand in hand, and our Sages have said, "The substance that is at their feet" — this refers to money.

It is appropriate that he increase his *tzedakah* — in the literal sense — and especially to institutions that are engaged in the education of Jewish children in accordance with the purity of holiness, for they too are in the category of the "foot" of the general stature of the Jewish people. An increase in the vitality of the spiritual person certainly adds to the vitality of the physical person.

And since everything is by *hashgacha pratis*, and his request was received in the month of Kislev, the day after the *Chag HaGeulah* of our *Rabbeinu HaZaken*, the author of the *Tanya* (the authority on the *nistar* of Torah) and the *Shulchan Aruch* (the authority on the *nigleh* of Torah), and the victory of the teachings of Chassidus, it is my duty (and also my privilege) to encourage him regarding the necessity of establishing fixed times for the study of the teachings of Chassidus, for at least a short while every day, with an increase on *Shabbos Kodesh*. Likewise, he should observe the *takanah* of reciting the monthly *Tehillim* *shiur* — as it is divided for the days of the month — every day after morning *davening*.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above.

## 7228

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter, in which you ask for further clarification regarding my letter from the end of last year:

It is obvious that my intention in that response was not merely to habituate you to the avodah of *iskafya* and nothing more. Regarding what I wrote about remaining on the *meshek* (farm/settlement), this was in reference to your statement that you do not have a profession. In connection with my clear opinion that it is desirable for you to enter into a *shidduch* in a good way, both materially and spiritually, being on the *meshek* will certainly allow you to arrange your schedule so that you can learn a profession. Surely, the management of the *meshek* is also interested in the benefit of its members. Furthermore, the issue of housing and the like is resolved (at least for the initial period). Based on the above, it is also understood that my instruction was not a directive for many years to come, but only until you have a profession and have entered into a *shidduch* in a good and auspicious hour. After that, you and your future wife—may she live and be well—will decide together how and where to proceed.

2) A second point: As is apparent from your conduct and your letter, for the time being, you have not accustomed yourself to regular, fixed work from day to day. This is a matter that is most crucial for living life as it should be lived—to be master over one’s spirit and to occupy oneself with what is desirable, not necessarily with what one feels like doing, and specifically on a daily basis. *V’ka’l* (and the rest is understood).

3) Regarding what you wrote—that you are currently unable to engage in *shidduchim* matters because your spiritual state is not as it should be—my hope is that the very act of entering into life as commanded in our holy Torah, the Torah of life, will make the battle of the *yetzer* easier for you, as well as the improvement of all the matters about which you write. This has been seen tangibly with many people in years past and in our own days as well.

4) Regarding what I wrote—that the efforts in a *shidduch* must be [conducted in a certain way]—the intention is simple. Unfortunately, in some circles, people have permitted themselves behaviors that are absolutely undesirable, under the pretext that this is done as part of searching for a suitable *shidduch*. *V’da’l* (and you will understand). In Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—many *shidduchim* are concluded in a manner of the desired *tzniyus* and are successful both materially and spiritually; this is what I intended.

5) Regarding your question as to how you should engage in the dissemination of Chabad Chassidus, its guidance, and its conduct—since you have not yet fulfilled "adorn yourself" (*kashot atzmecha*): The answer to this is twofold. First, it is impossible to withhold the knowledge of the aforementioned Torah from those in your surroundings just because you are not yet as you should be; they are not to blame for that. Furthermore, if one is not fixing oneself as much as is necessary and is still lacking, it is obvious that one should not add to this the further deficiency of failing to disseminate *Chassidus*. Given the magnitude of this matter of dissemination (which is also the subject of the teaching, "He who is meritorious and makes the many meritorious... the merit of the many depends on him"), the opposite is understood, *chas v’shalom*. Indeed, regarding the matter of "adorn yourself," a person must seek and find all possible ways and means to increase success in this. When you know that you must speak in an hour’s time about important matters before several people face-to-face, this will certainly and surely make the aforementioned battle easier and bring victory closer.

May it be the will of Hashem that, as we approach the days of Chanukah—whose theme is "the wicked delivered into the hands of the righteous, and the wanton into the hands of those who occupy themselves with Your Torah"—that in the personal battle of each one of us, the wicked will also be delivered into the hands of the righteous, and the wanton into the hands of those who occupy themselves with Torah, as this matter is explained in the holy *Tanya*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned matters, and for an illuminating and joyous Chanukah.

## 7229

B"H, 28 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...And regarding the final point you mentioned, concerning your son, may he live, and concluding that he has been and continues to be given antibiotic pills every day.

It is surely known to you that in the United States, the fervor for these pills has already waned, and people are beginning to be wary of their "excessive" use. Even more significantly, they have begun to notice undesirable side effects. It is understood that this comment is only in a general sense, and is intended only to prompt you to speak with the attending physician about giving this the proper attention and consideration—whether it is desirable to continue the use of the aforementioned pills, etc. It would be best to encourage him to inquire about this with those who have specialized in **research** in this field, since, as a rule, attending physicians do not have much time for such research, and in particular, the factories that produce these pills are, naturally, not pleased with such investigations.

I am greatly astonished by your doubt regarding the continuation and the framework of your son's education in the near future. Experience has shown that in such matters, the primary concern is the level of *yiras shamayim* in the education. For to the extent that it is not strong in this regard, the "street" and various other factors will act to diminish *yiras shamayim*. And, unfortunately, regarding the two schools you mention, one does not hear anyone complaining that their level of *yiras shamayim* is "excessive."

With respect and blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned matters, and from time to time in a manner of "increasing and continuing," as instructed by these days of Chanukah, where the *halacha* follows Beis Hillel to "increase and add light."

## Zekel

B"H, 28 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yisroel Menachem, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

After a very long interval, I received your letter of 20 Kislev, signed on the day of light, the day of tidings and redemption, 19 Kislev.

In it, you write of your participation in the farbrengen of that day. May it be the will of Hashem that the impression of that day continues throughout the entire year, through the "candle of a mitzvah and the Torah of light," and the "light of Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus.

Regarding what you wrote about your health... you are surely consulting with a specialist physician and following his instructions, for the Torah has granted the physician permission to heal.

And may the merit of your keeping the shiurim of Chitas (Chumash, Tehillim, Tanya)—which we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is a segulah for many matters—stand by you to bring good tidings in all the aforementioned.

Regarding your request for guidance in avodas Hashem on how to conduct yourself—in general terms, these matters are explained in the books and maamarim of Chassidus. In specific terms, it depends on various factors, such as the nature of one's soul, one's available time, etc. Therefore, you should consult with the anash in your vicinity, for it is already said, "In a multitude of counselors there is salvation."

Regarding your observation on the words of our Sages (Bava Kamma 98b) that everyone is obligated to remove chametz on Pesach, even though it is known that the obligation to remove chametz rests only upon the owner:

See the Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe, Siman 443, Seif 7, which explains that even though the responsibility for the chametz is not his, he must still remove it so that the owner of the chametz does not transgress the prohibition of "it shall not be seen," **for all of Israel are responsible for one another**, and not merely for themselves.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and in a manner of "increasing and continuing, increasing and adding light," as instructed by these days of Chanukah, according to the ruling of Beis Hillel.

Regarding what you wrote about the interpretation of gematria—see the Tosafos Yom Tov at the end of Chapter 3 of Avos: "A name applied to **all** matters of calculation."

See also the Aruch HaShalem under that entry for several examples.

Regarding your question on what is brought in Yalkut Reuveni, Parshas Bracha, from Sefer HaTemunah, that Moshe and Tziporah were buried in the Me'aras HaMachpeilah, which contradicts several statements of our Sages—we find conflicting Midrashim on many matters. It is worth noting a third Midrash (Sifri, cited in Yalkut Reuveni there) that a tunnel leads from the burial place of Moshe to the burial place of the Patriarchs.

***

**R' Yisroel Menachem:** Goldringer, New York.

## 6131

B"H, 28 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After the longest of intervals, I received your letter from the 15th of Kislev, in which you write regarding your state of mind concerning enrolling in an accelerated course for uncertified teachers, etc.

It is clear, based on what I have heard and know about you, that Divine Providence has gifted you with a talent for education, for absorbing knowledge properly and in an orderly fashion, and in general, with those qualities required for success as a teacher, educator, and guide.

It is also understood that each one of us, within the general population of humanity, is not always in the same state of mind. For man is in a state of "ascending and descending," and who is greater than us in this regard? Even true, complete tzaddikim—as this description is explained by our Alter Rebbe—are subject to this. And yet, he explains that even regarding them, the verse states, "A tzaddik falls seven times and rises."

It is just that for a tzaddik, this is a fall relative to his previous level, etc.

From what has been said, it is understood that it is normal for the level of concentration not to be the same for you at all times, and the same applies to self-confidence, etc. Especially when, to all of the above, the machinations of the yetzer are added—as it wishes to distract a person from their avodah to their Creator. One of the foundations of this avodah is tranquility of the soul and absolute bitachon that "everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good," and that the talents given to a person were certainly given with the possibility of utilizing them as well. It is among the machinations of the yetzer to entice a person [to believe] that this temporary and normal descent is not as it seems, exaggerating it and magnifying it in their eyes, etc.

The conclusion from the above is that you must completely divert your mind from thoughts that are the opposite of the quality of bitachon—the foundation of our faith and our Torah, the Torah of life—and not be impressed by the fact that sometimes you do not find within yourself the strength for concentration as it was a day or two ago.

Furthermore, and this is also essential: acquire a friend and companion with whom you can speak openly. It has already been said, "If there is anxiety in a man's heart, he should speak of it," even though, as mentioned, this anxiety is a product of the imagination, the source of which is the enticement of the yetzer. You will certainly, most certainly, reach your goal—to succeed in the holy work as a teacher in the field of Chabad, and "He has made everything beautiful in its time."

I am sure you participated in the activities of the holy day, the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, which is the Rosh Hashanah for the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its practices. My hope is that, in general, your state of mind has also improved, and you will bring good news regarding this.

With blessings for good tidings in all that has been mentioned.

## 722

722

B"H, 29 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interruption, your letter of 17 Kislev has arrived. I hope that your future letters will be in a manner consistent with the guidance of the days of Chanukah: that one must increase in lights and illumination. The inner content of this is in accordance with the verse, "For a mitzvah is a candle and Torah is light." May this be the case in your personal affairs, as well as in the work of strengthening and spreading Yiddishkeit and Chassidus in particular, also in a manner of *mosif v'holech, mosif v'or* (increasing and progressing, increasing and illuminating).

And despite all the difficulties, it is certain that regarding this, too, it has been said: "There is nothing that can stand before the will." True, it requires effort, but we have seen in recent years that one succeeds in this more than one had imagined (which you have surely seen in your work, as well as your husband, the Rav, may he live, in his work, and this is the case in **every** place).

And as we have heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, when a soldier goes into battle, he goes with a joyful victory march, which makes it possible to increase the victory and also brings the victory closer. So too in the aforementioned: when you and all those who do this work go with joy and certainty in the victory of the work, it will come more easily, sooner, and to a greater extent...

And the main thing is to strengthen oneself in *bitachon* (trust), that Chassidus will prevail everywhere, and also in... and therefore, *ashrei chelkam* (happy is their portion) that you are involved in this work, and doing so *b'simchah u'v'tuv leivav* (with joy and goodness of heart), as our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, demand of everyone.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 7,233

By the Grace of G-d
5th Chanukah Candle, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi S. Sassoon 
15 Sollershott East
Letchworth, Herts.

Sholom uBrocho!

... I take this opportunity to express my gratification at the two books which you published in honor of your sons Yitzchak and David’s Bar Mitzvah: the *Moshav Zekenim* and the exegesis of Rabbi Abraham, son of the Rambam. May G-d grant that since their entering under the yoke of the Mitzvos was associated with the dissemination of *Toras Rishonim*—*Rishonim k’Malachim*—your sons may merit to walk in their ways, to practice and spread the Torah and Mitzvos with joy and gladness of heart.

I cannot forgo this occasion without mentioning the fact that this year is the 200th anniversary of the *Histalkus-Hilula* of the Baal Shem Tov, who emphasized the dissemination of the Torah and *Penimius haTorah* among the widest possible circles, as stated in *Iggeres haKodesh* of the Baal haTanya regarding the "dissemination of the fountains abroad." Moreover, this emphasis is coupled with *Ahavas Yisrael*, with vitality and animation. And as with the case of all remembrances among Jews, the underlying significance is the practical application and lasting inspiration of the teachings of the *Baal haYovel*.

 With best wishes for an inspiring Chanukah, and with blessing.

P.S.
As is my custom in such matters, for the sake of affection, I have noted a few comments, albeit in haste, as time permitted.

**Moshav Zekenim**

**At the beginning, 1a:** The *shita* beginning with the word *Aseh*. It seems it should be *Ve’aseh*. This is also the case in *Bereishis Rabbah*, end of chapter 11, and elsewhere.

The answer "and one may say" (*v’yesh lomar*) is in the commentary of the *Riv’a* here.

**From one subject to another:** In the commentary of the *Riv’a* cited on page 56, it should be *Yaakov* instead of *Leah*. This is found in the printed commentary of the *Riv’a*.

In the index, *Riv’a* is noted on page 158, but I did not find it there.

It requires study why it is not listed in the index under Rashi, even though it is mentioned in many places [under the name "Rashi" (for example: 222, 371, 402) or "R. Sh." (2, 62, 112, 158)]. Perhaps it is because there are so many instances.

**Commentary of R. Avraham ben HaRambam**

**At the beginning, Note 1:** This is also the case in *Pirkei D’Rabbi Eliezer*, end of chapter 7.

**Note 9:** To note from *Bereishis Rabbah*, end of chapter 7.

**In the text:** "A living being that has a soul." To note from Rashi’s commentary on verse 20, 24. See also *Zohar Chadash*, *Bereishis*, *Midrash HaNe’elam*, chapter 4; Rambam, *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, chapter 4, 8-9.

#### ***7,233***

**Rabbi S. D. Sassoon:** Additional letters to him—see above, Vol. 11, 3,591, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 724

724

B"H, 30 Kislev, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Chaim Abba, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

After a long interval, your letter from 4 Chanukah was received.

Regarding what you wrote concerning customs associated with a Bar Mitzvah—I have not heard of specific instructions on this, other than what is printed in *Hayom Yom*, that one begins to put on tefillin two months beforehand; for a few weeks without a *bracha*, and once he is accustomed to putting them on, with a *bracha*. You should ask among *anash*, as perhaps they know how this was practiced in their places in our country in the past.

It is also appropriate for the Bar Mitzvah boy to review the *maamar* beginning with the words *Ita b'Midrash Tehillim*, and it is easy to learn it by heart; your son should do this as well.

I hope you participated in the *farbrengen* of the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, and may it be His will that its impression be evident throughout the entire year.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## Zekela

B"H, Days of Chanukah, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.
The Bicentennial Year of the Histalkus-Hillula of the Baal Shem Tov, z"l

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Motzaei Shabbos.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with the content and the inspiration of these days of Chanukah—whose essence is the lighting of the candles, the candles that are "for all time," "towards the face of the Menorah," and all the blessings that are never nullified (see Ramban, beginning of Parshas Behaaloscha)—and in accordance with the Halacha of Beis Hillel, that we "increase and continue, increase and shine."

May it be so with your activities in the holy work throughout the entire year: to increase in the "candle of a mitzvah and the light of Torah," and in the "candle of Hashem, the soul of man"—both your own and that of others—with joy. May these activities be permeated with light and the vitality of the soul, illuminated by the light of the inner dimension of His Torah, which is drawn from the level of the inner dimension and essence of the Ohr Ein Sof, Baruch Hu (see the Iggeres HaKodesh of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe [Rashab], n'e, printed in Hayom Yom for 19 Kislev).

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and a happy Chanukah,

**M. Schneerson**

## Z'KLO

B"H, Days of Chanukah, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.
The Bicentennial Year of the Histalkus-Hillula of the Baal Shem Tov, z"l

Greetings and Blessings!

...Thank you for the good news regarding the improvement in the health of your wife, the Rabbanit, may she live and be well. And since the halachic ruling is that "his wife is as his own body" (Kesuvos 66a).

(And as in many other places, it can be explained in the inner dimension of Torah—see Zohar I, 91b, and also see the Arizal’s Likutei HaShas to Berachos—that the reason for the law in the revealed dimension of Torah is revealed.)

I am certain that this is the case for you as well, and that the fainting spell has been uprooted from its source.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the matter of "the verse repeats it to imply that it is a requirement" (le'akev), and that it is seemingly not limited to Kodshim—everything is by Divine Providence. Your letter was received when I learned that this sicha is being printed in *HaMaor*. I requested that the references be noted to Tosafos, Menachos 38a, bottom; *Yad Malachi*, *Lekach Tov*, Rule 5; and see also *Osiyos D'Oraysa*, Rule 12.

As for the difficulty you raised regarding the language (in Tosafos, Pesachim 11a, top right) "such as Kodshim"—which *Lekach Tov* also addresses—it is understood according to the aforementioned Tosafos in Menachos.

In *Shita Mekubetzes*, Zevachim (5a)—in the edition I have before me, the text reads "they are **merely for the matter of** validity," and this corresponds to the continuation "for the matter of acceptance," meaning that the mitzvah is a definition regarding the matter of validity or acceptance (and the definition of "requirement" corresponds to it), and not a third matter added to the matters of validity and acceptance.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the words of the Ramban on the verse "And there was light," that it does not say "And it was so"—[and in *Torah Sheleimah* it notes the Zohar and *Sefer HaBahir* which raise this same question, and it seems this is what the Ramban intended when he wrote "from the way of the hidden/Kabbalah." See also *Kesser Shem Tov* at the end, and *Ohr Torah* by the Maggid on the aforementioned]—regarding our light, see Chagigah 12a.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the words of *Torah Or* in the maamar *B'Chaf-Hei B'Kislev* regarding the matter of the lighting of the candles in the Beis HaMikdash—in this discourse, it explains the opinion of the poskim that the lighting of the candles was only in the evening, with the wicks facing east and west (Responsa of the Rashba; Ramban; Tosafos, s.v. *U'Leheitiv*, Yoma 71a; and see *Tosafos Yom Tov*, Chapter 7 of Yoma and Chapter 3 of Tamid). It explains the order in the morning: the trimming of the seventh candle, the trimming of the sixth candle, the lighting of the sixth candle, the lighting of the seventh candle. The matter is extensive, and this is not the place to elaborate.

***

The letter was written to Moreinu HaRav Ephraim Eliezer Yalles, in the margins of the general text found in the previous letter.

Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 18, 6582, and in the references noted in the footnotes there. Below, 7232, 7447, 7773, 7819.

**HaMaor:** And in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 4, p. 1253, footnote 3.

**Regarding the lighting of the candles in the Beis HaMikdash:** See also above, Vol. 17, letter 6145.

## 7237

B"H, Days of Chanukah, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the farbrengen on the Day of Good Tidings, the Day of Redemption of our Rebbe HaZaken, and our own redemption and salvation of our souls in...

May Hashem grant them life.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I learned of your farbrengen on that bright day, 19 Kislev, which is referred to by our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, as the "Festival of Festivals."

Surely, as in every gathering of Bnei Yisrael who tremble at the word of Hashem, words of Torah were heard, and in a manner that will bring these words into action—that is, to an increase in Torah and mitzvos throughout the entire year that follows.

The Holy One, Blessed be He, joins a good thought to an action, especially when the thought is conceived and accepted upon oneself on a day of auspiciousness (*yom segulah*).

And according to the teaching of our Sages that "merit is brought about on an auspicious day," may it be the will that the beginning of this [increase] should be during these days of Chanukah. For the halacha follows Beis Hillel, that one "adds and increases" in the candle and the light. The allusion here is understood based on what is said, "For a mitzvah is a candle and the Torah is light," and the miracle of the oil, as explained in many places, alludes to the secrets and the inner dimensions of the Torah.

May each and every one illuminate himself and his surroundings with the "candle of a mitzvah" and the "light of Torah," and with the "light of the Torah"—which is the inner dimension of the Torah, which in our generations has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus.

Especially as we are in the bicentennial year of the passing-hillula of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory. As is known from his *Iggeres HaKodesh*, when his wellsprings spread outward—the wellsprings of his Torah, which is the very teachings of Chassidus—then the Master will come, this is King Moshiach.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7237***

A similar letter was sent to several [others].

**Festival of Festivals:** See also above, Vol. 18, Letter 6202.

## 7,138

B"H, days of Chanukah, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, possessor of noble character traits, engaged in communal needs, scion of a noble lineage, etc., R' Shneur Zalman, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Although it has been a long time since I received a personal letter from you, it is understood that Anash, may they live, write to me about this of their own accord, especially when I inquire about your well-being. You will surely understand the astonishment, mingled with pain, caused by the news that for the first time since the founding of Kfar Chabad, you did not participate in the farbrengen of 19 Kislev there. It is superfluous to elaborate to one such as yourself on the magnitude of the matter in all its details, and the importance of your presence at the farbrengen of the Chag HaGeulah in Kfar Chabad, especially since the matter concerns influence upon the many, and the inner point of *hafatzas hamaayanos*, particularly in this auspicious year—the 200th year since the histalkus-hillula of the Baal Shem Tov—as I have emphasized several times in my letters this year.

It is also understood that I have no doubt that there were surely important reasons for this. But regarding others—it is human nature that people do not come to ask for an explanation, nor do they sit and wait for someone to come and resolve their questions. In the vast majority of cases, even if one explains the reason to them, they do not accept it, for each person invents and explains a reason that fits their own spirit and perspective.

It is further understood that I do not intend, G-d forbid, to preach morality, and certainly I did not come to cause you pain, G-d forbid. But since in all such matters it is certain that the *sitra achra* (through people who advise him) interferes, and as the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, goes: "Sometimes he dresses himself in the garb of a righteous, innocent, humble person with good character traits" (the matter is transcribed in its entirety in *Hayom Yom*, 23 Sivan), it is possible that this was the case here as well, causing your non-appearance at the farbrengen. The *sitra achra* is liable to disguise himself again in the aforementioned garb and confuse matters such as these in the future, which is why this letter is written. My hope is strong that then he will not succeed, especially since the merit of the many assists you in utilizing your influence in the aforementioned area of *hafatzas hamaayanos*.

I will repeat my blessing once again and join the multitude of those who bless you on the occasion of your reaching seventy years of age. According to the tradition from my father-in-law, the Rebbe (who said that it is an ancient custom) that from the day one turns thirteen years old, one has a connection to the 14th chapter of Tehillim, and so on each year in order, upon your reaching seventy years, the chapter that corresponds to you is chapter 71. May it be the will [of Hashem] that the words of the Sweet Singer of Israel be fulfilled in you: "And even unto old age and gray hairs, O G-d, forsake me not, until I declare Your strength unto the generation, Your power to everyone that is to come."

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

Enclosed is a copy of my letter which will surely interest you, as it concerns the matter of chinuch.

## 729

Brooklyn
3 Teves, 5720

Mr. Moshe, may he live
Peace and Blessing!

I write to express my gratitude to you for your efforts and actions regarding the rescue of the holy Zohar with the annotations of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which have just reached me.

Beyond the immense importance of the matter itself—the rescue of words of Torah—there is, of course, a special personal nuance for me, as with all matters concerning the inheritance of our fathers. This is especially true as I recall the toil and labor, combined with the enthusiasm, with which my father-in-law, the Rebbe, engaged in the aforementioned work.

May it be the will of Hashem that for many more years you will engage in matters of Torah and mitzvos in general, and in a positive manner, through a great mitzvah such as the redemption of captives mentioned above.

According to the teachings of Chassidus, a person’s service in holiness—the work of *birurim*—is the redemption of the sparks of holiness that are in exile, and the redemption of the person’s own *nefesh elokis*, a specific spark of the *Shechinah* within the soul of every Jew (as explained by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in many places, including *Tanya, Iggeres HaKodesh*, ch. 4).

May this be done with tranquility and a good heart, and in a manner of "increasing and going forward, increasing in light."

With respect and blessing, and with a closing similar to the opening, expressing thanks for all the above.

P.S.
Although the following words may perhaps not be entirely appropriate to the above, I nevertheless found myself obligated to include them as well, in order to fulfill the command, "And you shall be clean before Hashem and before Israel." This is especially so in light of the rumor that reached me, that you were surprised by the lack of a response to your letter in which you wrote about the matter of the visit to Soviet Russia.

The lack of a response stemmed from two reasons, as our Sages have taught us:
1) Just as it is a mitzvah to say something that will be heeded, so too is it a mitzvah [to refrain from saying that which will not be heeded].
2) One does not answer [when the question is not appropriate].

To explain my words, by way of introduction: Of course, the true purpose of the visits of our fellow Jews to that country in the past, according to my approach—and surely according to your approach as well—is so that through this, they would be strengthened there in their battle for their Jewish character, and be encouraged in their spirits, seeing that there are many brothers who share their views. [They would realize] that if, G-d forbid, they were in similar conditions, they too would fight for the preservation of their form and character and stand firm in all the trials and struggles, etc.

Surely, during your visit there, to the extent that you were able to come into real contact with those of the type mentioned, and observed their way of life and the difficulties and obstacles in their path, you saw and realized that despite the fact that in every single detail they are dependent on hostile factors and are fought against in every matter of Torah and mitzvos, they nevertheless guard them with all their might—to the point of actual *mesiras nefesh*, and certainly to the point of danger to their economic situation, lack of livelihood, etc. They do not shrink back, even regarding their children, from conducting themselves in the aforementioned manner, provided that they remain faithful to the Torah and its mitzvos. Therefore, they set times for Torah during all their free hours, they guard the Shabbos and Yom Tov, and certainly the kashrus of their food. A significant portion of them even go so far as to keep their beards and *peios*, despite this being a prominent sign that they are devout Jews, and much more. Even though, presumably, it is precisely these individuals with beards and *peios* who avoid meeting with visitors from abroad, because the surveillance regarding them is many times greater, and any slight movement can be used as a pretext to persecute them. Therefore, it is possible that you did not meet with them specifically, but my hope is that you were at least told about them.

After the aforementioned introduction, you can imagine for yourself the reaction of our fellow Jews who stand in the aforementioned movement, and have lived in it for **decades**, when, after having merited to meet with fellow Jews coming from countries where Torah study and the fulfillment of mitzvos are practiced without any obstacles whatsoever—and all the more so when the visitors come from the Holy Land, etc.—they see, first and foremost, that in all the visitors' conduct, they strive so that it is not at all apparent that they are Jews, whether in their facial appearance, their clothing, or regarding their *tzitzis*, etc. And when they are asked—of course, in a delicate and indirect manner, so as not to offend, G-d forbid—what they do and how they utilize their complete freedom regarding Torah study and the fulfillment of mitzvos, they receive an answer that so-and-so is a soccer player and is successful, another acts in the theater, and the like. And the "best" among them are those who are indeed observant of Torah and mitzvos, but they have invested their best energy and their best strengths in studies, which they also pursue at the Communist university, in complete freedom without any hindrance, except that from time to time they have fixed times for studying our holy Torah, the Torah of life.

And it is a matter of great concern whether the benefit of the visit regarding the encouragement of the spirit of our brothers who are there is greater than the loss, or [the opposite].

I will not deny that immediately upon receiving your letter regarding the trip, I wanted to write all of the above, but I anticipated what the results would be, and therefore I chose silence, based on the two points mentioned above.

To conclude "on a pleasant note," to add a little "comfort" regarding the above: the delegation of young rabbis who traveled there from the United States two years before your visit—based on the points mentioned—the "doubt" regarding the benefit of their visit is even greater than regarding the visit of yourself and your colleagues. This is because they traveled as official representatives, rabbis in Israel, and the reaction there is understood from the short and pointed question received from there, in the name of our fellow Jews—and not necessarily religious ones, and furthermore, even from non-Jews—that soccer games exist among them as well, and they do not need to come specifically from the United States. And I ask for forgiveness for what was said above.

But in truth, even the above comes after much restraint and *tzimtzum*, for the argument is not necessarily because they visited, but a deeper, more internal and spiritual argument, to those like myself:

After everything that our fellow Jews have endured, which increases **many times over** the responsibility of all those who remained, as brands plucked from the fire—and all the more so those who live in the Holy Land, may it be built and established—their responsibility is to fulfill, at least as much as possible, what was done by our fellow Jews who were killed for *Kiddush Hashem*, in matters in which we are **distinguished** from all the nations; that is, matters of Torah and mitzvos. And this must be in a manner that is open to the eyes of all, and not like the slogan of the *Maskilim* of the past, "Be a Jew in your home and a man when you go out," the results of which are evident in the second or third generation of the *Maskilim*.

To say the words simply: Especially regarding the young people who grew up in our generation, the generation of destruction (for they do not have to change a worldview of 30–50 years, which is an extremely difficult thing), these young people must give a spiritual accounting to themselves that they are filling the place of the cream of our people, the children of Israel. They must walk in the public square in such a way that all who see them will recognize that they are of the seed of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov. And in the Holy Land, may it be built and established, in particular, they should be recognized as observers of Torah and mitzvos in every necessary way. This should not be through the fact that they speak Hebrew, but rather through the fact that when one meets them in the street, they will say about them that they surely must be from Meah Shearim. And when they are asked how and with what they spend their time, the situation and the answer must be with complete simplicity: that they spend all their time in the study of Torah and the observance of its mitzvos. And since he is forced, according to the order that the Holy One, blessed be He, established in His world, to also earn a livelihood in the simple sense, his work is temporary, in a manner that does not require the investment of much energy—and certainly not the investment of his *Chabad* [intellectual] energy and his power of thought in general—in matters that even non-Jews are enthusiastic about.

There is room to say that you might ask me, why is this "sicha" and this demand not heard from the mouth of such-and-such rabbi or such-and-such leader, etc.?

It is possible that the reason is because of the two points mentioned above. But the main thing is that this question is not a refutation of the point, for either way, if it is the truth, then one should accept the truth from whoever said it, and if it is not the truth, then one must prove how the argument is invalid.

As mentioned, the above is directed to the young people of the children of Israel everywhere, and first and foremost in the Holy Land, may it be built and established, and especially first and foremost to those whom people look at—in whatever circle it may be—as representatives of the children of Israel.

With respect and blessing.

## 7140

B"H, 4 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I confirm receipt of your letter from Rosh Chodesh Teves, and even more so, the one from the seventh night of Chanukah, along with the enclosed *pidyon nefesh*. It will be read at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May Hashem Yisbarach grant that, just as you have brought this request, you should also report good news regarding all the matters you wrote about.

Regarding your writing that you are unable to find buyers for the business:

Perhaps there is a way to travel to Montreal for a few days to seek a source of *parnassah*. At the same time, a buyer might be found in Montreal, and not necessarily in the place where you are currently looking.

Since, as it is written, "there is no one among us who knows how long" (due to hidden reasons), one must seek various paths, and may Hashem Yisbarach provide the path that is best.

May it be His will—since we have just come from the days of Chanukah, where the time for the *mitzvah* of lighting the candles is *mishtashke hachamah* (when it becomes dark)—that a Yid lights and illuminates, not only for himself, but also *al pesach beiso mibachutz* (at the door of his house facing the outside), so that the light reaches there as well. And this is not always in the same measure, but specifically in a manner of *mosif v'holech mosif v'or* (increasing and continuing to increase in light), until the Ramban (on the Torah, Parshas Beha'aloscha) says regarding the miracle of Chanukah, "The candles of Chanukah, the candles that are forever, and all the blessings that are never nullified"—referring to the blessings of "May Hashem bless you and guard you," and as our Sages expound, "that your assets may be blessed."

May it be so *b'egla didan* (speedily in our days) regarding your situation. Then you will be occupied, not with what you wrote about—for our Sages say, "the wheel turns," and if, *chas v'shalom*, one finds oneself at the very bottom, it is a sign that an *aliyah* (an ascent) is already beginning—but rather, your occupation will consist of how to justify to yourself the questions and the style of them. Although in *Birkas Hamazon*, and specifically in the first blessing which is *d'oraisa*, we say explicitly, "He who feeds the entire world with His goodness, with grace, with kindness, and with mercy"—well, as the saying goes, if only we were already at that level.

With blessings for good news in all the aforementioned.

## 7101

B"H, 6 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following the longest of intervals, your letter from Motzaei Shabbos was received, along with its enclosure. In response to your three questions:

1) Regarding the camp: In my opinion, since last year you saw and were convinced of the necessity of the matter—especially in the New England region—it is understood that it is worth the effort and exertion to continue the boys' camp next year as well. Since there are still several months before the start of the season, appropriate promotion will surely be effective in attracting those circles that can pay the required fees. Therefore, one should hope that there will be no deficit, and it may even be possible to pay off at least a portion of the past debt. Although you write that you wish to continue the camp for the sake of Heaven, we see tangibly that for a project to have continuity, the budget must be met. Therefore, one must do everything necessary in the natural way to achieve this. And since Chazal have said that "all beginnings are difficult," the period of beginning has already passed, and therefore it will be easier.

2) Regarding your question as to whether one should increase in tefillah concerning success in material matters and the like, as well as in matters of health:

It is surprising that there is any doubt or question about this, for we have been commanded in our Torah—the Torah of life—to "guard yourselves very carefully." The Rambam rules in Hilchos Deios, at the end of chapter 3 and the beginning of chapter 4, that a person must ensure that his body is healthy and whole, for this is one of the ways of Hashem. It is a general ruling that a person must guard the health of his body and all his affairs. In the words of our Alter Rebbe in his Shulchan Aruch, Hilchos Nizkei Guf V'Nefesh, section 4: "A person has no authority over his body at all... to cause it any pain," etc. See also there in Hilchos Shemiras Guf. There is no need to elaborate on a matter that is well-known. Furthermore, according to many Rishonim, when a person feels a need for something, such as bodily health, it is a positive commandment from the Torah to daven to Hashem for it.

3) Regarding what you wrote about a camp for children as well: Since, according to your letter, the camp for children still requires clarification and demands great effort and exertion, in my opinion, you should not burden yourself with an additional new project, such as a children's camp, at least for the coming year. Depending on the results of this year, you can decide how to proceed in the summer of 5761.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, with tranquility and a good heart.

#### ***7101***

**To increase in tefillah:** In continuation of this—see letter 7104.

## 7242

7242

B.H., 7 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn

To the avreich, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished Rabbi Naftali, may he live,
Hakohen

Greetings and blessings!

I hope that you arrived safely in London, and I am interested to know if, during the journey, you had the opportunity to meet with Mr. Shneur Zalman Yaffe and his family, may they live, since you were traveling on the same ship. Also, whether there was an opportunity in such a setting to spread the wellsprings outward (*hafotzas hamaayanos chutzah*), as we have spoken about many times regarding the necessity to utilize every matter and opportunity in this direction. This is especially so according to the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, as explained regarding the matter of the children of Israel wandering in the lands (printed at the end of *Likutei Torah*, Kehot edition).

Furthermore, for the sake of preference and addition, I have come to urge that during your stay in London, you should certainly speak—in addition to conveying regards from here and sharing matters from the *farbrengens* here—about the evening yeshivos, the good works and the magnitude of the matter, and how this has sparked a fundamental change in the students and in their entire environment, etc. One should not act with a sense of false humility regarding this, for regarding such things it is said, "And I will walk in a broad place," especially when it concerns the practical outcome and the results of the work regarding the evening yeshivos in London. The test in such matters is known—from which side the arguments come, etc. (printed in *Hayom Yom*, 23 Sivan).

It is obvious that there is no contradiction between the above and what I spoke to you about regarding the evening yeshivos in a private conversation—for in matters of *kedushah*, we are commanded to "ascend in holiness," and not to be satisfied **at all** with achievements of the past, or even the present. In matters of *kedushah*, to use the language of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in his *Tanya*, end of Chapter 19: "The level of the head and brains of lower levels are below the level of the heels and feet of levels higher than them." Our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe did not stop there, but established the matter even further, as he concludes: "And as our Sages said, the feet of the *Chayos* are opposite them all." This matter is explained regarding what preceded it, in an even more emphasized phrasing, that "all levels and degrees below are **as nothing** compared to the levels and degrees above them."

This is also the foundation for what I spoke to you about regarding the second stage in the development of the evening yeshivos. With the help of the talents you have been gifted with, if you utilize them as required and with the necessary energy for this matter, I hope that the second stage will also arrive soon. Then, regarding the entire matter, one should apply the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe mentioned above. However, it is understood and obvious that this is not only in the sense of "as nothing," but—and this is the main point—that the previous stage, the current situation, is a level and degree in *kedushah* to the extent that it is called "head and brains," etc., and this is understood.

If you find a day or two free, it would be appropriate for you to visit Manchester, and primarily the yeshivah there, and convey my regards to the *Rosh Yeshivah* and the *Mashgiach*, may they live, and with his permission, convey my regards to the students of the yeshivah, may they live. It is understood that my regards mean that you should share some matter of Torah and *hisorerus* that you heard during the *farbrengens*. I rely on your understanding as to which matter you will choose.

With blessings for success in all the above and for good news,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7143

B"H, 7 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the sixth night of Chanukah, requesting a blessing for success in your studies, and noting that Chanukah is the time when Yisrael fights for the study of the holy Torah.

At an opportune time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good.

However, along with this, it is understood and also simple that you must fulfill the instruction of our Sages: "You have labored" — and the promise will be fulfilled — "and you have found."

This is similar to the war of the days of Chanukah that you write about. The war was not against every form of Torah study, but rather, as we say in the *Al HaNissim* prayer, specifically "to make them forget **Your Torah**." That is to say, they did not oppose the study of Torah, provided that at the time of study, the element of connection to the Giver of the Torah was not engraved upon it. Likewise, regarding the *mitzvos*, they did not oppose all *mitzvos*, but specifically "**the statutes of Your will**," meaning *mitzvos* that have no [rational] reason. Against this, the Children of Yisrael fought, and consequently, they retained the study of Torah in general and the fulfillment of *mitzvos* that also include *eidus* (testimonies) and *mishpatim* (laws).

And in this very same way in our days, as the *Mishnah* rules, in order for the Torah to be preserved, one’s fear [of Heaven] must **precede** one’s wisdom. The way to arrive at fear of Heaven and love of Hashem is as the Rambam rules in *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, beginning of chapter 2: that the way to arrive at His fear is by contemplating the greatness of the Creator, blessed be He, etc. May it be His will that you conduct yourself in this manner, and also influence your friends, may they live, in this regard.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

744

B"H, 7 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Annual Banquet of the Ladies Auxiliary of Brownsville and East New York for the Lubavitcher Yeshivos "Tomchei Tmimim"

By this, I mean not only the preparations for the banquet, but also the "collection" of the good results—both financial and spiritual—for the results of an **annual** undertaking should be felt throughout the entire year.

As I have emphasized several times, this year is a special *segulah* year, as it marks 200 years since the *histalkus-hilula* of the Baal Shem Tov, the founder of Chassidus in general, and 200 years since the Alter Rebbe, the founder of Chabad, began his public work on a broad scale.

And afterwards, he began to reveal—to everyone, and continuing until this very day—the *derech* of Chassidus with its warmth and light, which was then further broadened, and with the greatest *mesiras nefesh*, declared and illuminated by the Alter Rebbe.

The *zechus* of this holy work will surely stand by each and every one of you and your households—may they live—for success in all your matters, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## Jakomo

B”H, 11 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn

Mr. Yaakov Elchanan, shichyeh,
Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 5th of Teves, in which you express surprise that at the farbrengen of the day of Besurah and Geulah, 19 Kislev, in Kfar Chabad, there was no public mention regarding our brethren, the Children of Israel, who [are in Russia], at a time when, seemingly, they should have prayed for them at the aforementioned gathering, etc.

Your bewilderment is all the greater, as you are certain that many of those present have relatives there, etc.

Your first point of wonder is answered by your second: precisely because the matter is bound up with the very souls of the leaders of the gathering and the people of Kfar Chabad in general—for everything they endured before leaving that place is etched deep within their souls—and especially since the vast majority of them have very close relatives there, both physically and spiritually, it is impossible, when considering the nature of the human soul, for them to fulfill their obligation in this matter by reciting a short prayer or a chapter of Tehillim and the like, and **immediately** thereafter to continue with the **joy of the farbrengen**, etc. For in many situations—and especially in the situation mentioned—a person is not master of his own spirit, even if he were to summon his best efforts, due to the festive nature of the day, the joy of the occasion, and the honor of those gathered. It is understood, and indeed simple, that in a matter as internal and soulful as this, there is no place for public display. In the days before the holiday, after the holiday, and even during the holiday, but not at the time of the farbrengen, the people and the situation there are certainly not only remembered, but stand alive before their eyes. This is the case for the vast majority of Anash who left that place. Nevertheless, the connection to that place remains in full force—and indeed, it is alive. The letters of Anash are a testament to this, as they inquire about the welfare and well-being of those who are there; these are letters written with a special vitality.

Moving from one subject to the same subject: It is explained in many places that all the Children of Israel are as one man, one complete **stature**. From this it is understood that, just as in the analogy, an added strengthening in one limb of the stature naturally adds strength and vitality to all the limbs, so too is it literally in the reality it represents, and even more so. For in spiritual matters, space does not create a barrier, and the laws of physical nature are transcended. From this it is understood that as each one of us here adds in Torah and mitzvos—matters that bring about Geulah in the literal sense to this "small world," which is the human being—we increase the light and the good, and push away the *sitra achra*. Through this, there will be an increase **there** as well, no less than through sending a package or the like, and indeed, even more so. Given what you wrote in your letter regarding your family background, I hope that no further proof is needed that only Torah and its mitzvos have the capacity to increase the light and the good in our world, this physical world. And as the distress increases, G-d forbid, the necessity for adding in the aforementioned increases manifold. And since it is a necessity, the full ability to fulfill the demand of this hour has certainly been granted, and the moral lesson is surely understood.

On this occasion, and since everything is by Divine Providence, I would like to urge you specifically regarding the absolute necessity and the personal obligation to set times for the study of the *pnimiyus haTorah* (the inner dimension of Torah), which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. This is especially pertinent as we are in the bicentennial year of the passing and *hillula* of the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory—a year of *segulah* for the spreading of his wellsprings, which is the teaching of Chassidus, until they reach even the "outermost" places, as stated in his famous *Iggeres HaKodesh*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 748

B.H., 11 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 6 Teves.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the matters about which you write.

Regarding what you wrote—that you are, G-d forbid, not succeeding in anything—it is understood from many places in our Torah, the Torah of life, that it is forbidden for a Jewish person to say such a thing, or even to think along those lines. It is also contrary to common sense, for the foundation of our faith is that everything is by Divine Providence, and "from the mouth of the Most High, evil does not proceed," G-d forbid. Furthermore, it is a known ruling that "everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good." Rather, as explained in many places, the more one strengthens oneself in the matter of faith and trust, and in the central point that—as mentioned above—everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good, the more one sees this truth tangibly, and sooner. See the explanation of this in the Tanya (according to the subject index of the Tanya, Kehot Publication Society).

This is the place for me to urge you to observe the three daily study portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which we heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that they are appropriate for every soul and are a segulah for many matters, including what was mentioned above.

Regarding what you wrote about the conduct of so-and-so, etc., which is not at all satisfactory, and that you feel forced to remain silent:

It is known and seen tangibly that there are many ways to exert influence, and speaking is not always the most effective method, especially speaking in a direct manner. Since our Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, has informed us that "a Jew cannot and does not want to be separated from Elokus," and this is also alluded to in the ruling of the Rambam in Hilchos Geirushin, end of chapter 2, there is certainly some way to influence the aforementioned person as well. It is just a matter of searching for it; "you have labored and you have found."

A general point in this regard is that often the way to influence is more effective indirectly, through friends, than directly or through relatives. May it be His will that just as you brought the request, you will bring good news regarding this.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita
