## 7252

B"H, 13 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, and in accordance with your request, this reply is being sent without waiting for its turn.

You write with a question regarding a woman who has already undergone two Caesarean sections (a birth in an unusual manner). Since she is now about to give birth, the doctor suggests that if this birth also takes place in the aforementioned manner, then in his opinion, there is a concern should she conceive again. Therefore, he wishes to perform, after the birth, a type of surgery so that she will be unable to conceive again.

Now, it is generally not my role to issue halachic rulings. However, what is seemingly surprising in the aforementioned is that it is well-known that the opinion of doctors (specifically in recent years) is that even after a birth in an unusual manner, a normal birth is possible. Furthermore, in their view, there is no limitation regarding health on the number of births in an unusual manner; rather, it depends on the general state of the woman’s health at the time of the birth. That is to say, one cannot decide regarding a concern for a future pregnancy and birth except in accordance with the state of health **at that time**, and for this, there are many remedies for maintaining health in general, as well as for strengthening the mother, and the like.

Furthermore, it is known that the ruling of the Tzemach Tzedek is that in a place where there is a concern regarding pregnancy, as mentioned above, he permits the use of a *moch* (contraceptive). Based on the reasoning, it appears that this is easier than a surgery that completely negates the possibility of conception.

And to add (and surely the doctor will also explain this), for the most part, the surgery to prevent pregnancy is performed by tying (and blocking) the tubes in the woman. Often, it happens that this tie comes undone, and the possibility of conception returns to its previous state, only that one **does not** know about it. In other words, from the perspective of the goal of avoiding pregnancy, it requires study as to what is better: whether in the manner of the aforementioned ruling of the Tzemach Tzedek, or in the manner of the aforementioned tying of the tubes.

And one more point to add, which is also essential: in general, according to the research and inquiry in the field of medical science in recent years, every single day is prone to innovations and discoveries. Therefore, a person should refrain from doing such things that cannot be reversed afterward, even if a treatment is discovered that negates the necessity of the procedure that was performed.

Since you write that the aforementioned doctor is a *shomer Torah u'mitzvos*, in addition to being an expert in the matter, it is appropriate that after you clarify the aforementioned points with another expert doctor in a principled manner, you should speak once again with the *shomer Torah u'mitzvos* doctor and clarify all of the above.

May the Ribono shel Olam, who watches over each and every one with *hashgacha pratis*, show them the correct path of how to conduct themselves in the aforementioned matter.

I will repeat my blessing that the Ribono shel Olam should fulfill the days of her pregnancy properly and with ease, and that she should give birth to healthy children at the proper time and with ease.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 7153

B"H, 13 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, distinguished, and upright, engaged in communal needs, R' Aryeh, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter from the eve of the second day [of the week], in which you ask about the change in wording in Rashi’s commentary on the Torah (Vayigash 46:28) from the wording of the Midrash (Bereishis Rabbah, Parsha 95). Rashi cites the phrasing, "from there instruction (hora'ah) shall go forth," whereas in the Midrash it states, "that he should teach (moreh) words of Torah therein."

It is well known that many Midrashim that were available to Rashi and the Rishonim in general have not reached us. Furthermore, even among the Midrashim that we do possess, there are various textual versions. The wording in Tanchuma is: "that he should teach (moreh) instruction (hora'ah) there."

Regarding the fact that Rashi chose this version, similar to Tanchuma and not the version in Midrash Rabbah, one can say simply that it is closer to the literal meaning (peshat) of the verse, "to instruct (lehoros)" rather than "to teach (lilmod)." This is the distinction between learning Torah and the manner (which comes later) of issuing a halachic ruling (paskenen a din). Rashi, in his commentary on the Torah, always strives for the interpretation to be as close as possible to the literal meaning of the text, whereas in the Midrash, one sometimes specifically seeks the homiletical approach (derush), and this is simple to understand.

And if you were to say that Rashi includes the meaning of the Midrash, the difference between these two matters—"that he should teach words of Torah"—could refer to the study of Torah, not necessarily regarding a halachic ruling. However, for a halachic ruling, there must be the study of Torah. Therefore, Rashi uses the term *hora'ah*, which is closer to the language of the verse, and at the same time, *hora'ah* includes the study of Torah, as "he who has two hundred [maneh] also has one hundred."

It is worth noting what we have heard regarding the teaching of the Alter Rebbe on the parsha of "Vayechi Yaakov," and on this Rashi commentary about which you write (see Hayom Yom, 18 Teves).

May Hashem Yisbarach help that each of us should accomplish in our own "Egypt" in the manner described in this Torah of the Alter Rebbe, and may this be with vitality, warmth, and Chassidic enthusiasm.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 725

[14 Teves 5720]

...Regarding what is explained in Chassidic discourse (Sefer HaMaamarim 5629 of the Rebbe Maharash, s.v. Vayigash, p. 18) concerning the distinction between the Mishkan and the Beis HaMikdash, which corresponds to the distinction between Yosef and Yehudah, and therefore the Mishkan was made of shittim wood, etc. He raises a difficulty: for even in Shiloh, it was a house of stone (Mishnah, end of Zevachim).

The resolution is that in Sefer HaMaamarim, he explains this according to the interpretation of Rabbi Zeira (Yerushalmi, Megillah, end of Chapter 1) regarding the aforementioned Mishnah in Zevachim, that the stone structure was only ten tefachim high, and upon it were the curtains and the boards, etc.

If you were to say that no one disputes this interpretation—(though the version in Midrash Tehillim, end of Psalm 78, and in Midrash Shmuel, Chapter 3, requires further study)—the reason this interpretation is not cited by the Rambam at the beginning of Hilchos Beis HaBechirah is that he was extremely brief there in general. His reason is that what has been, has been.

It should further be noted that in other places, the distinction between the Mishkan in the desert and the Mishkan of Shiloh is explained in a similar vein (see Likutei Torah, Bracha 99d; Sefer Maamarei Admur HaZaken, Hanachos HaRaP, p. 81). However, in those sources, the detail explained is that in Shiloh, the concept of "rest" began, whereas it did not in the desert; while in Sefer HaMaamarim, the detail explained is that it was in the portion of Yosef. This corresponds to the two aspects of Shiloh, which is called both a "house" and a "Mishkan," as our Sages have said. And this is clear.

**Note.** In Likutei Torah there—see also the glosses of the Rebbe (printed at the end of the Kehot edition of Likutei Torah). It appears there are other printing errors there (as well as in Sefer Maamarei Admur HaZaken). For example, what is written that there was no protruding wood (**in Shiloh**), etc., and therefore the Rambam counted, etc., in the building of the Beis HaMikdash, etc.—and therefore one should not raise a difficulty from this against what is written in Sefer HaMaamarim...

Regarding what is explained in Chassidic discourse concerning the second paragraph of Krias Shema, that it precedes "And you shall bind them" with "And you shall teach them," which is the order for the Future to Come where "action is primary"—this does not seem to align with what is stated (Berachos 35b) that the second paragraph applies when one is not doing the will of Hashem.

This can be explained by the fact that even in the Future to Come there will be several levels, "from the greatest to the smallest," and "the youth of one hundred years shall die," even though **in general**, the order then will be to unify higher unifications to draw down higher lights from Atzilus, as is explained in Iggeres HaKodesh by the Alter Rebbe, end of Epistle 26.

## Z'kand

B"H, 15 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 3 Teves, in which you outline the main points of your life story and the recent changes in your religious observance—that you have returned, in your words, to the "sources," the source of living waters, our Torah and its mitzvos, of which it is said, "and you shall live by them."

Indeed, from this very phrasing—"returning to the sources"—it is understood that in truth, this is not a matter of innovation in essence. On the contrary, a person is returning to his true place. Therefore, as you proceed along this path from strength to strength, your resolve and determination to continue in this direction will strengthen from time to time. This is on the condition that you are not deterred by the battle with the yetzer, which is liable to use various strange and unusual ways to entice a person—and not only in matters of avodas Hashem, but even in generally good deeds that even non-religious people among the nations of the world practice. Despite all this, the yetzer entices and incites. However, our Sages of blessed memory have informed us that the Creator of man has given each person the strength to overcome this battle, to be victorious, and to go from strength to strength.

Regarding what you wrote about the pressure of your financial situation—that you therefore need to receive assistance from your mother, may she live and be well, even though her own situation is extremely strained and she must support her household, etc.

It is not clear from your letter in which field you are studying and how much time remains until you complete your course of study. However, in general, according to what is heard here, many students at that same institution, alongside their studies—and especially in the year or two before graduation—also engage in part-time work, such as giving private lessons and the like, in a way that does not at all interfere with the time they need to succeed in their studies. And even until then, studying a profession is a preparation for a more suitable arrangement in life for decades to come. That is to say, the effort and toil during the time of study is an investment that will bring good fruit many times over and for a long time. Certainly, with effort on your part, you will then have the ability to satisfy your mother, may she live and be well, with much nachas, so that she will see the good fruit of her labor and the help she provided you to study and complete your education.

It is understood that there is no room for apology on your part for writing to me, and you should continue to do so in the future. My hope is that your next letters will bring good news regarding the matters mentioned, and first and foremost, regarding the improvement of your state of mind and the strengthening of your trust in Hashem, may He be blessed, who oversees each and every person with hashgacha pratis, down to the finest details.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## Z'kenah

B"H, 15 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn

To the Gabbaim and leaders of the Tzemach Tzedek Nusach HaAri Synagogue,
184 Henry Street, New York
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

I have received word that the New York City administration intends to demolish the building in which your shul and beis medrash are located. Surely, this will be done in accordance with law and regulation, in exchange for a sum sufficient to acquire a shul and beis medrash suitable for your customs and needs.

It is surely unnecessary to draw your attention to the great necessity of finding, in good time, a location and building to which you can relocate the shul and beis medrash, in order to continue your activities in a manner consistent with the nusach and tradition of many years—the Nusach HaAri and its customs regarding davening and shul matters in general—together with the shiurei Torah studied in public, in the manner of our ancestors and as you have conducted yourselves in your shul and beis medrash until now.

However, based on the statement of our Sages that "one only urges those who are already diligent," I am writing to add that you will surely continue these aforementioned activities in the new location just as you have conducted yourselves until now. My intention is that it be done independently, without partnerships or the like, so that you will have the full ability to preserve the purity of the customs, the nusach, and so on. As is known, our holy Torah places great emphasis on this: "Be careful with the customs of your fathers, for they are in your hands" (Beitzah 4b).

May it be Hashem's will that the desire of Hashem shall succeed in their hands, to continue all the matters of the Tzemach Tzedek Nusach HaAri shul and beis medrash in a manner of "increasing and going forward, increasing and adding light."

And soon may the prophecy be fulfilled: "The synagogues and houses of study in Bavel are destined to be established in Eretz Yisrael," with the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu in the true and complete Geulah.

With respect and a blessing for success.

## Z’keno

B”H, 15 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interruption, your letter from the fourth day of Chanukah arrived, in which you write about your situation regarding your studies and examinations, and the various thoughts regarding the future.

As I have written recently—and as I believe we also spoke about when you were here—after one invests so much effort, time, energy, and money into a matter, whatever it may be, one **must** do **everything possible** to utilize it in the best way. Especially since this concerns a matter where, as I understand from your letter, the majority has already been accomplished, it is certainly understandable that one must make the effort to finish the remaining part as well, so that what was done previously should not be lost.

Understandably, it is difficult to point out specific details here, because this depends on many particulars, examinations, and possibilities. It is also understandable that if one cannot manage to accomplish the full one hundred percent, then 90 is better than 80, and 80 is better than 70. Based on the possibilities, and by assessing your strength and the surrounding situation, you should choose the **greatest** result that can be achieved after such long-term exertion.

Since you have been in that place for several years, and are in contact with professors who have also known you for several years—and especially since your wife, tichyeh, is with you, and according to the statement of our Sages, "his wife is as himself"—consulting with them will fulfill the concept of "victory through many counselors," so that you may decide and **act** in the way that is best in all respects.

At a time of favor, I will mention you and your family, shichyu, at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be His will that you report good news in this matter.

On this occasion, I would like to draw your attention to the practice of reciting the daily portion of Tehillim (as the Tehillim is divided according to the days of the month) each morning after davening, and on weekdays, to give a few coins to tzedakah before davening in the morning. Your wife, tichyeh, should maintain the good custom of Jewish daughters to give tzedakah each time before lighting candles on Erev Shabbos and Yom Tov. All of this serves as a channel and vessel for an increase in blessing from Hashem Yisbarach.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

7557

B"H, 15 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After the longest of intervals, your letter from the third night [of Chanukah] was received, in which you describe your participation in the activities of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad and ATAH in general.

May it be Hashem’s will that you continue to increase these efforts, and then some. For this is the necessity and demand of the hour, and we have been promised regarding such matters: "You have labored and you have found." This is especially true as the merit of the many assists you, and particularly since we are in the bicentennial year of the histalkus-hilula of the Baal Shem Tov, a year of special potential for "spreading the wellsprings outward," which is the essence of the teachings of Chassidus.

Regarding what you wrote at the end of your letter—that all of the above has no effect on your personal affairs:

Since the Alter Rebbe writes that through every such activity, one’s mind and heart become a thousand times more refined, it is certainly and absolutely the case in reality. However, it is understood from his language, "they become refined," that:

1. At the very least, some action must be taken to utilize this superior preparation of the mind and heart, and then the success of that action will be a thousand times greater. This will certainly be the case for you. Do not be impressed by the enticements of the yetzer hara, which seeks to cause you any sense of discouragement, chas v’shalom. This matter, and the advice for it, is explained in many places in Chassidus, including in the Tanya Kadisha, as indicated in the index of subjects at the end of the sefer.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 19,258

[15 Teves, 5720]

In response to your letter—which lacks a date of writing—sent after a long hiatus, in which you write regarding your current livelihood situation.

My general perspective is well-known: it is worthwhile to make an effort to arrange one’s livelihood in a way that does not involve excessive worry. This is, of course, explained well in Chassidus regarding the concept that livelihood must be [pursued] without "a heart and a heart" [i.e., without duplicity or divided focus]. Therefore, it is worthwhile to contemplate and endeavor to gradually shift your livelihood toward matters that will not involve the aforementioned worry. My hope is that through contemplation and searching, you will eventually find this, and may Hashem grant you success so that it comes about without excessive searching...

## Zekant

B"H, 18 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the Tenth of Teves—which will soon be transformed into joy and gladness—I have read with interest what you wrote regarding your study program and so on. Surely you will not be satisfied with your achievements thus far, but will endeavor in an appropriate manner to add to them. Given your appropriate acquaintance [with the subject matter], there is great hope that you will succeed in this as well, especially since the merit of the many—your students and those you influence—will assist you.

Regarding what you wrote about *u'faratzta* as it pertains to yourself: it is understood that the straight and best path is the simple one—to increase in the study of Torah for yourself and in your surroundings, and in the fulfillment of its *mitzvos* as is proper. You should not be impressed at all by the stratagems of the *yetzer* [hara], which stands to interfere with the aforementioned by means of various strange arguments. One of its tactics [...] is to cause a decline in spirit due to a lack of perfection and the like, from which it is but a small step to a state of despair, *chas v'shalom*, and the like. Furthermore, it sometimes clothes this in the guise of *yiras shamayim* and so on, as is also understood from the words of our Rebbeim (printed in *Hayom Yom*, 23 Sivan). The test for this is simple and explained there: when one sees that the aforementioned arguments diminish one's energy for studying Torah and fulfilling *mitzvos*, this is a complete clarification of who is doing the arguing.

You should divert your attention from all matters of sadness, as is explained in the *Tanya Kadisha*, and engage with joy and goodness of heart in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit in your surroundings. This will also effect a refinement in the vessels of your *neshamah*, as stated by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe—the arbiter of the *nistar* of Torah and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the arbiter of the *nigleh* of Torah—that your mind and heart will become a thousand times more refined, and then your study and your activities will succeed a thousand times more.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 76

B"H, 18 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the tenth month—may it soon be transformed into joy and gladness—in which you write regarding the situation in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, following the earthquake that occurred. You note that it seems those who ought to be leaders are unaware of the directives of the leaders of previous generations, and that it is a mitzvah to inform them, etc.

As for me, it is a matter of question whether the issue lies in a lack of knowledge, or rather in the fact that they are actively seeking—and choosing—new and strange paths, and to the wise, a word is sufficient. Even with only a moment’s reflection, it is understood and quite simple that the approach of Rav S.R. Hirsch, of blessed memory, in his time, is not at all suitable for Eretz Yisrael (nor for the United States). Furthermore, it is liable to cause great harm [confusing the youth with questions and doubts that are not at all within their four cubits, and then attempting to resolve the question, at a time when no one is interested in such pilpul; rather, they are searching for the absolute truth, without paint or makeup, in the manner of the Sages’ dictum: "The more straightforward, the better"]. This is apparently tangible to any honest person who observes without being biased by the education they received from their father or themselves, and this is well-understood. Especially since it is even doubtful whether it would not have been better had they not been educated in a system of questions from distorted perspectives and long, dangerous answers, but rather to walk only on the straight path, studying the Torah of Yisrael—the Torah of the upright—like our ancestors, believers the children of believers, without the intermingling of foreign branches and external philosophies.

Regarding your question as to whether I am interested in knowing matters concerning the leadership of the Rebbe, the father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—our Sages have already stated that a precious thing is worth its weight in gold. Especially since, in the usual course of events, it is impossible to recount such things without some new detail or nuance, provided it is conveyed by an eyewitness who is precise in their transmission.

May it be the will of Hashem that, since many of the signs from the Beraisa at the end of Maseches Sotah have already been fulfilled, the main thing will be fulfilled in our very near future: the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu, the true and complete Geulah, a redemption from all exiles.

With respect and blessing.

## 7162

7162

B"H, 20 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod
May Hashem protect them and may they live

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter and your inquiry:

I will reiterate once again that it is understood and quite simple that it is extremely distressing that for several months now I have been urging the matter of the students’ pilpul collection, and until now it has not been brought to fruition.

2) It is likewise understood and simple that if the name Tomchei Temimim is borne by the yeshiva—as is explained at length in the Kuntres Eitz Chaim, and as the will of our Nesi’im, the founders and directors of the yeshiva, is well known—then the study of Chassidus is mandatory, and specifically through true understanding and comprehension, not in the manner of "Chagas Chassidim."

It is therefore simple that students who have been in such a yeshiva for a year or two, or even longer, should possess understanding and comprehension in certain subjects of the teachings of Chassidus, in a way that they are able to convey, both orally and in writing, what they understand regarding these matters.

Since there are many sources for books, kuntresim, and maamarim, surely after a year or two of study or more, they have the ability to instruct, stating that a certain subject was discussed in such-and-such a place and is also found in a second place [where, certainly, through the discussion in the second place, the explanation and understanding are enhanced].

And since the indexes for the holy Tanya, Torah Or, and Likutei Torah have been printed, the aforementioned can be done without excessive difficulty, and even without the effort that would otherwise be required.

According to this, it is highly puzzling what the true reason is for the fact that the aforementioned collection has not yet materialized, given that, according to your letter, the obstacle lies in the section pertaining to the teachings of Chassidus.

3) The wonder grows even greater, for among several students from Lod who have come here, it was clear immediately upon their arrival that they have the ability to write with appropriate clarity as mentioned above. Surely they did not acquire this ability during their journey from Lod to here.

4) Perhaps there are those who object in principle to the supposed innovation of the entire aforementioned matter, since fifty or a hundred years ago, such things were not practiced. There are two responses to this:

(a) Anyone who has seen the *HaTamim* booklets printed in Warsaw by the Rebbe Rayatz will find that there is a section there just like the one described.

(b) The test for matters such as these is well known—from which side the arguments come—based on what is explained in the *Hayom Yom* (23 Sivan). That is, to look at the practical results. We see tangibly that those students who engaged in the aforementioned gained vitality, at the very least in the study of the subjects about which they were writing. Furthermore, they influenced several of their peers to do the same. Additionally, the subjects were publicized even to those who until then had not known about them. The writing also compelled deeper study and greater understanding of the aforementioned subjects. From the positive, you hear the negative.

My intent is that by explaining to the students that there is no place to be interested in writing about these subjects, and that there is no place for innovation and proper explanation, etc., one sees **tangibly** the results of the aforementioned.

5) Perhaps there are those who fear and are anxious that, perhaps through the writing of a maamar on the aforementioned, the self-importance of the writers will increase.

Now, (aside from the fact that this is incomprehensible, since even in writing on the revealed part of Torah there is room for such a concern), the aforementioned concern exists also if one compels the students to repeat maamarim in public, to conduct a campaign so that they study Chassidus, and to explain the necessity of the matter in their own words, etc., etc.

And although it is understood and simple that through this (the lack of writing and the appearance of the aforementioned) the dissemination of the wellsprings outward is diminished—the "outward" of **oneself**, the "outward" of the four cubits, and the "outward" of the outside world—a task for which **each and every one** of us was commanded in the Iggeres HaKodesh of the Baal Shem Tov (and even more so, closer to our time, by our Rebbeim Nesi’im), surely the administration is also aware of all this.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe Shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

P.S.
Your letters from 11, 12, and 13 Teves, along with their enclosures, as well as the previous ones, have been received.

## 664

B.H., 21 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the annual dinner of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’vracha!

This year’s dinner of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch takes place on the auspicious day of 24 Teves, the yahrtzeit of the Alter Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, the founder of Chassidus Chabad.

* * *

A yahrtzeit is the annual commemoration of the final day of life in this world, Olam HaZeh, of a Jewish soul, and of its return to its Creator.

This day is the time for a summary of one’s entire life—of how the soul fulfilled its shlichus in this world.

Like all commemorations in Jewish life to which the Torah draws our attention, a yahrtzeit is not merely a remembrance that should remain in memory alone.

It reminds and demands practical action in the spirit of the soul-shlichus of the baal ha’yahrtzeit, and through actual deeds in this spirit, one unites—and becomes unified—with the creative work and eternal life of the baal ha’yahrtzeit.

According to the explanations of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and his father, the Rebbe (Rashab)—may their souls be bound in the bond of life—the inner point of the soul-shlichus, of the life and work of the Alter Rebbe, is—

As it is also reflected in the beginning of his name—

**"Shneur,"** two lights (**shnei or**) unified (in one word)—to unify the two Divine lights: the revealed light of Torah (**nigleh shebaTorah**), and the hidden, inner light of Torah (**nistar shebaTorah**), so that the inner should permeate, illuminate, and shine forth from the outer, so that it should be one whole and perfect Torah—**Torah Temimah.**

And, as explained in the Zohar, at that time there is also a unification in the same manner—the pnimiyus of the soul with the chitzoniyus of the soul—the revealed part of the Jewish soul with its point of Yiddishkeit.

This is also the inner purpose of the Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch yeshivos: that the talmidim should be **temimim**, in the spirit of **Torah Temimah**, as it was founded and explained by the Alter Rebbe, the baal ha’yahrtzeit.

* * *

All those who participate properly in the annual dinner of the Tomchei Temimim yeshivos on this auspicious day of 24 Teves, including those who were personally unable to be present but take their proper part in maintaining, strengthening, and expanding the Lubavitcher yeshivos, thereby carry and unite themselves with the creative work and activities of the baal ha’yahrtzeit.

May it be Hashem’s will that this participation be in a manner of ascent, with constantly growing vitality and dedication.

And the zechus of the baal ha’yahrtzeit, the Alter Rebbe, will surely stand by everyone who takes part in the support and expansion of the Tomchei Temimim yeshivos, which are conducted in his spirit and his derech, and will bring them Divine blessings in all that they need, in both gashmiyus and ruchniyus alike.

With respect and blessing,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## Zaks

B"H, 21 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write about the highly important work in the Ladies Auxiliary for the benefit of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, and conclude with the concern regarding how to proceed, as the work is taking a toll on your health.

As we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and also in the name of his father, the Rebbe—of blessed memory, of righteous memory, of holy memory—who were the founders and directors of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, regarding the great merit of helping, each according to their ability, to increase and expand the yeshivos: they also explained that this is a merit not only for after one hundred and twenty years, but that it is also a channel and vessel to receive the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach in those things one is in need of, here in this world.

It is therefore understood that one must hold fast to this and continue to do so, and see that the matter is pursued in truth, as one is involved in a cause for which our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, sacrificed themselves.

From this, it is also understood that the work involved in this should not only not cost one their health, but rather it should add to one’s health, just as any good thing that a person does or receives adds to them in all respects, health included.

It is also understood that it is possible—as with many other matters—that it may be associated with difficulties, or as you write, inappropriate behavior toward you from your co-workers. One must seek ways to improve this to the greatest extent possible, and surely, in any case, it will be possible to achieve this in part. But in any event, there is no place to say that because someone else is not acting as they should, one should do something that is not good oneself.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant you, together with your husband, the Rav shlita, good health for long, good years, and may you both continue, each according to your ability, to work for the support of all matters of Chassidus, with a good spirit and in a manner of ever-increasing growth.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe shlita,

Secretary

## 765

B"H, 22 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 20th of Teves, along with the *pidyon nefesh*.

It gave me great pleasure to read in your letter of your success in influencing youth organizations. May it be the will of Hashem that your success thus far will inspire both you and those you influence to increase your efforts in assisting the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Regarding the nature of human beings, it is said that "he who has one hundred wants two hundred, and he who has two hundred wants four hundred"—this should be the case many times over in matters pertaining to spirituality and holiness. It is understood and simple that the aforementioned will also increase the blessings of Hashem in your personal affairs.

Regarding the same matter, at a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and I will do so in the future as well, *bli neder*. However, as I have conveyed through the esteemed Chossid, a man of many accomplishments, [Name]..., we see tangibly that when one "forces the hour," it is not always effective; on the contrary, etc. Even though the distress that leads one to force the hour is understandable—and a person is not held accountable for his distress—we are not speaking here of matters of punishment, *chas v'shalom*. Rather, such is the nature of the order of things, to the extent that one can use the word "nature" in such a context. Since this matter has been explained in many places, that it is not desirable to force the hour, it is certainly within a person’s power to refrain from doing so. Especially since we see tangibly that forcing the hour has affected you with a lack of *simcha*, and consequently, a deficiency in energy, etc.—for this is also the logical explanation in the nature of the *nefesh habehamis* as to why this is not desirable.

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon you will bring good news, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed, including in your personal affairs—especially since you are correct in writing that this also touches upon general matters. May you utilize the matter of *iskafya* and refrain from forcing the hour, in a manner of true expansion in *gashmius* and *ruchnius*.

Blessings for good tidings, as mentioned above, speedily in our days.

## 616

B.H., 25 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After the longest of interruptions, your letter of 21 Teves was received, though even from it the reason for the interruption is not entirely clear.

It is, of course, most distressing to hear of the situation in... The reason for this, it seems, is based on the well-known sicha of the Rebbe Rashab—which we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe—that this is where the difference is evident between a faithful clerk and a person working for himself. The former does only what is required of him; that is, if a customer comes, he sells him the merchandise, and when the time comes to close the shop, he is justified in his own eyes and in the eyes of Heaven, for he stood in the shop from such-and-such an hour to such-and-such an hour waiting for a customer, and nothing more can be demanded of him.

This is not the case, however, regarding a matter that is one’s own. One is concerned that the matter should strengthen, expand, and spread in reality. If a customer does not come to his shop, he goes out and searches for him. And even after the shop’s closing time, not only does he not prevent or hinder a customer from coming, but on the contrary, he derives taanug from having made a profit even outside the framework. This is the essence of the sicha. To this, one must add that the customer also senses whether the person dealing with him is acting like a clerk—even if he observes all the details—or whether he is someone who is genuinely interested in the substance of the matter (and not merely in the attitude of "I have fulfilled my obligation"). Furthermore, he even feels in his heart distress that the customer does not come early to his door to seek the merchandise.

I do not know if what is written above is sharper than necessary, but in the final analysis, what difference does it make if it fits the description of the situation? For example, if one were to deal with his own livelihood or the search for an apartment in the manner of the aforementioned clerk, he can imagine for himself where he would be at this time and in what kind of apartment he would be living—provided he makes an honest accounting.

May Hashem grant success to each and every one of us, among all anash, to fulfill the will of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, in the way that they desired—which is to say, even more than the efforts of the most faithful clerk. After all, we are also approaching the yom hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Nasi of our generation.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

#### ***616***

**The difference is evident:** See above, Vol. 14, Letter 5454, and the references in the notes there—in connection with the precision of the expression "one who is engaged in Torah."

## 670

B"H, 25 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yosef, shichyeh,

Peace and blessing!

Your letter, in which you write regarding the Tanach you published for the soldiers of the IDF, has been received, and not long ago the Tanach itself was also received. I hereby wish to express my deep gratitude for this important and precious gift.

On this occasion, I would like to offer my blessing for the beauty of this edition. This, too, is founded upon the verse and the words of our Sages, of blessed memory: "This is my G-d and I will beautify Him" — beautify yourself before Him in the performance of mitzvos. If this is true at all times, it is all the more so in our generation, a "generation of orphans," where many judge the internal content by the external appearance of the thing.

Allow me to offer a comment in connection with the above, especially since if you agree with my observation, there is room to implement it in a larger printing. It is certain that the intention of every publisher of a holy book—especially a Tanach for soldiers and the like—is that the book should accompany them in their lives, not only on Shabbos and Yomim Tovim, but also—and in fact, this is the main point—on weekdays. This means that the book should be practical and endure for many days, which depends on the binding, the paper, and so on. I noticed that the paper of the copy sent to me is extremely thin. While there is, of course, an advantage to this—in that it does not take up much space and is convenient to carry in a pocket and the like—on the other hand, the paper is too weak to withstand daily use, and it seems that it is also prone to staining easily. I have seen several books printed on thin paper that is as light as the aforementioned, but much stronger.

May it be G-d's will that you utilize your potential and ability to disseminate traditional Judaism in circles that are ever-widening and spreading. And, to use a play on words regarding your position as an official in the Ministry of Defense: it is in your hands, and in the hands of your colleagues, to strengthen and promote the security (*bitachon*) of each and every one in the IDF, and within all of Klal Yisrael, by strengthening their faith (*emunah*) and trust (*bitachon*) in the G-d of Israel. This is as the dual instruction in the Tanach states: "Blessed is the man who trusts in Hashem, and Hashem shall be his trust (*mivtacho*), and he shall be like a tree planted by the waters..." and all the blessings enumerated there.

With respect and blessing.

## 7171

B"H, 26 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, scion of holy lineage, etc.,
R' Moshe Chaim Ephraim, shlita,

Shalom u’vracha!

I received your letter of Sunday with astonishment, in which you write regarding the letters about which I made a comment in my previous letter.

I write "with astonishment" because initially I said to myself that perhaps it was a mistake, or that someone had misled you into the aforementioned error. Yet, your letter comes to confirm once again that it is "true" that these letters belong to the Gaon HaRogatchover—a matter that is fundamentally and absolutely baseless.

It is surely unnecessary to inform you that thousands of letters, responsa, and pages of *chiddushei Torah* from the Gaon HaRogatchover exist, spanning a period of many years—decades. The common denominator in all these letters, responsa, and *chiddushei Torah*—without a single exception—is his unique style, which anyone can recognize. One can also recognize what absolutely does not belong to him, and the letters printed in the book *Doveiv Sifsei Yesheinim* are in a style that is the complete and absolute opposite of the Rogatchover’s style.

The reasoning that the aforementioned would instruct someone else to write in his name while he would [merely] sign it, or that due to many complaints and for the sake of the matter he would change his style, or that something would force him to deviate from his nature—is the opposite of the style and order of the Rogatchover’s entire life. It is also the complete and absolute opposite of the style and order of his life for decades, and in that very point, he did not deviate throughout that entire duration.

I am certain that not only would he not have wanted to instruct or speak in a different style, but he would not have been able to [and furthermore—even if it were a reality that the Rogatchover himself would come and testify that he wrote those letters, one would not believe him nor listen to his voice].

I have written all the above at some length because I am concerned by your aforementioned letter that you might perhaps write to others as well, insisting that what is printed—that these letters are from the Gaon HaRogatchover—is correct. It is my duty to point out that it is highly and most appropriate to refrain from this, because, as stated, there is no doubt that these letters are not from the Rogatchover. I ask for your forgiveness for these expressions, which perhaps are not the most diplomatic.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

***

**R' Moshe Chaim Ephraim:** Bloch, Bronx. Additional letters to him—above 7096, and in the references in the notes there.

**In my previous letter:** Above, ibid.

## 7122

B"H, 26 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It has been a very long time since we have received any letters or news from you. May it be the will of Hashem that this is a good sign, indicating that everything is in order and complete. May it also be so regarding the matter I am writing about below, which is:

I have received a most strange report—indeed, more than strange. However, since its source is from people who are fit to testify, and there are more than two of them, I am obligated to clarify the matter and take action accordingly.

The content of the report is that when a certain individual gives a *shiur* in public—on **any** topic whatsoever, whether in *nigleh* or in *Chassidus*—you, *tichyeh*, intervene **publicly**, specifically with *kushyos*, *pirchos*, *raminahu*, and contradictions, etc., etc. This has not happened just once or twice, or by chance, but has become a specific, established practice.

If the content of this report is, *chas v'shalom*, accurate, the astonishment—mingled with pain—is understandable. For this is an explicit law in the Torah regarding the great caution required against shaming one’s fellow in public in the context of *nigleh* of Torah. This is emphasized even more, and to a much greater degree, according to the teachings of *Chassidus* regarding the matter of *ahavas Yisrael*, and that all are compatible and have one Father—starting from the *Tanya Kadisha* and continuing through to "And they armed themselves... the vengeance of Hashem against Midian," etc.

One could offer a defense (though it is far too weak) that the intention is to clarify the law of Torah according to its truth, as one cannot tolerate, *chas v'shalom*, a distortion in any point or detail. But this is entirely incomprehensible: why must this be done specifically in public (where it appears as if there is a "strange branch"—that the gathered assembly should evaluate who is the one who is knowledgeable and expert, so to speak)? This is not the case if it were done in private, where there is no one present but the *Ribono shel Olam*, who will discern and estimate the praise of the one who found the *kushya*...

And if I merit it, these words will have an effect, such that those who have interfered with the above, for whatever reasons they may have had, will from now on assist twofold, in the manner explained in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* by our *Alter Rebbe* at the end of Chapter 9: If one was accustomed to reading one page, he should read two pages, etc.

With blessings for truly good news in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 7,273

B"H, 27 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter of 22 Teves, in which you write about your ailment—a stutter in your speech—and that you have already consulted a doctor, but it has not helped you.

It is somewhat surprising, as specialists in this field have various methods and modes of treatment, and surely they will find one that is suitable for you.

I must add, and this is the main point, that in general, this is dependent to a significant degree upon one’s self-confidence and nervous state. Therefore, the recommended advice in any case—even while undergoing various treatments—is for a person to strengthen their sense of *bitachon*. This is the foundation of our faith: *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach, that He is the Creator of the world, its Guide, and that He oversees each and every individual with *hashgacha pratis*, and that He is essentially good. From this, we understand the words of the Sweet Singer of Israel, "Hashem is with me, I will not fear," which negates the shame one feels before the people in whose presence one finds oneself. [One should have] a strong hope that Hashem will guide him in the path that is good before Him. As much as it is engraved in his understanding that he stands before the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, the fear of "what will those standing near me say about the way I speak" will diminish, and his speech will improve automatically, especially in conjunction with the treatment.

I would also add another point regarding the above: when you come to a word and fear that you will not be able to pronounce it properly, do not fight with yourself to pronounce that specific word; rather, replace it with another expression, and the like.

Since for everything one requires *siyatta d'shmaya*, it is understood that you should increase your consistency and diligence in the study of Torah and in the *hiddur* (beautification) of the performance of *mitzvos*. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
Surely you set aside a few coins for *tzedakah* every weekday before morning *davening*, and also keep up with the monthly *Tehillim* cycle—as the *Tehillim* is divided for the days of the month—to recite it every day, including on *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*, after morning *davening*.

And the concept of a *nisayon* is as it is written, "For Hashem is testing you," and according to the explanation of Rabbeinu HaZaken, *menaseh* is related to the word *nes*—a banner, an elevation. It is certain that anyone who takes part in the aforementioned effects an elevation in all of his affairs, including his personal matters. In the words of Rabbeinu HaZaken, his mind and heart become refined a thousand times over, and then one adds even more courage to the aforementioned activities, and matters arrange themselves in a manner of going "from strength to strength."

It is understood that it is your permission and your privilege to convey all of the above to all those participating in the activities of establishing the holy institutions and in *hafatzas hamaayanos*. May it be the will of Hashem that your words come from the heart and enter the hearts of those who hear them.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

## 745

B"H, 28 Teves, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Tuesday, in which you write that you distribute tzedakah according to your means to various places and causes, and a doubt has arisen in your mind: since you know that some of these are highly organized in matters of yiras shamayim, Torah, and mitzvos, while others—though they conform in every detail to the Shulchan Aruch and the Torah and mitzvos—are not as meticulous in their hidur (beautification/extra care), perhaps it would be better to give only to the former and cease support for those where there is doubt regarding their hidur.

Now, such thoughts always arouse suspicion as to who is inciting them—whether it is from the side of pure good, or if the "opposing side" is involved. The latter is capable of using many arguments, provided it prevents a Yid from engaging in Torah and mitzvos. Since it knows that if it stated its intentions openly, it would not be heeded, it searches and disguises itself in the cloak of piety. In a case such as this, after some time, there is room for a second argument: that one should not increase giving too much to a single institution, and that what was given previously is sufficient. Consequently, there will be a lack in the institutions and causes that are complete according to Torah but lack hidur, and there will be no increase in the "more meticulous" institutions either. In general, the warning of Chazal regarding many matters of tzedakah is well-known: not to over-scrutinize. And who is to say which institutions are complete according to Torah, even if they lack hidur?

One may hint here at a reinforcement of the reasoning mentioned in the prohibition of Chazal against giving one's gifts to only one Kohen (Eruvin 63a), even if that Kohen is one's own teacher.

The correct approach in matters of tzedakah is to establish minimum amounts for all holy, kosher institutions and kosher causes without searching and scrutinizing, etc., and to add to this amount for any institution that increases in hidur.

In this regard, I must also comment on your writing that you distribute tzedakah "according to your means," without explaining the interpretation. See the Tanya (as marked in the index of subjects—in the Kehot edition of Tanya) regarding the necessity to increase tzedakah **many times over.**

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6,277

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your two letters from 24 Teves, the yom hilula of the Alter Rebbe.

Regarding what you wrote concerning what to do with the funds that were received.

According to the statement of our Sages in such matters, one should use them for a *segulah* (provided, of course, that it is with the full consent of your wife, the *rabbanit* *tichyeh*). It is appropriate that you immediately set aside approximately a *chumash* (for one should not be overly precise in matters of *tzedakah*) for *tzedakah*. The remainder should be used over time for matters of Torah and *mitzvos*—and this, of course, simply includes the expenses for the *chinuch* of your children *sheyichyu* in accordance with the purity of holiness. In the meantime, however, you may invest them in something where the principal remains intact and bears fruit, and similarly regarding the investment in the trust fund. However, even regarding this, you should set aside from your own funds for *tzedakah*, whether as *maaser* or *chumash*, for we may act to the benefit of a person in their absence, especially a minor who is under the authority of her father.

I am sure you are preparing for the upcoming yom hilula, 10 Shevat, and may it be His will that its impression be felt throughout the entire year.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***6,277***

## 197

B"H, 3 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Teves, in which you write about what occurred about a month ago—a fire, may Hashem spare us—and that through the kindness of Hashem Yisbarach everything passed safely, and you do not know what caused it, etc.

It is surprising, for in your letter, the reason is also written, a few lines earlier. These are the words in your letter: "And I have not put on tefillin for many years because of, etc."

Regarding the mitzvah of tefillin, Chazal have said that the entire Torah is compared to tefillin. The intention of the mitzvah, in the words of the Shulchan Aruch, is so that we remember the miracles and wonders that He performed for us, etc., and that He (Hashem) has the power and dominion in the upper and lower realms.

This means that tefillin remind one of a miracle, and remind one that the Holy One, Blessed be He, also rules in this world regarding matters of livelihood, health, etc.—all those matters for which you request a blessing in your aforementioned letter.

Therefore, it is my hope that immediately upon receiving this letter, you will begin to put on tefillin every weekday, and also to daven every single day. On a day when it is not possible for you to go to the beis medrash to daven, you should daven in your home. On weekdays, before putting on tefillin, you should set aside a few coins for tzedakah. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all that was mentioned.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding what was written above and mentioned in your letter, as well as all your family members, may they live and be well.

With blessings for good tidings regarding the above.

## 719

B"H, 3 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 25 Teves, in which you write regarding the shidduch that seems right to both of you, but the family of the young woman is delaying the matter.

Although you write the reason given for the refusal on the part of her family, there is an impression that the inner reason is that they desire a more complete yiras shamayim on your part. If this is the case, it is understood and simple that you must fulfill this requirement—not only because the family demands it, but primarily because it is a commandment of the Torah, the Toras Chaim, and we are commanded to ascend in holiness. If we are commanded to do so in all places and at all times, how much more so in our times, and especially in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt, regarding which it is said: "The eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year."

When preparing for such a decisive and vital step as building a home in Yisrael—a building that will endure forever—the aforementioned is necessary and essential, and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

Together with the above, and since a person must act in the natural way regarding what depends on him, you should endeavor through friends and acquaintances of her family to influence those who are refusing to change their minds.

And since every matter is by Divine Providence, and you mention in your letter that your grandfather was among the founders and early members of the community of Mekubalim, I have the obligation (and the privilege) to point out to you the absolute necessity and personal duty to set times for the study of Pnimiyus HaTorah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. To elaborate on the simplicity of this matter at length is unnecessary.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 7182

B”H, 3 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 25 Teves, in which you outline what you and your family—may they live—have experienced until now, and how you have witnessed the kindness of Hashem in that your aliyah to Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—was completed in peace, and you ask for my advice regarding what you should focus on now.

First and foremost, it is understood and simple that you, and each member of your family—among all those who tangibly witness the kindness of Hashem—should express your gratitude, or in the language of our Sages, bring a "thanksgiving offering." In your specific circumstances, since this is the first year of your aliyah to the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year, you should dedicate yourself to perfecting your study of the holy Torah, the Torah of life, and to the proper fulfillment of its mitzvos. Therefore, at the very least (until the coming Rosh Hashanah, and this carries over) until after the upcoming Yom Tov of Sukkos, my clear opinion is that you should study in the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lod with great diligence and persistence. Certainly, not only will this not hinder your future success in earning a livelihood, but on the contrary, it will add to your success in this area. Given the obviousness of what has been said, there is no need for further clarification, other than to add that according to the instruction of our Rebbes, along with your own study—as mentioned above, with diligence and persistence in Nigleh and Chassidus—you should dedicate some of your time to spreading the wellsprings outward within the framework of the activities of the students of Tomchei Temimim in Lod, Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, and the like.

You surely know of the three daily portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya; at the very least, you should maintain them from here on out.

With blessings for good tidings in all that has been mentioned.

## 7,183

7,183

B"H, 4 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, whose work is the work of Heaven,
Moreinu HaRav Moshe Aryeh Leib, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 24 Teves, the Hillula of Rabbeinu HaZaken, in which you write regarding the positive shift concerning the *chiddushei Torah* of the students, may they live.

May it be Hashem’s will that this shift grow and expand, increasing in light in all matters of our Torah, the Torah of truth—*emes la'amito* (truth of truth)—to the exclusion of *din merumeh* (a deceptive judgment) [meaning, one who has not merited to clarify the cunning of the serpent, and consequently lacks *yirah*, or at the very least, lacks the *yirah* that must precede *chochmah*—which must be complete—specifically, the *yirah* that precedes]. The counsel for this is to "examine the witnesses thoroughly" (Tosafos, Megillah 15b) according to what is written, "And I will testify against them" (*va'avidah bam*), see Taanis 11a; *Likutei Torah*, *Pekudei* 4b and onward; *Biurei HaZohar*, *Shoftim*, and elsewhere. And this is simple (*kal v'chomer*). Then the *halachah* is in accordance with them, for they draw down the truth of **Hashem**—for in the beginning, "Hashem **Elokim** created," etc., and this is what the prophet says, "And Hashem Elokim is truth," as hinted at in Rambam, *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, Chapter 1, regarding *emes la'amito*; see there.

May it be His will, as we approach the day of the Hillula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the director and founder of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, that this come to fruition in deed and in truth, as mentioned above—in *emes la'amito*.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 7,184

[4 Shevat, 5720]

After a long hiatus, your letter from Erev Rosh Chodesh Shevat was received, yet even in it, the reason for the lapse in correspondence is not explained. ## 745

B"H, 4 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

I acknowledge receipt of your two letters, dated 24 Teves (and the one preceding it), which is the day of the Hillula of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and the Shulchan Aruch.

It gave me pleasure to read of your activities in spreading matters of Yiddishkeit. May it be Hashem’s will that you increase these efforts, and then some, in every place that your reach extends.

Regarding your request for details concerning the aforementioned—the method of dissemination, etc.—it is understood that one cannot set hard and fast rules, as this depends on the character of the individuals, the circumstances of the environment, and so on. In all such matters, the activist has only what his eyes see. However, we have been commanded to conduct ourselves in this regard in accordance with what is written: "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

Therefore, regarding the aforementioned, you should consult with Tzeirei Agudas Chabad and AT"H. Surely you will proceed in such a manner, as the aforementioned organizations possess experience in various circles, etc.

At an auspicious time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter. May it be Hashem’s will that you bring good tidings, and in this regard, also concerning the day of the Hillula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—that you utilize this auspicious day for Torah and mitzvos.

May it be Hashem’s will that its impression be evident throughout the entire year.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and in connection with your birthday—for a year of success in the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 7191

B”H, 6 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.
Year of the Bicentennial of the Passing of the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory

To each and every one of Anash,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Surely the day and the farbrengen of the Hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, who ascended to the supernal treasuries in the lands of the living—the tenth Hilula—will be holy (in every respect; and even more so, and primarily, through and in matters of avodah from below to above) and will draw down holiness (through and in matters of avodah from above to below) in all ten faculties of the two souls, and in the world that was created through ten utterances, by means of the ten types of human actions.

[It is a time] to make a true accounting of what has been accomplished over these ten years, to compare it to what was possible and what should have been done, and to resolve internally to fulfill and to increase, going from strength to strength.

May the merit of the Baal Hilula protect and increase success in all of the above: to disseminate, with tranquility, joy, and a good heart, the Torah and the mitzvos, and their inwardness—the maayanos—until they reach the outermost reaches, and the King Moshiach will come.

And may the prophecy be fulfilled:
"And you shall spread out to the west and to the east and to the north and to the south."

With blessings for good tidings in all that is mentioned,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7191***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 6, p. 290, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

**The tenth Hilula:** These are the words of the Baal Hilula in his letter from the year 5700: "This year is the tenth year since the ascent of my revered father, the holy Rebbe, of blessed memory, to the supernal treasuries in the lands of the living. The supernal world is like the lower world. Each person, according to his level in wisdom and knowledge, and especially in inner feeling (*tiefen gefihl*), will surely understand the superiority of the supernal world over the lower world. In the lower world, the number ten is a holy number; all the more so in the supernal world, where its holiness is an essential holiness and its superiority is an essential superiority, the number ten is holy, elevated, and sublime, even exalted" (in Kuntres 8, New York, 5700).

**Will be holy:** See Zohar Vol. III, 271a; Rabbeinu Bachya, beginning of Parshas Terumah; Mayim Rabim – 5636, ch. 32 and onwards.

**In every respect:** See Bechoros 58b.

**Of the two souls:** See Kitzurim VeHe'aros LeTanya, p. 63.

**Ten types:** See Rambam, Hilchos Deos, beginning of ch. 5.

**True (accounting):** See Torah Or 37a; Shaarei Orah, discourse beginning *Roni V'Simchi*, ch. 6.

**Internally:** See Kuntres HaAvodah, ch. 6.

**In every respect:** See below, letter 7199.

**In his letter:** In his Igros Kodesh, Vol. 2, p. 470.

## 7,127

B"H, 7 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Chaim Yitzchak, may he live.

Shalom and blessing!

In response to your letter of 27 Teves.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter. May it be His will that just as you have written your request, so too may you bring good tidings regarding it, and also regarding an increase in the study of the teachings of Chassidus within the totality of our Torah, the Torah of life. This will increase the arousal of the compassion of the master of the holy gravesite, who sacrificed his life for the dissemination of the wellsprings outward.

2) Regarding your question on the statement that "Va'ad" (ועד) is the same as "Echad" (אחד) through the transposition of letters (Zohar III, 134a): This is explained in many places, and at length in *Kovetz Lubavitch*, issue 11. The crux of the matter is that the *Aleph* and *Vav* are interchangeable among the *Ahu"i* letters, the *Ches* and *Ayin* are interchangeable among the *Acha"e* letters (the gutturals), and the large *Dalet* is interchangeable with a regular *Dalet*. The allusion in these transpositions is explained at length in *Imrei Binah*, *Shaar Krias Shema* by the Mitteler Rebbe, and in subsequent Chassidic texts.

3) Regarding what you wrote concerning the *Targum Yonasan* on *Shemos 14:21*, that on the staff were engraved, etc., and the six mothers and [others], for it is standard in many places to speak of the four mothers (Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah), and we do not call them fathers and mothers except, etc.:

It can be said simply that on the staff, it was not specifically the patriarchs that were mentioned, but rather every single tribe; therefore, they also added the mother of each one.

Enclosed is a copy of my general letter for the upcoming Yahrtzeit, 10 Shevat. May it be His will that you also bring good tidings in our midst.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned.

***
