**Va'ad is Echad:** See also above, Vol. 3, Letter 408, and the references in the notes there.
**In Kovetz Lubavitch:** And above, Vol. 2, Letter 220.
**Regarding what you wrote concerning the Targum Yonasan:** Explained at length in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 6, p. 304.

## 7188

7188

B"H, 9 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 3 Shevat, in which you write:

1) How to explain the foundations of the teachings of Chabad and its concepts to the masses.

It is understood that it is difficult to explain this with the necessary detail in a letter. Furthermore—and this is the main point—there is no need for this, as many of our anash are in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) who have been involved in this for many years. They have experience, particularly regarding the explanations suitable for the individuals and conditions of Eretz Yisrael. Our Sages have said, "There is no wise man like one with experience." Consult with these anash, and "in the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

2) Regarding the approval of your semicha certificate by the Chief Rabbinate.

It is understood that you must clarify the reason for the delay in the approval until now, and in accordance with that, fulfill what is lacking and make efforts to have it approved.

3) Relying on the beginning of your letter, that you belong to the sect and movement of the Chassidim, my hope is strong that you have fixed times for the study of Chassidus, as well as for its guidance and conduct. For regarding every part of our holy Torah—the Torah of life—it is said that study must lead to action, for action is the essential thing. And since we are not only commanded to study, but also commanded to "ascend in holiness," surely as one increases in study, there is a corresponding increase in practice. For no matter the current state of one's affairs in holiness, there is always room to add more, since we are connected to Hakadosh Baruch Hu, who is infinite.

Surely you have heard of the three daily shiurim—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and in any case, you should observe them from here on. We have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of righteous memory, whose yahrtzeit is the upcoming 10 Shevat, that they are equal for every soul and a segulah for many matters.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 745

B"H, 11 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Sunday, 9 Shevat, in which you write regarding public lecturing on matters of Kabbalah, and that you were told this is the custom of Lubavitcher Chassidim.

In our times, the concept of "Kabbalah" has become far too broad, and naturally, no one can be held responsible for what another person chooses to include under that title.

Regarding the practical reality: the people of Lubavitch and Chabad engage in the dissemination of the inner dimensions of Torah, which in our generation has been revealed through the teachings of Chassidus. In these teachings, matters explained in the books of Kabbalah are elucidated in many places. This matter is one of the fundamental tasks and efforts of the people of Chabad, as we are commanded by our Rebbes, our Nesi'im, who sacrificed themselves for the dissemination of the teachings of Chabad Chassidus—which is the very teaching of the Baal Shem Tov. There are many stories regarding the extent of their own dedication, as well as what they demanded of those who listened to their voice. They expressed their strongest hope that a bright and luminous day would come when this Torah would become the inheritance of all the children of Israel, without exception. And "inheritance" regarding Torah means study in a manner of understanding and comprehension, just like all other parts of Torah—study that leads to action.

It is surprising that, judging by the style of your letter, you seem unaware of this aforementioned activity. It is my strong hope that when you become familiar with the details of these matters in their depth and essence, you will participate and join the camp of those who dedicate themselves to the dissemination of the wellsprings of the teachings of Chassidus until they reach the "outside" (*chutzah*). May you utilize the power of your influence wherever it reaches for this stated purpose, and may Hashem grant you success.

With respect and blessings.

## 7190

B"H, 11 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 4 Shevat with the enclosure, in which you ask about the rumor that I supposedly sent a circular to all Chabad institutions and Chassidim regarding the way to write the year 5720—using a *chof kfufa* (bent *chof*) rather than a *pshuta* (straight *chof*), and that they should not dare, etc.

This style of reporting is incorrect. Rather, one of the Chabad institutions asked me toward the end of last year regarding this matter, and I wrote my opinion that it should be written with a *chof kfufa*. However, I did so for several reasons, and I did not write my opinion in the aforementioned tone—that they "should not dare."

One of the reasons is that I am not comfortable turning every single matter into a severe, stringent instruction. We have enough such matters already existing, which, for the time being, have not been accepted in some circles of *Bnei Yisrael*.

My reasons and rationale for the aforementioned writing style are primarily that the question at hand also pertains to the markings of the *simanim* (chapters) and *perakim* (sections) in our holy seforim, the page numbers in those seforim, and so on. There is a "custom in Israel" regarding this that has existed for hundreds upon hundreds of years, and it is most appropriate to consider it and conduct oneself accordingly. This is especially true when taking into account that in years past, the printing of seforim was called *meleches hakodesh* (holy work), and they related to it—and to its details—with precision. Furthermore, many printers were authorities and *baalei hora'ah* (halachic decisors) in many places where *Bnei Yisrael* resided. It is a simple matter, and everyone agrees, that regarding the *simanim* of the *Tur*, *Shulchan Aruch*, etc., it is written with a *chof kfufa*.

It is understood that there is **no** proof at all from the fact that in **isolated** places one finds it written with a *chof pshuta*. This is similar to other letters of *menatzpach*, and it is akin to the fact that sometimes *reish-nun-tav* (250) is written instead of *tav-reish-nun* (450), and there are hundreds and thousands of such examples in the *peirushim* and *michtavim* of our Sephardic brethren.

There is another reason for my aforementioned position [though, as mentioned above, the first reason is absolutely decisive in my opinion], which is what is brought in books of *remez* and *sod* (allusion and mysticism), that the letters of *menatzpach* signify numbers: a *chof pshuta* represents 500, etc. Why introduce a way of writing that contradicts this, even if we were to say it only applies to matters of *remez*?

By the way—regarding what is written in the circular enclosed with your letter concerning a *dagesh* in straight letters, the letter was received on Erev Shabbos Parshas Bo, at the conclusion of the *Haftorah* of which, there is a *chof pshuta* with a *dagesh*.

I will conclude as I began: despite all of the above, I am not comfortable making this way of writing into a fundamental, essential matter. Even if it is not as the *simanim* are marked in the *Shulchan Aruch*, as long as they fulfill what is written in those *simanim*.

With respect and blessing.

## 7191

13 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Wednesday.

I must express the doubts I had regarding whether to reply to it, as the intent behind the questions you write is not clear. However, by giving a fellow Jew the benefit of the doubt, and in accordance with the ruling of the Mishnah, my hope is strong that the intent is solely for the clarification of the truth. This is especially so in light of the known relationship of the Telshe Yeshiva—even while it was still overseas—to Lubavitch, to Chabad Chassidim, and to the study of Chassidus, and how even then there were groups of students in the Telshe Yeshiva who engaged in the study of Tanya, as is surely known to you, and even more so in this specific regard. I will address each point in order.

1) **Question:** Regarding the custom of wishing one another on 19 Kislev a "good year in the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus," you point out the consensus of Chazal that on Rosh Hashanah, a person is written and sealed for all the matters and events of the entire year.

**Response:** First, this custom has been practiced for many years, and it was printed and publicized in the United States as early as 5703, and prior to that by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding your comment concerning Rosh Hashanah, I did not understand it. Furthermore, as you yourself mention, a person is judged every day; it is obvious that this does not contradict the writing on Rosh Hashanah. This is explained in many places. See also the book *Asarah Maamarot* by the Rema MiPano, *Maamar Chakor Din*, Part 2, Chapter 1, and other places cited by Rabbeinu HaZaken in his *Likutei Torah*, end of Parshas Korach, and Rabbeinu HaZaken’s explanation on this matter. One should also note the words of the commentators on the Mishnah in Maseches Rosh Hashanah, at the beginning of Chapter 1, Mishnah 2: "The world is judged at four times," even though one of them is Rosh Hashanah. Many of the resolutions offered there can also be applied to our case.

2) You also remark, based on the above, why this custom does not also apply on the festival of Shavuos, which is the general Matan Torah, regarding the entirety of Torah.

**Response:** The above is understood and is also simple, based on the precision that Hashem did not establish a fixed date for the festival of Shavuos on the day of Matan Torah. For Shavuos sometimes falls on a Thursday, sometimes on a Friday, and sometimes on a Shabbos. It is only when we sanctify the months based on calculation that it falls on the time of Matan Torah (see *Responsa of the Rivash*, Siman 96; *Shulchan Aruch* of Rabbeinu HaZaken, beginning of Siman 494). Many reasons have been brought for this, and most, if not all, relate specifically to the Matan Torah of the **generality** of Torah. See *Torah Sheleimah* by Rabbi M. Kasher, in the supplements to Parshas Yisro, *Kuntres Zeman Matan Torateinu*, where he collects this from many books. In addition to the above, one can also say, quite simply, that the first Tablets did not endure, and the time of the second Tablets is Yom Kippur—a holy and awesome day, the day of the sealing in the three books, etc.—and as the Mishnah expounds, "on the day of his wedding," which refers to Matan Torah.

3) Regarding the fact that 19 Kislev is referred to as the "Chag HaChagim" (Festival of Festivals), you note that if so, it is a greater festival than Shavuos, and how can that be?

**Response:** This title—borrowed from the *Tikkunei Zohar*—has also been used for many years, for decades, and was publicized in the United States in the year mentioned above. Your comment is resolved by the precision of the term: it is the festival **of the festivals** specifically. The meaning is not as you suggest—that it is an additional festival—but rather the opposite, as is understood from the expression in the *Tikkunei Zohar*, Tikkun 21 (end of 59b), which states: "A festival **in all** times and holidays, the festival **of the three festivals**." The Vilna Gaon explains there that this refers to the middle point, which is what is revealed on Shabbos and Yom Tov. That is, it is the middle point **of** the festivals. See also the book *Be'er Lachai Ro'i*. The matter is also understood according to the revealed Torah, for the essence of the festivals is **simcha** (see *Chagigah* 10b), which connects the "for you" with the "for Hashem." As Chazal rule, there is no simcha except with meat, and specifically the meat of the *chagigah* offering—which is why in our time, there is no simcha except with wine (see the precise language of Rabbeinu HaZaken—the author of the Tanya—in his *Shulchan Aruch*, Siman 529, Section 7).

This is one of the foundations of the teachings of Chassidus, as emphasized in many places by the Baal Shem Tov and his students after him, and Rabbeinu HaZaken and his students after him: the concept of serving Hashem **with joy**. Another foundation is the service of Hashem with the **body**, not through fasts and self-affliction, as is the well-known interpretation of the verse, "If you see the donkey of your enemy" (referring to the materiality of the body), "you shall surely help **with him**" (and not by rejecting it or through self-affliction).

The significance of 19 Kislev is that our Rebbe was redeemed to freedom **below** because permission was granted **from above** to disseminate the teachings of Chassidus and its guidance.

For "a person does not bruise his finger..."—this means that from above, they agreed to the dissemination of this specific path, and this is the middle point of all the festivals.

4) You mention in a note that the Griz (Rabbi Chaim Soloveitchik) of Brisk and Rabbi Chaim Ozer of Vilna related to this matter with great respect, and you remark that this is not understood and ask for the source of this report.

Regarding the attitude of the aforementioned toward 19 Kislev and its significance, including the fact that it is a Rosh Hashanah for Chassidim and the teachings of Chassidus, this was printed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe—a copy from his records in the year 5662, at the time when the letter of his father, the Rebbe, regarding 19 Kislev was publicized and reached Vilna, etc. It was printed by his instruction in 5703, in the introduction to *Kuntres U'Maayan*. Surely you are aware of the very frequent meetings that took place between the three aforementioned individuals, in friendly relations, and not only regarding communal affairs. It is a pity that the public is not aware of this in the necessary detail, for then, most certainly, many sayings, refutations, questions, and differences of opinion—which do not always have their foundation in holiness—would have been nullified. And the wise will understand.

May it be the will of Hashem that in our near future, we merit the fulfillment of the prophecy that "Torah scholars increase peace in the world," and all the more so in their own special world, the world of Torah, and the fulfillment of the final ruling of the Oral Torah: "The Holy One, Blessed be He, found no vessel that holds blessing for Israel other than peace."

With respect and blessing.

P.S.
Certainly, if you have any comments, I would be pleased to receive them. As it has already been said, "And Vehav in Suph."

## 6,192

B"H, 14 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in the needs of the community,
R' Yehuda Zarchia Mordechai Leib Chaim, may he live.

Shalom and blessing!

After a long interval, your letter from the 5th of Shevat was received, which also included a report of the farbrengen of the bright and auspicious day, 19 Kislev. May it be the will [of Hashem] that its impression be evident throughout the entire year, and specifically in the inner point and the task of all those who have influence over Yisrael in this generation: the spreading of the wellsprings outward.

Regarding the style of your letter, [where you write] **that the light** could have been strong and bright, etc., and that the "leaven in the dough" hinders [the process], etc.—there is some truth in what you say, but not the whole truth. My intention is that the primary hindrance is from the **"vessels,"** meaning the actions of the person, who must draw down the Torah and its matters into every place his hand can reach. However, [you write that] the words of Torah are not received, etc.—in all of this there is some truth, for through actions performed properly and with *hiddur*, one adds to the light as well. In the language of the Zohar regarding Torah, [the goal is] "to increase it," and this is along the lines of our Sages' statement that Yisrael adds strength to the *pamalya shel ma'alah* (the Heavenly entourage), as it is written, "You will yearn for the work of Your hands."

May it be the will [of Hashem] that just as in the matter of water—for there is no water but Torah—the task is specifically to be a well of living water, so too regarding light—and there is no light but Torah—may the *ma'or* (luminary) within the Torah be the wellspring within the Torah (see *Korban HaEdah* to *Yerushalmi, Chagigah*, Chapter 1, Halacha 7), which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***6,192***

**R' Yehuda Zarchia Mordechai Leib Chaim:** Segal, Tel Aviv. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 18, 6,731, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 7193

16 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Yosef, may he live, known as Dr. Goldschmidt
Director of the Department of Religious Education, Ministry of Education

Greetings and blessings,

After the longest of intervals, I received your letter of 17 Teves, which was delayed in transit longer than usual and only recently reached me.

You are, of course, correct regarding the necessity for training and professional development in the field of teaching. Please believe me when I say that I am no less distressed than you that perfection is not more prevalent and to a greater degree, for there is no limit to the perfection of human beings—especially when the subject is education, where the influence touches every aspect of the student’s life. Surely, for someone like yourself, there is no need to elaborate on this. It is also clear that the people of Chabad in Eretz Yisrael in general, and those involved in education in particular—and above all the teachers, who, as you write, should be more perfect—recognize this and are no less distressed, perhaps even more so than I, since they come into contact with their students day after day. Therefore, it is not only certain that there is a sincere desire to improve as much as possible, but this also strengthens the hope for their success in this endeavor.

I must respond to one more point in your letter, which I believe we touched upon during our conversation when you were here: that in our era, which is full of revolutions and shifting values, while one must certainly not waive the minimum requirements for a teacher and educator, beyond that minimum, it is more important that the teacher possess a firm worldview, characterized by dedication and self-sacrifice for all the sanctities of our people, which is reflected in his own way of life. For then, he has the ability to instill a firm stance in his student as well, so that he will not be confused by the changes and upheavals in the street—and sometimes even at home—which are, in the style of our Sages, like the "suffering of the sling," sometimes swinging from one extreme to the other, which the student encounters frequently, from the far left to the far right.

My hope remains strong, based on our conversation and also from what I read in your letter—between the lines, at any rate—that your sympathy for Chabad education has not diminished; on the contrary. The same applies to your assistance and support, which remains firm in every respect. From this also follows the result of viewing the teacher not only in his current state, but in his state after his effort and striving to improve, out of dedication and self-sacrifice for his holy work in education, on the purity of holiness.

I reiterate that it is not my intention to exempt anyone from the effort to improve and increase their training, but rather to clarify the situation and, as mentioned, to put this perspective in writing once again, as a matter of principle: that in order for one’s wisdom to endure, one’s fear of Heaven must precede one’s wisdom. This accurate calculation is evident at all levels, especially in elementary schools.

Regarding what you write about a high school or secondary education within the framework of Chabad educational institutions, I do not see the possibility of a complete high school within the aforementioned framework for many reasons. On this matter, I feel an obligation to clarify my view further: in my opinion, there is no place to mix studies in a high school curriculum within the framework of a yeshiva, which must be entirely holy to Hashem through the study of Torah and its mitzvos. To such an extent that if there are individual students or a type of student who, for whatever reason, must be taught a high school curriculum as well, it must be done outside the walls of the yeshiva. [However, in Chabad, for several reasons, this matter is not on the agenda, at least for the time being.] There are already enough confusions and blurring of values that we are unable to rectify, without adding another area of confusion and a mixture of matters that are not, by their nature, meant to be mixed, and whose blending does not work well at all. The exceptions to this are vocational schools, such as the printing and trade schools in Kfar Chabad, but not a yeshiva.

Since we are today in the aftermath of Rosh Hashanah La'ilanot, and the verse states that "man is the tree of the field," I was reminded of the New Year’s blessing I sent you, which I hope you received in time, and primarily—that it be fulfilled in its entirety.

With respect and blessing,

## 7,194

B"H, 16 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi Avraham, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 11 Shevat, the day after the Yahrtzeit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you and all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of the Baal HaHillula. May it be His will that just as you have brought the request, you will also share good news regarding each one of them.

Regarding your question on the statement of our Sages, "When Adar enters, we increase in joy," and the corollary that "his [the Jewish people's] fortune is healthy"—how can this be, given that it was in this month that Moshe Rabbeinu, the shepherd of Israel, passed away?

The answer is understood from the discussion in the Gemara (Megillah 13b), which notes that there was a rationale to interpret the month in question in two ways. As our Sages say there, since the lot fell in the month of Adar, etc., but the conclusion was that he did not know [the significance of the month], and this determined and decided the entire month, regarding which it is said, "And it was turned about."

Regarding your question concerning the apparent contradiction between the statement of our Sages that the passing of the righteous is as difficult as the day [the Beis Hamikdash was destroyed], and the fact that we call this day a "Hillula" (a celebration):

The later authorities have already discussed this at length, and several explanations have been offered (collected in Sdei Chemed, Asifat Dinim, Ma'arechet Eretz Yisrael, sec. 6, and in Pe'at HaSadeh there; in the book Hillula D'Rashbi by Rabbi Margolies; and see also Likutei HaShas by the Arizal on Berachos 6b; Rashi on Yevamos 122a, s.v. **Reglei**—that it is an expression of Yom Tov; and elsewhere).

With blessings for good tidings.

## 795

16 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn

Mr. Avraham, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Although it was with some delay that the *avreichim*—the G-d-fearing, etc., may they live—conveyed to me that they visited your city and spoke with you, and that you possess influence in your city, as well as the question you asked them:

Regarding the statement of our Sages that three sounds travel from one end of the world to the other, etc., and some say even *radia*—and some wish to interpret the intent of the Gemara (*Yoma* 20b and there) as referring to radio waves—this aroused questions for you on the matter.

Now, it is impossible to interpret the Gemara as referring to the aforementioned radio waves **at all**. The name "radio" for these light waves is a matter of **convention**, which arose from the will of those who discovered these rays in the generation preceding our own, about fifty years ago. There was no necessity, nor any natural reason, that these light waves should be called specifically by this name. In fact, for **several years they were called by the name of Hertz** and the like. Consequently, there is no basis for your question, as it is not applicable to say regarding these rays what our Sages said there regarding *ridya*—see the *Aruch HaShalem* under that entry.

On this occasion, since everything is by *Hashgacha Pratis*—and the aforementioned is also included in this, by which I mean the fact that we have come into contact—it is my duty (and perhaps my privilege) to draw your attention, while asking your forgiveness, to the fact that every created being, and especially man, the choicest of all creations, must utilize all the possibilities granted to him to increase goodness, integrity, and justice in the world. As experience has shown, only then is one guaranteed that this will have endurance. [And what is even more relevant, so that one does not call the wicked righteous and the evil good, this is] only if these concepts are founded upon faith in the living G-d who leads the world **in practice**, and who oversees its affairs in their details. For were it not for this, we have seen in our own generation that the very nation whose culture was at the highest level—scientific research, philosophical systems, and furthermore, systems of ethics, etc.—was able, with the potential granted to it, to become the most horrific murderer, even from a simple perspective and even when compared to beasts of prey. Anyone who knows the deeds committed by the Germans—it would be unbelievable if we had not been witnesses to it in practice—and all in the name of justice and in accordance with the theory of ethics, etc., etc. Furthermore, among them were also those who held superstitious beliefs in "that man," etc., and together with this, they did not refrain from taking an active part in all the aforementioned deeds. I am certain that for one such as yourself, there is no need to elaborate on this. The conclusion to be drawn from contemplating the above is that, as stated, faith in the living G-d is essential [and not an abstract faith, that He is found in the seventh heaven and is not interested in what happens in this lower world, or that He only oversees things in a general sense and has no interest at all in the details of matters, which is liable to—and we have seen that in many cases it indeed did—lead to the aforementioned delusions, for the inclination of man's heart is evil from his youth, etc.]. We have no refuge or security to walk safely on the path of good and integrity except through a simple faith, which is also strong, in "I am Hashem your G-d who brought you out of the land of Egypt." From this comes the absolute consequence: "You shall have no other gods" of any kind. This aforementioned faith will lead to practical *mitzvos* in action, extending into daily life, such as "Remember the Shabbos day, etc." And then, only then, are we assured that we also fulfill "You shall not murder," "You shall not covet," etc.

Since, as the *avreichim*—may they live—told me, you are gifted with influence in a fairly wide circle, may it be His will that you utilize this influence in the aforementioned direction, and the merit of the many will assist you.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

## 7,190

B"H, 18 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Shimon, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

Following the longest of intervals, I received your letter from 3 Shevat, along with the two *pidyonos nefesh* enclosed with it, which will be read at a time of favor at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you and your wife, may she live, work with *mesiras nefesh* and dedication within the framework of the activities of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for which you will be remembered at his holy *tziyun*, in accordance with the needs of the institution and the matters therein. Certainly, this is also for your own benefit, for your activities are the channel and the vessels for receiving the blessings of Hashem, through an added *hisorerus* from the one who rests at the holy *tziyun*. Surely, for one such as you, elaboration on this is superfluous; I will only add that there is nothing that can stand before the will—when one truly wills it.

It is surprising that you do not mention the auspicious day, the *yom hilula*, and I hope that you participated in it and in its activities. May it be the will [of Hashem] that the impression of the *farbrengen* be evident throughout the entire year.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7,197

B.H., 18 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 13 Shevat: It is understandable that there is surprise and wonder that you have not written anything regarding the day of the Hilula and the farbrengen, for surely there was something to report about that day. Even though you have become accustomed to not writing on such occasions, there is no established precedent for such conduct, as it does not align with what our Rebbeim, our leaders, desired for the conduct of Anash. This is well known from the Alter Rebbe regarding this, and so on, up to the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of saintly memory, the master of the Hilula.

Regarding the content of your letter concerning the shidduch: I believe I have already expressed my wonder at the haste, which primarily concerns the age of your daughter, may she live. Furthermore, your letter states that "she is a very good teacher, and in order to receive the appropriate certification, she must study for more time." Moreover—and this is the main point—your idea that she should become engaged now, with the wedding taking place in a year and a half or two years, is not appropriate at all. These generations are not like the early days, and one should not confuse a young woman of her age with thoughts of an engagement for such a long period until the wedding. It is also understood that a wedding in a few months is also not the right approach, and it seems that you also sense this.

Based on the above, leave her to her studies and her holy work in chinuch al taharat hakodesh. May Hashem increase her success in her affairs, and after a year or more, you can take an interest in matters of shidduchim.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S. As you requested, the letter is being sent without waiting for its turn.

## 7,198

B"H, 18 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the fourth night [of Chanukah] which was received in due course (which was apparently sent via regular mail), in which you write regarding the prisoner who does not wish to submit a petition for clemency, so that it will not be construed as an admission of guilt for a crime of which he is innocent.

It seems to me that in such a case, the petition can be submitted by his wife or one of the family members, which negates the interpretation that submitting a petition implies an admission of guilt.

In the present case, where the family is in need of financial support, etc., the negation of the aforementioned interpretation is even more understandable. Furthermore, it should be explained to the prisoner that certainly, once he is outside, he will be able to prove his innocence more easily and more quickly.

Some time ago, I received regards from you via Mr. ... And although you do not write anything regarding yourself, my hope is that everything is in order and peaceful with you, and that the merit of your avodah in holiness—which is founded upon ahavas Yisrael, for "love your fellow as yourself" is one and the same with "love Hashem your G-d," as is known the interpretation of our Alter Rebbe on this, founded in the teachings of Chassidus which is the very teaching of the Baal Shem Tov—will stand by you in all that was mentioned, and for further growth, with proper health and peace of mind and body.

With respect and blessings for good tidings.

#### ***7,198***

From a copy.

**Interpretation of our Alter Rebbe:** See also above, Vol. 16, Letter 6,004, and the references in the notes there. Vol. 18, Letter 6,733.

## 699

19 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the distinguished Chossid, who toils in the vineyard of Hashem, etc.,
Rabbi Sh. Y. [Zevin], may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the eve of Shabbos Parshas Shirah, following a break in your correspondence that was quite unusual, which had already caused me concern. Perhaps the reason for this was what you wrote at the end of your letter regarding the passing of your brother, a”h.

May it be the will of Hashem that from here on, you shall only report good news, in a way that is visibly and revealedly good.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the question of the Chief Rabbinate — it is understood that I agree with your decision, for the reasons you wrote and for many others besides. I am grateful for the details you provided on this matter.

Yesterday, a few hours before receiving your letter, I was visited by representatives of the Claims Conference, and also by Rabbi Yehoshua Hutner, separately and without either knowing of the other. Naturally, I spoke with both of them regarding the Talmudic Encyclopedia. The aforementioned representatives reiterated their position that they value the project and wish to assist, but they expressed a desire for it to appear more frequently, implying that this is also a factor in limiting the increase of the funding.

When I presented the argument to Rabbi Y. [Hutner], he said that the two matters are not dependent on one another, because increasing the budget is extremely important even for the preparation of the entries; as the number of those working on it increases, the preparation of the entries will progress. To my question as to what the benefit is, given that this is the first draft of the entry, and you wrote to me that the pace at which the volumes appear is quite rapid relative to the possibilities, he replied that he hopes that as the writers of the entries become more accustomed and involved in the work, the time you need to dedicate to editing the entry, or to correcting and improving it—up to rewriting it entirely—will be reduced. He further added that, supposedly, in the first draft, entries have already been written up to the letter *Ayin*, and if the funding is sufficient, it is to be hoped that within three or four years—the duration of the Claims Conference’s current operation—they will be able to complete the aforementioned first draft entirely.

Naturally, I do not know the accuracy of this statement, but I told him on the spot that, knowing the outlook of the people at the Conference, this announcement would make the best possible impression on them—the announcement of both details: that there is already a first draft up to the letter *Ayin* [and there is room to say they will want proof of the truth of this], and even more so the addition that there is a plan to complete the writing of this first draft within three or four years. We agreed that as the time for submitting requests approaches, they will inform me of the situation, and perhaps they will also send a copy of the application they intend to send to the Claims Conference.

I would be grateful to you if you would also inform me of the current situation, and also, confidentially, whether there are among those participating in the aforementioned work in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established, those who are progressing from time to time in the aforementioned manner, such that it would ease your work and increase the pace of the volumes’ appearance.

Regarding what you wrote about "the tenth shall be holy" in any case—that when there are nine, a tenth is revealed from above—it seems from your style that you wish to compare this to the matter of "you shall count fifty days," even though in practice, in speech, one only counts forty-nine.

Seemingly, the concept of *mimaila* (happening of its own accord) is found only in the number fifty (in the Sefiros — the Sefirah of Binah), and not in the number ten (the Sefirah of Malchus). As with all matters of the inner dimension of Torah, this too has a parallel (a reflection) in the revealed dimension of Torah. This is that the *holiness* of the fiftieth day comes about in a completely *mimaila* manner (and it is precise to say the **holiness** of the fiftieth day — for surely the intention is not to the time that comes *mimaila*, as there is no practical difference regarding the fiftieth day compared to the days preceding it). This is unlike the tithe (*maaser*), where there is at least an action, only that: a) it is not the action of a human, but of the object being made holy, and b) it is not a human action but that of an animal — exiting the pen (a change of place) [or exiting the general group — through the counting of the person].

Seemingly, based on the matters explained in Chassidus, one should explain "the tenth shall be holy" in any case through the concept that resolves why in *Sefer Yetzirah* only three elements are mentioned, and not the element of earth, because it is included in the three. When one boils water over fire, and the air separates and connects them, the combined action of these three reveals the earthiness within the water, and this is not the place to elaborate. Especially since I have not yet found this explicitly stated.

I will conclude with something similar to the opening of your letter. I noticed that you wrote *Tash’ch* (5720) with a *chof k’fufah* (a bent *chof*). I deserve credit for having already answered this to those who asked me, and afterwards I heard that even regarding the *chof peshuta* (straight *chof*) and the *chof k’fufah* (bent *chof*), a dispute is igniting in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established! See *Likutei Torah*, Shir HaShirim 35c; *Responsa Hashiv Moshe*, section 1.

Enclosed is a copy of a letter I wrote to someone else not long ago.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, in both general and specific matters alike,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7100

7100

B"H, 23 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 20 Shevat and the one preceding it, I will address your questions in the order they were written.

1) Based on the teaching, "Love your fellow as yourself," which is a great principle of the Torah, it is understood that a Jewish person must take an interest in what is happening with his fellow Jew, especially in the language of the verse, "They helped every man his neighbor."

2) Regarding my manner of answering questions: We are commanded to provide a clear answer, as our Sages have taught. Sometimes this comes with elaboration—that is, an example or a lesson related to the matter—and sometimes it pertains directly to the question itself. Not all personal matters and circumstances are the same in this regard.

3) Regarding the "bnei aliyah" (those of high spiritual standing) whom you found in one circle and you feel are not present in another:
It is surprising, for you are surely familiar with the instruction of our Sages to view every single one of the Jewish people with a favorable eye. You are also familiar with the ruling of the Mishnah: "Who is wise? He who learns from **every** person" [see also the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov on this, printed in the *Zichronos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the appendices at the end, page 444]. It is obvious that many people have even glaring faults, yet the statement of the Mishnah applies to them as well. The intention is to learn from their positive qualities, not from their faults, even when the fault is prominent. This is a general answer regarding my stance on the question. More specifically: the principle that "if one has two hundred, he also has one hundred" is understood and simple in all areas. The result is that if there is a circle that, in addition to all the studies of the second circle, also studies the subject of fear of Heaven, it is impossible according to sound logic that specifically by **adding** this study, the results of the general study will be **diminished**. Especially since the study of our holy Torah is a study that leads to action; that is, it is impossible from the outset for the situation to be as you describe it. Since it seems so to you, it is likely that the reason is as mentioned at the beginning of this section: when you meet an *maskil*—someone whose primary occupation is intellectual study—you look for *oved* qualities in him at the highest level, and when you meet an *oved*, you look for *maskil* qualities in him.

4) Regarding your question of whether you should strive to connect and correspond with a certain individual: It is understood and simple that since you find in him several positive qualities from which you can learn, the correspondence is worthwhile.

5) Regarding the feeling during *davening* concerning the evil that one wishes to remove: As explained, this is from the "hidden supernal *chesadim*" (*Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Alter Rebbe).
As I wrote in my previous letter, the matter of *davening* and requesting the removal of [evil] is explained in many places, and furthermore, it is a core component of *davening*. This does not contradict what is explained there; for a person must *daven* that all the aforementioned be removed from him. If the matter has already occurred, then one must accept it with joy as a "perceived good," since it has come into actuality, and it is certainly from the "good of the hidden world." But before it is known whether his *davening* will be accepted, it is possible that it is due to some cause. If he *davens*, the cause will be nullified and he will not be forced to the "cleansing" mentioned in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 22, since the "excrement of the daughters of Zion" was nullified through his *davening* and request. See there in *Iggeres HaKodesh* where it is written that one should not flee or seek help and an advocate, but it does not at all negate a son’s request to his Father Himself. On the contrary, that is the essence, as in the well-known *davening* text: "And what I have sinned before You, wipe away in Your abundant mercies, but not through..."—which is the point mentioned above.

6) Whether it is permissible to evaluate your friend, whether he is an *oved* or not: It is understood that it is permissible **if** there is a benefit in it for yourself or for your friend. See the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov on the statement, "Who is wise," noted above.

7) It is understood that by contemplating specific matters, one can explain them to the intellect as well. On the contrary, this is the essence of the *avodah* of *davening* and the *avodah* of man in general: that it should be "with all your heart"—with both your inclinations—and the Torah and *mitzvos* must be as they relate to matters on earth, for "it is not in heaven."

8) Advice for contemplation or for being moved by the meaning of the words: It is understood that when you add to the time, the feeling also grows. Another point: when it is not possible to add to the time, one should divide the contemplation into several sessions. As is known from the story of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the *avodah* of a certain type of *Chassidim*—that every day they would contemplate a specific part of the *davening* with deep contemplation, and the following day they would continue with another part.

9) Regarding your statement that you are in doubt as to my attitude toward the conduct of a certain person who gathers... etc.: It is surprising and also distressing that you suspect me of such a thing. My intention concerns the matter where there is an explicit ruling in the *Shulchan Aruch* regarding "a woman's voice" etc., or mixed gatherings, etc. What makes the surprise even greater is that I have written and emphasized many times that this is one of the fundamental points in the Torah of Hashem and His *mitzvos*, and especially the Torah of Chassidus, which explains that there must be love for all creatures and one must bring them closer to the Torah, and not, Heaven forbid, bring the Torah closer to them and change it to suit them. I have also added that all rulings in the Torah are the will of the *Ribono shel Olam* [and this is explicit in our holy Torah, and especially in Chabad Chassidus in many places], and it is understood and simple that a mortal cannot, Heaven forbid, make a trade out of the will of the *Ribono shel Olam*, etc.

At a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, so that whatever you decide regarding the children's camp, it will be with success in all respects.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 217

B"H, Tuesday, 25 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Shomrei Shabbos Gemilas Chasadim Society of Brooklyn, N.Y.
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

I received with pleasure the news that the Society is holding a Melaveh Malkah on the evening of Shabbos, Parshas Im Kesef Talveh Es Ami, the eve of Rosh Chodesh Adar, to strengthen one another in your holy work of Gemilas Chasadim. This is the very attribute of the Creator of the world and its Guide, as per the instruction of Chazal to walk in the ways of the Ribono shel Olam. They further added that the Torah begins with Gemilas Chasadim, as it is written: "And Hashem Elokim made garments of skin for Adam and his wife, and He clothed them" (Sotah 14a, see there).

Furthermore, the great commentators explained that this verse teaches us of His (the Ribono shel Olam's) love and compassion for His creations; that even though they had sinned, He did not cease to cherish them, and He Himself exerted effort in their rectification and in Gemilas Chasadim. They emphasized that this intent is according to the literal meaning of the verse (Rabbeinu Bachya, Bereishis 3:21).

Based on this, it is also understood why our Rebbes, the Nesi'im—beginning with the Baal Shem Tov (this year being the bicentennial of his passing and Hillula), his students, the Alter Rebbe, and so on, up to the Nasi of our generation, my father-in-law, the Rebbe—placed such extraordinary emphasis on the matter of Ahavas Yisrael for every single person, even those referred to merely as "creatures" (see Tanya, Chapter 32).

May it be the will of Hashem that each and every one, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, fulfills all that is incumbent upon them—in the path of Gemilas Chasadim, as well as in the path of Torah and Avodah, and the Iskafya of the Sitra Achra (the primordial serpent) and its Is'hapcha.

In this, too, one follows in the ways of the Ribono shel Olam, as explained in the Targum Yonasan ben Uziel on the aforementioned verse, that "Hashem Elokim made... garments of honor from the skin of the serpent that He had stripped from it" (see Reshimot of the Tzemach Tzedek—in Sefer Derech Emunah—on the aforementioned verse).

Through this, the commandment at the beginning of the weekly Parsha we are entering will be fulfilled: "And they shall make Me a sanctuary, and I will dwell among them"—as explained at length in the Hemshech *Basi L'Gani* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Hemshech of his day of Hillula.

With blessings for success and for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 614

B"H, 25 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn

To the avreich, the G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent, whose work is the work of Heaven, etc.,
R' Naftali, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and Blessing!

After a very, very long interruption, your letter was received, which you began writing on 10 Shevat, the day of the Hilula, and which was apparently sent many days after that.

May it be the will of Hashem that you continue to bring good tidings, in accordance with the ruling of our Sages: "Good to Heaven, good to people, and good to the one who produces fruit," and may this be in a manner of "increasing and continuing, increasing and illuminating."

Surely, from 10 Shevat until the day your letter was sent, many things have been added, and especially up until the day this letter was received. This is particularly true since this year is the bicentennial of the passing and Hilula of the Baal Shem Tov, and the days between the Hilula, the days of the month of Adar, and the days of Purim and those that follow, are days that are transformed (in those days, at this time, the matters of the *sitra achra*) into joy and a Yom Tov, etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that these influences continue throughout the entire year and in all worldly matters, by having them drawn down into all matters of the *nefesh* (as is known, the concept that creation is divided into *olam, shanah, nefesh*), and this is understood.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for good tidings in all the above.

P.S.

Regarding what you wrote about the *shoshvinin* on the side of the bride, may she live: if there are no specific customs in their family, it is advisable that in addition to the *shoshvinin* couple, the groom should also be accompanied by her mother, may she live, and her husband, may he live.

It is well known and publicized that our custom is for the groom to wear a *kittel* under the *chupah*. Because of this, on Yom Kippur in the year of his wedding, he does not wear a *kittel*, and he begins doing so in the following year.

It is also understood that under the *chupah*, as well as during the *Mincha* service beforehand in which he recites *Al Chet*, and from the *chupah* onwards, he must wear a *gartel* during his *davening*. Surely you are also aware of the custom to untie all knots in the groom’s clothing (such as a necktie or shoelaces, and the like), and that the groom should not have money, gold, or precious stones, etc., in his pockets at the time of the *kiddushin*.

## Zera

B"H, 25 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the eve of the second day.

It is a well-known custom in Israel that regarding the time and place of the wedding, the families of the bride and groom should discuss it between themselves. May it be His will that whatever they decide, it should be at a propitious and successful time and in a propitious and successful place. Once they have decided on these matters, they can then decide regarding the necessary papers and documents (naturally, in consultation with the lawyers who handle such matters).

It is understood, and indeed simple, that the suggestion that he should at least complete the first part of Yoreh Deah and receive semicha is very correct. This does not pertain to the matter of his material livelihood. It is also understood that one should not postpone the aforementioned study until after the wedding; rather, he should begin as soon as possible, and in the course of time, he will be able to decide when he will complete it. After all, there is a strong hope (based on the halachic ruling regarding a shochet, which requires it anyway) that he is already proficient in the laws of shechita, etc., and this is an important part of the first section of Shulchan Aruch Yoreh Deah.

It is my hope that he has fixed times for the study of Chassidus every single day, with an increase on Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem, as the necessity of this matter is explained in many places.

Regarding the apartment - it is understood that he should prepare a temporary apartment, and together they will choose a permanent apartment later.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 690

B"H, 27 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, R' Shaul Yissachar, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 24 Teves, the day of the Hilula of Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya—the arbiter of the *nistar* (hidden) dimension of Torah—and the author of the Shulchan Aruch—the arbiter of the *nigleh* (revealed) dimension of Torah—

Regarding what you wrote concerning the reading of "Vayechal" on a public fast day and similar matters:

I have not heard any oral instructions on this. As for what I have found in the responsa and *reshimos* of our Rebbes, and in the *Acharonim*, I have brought the conclusion and the custom regarding this in the *Likkut Minhagim* printed at the end of the *Reshimas Megillas Eichah*. Please see there, as well as the footnotes for the sources. I would add what has come to my attention since that printing: *Responsa Tzafnas Paneach*, Part II, Siman 31; and *Responsa Minchas Yitzchak* by Rabbi Weiss, may he live, of Manchester, Siman 65. In any case, we have nothing to follow but the halachic ruling of the Tzemach Tzedek, for in every place we are in the *atra derav* (the domain of our Rebbe).

Thank you for the *sefer* *Mishmeres Shalom* which you published. May it be G-d’s will that for many more years you continue to publicize the customs of the students of the Baal Shem Tov and their students, as part of the general *hafatzas hamaayanos* (spreading of the wellsprings), as written in the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of the Baal Shem Tov, until they reach "outward" (*chutza*). Through this, we hasten the coming of Malka Meshicha, as explained in the aforementioned *Iggeres HaKodesh*.

And finally, it was a pleasure to receive regards from you through your son, Rabbi Avraham Yehoshua, may he live, and through him I also received regards from our fellow Jews, may they live, who are there—*v'da l'ma'in* (and the wise will understand). May it be G-d’s will that you and your wife, may she live, bring good news regarding the true good in all your affairs. In this, of course, and quite simply, a traditional Jew receives *nachas* from his children and descendants, may they live.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 719

B"H, 28 Shevat, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Chaim Yosef Shlomo, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

...And as we find ourselves in close proximity to the month of Adar, which is a month of success for the Jewish people in all their affairs, may it be the will [of Hashem] that it brings good tidings regarding all the matters about which you write, both in terms of the health of the soul and the body alike. This is also explained in the teachings of Chassidus, and the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov is well known—especially as this year is the bicentennial of his passing and hillula—regarding the verse "When you see... you shall surely release it with him," specifically with the body.

With blessings for good tidings.

Regarding what you noted in Bava Kamma, Mishnah, Chapter 8, Mishnah 1—to resolve the commentary of Rashi regarding an *eved ivri* (Hebrew slave) being appraised, based on the note of the *Ma'adanei Yom Tov* and the *Tosafos R' Akiva Eiger*—this is also discussed in *Tiferes Yaakov* on the Mishnah there. And to comment on your note: 1) Surely even one who sells himself goes free in the Yovel year. 2) The explanation of the Mishnah must be equal for the Rabbis and for Rabbi Eliezer, who holds that even one who sells himself is only for six [years] (*Kiddushin* 14b). And what appears to me regarding Rashi's commentary—that he rejects the interpretation that he is appraised like a *eved kenaani* (Canaanite slave)—is that the Jewish people do not have this valuation, since it is forbidden to make him perform the work of a slave; rather, one is commanded regarding him, "it is good for him with you," and more. Therefore, he explains it specifically as a *eved kenaani*, and as per the note (question) of the *Ma'adanei Yom Tov*—one appraises the difference between selling in parts and selling all at once, and one deducts this. *V'kal l'havin* (and it is easy to understand).

#### 719

R' Chaim Yosef Shlomo: Grunwald, Jerusalem.

## 711

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification regarding your birthday:

You have surely followed the custom of Anash in recent times: giving tzedakah on your birthday before Shacharis and Mincha—or on the preceding day if the birthday falls on Shabbos or Yom Tov—and studying an additional shiur in both Nigleh and Chassidus. [You should also] receive an aliyah to the Torah on your birthday or on the Shabbos preceding it, and study the three daily shiurim—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—on your birthday.

May it be the will of Hashem that this be a year of success for you in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos with hiddur.

With blessings for Torah study with yiras shamayim,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

You are surely aware of the three daily shiurim that are appropriate for every soul—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and you should maintain them from here on.

Regarding your request for advice on how to avoid wasting time: memorize the entire first se'if of Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim, siman 1.

Review it from time to time, and also become proficient by heart in several chapters of Mishnayos, and at the very least, one chapter of Tanya. Consult with your mashpia regarding which chapters [to choose].

## 7117

B"H, 5 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the Vaad Neshei Chabad in Kfar Chabad,
May Hashem grant them life.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of 19 Shevat,

In general, the proposal to publish a booklet for Neshei Chabad in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) is correct. It is understood that it must be in the language spoken by the majority of the Jewish women and girls in Eretz Yisrael, for the purpose of the Neshei U’Bnos Chabad organization is to bring Jewish women and girls from all circles closer, in a manner that is ever-increasing.

However, it would also be worthwhile to include a section in Yiddish, as well as in the Arabic language spoken by our Jewish sisters of Sephardic descent who have immigrated from Morocco, etc.

But there is a twofold condition: that the material for the booklet be prepared with calm deliberation and not in haste at all. Since some booklets have already been published here by the Neshei Chabad of this place, which you surely have in your possession, this will certainly facilitate the planning, preparation, and publication, even though there are surely details that need to be changed from the booklet here to suit the conditions of Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that the desire of Hashem will succeed in your hands, to expand the Neshei U’Bnos Chabad organization in cooperation with the other Chabad institutions in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), and may this be with tranquility, joy, and goodness of heart.

The great value and importance of the participation of Jewish women and girls is also emphasized by the upcoming days of Purim, which involved a miracle through Queen Esther and Mordechai the Jew, as related in the accounts of Chazal regarding this.

With blessings for good tidings and success in all that is mentioned.

## Z'riach

B"H, 9 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Committee of the Chabad Housing Project in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be built and established speedily in our days by Mashiach Tzidkeinu,
May they live,

Peace and blessing,

With pleasure and joy, I received the news regarding the "laying of the cornerstone for the Chabad housing project to be established, G-d willing, in the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt."

May it be the will of Hashem that the laying of the stone be at a propitious and successful time, and that the housing project be built, established, and completed in Chabad, and that all its matters be fulfilled speedily, at a propitious and successful time.

May this housing project be built by the Builder of Jerusalem, such that every house within it will be a "great house," according to the opinion of our Sages—a house where Torah is grown, where tefillah is grown, and where the one who dwells and uses it is "great," for "to him [is]... this Torah," which begins with acts of kindness and ends with acts of kindness.

May these homes be founded, built, and conducted according to the teachings of Chabad Chassidus, which is the very teaching of the Baal Shem Tov (this year being the two-hundredth year since his passing and hilula).

And in each one of them, and in the housing project as a whole, may the verse be fulfilled: "And I will dwell among them"—within each and every one. This is in accordance with the explanation of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe: He dwells and is enclothed within each one to give him life and sustain him, etc., he and all that he has.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with the desire of our Rebbeim, the Chabad housing project will be a place from which the wellsprings spread throughout the entire surrounding area and beyond, in a manner of "going and spreading, going and shining," until the prophecy is fulfilled that Jerusalem will spread over the entire Land of Israel, and the Land of Israel over the entire world.

With blessings for success in all the above, and regards to all the participants, may they live, in the laying of the cornerstone of the Chabad housing project.

P.S.
Regarding the manner of laying the cornerstone: The marking of the foundation—the beginning of the building—has a basis in many places in our Torah, our Torah of life. Furthermore, it is also accompanied by Hallel and thanksgiving to Hashem, "for He is good, for His kindness endures forever toward Israel." In the language of the Zohar (Vol. III, 50a): "When one begins to build, one must mention with one's mouth that it is for the service of the Holy One, blessed be He, that one is building... and then Divine assistance rests upon it, and the Holy One, blessed be He, calls peace upon it."

Based on the words of our Sages, "You shall walk in His ways; just as He, etc."—and the Holy One, blessed be He, looked into the Torah and created the world, the beginning of which was the Even Shetiyah (Foundation Stone) from which it was founded, etc.—it is understood, and indeed simple, that prior to the laying of the stone, words of Torah should be spoken. Based on the above, these should be words of Torah that speak of the matters of a house and a dwelling, a significant portion of which can be found in the Chabad discourses on the verse "A Psalm, a song for the dedication of the house."

The act of laying the stone—based on the words of our Sages that the world exists only by the breath of the mouths of school children, a breath that has no sin—it is appropriate that it be done by school children (see Hilchos Talmud Torah by the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 1, Section 3).

Likewise, according to the verse, "Thus said the L-rd G-d: Behold, I am laying in Zion a stone, a tested stone, a precious cornerstone, a firm foundation," it is proper that the cornerstone be specifically a stone that is "by the hands of Heaven" (even though afterwards one may add mortar, etc., matters that are by the hands of man). This also corresponds to the matter in spirituality—that the beginning and foundation of every building and endeavor is the granting of strength from Above, an *is'arusa d'leila*.

Furthermore, I would note that I have heard a rumor that there are those who, at the time of laying a cornerstone, write the matter on a scroll—some are particular that it be written in *ksav ashuri*, etc.—and place the scroll upon or under the cornerstone. Beyond the well-known responsum of the Rambam regarding the sanctity of *ksav ashuri*, etc., however the writing may be, one should refrain—especially in this generation—from introducing new customs, unless a firm foundation for them can be found in our Torah, our Torah of life. In the phrasing of our Sages: "Anyone who adds to this, detracts" from the affection and importance of the accepted customs of Israel, which are themselves Torah.

## Zrit

B"H, 10 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interruption, your letter from Tuesday arrived, along with the enclosure.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you once again at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the contents of your letter.

In response to your question regarding wine for the Arba Kosos: when you speak with your doctor, he will permit you to make juice from boiled grapes. Ask him whether it is better with sugar (naturally, Kosher for Pesach sugar) or entirely without sugar. Orange juice is not to be considered at all for use for the Arba Kosos.

Regarding the medications you need to take, you should ask the doctor to write you a prescription and send it to Dr. Seligson at the address provided below. Hopefully, he will be able to arrange it in a way that it is Kosher for Pesach; the sooner you do this, the easier it will be to process.

With blessings for a joyous Purim and for health.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6220

B"H, 10 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rav Gedalya, may he live and be well,

Shalom and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 8th of Adar.

May it be the will of Hashem that from this point forward, neither you nor any of the members of your family, may they live and be well, shall know any sorrow or distress, and that you may find only goodness and kindness all your days.

In this, it is understood and also simple that your matters of livelihood will be arranged as they should be, in a manner of tranquility and honor, and may you bring good tidings regarding yourself and every one of your family, may they live and be well, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed.

With blessings to him and to the entire family, may they live and be well.

P.S.

Regarding what you wrote about the prayer recited after learning that is printed in the Siddurim — I have not seen it customary among anash to recite it.

Regarding the recitation of Tachanun during Mincha, it is our well-known custom to recite it (except, of course, on those days noted in the Siddur of the Alter Rebbe before "U'va L'Tzion"). This is in line with what I once heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the day of a Yahrtzeit, where our custom is to recite Tachanun. He quoted the Tzemach Tzedek: "When else is there such a time to beseech [Hashem]?" This is similar to the case of Mincha, for our Sages have said, "A person should always be careful with the Mincha prayer, for Eliyahu was only answered during the Mincha prayer."

Regarding the additional name — please inquire with a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah* in your vicinity.

The customs for the twelve months [of mourning] and for the Yahrtzeit are printed in the *kuntreisim* for 10-13 Shevat and 2 Nissan.

## 7211

B"H, 10 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a long interval, your letter of 23 Shevat arrived, in which you write about your current state of mind and also a summary of your affairs from the past.

According to what is explained in our holy Torah, and with further elaboration in the books of mussar and Chassidus, regardless of all these matters, one must be *besimcha u’tuv levav* (with joy and a good heart). The reasons for this are explained at length, including according to logic, as it is also written in the Rambam in *Sefer Yad HaChazakah*, at the end of *Hilchos Lulav*, regarding how the fulfillment of a *mitzvah* must be. And it is written, **"In all your ways know Him,"** meaning that it must be with a good heart, and also as it is written in *Tur Orach Chaim* and *Shulchan Aruch*, Siman 231. And if this is commanded for everyone, it is even more necessary when one sees that dwelling on the conduct of the past leads to weakness in health, or to a lower quality of mood. I hope that for someone like you, there is no need to elaborate on this too much.

May the Ribono shel Olam help that from now on, you should be strong in *bitachon* in the Ribono shel Olam, who oversees each and every person with *hashgacha pratis*. He is the essence of good, and He has instructed how a Yid should conduct himself—to be calm and cheerful, and to serve Him in that manner, and also with *simcha*. It is especially necessary to conduct oneself this way when the Ribono shel Olam blesses one with family life, as the mood of the husband affects the wife and children, *sheyichyu*.

May it be His will that you report good news in this regard, especially since we are in the days before Purim, which are days of *simcha*, etc. May it be so for you, and may you continue and maintain such conduct throughout the entire year.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 622

622

B"H, 11 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 9 Adar, in which you ask where to begin regarding internal *avodah*.

In general, regarding such matters, one should articulate his thoughts and questions before his *mashpia* of *Chassidus*, and he will guide him.

In a general sense, let the contemplation written in the *Tanya*, beginning of Chapter 41, be engraved in your mind—how Hashem stands over him and examines his kidneys and heart, etc. Likewise, the matter explained in *Kuntres HaAvodah* regarding the necessity of internal and personal *avodah*. Furthermore, and most importantly, maintain the *yeshiva* schedule in *nigleh* and *Chassidus*, and the time for *davening*. This also applies to physical health, for through this, one becomes accustomed to order in daily life, and it becomes much easier for one’s *avodah* of Hashem to also be in an orderly fashion, which is the specific requirement of internal *avodah*.

I trust you are keeping the three well-known *shiurim* of *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*. It is also appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked if this has not been done within the last twelve months.

With blessings for a *Purim Sameach*.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 760

B.H., Shushan Purim, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Shalom Levin

Greetings and Blessings,

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 7th of Adar, as well as your previous ones. Naturally, I read with special interest what you write regarding the expansion of the school network, particularly for that age group not covered by general compulsory education. Although, of course, the small number of students is regrettable—at least for the time being. It is a pity that this matter apparently did not find an appropriate response; after all, in a few weeks, the problem of the long summer vacation will arise, during which many hours of idleness are added to the lives of the youth, even the youngest among them, and according to reports, only a small percentage attend summer camps and the like.

I read with special interest your note that the Teachers’ Association will hold memorial assemblies for the Baal Shem Tov. It is well known that even before he was revealed, the Baal Shem Tov’s primary avodah was in the education of Jewish children, beginning their education with words of gratitude to the Creator and Guide of the world, by teaching them to respond "Baruch Hu u’Baruch Shemo," "Amen," and the like. In the field of education, the proof of a method’s correctness is that it bears fruit and the fruits of fruit under various, and even strange, conditions.

We see clearly that over a period of two hundred years, the method of the Baal Shem Tov has encompassed hundreds upon hundreds of thousands of Jews of all circles and types. Here it is worth noting that, unfortunately, there are those who err and think that the Baal Shem Tov, G-d forbid, was lenient regarding practical mitzvos. For many, this error stems from their ignorance of the clear halachic ruling of our Sages, "It is not the study that is primary, but the action," which is also emphasized in many places in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, his students, and his students' students.

On this occasion, I would like to clarify through you if there is any basis for the strange report that appeared in the local press here, which claims that the study of "comparative religion" is being introduced into the curriculum of schools in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established)! Even if one were to say that the emphasis would be that their religions are different, etc., it is still astonishing—why confuse the minds of the students regarding the religions of the Christians, Muslims, and the like? Furthermore, according to the wording of the aforementioned report, this study was introduced even into the curriculum of secular schools! In normal years, I would say that this report has no basis, but in our current times, the saying of our Sages is particularly applicable: "Do not be dismissive of anything." Please inform me if you have any information regarding this.

One of the reasons for the delay in my response was also the disaster in Agadir. Although the latest reports from there announced the rescue of a certain number of students, thank G-d, even one soul in Israel is an entire world, and all the more so many of them. May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that our brethren, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be, should not experience any distress, and may all strengths and resources be utilized in matters of goodness, going from strength to strength.

As we stand on the day after Purim, regarding which it is said, "The Jews had light and gladness, and joy and honor"—literally, for "no verse loses its literal meaning"—and also in the inner dimension of the matter, as per our Sages' interpretation, "light" refers to Torah, etc., may it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that this be so for each one of us within the entirety of Klal Yisrael.

With respect and blessings for good tidings.

Regarding your concluding remark, that you take the liberty of saying that every believing Jew must pray for my welfare and success, etc.—my hope is strong that you have not suspected me of any contrary sentiment, especially given the emphasis on this point in the method of the Baal Shem Tov, which is the method of Chassidus.

After all, even the commandment in the Torah, "You shall surely rebuke your neighbor," is preceded in that very same verse by "You shall not hate your brother in your heart," and immediately follows it, in the subsequent verse, with "And you shall love your neighbor as yourself; I am Hashem."

Rather, it is my absolute belief—and furthermore, in my opinion, this is also founded on common sense—that the welfare and success of every single Jew depend on our holy Torah, which is called *Toras Chaim* (the Torah of life), from the word *hora'ah* (instruction) on how to live the true life worthy of the name, and on the fulfillment of the mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "And he shall live by them." If this is true for every individual, all the more so is it true for those who have influence over a circle and environment; the larger the circle and the influence, the greater the necessity and exclusivity of the connection between welfare and success and the Torah and its mitzvos.

## 6,220

B"H, Shushan Purim, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yitzchak Koren
Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter in due time, containing the good news that the matter of the yeshiva in Kiryat Gat has entered a more practical stage, as well as your previous letter. Please accept my apologies for the delay in responding, which was due to an abundance of preoccupations, and recently, also because of the tragedy in Agadir. Although the latest reports from Agadir indicated that a certain number of the students were saved, thank G-d, nevertheless, even one Jewish soul is an entire world, and all the more so when many are involved. May it be His will that our brethren, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be, should not experience any matters of distress, and may all strengths and resources be utilized for matters of good, going from strength to strength, going and illuminating.

In continuation of this desire, it is my hope that over time, matters of goodness and progress have also been added in Kiryat Gat. Surely you will not withhold the good from informing me, and my heartfelt thanks are extended to you in advance.

I read with special interest about the opening of the seminary for religious teachers. Surely, in the style of the Megillah, this will be conducted in a manner of "their laws are **different** from every people," with an emphasis on this. I emphasize these words in connection with a strange report that appeared in the press here, as if they are introducing into the curriculum of the schools in the Holy Land—may it be built and established—the study and comparison of the religions of the world—religions, in the plural. Even if one were to say that they will emphasize the matter of "their laws are different from every people," it is still a wonder, for why confuse the minds of the students, both boys and girls, regarding the religions of the Christians, the Muslims, and the like? And it is even stranger that, according to the phrasing of the aforementioned report, the aforementioned study will be introduced even into the curriculum of secular schools.

In normal years, I would say that this report has no basis, but in our current era, the saying of our Sages, of blessed memory, is most confirmed: "Do not dismiss any matter."

I will conclude on a good note, with what you write at the end of your letter regarding the impression from 19 Kislev in Kfar Chabad and the feeling of hispaalus, etc. May it be His will that this hispaalus and impression continue for each of the participants throughout the entire year, and especially in this auspicious year, the bicentennial year of the passing-hilula of the founder of the Chassidic path, our master the Baal Shem Tov, may his merit protect us, whose mission was to awaken the essence of the soul in every single Jewish man and woman, as is also hinted at in his holy name—Yisrael.

And as we stand on the day after Purim, of which it is said, "The Jews had light and gladness, and joy and honor," both in its literal sense—for "no verse departs from its literal meaning"—and also in the inner dimension of matters, as per the exposition of our Sages, of blessed memory, that "light" refers to Torah, etc., may it be His will that this be so for each one of us, within the entirety of the Jewish people.

With respect and blessings for good tidings.

As to how to achieve this—whether by suspending the connection for a time or in some other manner—you should consult with anash who know the aforementioned person and can gauge which path will be more effective.

May Hashem, who oversees each and every one with Divine Providence, grant you success in this, especially as we are in the month of Adar, when "the Jews had light and gladness, and joy and honor," as is well known from the words of our Sages regarding this.

With blessings for success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**
