## 271

B"H, 18 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 7 Adar.

It is a well-known adage of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, that just as one must know one’s own shortcomings, one must also know one’s own virtues. This is especially true given that it is a known tactic of the *yetzer hara* to cast a person into a state of despondency, or worse, by arguing that since one is not succeeding, what difference does it make, etc. Even though the *yetzer hara* is an expert in his craft, Hashem has created for us the Torah as an antidote—specifically the teachings of Chassidus Chabad, which explain his tactics, including the aforementioned tactic, where his (the *yetzer hara’s*) only intention is to lower a person from his level. Yet, in every person of Israel, their second soul is literally a "part of Elokus from above," and even at the moment of sin, it remains in *emunah* with Him, may He be blessed. Therefore, it is self-understood that in one moment and in one instant, one can overcome the tactics of the *yetzer hara*. This is especially true for those who have merited to study in the Tomchei Temimim yeshiva, established by our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, and who dedicate their time to education in purity and to bringing the hearts of the children of Israel closer to our Father in Heaven.

However, it is obvious that one must take action in this regard. Although all beginnings are difficult, from time to time the matter becomes easier, and the promise "little by little I will drive them out" is fulfilled. You should completely divert your attention from the unfair assessment you wrote in your letter, and instead increase your consistency and diligence in the work you are doing, as well as in your dedication and self-sacrifice as an educator and guide. May you share good news regarding all of the above.

At an opportune time, we will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Every weekday, before morning davening, set aside a few coins for tzedakah. *Bli neder.*

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 7232

B"H, 19 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn

R' Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

May it be the will of Hashem that, as we find ourselves in the month of Adar—about every day of which it is said that "we increase in joy"—from which it is understood that the matters of Adar that bring about joy, i.e., the matters of the Megillah, have influenced all the days of the month; may it be that now, at the very least, the concept will be revealed that "the people of the land became Jews" (Yehudim). If so, then all the more so for those hinted at by the second yud, as discussed at the Purim farbrengen in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and the Tzemach Tzedek that we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

In a parenthetical note, it should be pointed out that the concept of the two yuds is also hinted at in the nigleh of Torah—consistent with my approach for some time now, that everything discussed in nigleh has its parallel in nistar, and everything said in nistar has its parallel in nigleh—in the exposition of our Sages on the verse "Vayitzer" (He formed) written with two yuds; see also the Tzemach Tzedek’s glosses, page 81 and onwards.

Many thanks for the encouragement in general, and also for what was enclosed regarding the incident, may Hashem spare us, in Morocco.

May it be the will of Hashem that, just as we make a blessing over thunder—"He Who performs the work of Creation"—so too, in a similar vein but with a new interpretation, may all matters be transformed into joy and a Yom Tov for the two "firsts": Yisroel, who are called "first," and the Torah, which is called "first."

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

The shipment was delayed, and this is the reason for the delay of the letter, 28 Adar.

## Gerald

B"H, 22 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 14 Adar, Purim d'Prasot, in which you outline the main chapters of your life, your current work in the field of teaching and guiding religious working youth, and your desire to connect more and more to Torah, though reality is filled with stumbling blocks, Heaven forbid.

It is well known, as explained in Sifrei Mussar and with greater clarity in Sifrei Chassidus, the concept of "according to the camel is the load"—meaning, that together with the trials, the strength appropriate to overcome them is also granted. Moreover, our generation has clearly merited to see, tangibly, that when one decides with the appropriate firmness to walk the straight path according to the *Sefer HaYashar*, our holy Torah, one finds that the difficulties are fewer than anticipated, and the strength to overcome them is far greater than one had imagined. If this is true for every individual, how much more so for one upon whom many depend—that is, one who influences the many through education and guidance. Any growth he achieves is multiplied many times over in those he influences, his students. Regarding all of this, it is said, "There is nothing that can stand before the will," especially when one contemplates the responsibility (and the privilege) resting upon his shoulders. If one who sustains a single soul in Yisrael is considered as if he sustained an entire world, how much more so when it concerns many souls, particularly among the youth and the young, each of whom will, in the near future, build a home in Yisrael. The conduct of that home will be influenced by and correspond to the guidance received from their earliest youth.

May it be the will of Hashem that, as we find ourselves in the month of Adar—of which it is said, "For the Jews there was light and joy, etc.," and our Sages explained, "Light—this is Torah"—that the Torah and its study be in a manner that leads to the action of light for all the children of Yisrael in all their dwelling places.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

#### ***Gerald***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 22, p. 361.

## Z'rela

B"H, 24 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Friday, regarding your question about the rumor concerning the *pask din* of the Tzemach Tzedek regarding the trimming of the beard.

It is explained at length in his *Shu"t*, *Yoreh Deah* section, siman 93. See also his *Chiddushim* on *Shas Makkos*, chapter 3; *Piskei Dinim* for *Yoreh Deah*, siman 181 and 182; and the wondrous things in his *Reshimot* on the verse, "And He, being merciful, forgives..." (*Tehillim* 78:38), regarding how deeply this matter touches the highest levels.

2) Regarding the advice for laziness and distracting thoughts — one should study the *Tanya Kadisha*, focusing on the various matters that are helpful for what was mentioned, and what is explained there at the beginning of chapter 41. See also the **Pask Din** at the **beginning** of the *Shulchan Aruch*, at the beginning of siman 1, regarding the verse, "I have set Hashem before me always."

3) Regarding what you wrote about the study of the *Chitas* (*Chumash*, *Tehillim*, *Tanya*) — that it might, G-d forbid, arouse hatred, etc.

This is the case with all parts of our Torah, as explained by our Sages regarding the hint in the name *Har Sinai* (Mount Sinai), upon which the Torah was given, that it was then that hatred descended, etc. See there.

It is understood that studying the *Chassidus* portion of the aforementioned *shiur* is not sufficient at all. The matter of this *shiur* is a specific, unique thing. There must be *kevi'us itim* (fixed times) for the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of *Chassidus*. As is explained in the introduction of the *Ramak* (Rabbi Chaim Vital) to *Shaar HaHakdamot*, the lack of this study delays the *Geulah* and prolongs the exile of the *Shechinah* and the exile of the Children of Israel. This matter is brought in many places, including in the books of the *Gra*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

***

**The beard:** See also above, letter 6,101.

## Z'ralet

B"H, 28 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Chaim, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 22 Adar... May it be the will [of Hashem] that, as you conclude your letter, the statement of Chazal—which is also a directive—will be fulfilled: "Torah scholars increase peace in the world," and may this be in a manner that is "increasing and continuing," commensurate with the urgency of the hour.

Especially as we find ourselves at the conclusion of the month of Adar and are entering the month of Nissan, a transition from one redemption to the next. In both, the point of closeness and unity of all Bnei Yisrael to one another is emphasized (Tanchuma on the verse Shemos 2:14; the reason for *mishloach manos* is brought in Responsa Chasam Sofer).

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

...Regarding what you wrote concerning the ruling of the Alter Rebbe in his Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim 553:14, that it is sufficient to have the intention of "for the sake of the mitzvah" [when baking] that "you shall eat matzah," and not specifically for the [commandment] "in the evening you shall eat matzah"—implying that according to this opinion, there is a mitzvah to eat matzah all seven days (and so it is written also in Torah Sheleimah, in the supplements to Vol. 11, explaining the Gemara in Pesachim 40a)—it is impossible to say so. For the opinion of the Alter Rebbe on this matter (ibid., end of 475) is like the Rambam, that there is no mitzvah at all except on the first night. This is also indicated by the plain language of the Rosh and the Tur Shulchan Aruch, even though they are the proponents of the second opinion in 553:14, as noted there in the *mekoros*. This is also indicated in Rambam, Hilchos Chametz U’Matzah, Chapter 5, Halacha 10 (see there in the *mekoros* and in Tzafnas Paneach by the Rogatchover). As to whether the definition of "for the sake of the mitzvah" and the various opinions regarding eating matzah all seven days apply here at all—this is discussed at length in Torah Sheleimah there. And this is not the place to elaborate.

*Z'ralet*

**R' Chaim, may he live:** Stein.

B"H, 28 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn.

Regarding your question as to which *maamarim* you should continue with—it is understood that it must be with *maamarim* that are well-edited. Therefore, it should be from the printed *maamarim*, especially since many of them include footnotes, references, and so on.

With blessings for good tidings and also for the health of your father, may he live.

**M. Schneerson**

## 770

B"H, 29 Adar, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, your letter from Erev Purim was received.

May it be the will of Hashem that since a better state of mind is evident in it, this should be the beginning of going "from strength to strength" in this regard. This is especially true since a firm sense of *bitachon* leads to *menuchas hanefesh*, joy, and a good heart, which are among the foundations of our holy Torah, particularly according to what is explained in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and Chassidus Chabad.

It was pleasant for me to read in your letter about your visits to Kfar Chabad, to the seminary and to Beis Rivkah. May it be the will of Hashem that in this matter as well, the details you write about will improve, within the context of the institution's affairs as a whole. This is especially relevant in light of what is known: that the education of the younger generation is like tending to a seed, where every addition to it grows many times over, both in quantity and in quality, when the seed grows and becomes a tree that produces fruit. From this, it is understood that every effort in this area is worthwhile, and that one is granted additional strength and *siyata d'shmaya* from Above specifically for this.

Regarding what you wrote about the plan to visit your relatives abroad, surely this is with the consent of your husband, *shlita*.

Certainly, you will connect this with some *mitzvah* matter, which permits leaving *Eretz Yisrael* (may it be built and established). May it be the will of Hashem that your trip be at a good and auspicious time, in a good manner, and with proper health.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, with *menuchas hanefesh* and proper health.

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 742

*[Late Adar, 5720]*

By the grace of Hashem, Thursday, Vayakhel-Pekudei, 5720.

To the holy presence of our Master, the Rebbe, the holy Gaon, shlita.

In the Shulchan Aruch of our Rebbe [the Alter Rebbe], in Hilchos Shabbos, chapter 357, paragraph 1, it states: "A courtyard that is smaller than four amos by four amos and is adjacent to a public domain, one may not pour water into it on Shabbos during the summer months. Since it is not four amos, the two se'ah of water that a person is accustomed to using each day are not likely to be absorbed into it, and it is as if he is pouring them into the public domain. And even though there is no Torah prohibition in this pouring from a courtyard into a public domain (if [see chapter 159, paragraph 6, and Magen Avraham, chapter 328, subsection 53, and Sanhedrin 67b, and examine it closely; and this is also implied in the Ritva in the Beis Yosef], he does not pour them directly into the public domain, but rather at a slight distance, such that their exit into the public domain happens on its own, and it is not the force of his pouring itself, but rather his force is merely a cause)."

It seems that the simple intent of our Rebbe is to resolve what is stated in Eruvin, page 88, that if one pours water in a private domain and it flows further into a public domain, it involves only a Rabbinic prohibition. On the face of it, this is puzzling, for the water moves from his direct force, just like one who throws from a private domain to a public domain; why should it be permitted by Torah law? To this, our Rebbe says that the lack of a Torah prohibition when pouring in a private domain applies when one pours at a distance from the public domain, in a manner where the water does not exit from his direct force. This is unlike when one pours adjacent to the public domain and they exit immediately, which is similar to rolling an object from a private domain to a public domain.

However, regarding the citation on the side, "see Shas Sanhedrin, page 67," nothing of this matter is found there at all. In my opinion, it is a printing error, and it should say page 77b of Avodah Zarah, where it is stated there regarding "one who casts a stream of water at his fellow," that we distinguish between a first force and a second force, and Rashi explains there that there is a distinction between near and far; see there.

Furthermore, regarding what our Rebbe cited concerning the requirement that it be far from the public domain, which he attributes to the Ritva, I have not found this in my limited capacity.

Now, from the language of Rabbi Yonasan brought in the Beis Yosef at the beginning of chapter 357, it appears clearly that even in a place slightly distant from the public domain, it is not sufficient; rather, it must rest for a moment before exiting outside. It seems his opinion is like that of the Rameh in Sanhedrin, page 77b, regarding the distinction he makes concerning "casting a stream of water" between a first and second force. He writes there that the most clarified of the interpretations is that a second force means that it was interrupted slightly, like what is stated in Bava Basra, page 117, that "the water ceased and then fell," which are the words of the Gemara itself. He rejects the interpretation of the commentators who distinguish between a near and far location. According to his words, it must be like the interpretation of Rabbi Yonasan, that all the permissions here are only when they rested slightly before exiting into the public domain. Yet, from our Rebbe, it implies that he holds the primary distinction is between near and far.

One can bring proof for our Rebbe that there is a distinction between near and far—that "far" is considered a second force and is therefore permitted by Torah law—from the Gemara in Chullin, page 107b, regarding the "bucket of the drawer," that if he does not bring his hand close to the bucket, it is not considered the force of the pourer. Thus, the distance makes it a second force. Later, I found this proof in the book *Siach HaSadeh*.

The one who bows before your holy splendor.

## 772

*[Late Adar 5720]*

...On Tuesday, Parshas Tetzaveh, I went... During the conversation, I mentioned that every physical thing in this world is composed of four elements, and there are no more than four elements, as explained in Chassidus. He replied that this is indeed explained in the Rambam, but today it is agreed upon by all of science that there are ninety-six elements. In any case, the Rambam said this according to the theories of his time...

In the Rambam’s Sefer HaMitzvos, negative commandment 179, regarding the Rambam’s principle that if a prohibition is mentioned more than once without adding a new detail, one is only liable for one set of lashes. It is explained there in his words regarding leprosy that one is liable for six. He said that the Rambam stated this as his theory regarding spontaneous generation, and now in biology, it is agreed that this is not true...

He agreed that I should ask the Rebbe shlita one thing: whether this matter of the four elements is a part of the Torah, and if one does not believe in it, what is his status.

1) [Four elements] in the words of our Sages does **not** mean that they cannot be divided or split, but rather that they are the "foundational" parts from which everything is composed. This has no relation to the number of elements in chemistry. There are **early** commentators on the words of our Sages who explain "elements" as referring to their **properties**: cold and moist, hot and dry, etc. This is not the place to elaborate. Therefore, they are called **natures** in the Midrash.

2) This was agreed upon 50 **years ago**, but now it is "agreed" that each of them is composed of several parts. And how many **types** of parts there are — **no one knows at all** yet. Some hypothesize that they are **four elements**: matter, antimatter, positive, negative.

3) And this is the "theory" of the **Torah**, and it is brought in **many places** by Tanna'im (Toras Kohanim, Shemini 11:44 **and elsewhere**) and Amora'im (Shabbos 107b), and this is a **foundation** for several halachos.

4) The entire consensus is by way of **conjecture, and as follows:** Since they found (via microscope) small eggs in the place of decay, it is possible to say that these species were formed from them. **There is no proof** that they were formed from the decay as the Sages stated, and if so, one cannot say that they are different from other living creatures.

5) For it is found in Bamidbar Rabbah, ch. 14, 12; in the Zohar in too many places to count, **and elsewhere.**

## 7,243

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the educational institution of *chinuch al taharat hakodesh*
"Oholei Torah," Brooklyn, N.Y.
May Hashem preserve them and may they live

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your notification regarding the arranging of a dinner for the benefit of the institution on the upcoming 6th of Nissan.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the preparations, and consequently the results as well, be met with great success, to enable the existence and expansion of the educational institution, both in quantity (a greater number of students) and in quality (the ability to deepen their learning).

It has already been stated that the *segulah* of this year—the 200th anniversary of the *histalkus-hilula* of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, the founder of the general *Toras HaChassidus*—is that his first *avodah*—before he revealed himself as the Baal Shem Tov—was the education of Jewish children, even very young ones, teaching them to say *Amen, yehei shmei rabba*, *Barchu*, *Kedushah*, *brachos*, etc., as we have heard this many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

So too today, the greatest effort and *hishtadlus* must be placed in this field of *chinuch al taharat hakodesh*, including for very young children, who will in time, with the help of Hashem, be great, upright Jews, *shomrei Torah u'mitzvos* and *lomdei Torah*.

And may the merit of each and every person participating in the assistance for the *chinuch al taharat hakodesh* institution, "Oholei Torah"—and whatever you will surely add to this—stand for you to be blessed with all good things, both materially and spiritually together.

With blessings for success.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7244

B"H, 2 Nissan, the day of the histalkus hilula of the Rebbe (Maharash), which is also the first day of the nesius of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, 5720 — the bicentennial year of the histalkus hilula of the Baal Shem Tov, ztzkllh"h nbg"m zy"a.

To each and every one in Kfar Chabad—founded and directed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe—may Hashem grant them life:

Peace and blessing!

Approaching the festival of matzos, the season of our freedom, which is arriving for us and for all of Israel for the good, I hereby express my blessing to each and every one of them: a blessing for a kosher and happy holiday, the season of our freedom—freedom from all matters that distract from the avodah of Hashem with joy and a good heart.

For the obligation of the avodah of Hashem must never cease from a person (all Jews—spelled with two yuds—from youth to elder, children and women) even for a moment throughout all his days.

And according to the teaching of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe: The first night is *michla d’meheimanusa* (food of faith). The second night is *michla d’asusa* (food of healing). If the healing brings the faith—where he says, "Thank You, G-d, for my healing"—he was, after all, sick. But if the faith brings the healing, one is not sick to begin with.

May this freedom be in such a way that, from the outset, no confusion or distress, chas v'shalom, shall come.

And may they draw from this freedom and joy into all their affairs, both private and communal, throughout all the days of the entire year.

May it be the will of Hashem that in this year, and in these very days, the saying of our Sages will be fulfilled: "At the conclusion of the seventh year, the son of David comes," and may He redeem us with the true and complete Geulah—freedom in its perfection—until we "spread out to the west, east, north, and south."

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach, with true expansion, and for a healthy and happy summer.

I have sent *matzah shmurah*, and I request that the General Committee of Kfar Chabad, together with the Spiritual Committee and the Rabbi, the chossid, the G-d-fearing man, etc., Harav Hagaon Harav Hachossid, our teacher, Rabbi R. Sh. Z. shlita, the mara d'asra, at their head, distribute it to the residents of Kfar Chabad and to the choice activists of Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt, shlita.

May it be the will of Hashem that it should perform its function—the function of *michla d’meheimanusa* and *michla d’asusa*—in its fullness and perfection.

#### ***7244***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 7, p. 245, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

**Obligation... his days:** The language of the letter in the introduction to Sefer HaChinuch.

**Constant obligation:** See Tur Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim 231. And similarly regarding Chassidus and its matters—as per the instruction of the Rebbe Maharash (Sefer HaToldos 86a).

**With two yuds:** Those over whom the ten powers of the *nefesh habahamis* rule, and those over whom the ten powers of the *nefesh habamis* rule—a sicha of the Tzemach Tzedek. And see his notes to Tanya, Chapter 1 (Sefer HaKetzurim, p. 81 and onwards).

**Children:** That even they require atonement (Nedarim 35b; and see Kerisus 16a), even though they are not subject to the law, etc. (see Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe, Yoreh Deah 2:2; Pri Megadim, Introduction to Orach Chaim, Part 2, 3; and elsewhere).

**Teaching of our Rebbe:** Yom Yom, 15 Nissan. And see the commentaries on the verse in Beshalach 15:26.

**Saying of our Sages:** Sanhedrin 97a.

**Spread out:** See Maorei Ohr, entry *Peretz*.

**With two yuds:** See also above, Letter 7232.

**R. Sh. Z.:** Gorlik, the Rabbi of Kfar Chabad.

## Gérôme

B"H, 6 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following a very long hiatus, your letter from Erev Rosh Chodesh Nissan was received. It is surprising that you make no mention of your setting fixed times for the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*—which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. It appears that you do not connect the matters you write about to this at all—which perhaps also explains the confusion you are experiencing regarding those very matters. For *pnimiyus haTorah* is called the "Tree of Life," where there is no difficulty, no dispute, etc., and where the *talmidei chachamim* are not sustained by the *amei ha'aretz* but rather from the side of good, etc., as stated by *Ra'aya Mehemna*, Moshe Rabbeinu, and explained in *Tanya Kadisha* by our Rebbe HaZaken, *Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 26.

The question is well-known: there are many who do not engage in the aforementioned study, yet they spend their days and years in pleasantness.

However, in addition to all the explanations for this **ancient** question, one who has been privileged by Divine Providence to know of this Torah—the teachings of Chassidus—and has even begun this study (and perhaps progressed beyond the beginning), is not comparable to those who have not been privileged to know of its very existence. And the rest is understood.

May it be the will of Hashem that, at the very least, from here on—without waiting for further awakenings or hints—you will set fixed times for the study of *pnimiyus haTorah* every single day, with an increase on the holy Shabbos, which is sanctified to Hashem. This fixed time should be not only a fixed time in the schedule, but also a fixed time in the soul. May you find relief in both spiritual and material matters alike, and may you bring good news in response to all that has been said.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 767

B"H, 6 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...While it is understood and simple that the printing of holy books—especially those that are beneficial for the dissemination of Torah—is of immense value, nevertheless, just as with literal tzedakah, it must be done as it should be, meaning: when one exhausts all of one’s possibilities and capabilities. This is certainly true regarding spiritual tzedakah as well. And is it to be believed, even according to your own estimation, that this constitutes the full utilization of all your strength—through the printing of books, etc.—while there is no involvement at all on your part through speech and advocacy, etc., in the issues facing the Jewish world in general, and in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and the holy city of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established, in particular? Not even regarding the most burning issues?

There is room to say that you are not satisfied with how others are acting in a certain way, or with the fact that others are not acting at all. But it is understood and simple that this is no excuse to add yet another matter that is not as it should be, on top of what others are doing that is not as it should be.

There is another argument we have heard: "What can I accomplish, and what good will it do? Who am I?" etc. Regarding such things, they said, "The humility of Rabbi Zecharyah [ben Avkulas] destroyed our house..."

In our current case, where each of us hopes to be worthy of being part of the army of Hashem—which is one of the themes of the festival of Pesach—the entire concept of maintaining an army is not based on intellectual understanding, but on hearing the command and fulfilling it. And the command of our holy Torah, the Torah of life, is: "You shall surely rebuke your neighbor," and as a preface to this, "You shall not hate your brother in your heart," and concluding and sealing with, "You shall not take revenge... and you shall love your neighbor as yourself; I am Hashem." And the commandment, according to the ruling of the Torah, is up to **one hundred** times. There is no need to elaborate on such a simple matter.

I believe I have already written to you regarding the above. And "two are better than one." I look forward to hearing from you with good news regarding the above.

## 6248

[7 Nissan 5720]

It is obvious that one must arrange a *mechiras chametz* there.

The benefit is certain. Beyond the essential aspect (the matter of *bal yira'eh* and *bal yimatzei*), there is also the *hisorerus* and the reminder regarding the prohibition of *chametz*, the custom of our fathers, and so on.

As for the concern that perhaps they will take from the *chametz* during *Chol HaMoed*, etc.: 1) It is obvious that many of the aforementioned will not do this. 2) Even regarding those who are suspected—certainly, the *tikkun* is not nullified. 3) Even regarding one who does take from it—according to many opinions, the sale is not nullified [**this is the implication of the Alter Rebbe’s opinion in Seder Hachsharas Keilim, sections 13-14**]; rather, he is merely a thief regarding what he takes, and nothing more. 4) Even according to the one who says the sale is nullified, one could say that this is only from that point forward—and he was saved from the prohibition of *bal yira'eh* and *bal yimatzei* until that moment. And regarding a *lav* that does not involve an action (*ma'aseh*), according to many opinions, one is not *malkin* (liable for lashes) even if he performs an action. 5) Even according to the one who says that one is *malkin* for it, it is a matter of *tzarich iyun* what the decisive factor is: whether one is in the prohibition of *bal yira'eh* and *bal yimatzei* for all eight days of *Chol HaMoed*—except in a way that one is not *malkin*—or for a shorter time, except for **one** moment—the moment the acquisition is nullified—he stands in a *lav* for which one is *malkin*. 6) Even if you were to say that the sale is nullified retroactively, on the contrary, according to this, one could say that **there is no action here** and one is not *malkin* for it, because the sale never existed, and there is no place for an acquisition during *Chol HaMoed*.

You should clarify with the rabbis with whom you are debating: Is it possible to add, and what is the benefit of adding, to the aforementioned *shtar* (contract): a) That the Jew who is selling, **if he wishes**, or his agent, shall be authorized by the non-Jew who is buying—**and not *k'ein* *mechiras chametz***—to sell on his behalf or to give as a gift from the items being sold.

**Or** b) That he sells to him, etc., until the measurement during *Chol HaMoed*, and apart from what will be taken from the items listed in the *shtar*, also on the days following that.

It is understood that they must warn the sellers that they are forbidden from doing the above. But even if they violate **this** prohibition, there is no concern of the sale being nullified, since it was on that understanding, etc.

#### ***6248***

Printed in the *Haggadah Shel Pesach* with *Likutei Ta'amim U'Biurim* (5746 edition and onwards, p. 453). It is a response to R. Shmuel Pesach Bogomilsky—to his question on behalf of Rabbi Speizman (see letter 6219 below), whether it is worthwhile to arrange *mechiras chametz* in a city where it is possible that some of those who sell will take from the *chametz* during *Pesach*.

**In the publisher's note there:** Regarding several details in the following letter, there is a *shakla v'tarya* in several books—see the sources cited: *Sdei Chemed*, *Ma'areches Chometz U'Matzah*, *Klal* 9, subsection 35; *Sha'arei Tziyunim B'Halacha* to *Kitzur Shulchan Aruch*, end of section 114; *Otzar HaPesach* (N.Y. 5726), sections 444, 448; *Erev Pesach Shechal B'Shabbos* (Eretz Yisrael 5734), chapter 4 at the beginning, and others.

## Zermatt

B"H, 8 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished, a man of fine character, etc.,
R' Yisroel, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 4th of Nissan.

As we approach the Festival of Matzos, the season of our freedom, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good, I hereby extend my blessing for a kosher and joyous holiday, and for true freedom—freedom from material worries and spiritual anxieties, and from anything that hinders the service of Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

May you continue to draw from this freedom and joy throughout the entire year, especially since the service of Hashem, as commanded in our Torah—the Torah of life—encompasses all of a person’s affairs throughout the entire day and night, as it is written: "In all your ways, know Him."

With holiday blessings.

P.S.

It was pleasing for me to read in your letter regarding the preparation of the questionnaire for the yeshiva students, as it is tangibly evident how this stimulates interest and increases the diligence of the students.

May it be Hashem’s will that this increases further and further (as per the Sages in Sanhedrin 21a), to a very great extent, as explained by our Alter Rebbe in Likutei Torah, Parshas Shelach (38c).

Indeed, this too is a matter of the season of our freedom, the festival of Pesach, as it is written: "When you bring the people out of Egypt, you shall serve G-d upon this mountain"—specifically *avodah* (service), which implies exertion, and even greater exertion, as per the Alter Rebbe’s precise interpretation based on the term "tanning hides" (*avod oros*); see Torah Or, beginning of Parshas Mishpatim.

Regarding what you wrote about the travel of students from here to the Tomchei Temimim yeshiva in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, the matter has been referred to the administration of Tomchei Temimim here, and they will surely be in touch with them.

#### ***Zermatt***

**R' Yisroel, may he live:** Grossman, Jerusalem. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 18, 6,866, and in the notes referenced there.

## 7,150

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in the work of Heaven,
R. Y. (may he live and be well),

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter dated the day of the Hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory.

At a time of favor, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in connection with their reaching the age of obligation for Torah and mitzvos.

May it be His will that from the age of thirteen for mitzvos, they grow to the age of fifteen for Gemara, and so on, and may their parents (may they live and be well) derive from them much true nachas—a Jewish, Chassidic nachas.

Great is the merit of all those who raised and educated them in the way of the King, the King of kings, and who have seen good fruit from their labor: students whom all who see them recognize as the seed which Hashem has blessed.

Moving from one subject to another within the same theme: since they have grown up in our generation—a generation of spiritual destruction, Heaven forbid, with terrible decrees and the like, a "Mitzrayim" (Egypt) the likes of which have never been seen—may it be fulfilled now in our generation, the generation of the footsteps of Moshiach, and speedily in our days, that they will say, "This is my G-d and I will glorify Him." As our Sages of blessed memory taught, "They recognized Him first"—referring to the coming of the first redeemer, who is also the final redeemer, our righteous Moshiach, in the true and complete Redemption.

With respect and with blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

P.S.

Regarding the custom of some of Anash that bochurim who lead the davening refuse to wrap themselves in a tallis, and similarly regarding an aliyah to the Torah, hagbah, and the like:

This is based on the instruction of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im (as printed in Hayom Yom, 19 Kislev), that the shaliach tzibbur does not wrap himself in a tallis for Maariv, neither on Shabbos and Yom Tov nor on Rosh Hashanah. From this, it is understood that there is no slight whatsoever to the honor of the congregation or the like. This serves as a foundational principle (binyan av) regarding Shacharis as well, for those who do not wear a tallis gadol when they daven on their own.

And according to the narrative of our Torah—for even a narrative of the Torah is an instruction—(Sukkah 32b): "Rav Acha bar Rava **was meticulous**..." since it came from the mouth of Rav, etc. Especially since in the case at hand, there is also the matter of reciting a blessing, about which there is much back-and-forth. The simplest advice to avoid a doubt regarding a blessing is to avoid the question entirely, and the wise will understand. It is understood that all of the above is on the condition that it does not lead to machlokes, for peace is great, and the entire Torah was given only to bring peace to the world.

## Zerna

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn.

To those gathered at the wedding celebration of the avreich, the chossid, the temim, R' Y. Sh. [Landa] shlita, who signed the letter of birthday greetings, may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received the aforementioned letter of blessing. As is already stated in our holy Torah, the Torah of life: "Whoever blesses others will be blessed," and the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam is even greater than the primary intent.

This is especially true when the blessing comes from a Chassidishe farbrengen. As is well known, the Alter Rebbe said regarding the *petek* that descends from the highest heavens, etc., that "what a Chassidishe farbrengen can accomplish, the angel Michael cannot accomplish." The explanation of this is found in the letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, printed in *Kovetz Michtavim* 1.

Through the blessing of Hashem mentioned above, it is understood—and indeed simple—that it includes the heart's desires of every Yid, specifically for a kosher and joyous Pesach, true freedom, and the ability to draw that joy and freedom into all the days of the year.

With respect and with the blessing of a kosher and joyous Pesach.

## 7254

B"H, 10 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...As we stand before the festival of Pesach, the time of our freedom—which was then not only freedom in the literal sense from the slavery of Mitzrayim, but also freedom from the limitations of nature—everything occurred through open miracles. This is true both at the beginning of the freedom—the striking of the Mitzriyim and the healing of Yisroel at the very same moment, which is the opposite of even the nature of holiness, for here the attribute of Gevurah and the attribute of Chesed were manifest simultaneously [and therefore this was possible only through the Ribono shel Olam Himself, "I, and not an angel; I, and not a seraph; I, and not a messenger," for He alone, in the words of the Rashba in his responsa, is the One who accomplishes the impossible]—and likewise at the conclusion of the festival of Pesach with the splitting of the Yam Suf, even though, on the face of it, there was no necessity for this open miracle, since they ascended on the same side they descended (Tosafos, s.v. *K'shem*, Arachin 15a)—

May it be His will that it be so in all matters of Torah and its mitzvos, and all the more so in the area of chinuch. For in connection with the exodus from Mitzrayim, it was the children who recognized Him first, leading up to the culmination of the matter at the giving of the Torah, which came about through the guarantee of "our children are our guarantors."

I conclude as I began, with strong hope regarding your most positive attitude toward the aforementioned institutions, especially since you have invested in them so much empathy, assistance, and friendship.

With blessings for a kosher and joyous Pesach, and for true freedom from all matters that distract from avodas Hashem, with joy and a glad heart, and with respect.

#### ***7254***

Published in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 7, p. 243.

## Zareng

B"H, 10 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter, along with its enclosure, reached me after a long delay. Its content expresses your wonder and bewilderment regarding the dispute you have with Tzeirei Chabad in Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established speedily.

Now, although I am not versed in the details of the matter about which you write, knowing the mesiras nefesh of the activists of Tzeirei Chabad of Jerusalem—and indeed, of all Tzeirei Chabad throughout Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established—in every matter of strengthening and disseminating Yiddishkeit, there was certainly a strong and well-founded reason for their conduct regarding the matter you describe. As I surmise from your letter, and also from reports in the press regarding the aforementioned matter, it appears their reasoning stems from the strong directive given to them—and to all Chassidei Chabad—by our Rebbes, the Nesi’im, to distance themselves as much as possible from any matter of partisanship, regardless of which party it may be, even the most positive one. The reason for this directive has been explained in writing and even more so orally: our task is to disseminate Yiddishkeit among all of Bnei Yisrael, and at the core, to disseminate the teachings of Chassidus, even to the "outside" (*chutza*). Therefore, we are obligated to distance ourselves as much as possible from any matter that could diminish the possibilities of this dissemination, to the extent that even a doubt, or a double doubt, in this regard is treated with stringency.

It is my firm hope that after you reflect upon what has been said, and in accordance with the statement of Chazal, "Judge every person favorably," you will find merit for Tzeirei Chabad in this matter as well. Not only will you not hold it against them, but you will assist them in their work of disseminating the wellsprings—and, on the contrary, increase the assistance you have provided until now, for surely this aforementioned task is precious to you as well. May it be Hashem’s will that I receive good tidings from you regarding all of the above, for great is peace, as the entire Torah was given to increase peace in the world.

As we approach the festival of Pesach, the time of our freedom, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good, I send you my blessing: a kosher and happy Pesach, and true freedom from all matters that distract from the service of Hashem, with joy and goodness of heart.

With respect and blessing.

It is understood and simple that in what I wrote above regarding the directive against partisanship for Chabad, its people, and its affairs, I did not come, G-d forbid, to disparage partisan activity founded upon Torah and mitzvos. Rather, I intended to emphasize that even this activity is not among the tasks of Chabad and its people, for "it is established by a greater degree"—the dissemination of the wellsprings, specifically in a way that reaches even the **"outside"** (*chutza*). And although the general task of all Bnei Yisrael is one, as the Mishnah states, "I was created only to serve my Creator," within this service itself there are many types, kinds, and details, and each one shall ascend in his own path to the House of G-d.

## 7,000

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and accomplished, whose work is holy work, R' Ben Zion Moshe Yair, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

Approaching the festival of Matzos, the season of our freedom, which is arriving for us and for all of Israel for the good, I hereby express my blessing for a kosher and joyous holiday and for true freedom—freedom from material worries and from spiritual worries, from anything that hinders the avodah of Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

And may this freedom and joy continue throughout all the days of the year.

Especially since the avodah of Hashem, as we are commanded in our Torah—the Torah of life—pertains to all of a person's affairs, throughout the entire day and night, as it is said: "In all your ways, know Him."

With respect and holiday blessings.

P.S.

The book *Kinor Ben Dovid* was received, and many thanks for the aforementioned gift. May it be His will that for many years he will increase his strength for Torah, until we merit the coming of Ben Dovid and the fulfillment of the prophecy, "And My servant Dovid shall be prince over them forever."

It is surprising that in the lines on the title page of the book, the year 5720 (תש"כ) is written with a *chof peshutah* (final *chof*), especially since, according to the hints of the Torah, a *chof peshutah* represents five hundred, as noted in several places in *Midrash Talpiyot* under the entry for letters. In such matters, and especially in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, caution is required so that others do not learn from this, etc., as per the Mishnah in *Avos* (Chapter 1, Mishnah 11): "And they will drink, etc., and the name of Heaven will be profaned, etc." And we conclude with good.

## Z'renah

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Benjamin West
Greetings and Blessings!

Thank you for the book "Struggles of a Generation," as well as the previous publications. It is my hope that you will continue to send your publications to our library in the future, and I thank you in advance for doing so.

Certainly, it is the duty of those who came to our country in the past, before the memory fades, to commemorate it in all its details—especially its struggle for its true existence through the preservation of its character. Therefore, to you and to all those who assist you in such matters, it is fitting to say *yasher kocho*, for this is a matter that the time demands, especially in our era, where a single year is now an entire epoch filled with revolutions.

In these days before the time of our freedom, may it be the will [of Hashem] that all segments of our people emerge from their respective exiles: those who are in physical exile should emerge from their physical exile, and those who are in spiritual exile should emerge from their spiritual exile—from slavery to true freedom. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "Do not read *charut* (engraved) on the tablets, but *cheirut* (freedom) on the tablets," for true freedom for us is that which is bound to the *Luchos HaBris*, the "writing of Elokus," which unites the two extremes: on one hand, the *taanug*, the "delights" of the *Ribono shel Olam*, which is limitless and *Ein Sof*, and at the same time, it is a *Toras Chaim*—a guide for daily life in our physical and material world.

This is the task of the Jewish people in all generations and in all places, as hinted at in the dream of our forefather Yaakov: "a ladder set on the ground and its top reached the heavens"—to unite the "below" with the "above," in such a way that "Behold, Hashem stood over him," as the seal and conclusion of the matter there.

With respect and with blessings for a kosher and happy holiday.

## Zarnu

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...I have passed your response on to the Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch, but in general, I must express my bewilderment. In my opinion, the attitude toward this matter must correspond to the reality—namely, that this is an institution of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisroel, and is conducted by him. For the actions of the tzaddikim endure forever. From this, it is understood that anyone who takes part—and certainly one who is a representative and deputy of the founder, especially in a central location—is a representative and shaliach of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe. And the principle that "a person’s agent is like himself" applies with even greater force regarding tzaddikim, who are beyond the limitations of space and time, especially after their histalkus and hillula, etc. This is, of course, understood from the explanation in Iggeres HaKodesh, section 27, of our Alter Rebbe, since [the essence of the tzaddik, the level of his ruach] is not contained within a vessel and is not in the category of physical space; see there.

When one contemplates what has been said, the astonishment and bewilderment are understandable: how can it be written that because someone expressed themselves in an inappropriate manner, or even performed an inappropriate action, they are prepared to cease their shlichus and representation, chas v'shalom? I will not elaborate further on this lack of understanding of the matter, and perhaps there are hidden reasons for what was said.

## 757

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brethren, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

As the upcoming *Chag HaMatzos* approaches, I send my wishes and blessings to our brethren, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be, with the blessing of a "kosher and joyous *Chag HaPesach*, the time of our freedom."

**Chirus** — true liberation — is a complete liberation: liberation of the person as an individual (*olam katan*), and as a component of the world around them. This implies a twofold liberation: an **internal** one — liberation from internal obstacles, which stem from innate or acquired traits, acquired through upbringing, habit, etc.; and an **external** one — liberation from the obstacles that the surrounding world forces upon the person.

* * *

Our Sages, of blessed memory, who present an entire system in a brief expression, have expressed the above in a few words, and in doing so, also pointed out the path and the means to this liberation, saying: *Charus al haLuchos*... *Chirus* from the subjugation of kingdoms, from poverty, foolishness, suffering, and constriction.

The *Aseres HaDibros* on the *Luchos*, in which all *mitzvos* are hinted at, begin with the declaration: **"I am Hashem your G-d, who brought you out of the land of Egypt, from the house of bondage"** — I am G-d, **your** G-d, who led you out of the land of Egypt, from the house of bondage.

The first and most fundamental thing that is engraved in Jewish life, and stated by the Ribono shel Olam to every single man and woman, is: I am **your G-d**, here in your personal life and conduct.

The name **"your G-d"** specifically emphasizes that the Ribono shel Olam is the Master of Ability and the Master of all forces (everything is possible, and He rules over all forces), from which comes the twofold liberation: **"from the land of Egypt"** — from the limitations and undesirable traits (*ma'aseh eretz Mitzrayim*) that came through the influence of living in Egypt; and **"from the house of bondage"** — from the subjugation to Pharaoh and Egypt, to the world around.

From this also comes the twofold instruction — regarding internal and external life — to every single man and woman: **"You shall have no other gods"** — there should be no idolization for you of anything whatsoever, other than the Ribono shel Olam; **"Remember the day of Shabbos to sanctify it,"** etc. — do not submit yourself to the conduct and demands of the outside world.

* * *

*Torah* also has these two moments: the internal, the *neshamah* of the *Torah* (**Pnimiyus HaTorah**), and the part that is connected with action, studying *Torah* and fulfilling *mitzvos* (**Nigleh D'Torah**), where the internal, the *neshamah*, enlivens the external.

*Pnimiyus HaTorah* has been broadly explained and disseminated in recent generations through *Toras HaChassidus*, founded by the Baal Shem Tov, whose *histalkus-hillula* marks two hundred years this year.

One of the teachings of *Toras HaChassidus* that the Baal Shem Tov emphasized many times is: **"I have set Hashem before me always"** (*Shivisi Hashem l'negdi tamid*). Every Jew must perceive that they stand before the Ribono shel Olam, to the point that everything in the world around them and everything within them is *shivisi* (equal to them). And this must be **tamid** — always, not only while standing in *Shemoneh Esrei*, the highest level of *tefillah*, and not only at special times of the day, like at the beginning of the day. That does not yet provide the full *shivisi*, the full *chirus* from being influenced by the world (internally or externally), because at other times a person can again fall into *avdus*, subjugation to their own nature and to the world around them. The **"Hashem before me"** must be in the fullest sense of **tamid**; it must permeate every action and movement of the person, down to eating, drinking, and speaking with people, etc. And then they are not *nispa'el* (moved/affected) by internal and external obstacles and achieve true and full *chirus*, both from the "land of Egypt" and from the "house of bondage."

And this *Hashem l'negdi tamid* also brings about that the *avodah* of a Jew, which, as mentioned above, encompasses both realms of human life, both the internal and the external, should be carried out with joy and goodness of heart. As the Alter Rebbe, *Baal HaTanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, explains at length: when a Jew contemplates how the Ribono shel Olam is with every Jew, gives them His *Torah* and *mitzvos*, and desires to always be, *kiviyachol*, with every Jew, **"And I will dwell among them"** (*v'shachanti b'socham*) — within each and every one — the heart must be filled with the greatest joy and enthusiasm.

* * *

May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that every single man and woman should achieve true and full *chirus*, the spiritual and physical liberation, and from this liberation may we come, speedily in our days, to the full and true *Geulah* through *Moshiach Tzidkeinu*.

With the blessing of a kosher and joyous *Chag HaPesach*,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 7258

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished, occupied with communal needs, possessor of noble character, scion of a distinguished family, etc., R' Shneur Zalman, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I trust you have arrived safely in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. Every time one arrives there, it is considered an "ascent" (*aliyah*). I send you, along with all of Klal Yisrael, my heartfelt wishes that you continue to ascend higher and higher in fulfilling the words of our Sages, "I was created only to serve my Maker." What is especially dear to us, Anash, is the dissemination of the teachings of Chassidus and its guidance. Since our Torah is a "Torah of life," it connects spiritual and material matters, ultimately bringing them to a state of complete unity.

It is understood that the above includes my warm gratitude for your assistance to Kfar Chabad, the Chabad settlement in Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established, and the other Chabad institutions in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. And according to the statement of our Sages, "one mitzvah leads to another," my hope is strong that this will be the case regarding the new Kfar Chabad (even if as a branch of the aforementioned Kfar Chabad)—which would be, by my count, the third Kfar Chabad, and by your count, the second. May this be accomplished with tranquility, joy, and a glad heart, in a manner of ever-increasing activity and outstanding success.

With respect and blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, and for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## Gerant

B.H., 11 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Professor Yehuda Even Shmuel, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings,

A few days ago, Mrs. Chana Sulzberger visited me and delivered your personal regards, as well as the first three volumes of the *Moreh Nevuchim* published by you. I thank you for your thoughtfulness and your gift. I trust you will also send the remaining volumes as they are published, and I thank you in advance. In general, I would be interested in receiving your other publications for my library in exchange for our own publications that might interest you, according to the catalog being sent to you.

I was particularly impressed by the effort you invested in these volumes as an editor and commentator, especially since I have heard several times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the leaders of Chabad—beginning with the Baal HaTanya, whose *Shulchan Aruch* cites the *Moreh Nevuchim* in many places—have always held the Rambam and his books, including the *Moreh Nevuchim*, in high regard. Furthermore, the Tzemach Tzedek had a special *shiur* in *Moreh Nevuchim* with his youngest son, who was as dear to him as his own soul. He would explain the *Moreh Nevuchim* based on the foundations of Chassidus and Kabbalah, as evidenced by several remaining manuscripts, which have also been printed in the *Reshimot* of the Tzemach Tzedek on the *Moreh Nevuchim*. I have instructed that *Sefer HaChakirah* by the Tzemach Tzedek be sent to you in a separate package, where the aforementioned notes appear in print, in addition to the Rambam’s theory of attributes, which is explained in several *maamarim* of Chassidus that are still in manuscript form [in addition to the *maamar* in *Likutei Torah* by our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, *d.h. Eileh Pekudei HaMishkan*, page 6c].

As we approach the festival of Matzos, the season of our freedom, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good, I hereby express my blessing to you for a kosher and happy holiday and for true freedom—freedom from material worries and spiritual worries—from everything that hinders the *avodah* of Hashem with joy and a glad heart. May you continue this freedom throughout all the days of the year, especially since the *avodah* of Hashem, as we are commanded in our Torah, the Torah of life, encompasses all of a person’s affairs throughout the entire day and all the night, as it is said, "In all your ways, know Him."

With respect and holiday blessings,

I will add a note, though on the face of it it is minor: given the introduction, where the name of the Rambam is holy to the highest degree in the eyes of the entire nation and all its circles, every detail associated with him is etched in a special form. Therefore, what appears on the envelope—"Rambam" without the abbreviation marks—contains a sort of "dissonance." In normal years, perhaps one would not pay much attention to this, but in our current era, where, unfortunately, there are those who wish to create a break between the generations and erase several hundred years from the history of our people, every nuance and thread that connects the present with the past in an unbroken continuity must be guarded, strengthened, and reinforced, even when it is only a matter of quotation marks and abbreviation signs.

On the other hand, moving to another subject, I was pleased to see that although in the precise copy the name of the book should be *Moreh HaNevuchim*, with the definite article, as cited several times even in the words of the translator Ibn Tibbon, it has been accepted among the people of Israel to write it without the *hei*, as it also appears on the envelope and in the page headers of your edition.

## 716

B"H, Erev Pesach, 5720
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and distinguished one, who engages in the work of Heaven,
R' Shmuel, may he live,

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter of the 9th of Nissan.

I was pleased to read of your proposal to organize a gathering of school students in your district in connection with the bicentennial year of the histalkus and hillula of the Baal Shem Tov.

It is understood that since music is also mentioned in this regard, you must ensure (ba'varenen) that it is performed only by boys and men, and this is simple to understand.

Regarding separation: if it is possible, it is worthwhile to hold the gathering for boys and girls at the same time, in order to **highlight** the concept of separation. However, if it is not possible to guarantee the separation, or if there is even a doubt—and all the more so regarding the matter of music—then there is no choice, and the condition of "it is impossible otherwise" must apply, meaning there should be two separate gatherings.

Regarding what you wrote about distributing gifts: I have passed this on to the committee regarding the *Kuntres Mincha Ma'ariv*. Perhaps it would be worthwhile to translate the *sicha* from Gan Yisroel here into Lashon HaKodesh, as it is appropriate for students of that age, and it contains sayings from all our Nesi'im.

At an *eis ratzon*, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever they may need. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach for you and your family, may they live, and with tidings of good news.

P.S.
In accordance with the urgency of the matter, this letter is being sent without waiting for its turn.

***

**R' Shmuel, may he live:** Chefer, Bnei Brak. Further letters to him: above, Vol. 17, 5891; below, 7001.

## 770

B"H, 18 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the *pidyon nefesh* along with its enclosure.

At an auspicious time, it will be mentioned, along with all those you wrote about, at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

It is a great wonder that in all your letters you do not mention anything regarding your holy activities—that is, the fulfillment of your duty to disseminate Torah and *mitzvos* wherever your hand can reach. After all, it is clear that matters of Torah and *mitzvos* **are themselves** the conduit and the vessels for the blessings of Hashem and their drawing down. Efforts made through natural means are nothing more than the creation of vessels in the natural order for what has already been decreed and drawn down from Above. Furthermore, the creation of these vessels is necessary only because of the order of this world, not because of the essence of the matter itself. This is explained in many places, including in the *Kuntres U'Maayan* on the verse, "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do." From this, it follows *a fortiori*—if one exerts themselves and strives to the utmost, without regard for any obstacles or hindrances, in the effort to create a vessel for a mundane matter, how much more so must there be effort regarding the essential matter! Given the simplicity of the matter, there is certainly no need for further explanation for someone like you.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding the above, with the premise that the ability has been given to every single one of the children of Israel to accomplish this, since everyone has been commanded in this. Surely the words of the Baal Shem Tov and the *Nesi'im* of Chabad in their explanation of this are trustworthy: that this is what is meant by the verse, "From Hashem are the steps of man established, and He desires his way."

With blessings for good tidings and for a kosher and happy Pesach.

Due to the holiness of the festival, the Rebbe shlita has not signed personally, and I sign on his behalf.

The Secretary

## 6,263

B"H, 18 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Chaim, may he live, HaLevi.

Shalom u'Bracha!

I was pleased to receive your letter from the eve of the festival of Pesach, the season of our freedom, in which you write regarding the success of your activities, especially in the area of education on the basis of purity and holiness, even though much is still lacking. My hope is strong that the success achieved until now will awaken within you additional, inner, and essential powers to strive in these matters and even more so. This is all the more true—*kal v'chomer*—given that in your efforts at the inception of this work, when, as Chazal say, "all beginnings are difficult," Hashem granted you success in the current situation. It is understood that it is most distressing that there are factors that interfere, etc., as you wrote, but "there is no one among us who knows" the reason for the conduct of this physical world of ours, which is called the *olam* of *kelipos*, etc., as is written in *Tanya*, chapter 6 and 33, and in many other places. Yet, we see the wonders of the One who is perfect in knowledge, that specifically in this *olam* the Torah was given, and specifically in this *olam* the *Ribono shel Olam* desired to have a *dirah b'tachtonim* (dwelling place in the lower realms)—see there in *Tanya*, chapter 36. Rather, it is incumbent upon man, whose *neshamah* is a "part of Elokus from above" and who was created in His image and likeness, to prepare the *dirah* and refine it, and this is well understood.

May it be the will that you carry out what has been mentioned within the framework of your general activities of spreading Yiddishkeit and its *mitzvos*, from a state of true freedom from all matters that distract from the service of Hashem, with joy and goodness of heart.

With blessings for good tidings and a kosher and happy Pesach.

Due to the holiness of the festival, the Rebbe shlita has not signed, and I am signing on his behalf.

## Jerso

B"H, 20 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

You have surely received my response to your previous letter in a timely manner. Regarding the subject at hand, and by way of introduction: it is well known that the demand and directives of our Rebbes are that a Yid must conduct his affairs with joy and a good heart. Not only must he do so, but he is capable of doing so. This is not merely a matter of accepting the yoke of Heaven; when one engages in the proper contemplation, one can explain this even to the *nefesh habehamis*, until the intellect of the *nefesh habehamis* itself understands and agrees to it.

To my great surprise, in every one of your letters—regardless of the many positive changes from one to the next—the common denominator remains a profound dissatisfaction with your situation in [Jerso], both materially and spiritually. No matter how much is written regarding the success in matters of Yiddishkeit, it is immediately followed by the sentiment that it is not as it should be, and that it can be, and must be, different.

It is understood that the intent of *shlichus* is not only to bring Yiddishkeit to [Jerso], nor is it merely that one is doing a favor for the Yidden of [Jerso]; rather, it is primarily a source of benefit and good for the person performing the *shlichus* themselves, in their own personal affairs.

Just as in all human endeavors, it is possible that your decision could have been different, or made in a different manner. Therefore, I wish to emphasize once again—what should be self-evident—that the matter of your travel and the *shlichus* is not intended to be done against your will. Furthermore, it is certainly understood that after a trial period of a year or more, it must not be a matter of being there against your will, as this also impacts the success of the endeavor.

The intent of the above is that regarding your decision for the future, you should feel completely free in your situation (together with your husband, the Rav, may he live and be well) in [Jerso], just as if you were currently in Brooklyn and had to decide whether to go there. After proper contemplation of the matter, inform me of your decision—naturally, in open terms—and we will see to arranging the matter according to your decision.

May it be the will of Hashem Yisbarach, who oversees each and every one with *hashgacha pratis*, to lead you and your husband, the Rav, may he live and be well, in goodness in all details, in a goodness that is visible and revealed, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good tidings.

Due to the sanctity of the *moed*, the Rebbe shlita has not signed personally, and I sign on his behalf.

The Secretary

## 767

B"H, 23 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 29 Adar, which has just been received, in which you write the main points regarding your family situation and your current means of livelihood.

It is understood and simple that there is no place at all to say that there is, Heaven forbid, a decree upon a person from the Children of Israel that their livelihood must necessarily be in a manner contrary to the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of Life. This is all the more so when the person in question is in the Holy Land, may it be built and established, of which it is said, "The eyes of Hashem your G-d are upon it from the beginning of the year to the end of the year." Rather, for reasons known to the Creator and Guide of the world—which we cannot fathom—a trial is sometimes presented to a Jewish man and woman. When they firmly resolve to withstand the trial, the Ribono shel Olam assists them, as is explained in the words of our Sages in many places. Certainly, regarding your situation, the difficulties are fewer than elsewhere, since, as you write, you reside in Bnei Brak, which is known and famous for the observance of Shabbos Kodesh within it, and in matters of Torah and mitzvos in general. And since it is said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation," you should consult with your friends after detailing the situation to them and what you have experienced until now. The Ribono shel Olam will grant them the correct idea of how to advise you, especially since we are coming from the time of our freedom, which is freedom from all matters that distract from the avodah of the Ribono shel Olam.

Since the above also indicates a lack of bitachon, etc., it is appropriate that you have your tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos in your home, to ensure they are all kosher according to the law. Furthermore, every weekday before morning davening, set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

May it be His will that you strengthen your bitachon in the Ribono shel Olam, who oversees each and every person with hashgacha pratis, and may your resolution for the good in all the above draw down the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam in all that is needed.

With blessings for good tidings in all that is mentioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6160

B”H, 23 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 18 Nissan, in which you write regarding the matter of a shidduch: the essential point is missing from your letter, in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, Toras Chaim. The primary requirement is as it is written, “A woman who fears Hashem, she shall be praised” (Mishlei 31:30)—meaning, the standing of the young woman in question regarding Yiddishkeit and mitzvos as they relate to actual daily life. For the conduct of the home, and to a significant extent the conduct of the husband as well, depends on the attitude of the *akeres habayis*—the woman—toward these matters. Furthermore, it is understood that one should not approach the matter of a shidduch and marriage while mixing in the issue of *chinuch*—attempting to change the woman and her outlook. These are two separate matters, and one should not be mixed with the other. Additionally, it is not clear from your letter whether you have clarified these points with her, or whether you have not yet spoken about this decisively.

Since it appears from your letter that you are not entirely objective about the matter—which is not surprising—it would be appropriate for you to ask your friends to clarify what I wrote at the beginning of this letter, namely, regarding the religious standing of the young woman in question, and then see how to proceed.

May it be the will of Hashem, who oversees each and every person with *hashgacha pratis*, that He guide you in the best way regarding all of the above.

It is understood that every matter requires *siyatta d’shmaya* and the blessing of Hashem, and the way of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is *middah k’neged middah*, only many times over. Therefore, it is most appropriate that you utilize the time you must still spend in your current surroundings to disseminate Yiddishkeit and its matters there. This is in accordance with the instruction of Chazal that “the deed is the essential thing”—meaning, the performance of practical mitzvos. Through this, by increasing the blessings of Hashem for those you influence (by bringing their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven), you will increase the blessings of Hashem in your own affairs.

It is appropriate that you have your tefillin checked (if this has not been done within the last twelve months), and also that every weekday, before putting on tefillin, you set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

#### ***6160***

**The matter of *chinuch*:** See also above, letter 6122, and the references in the notes there.

## 700

B"H, 23 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter.

When you provide your mother’s name as well (as is the custom to mention in prayer), you will be mentioned at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the matters about which you write.

Regarding what you wrote about distracting thoughts: The advice given for this, first and foremost, is to have your tefillin checked to ensure they are kosher according to the law. Furthermore, you should divert your mind from all the thoughts you wrote about. This diversion is not a battle against the thoughts, but rather a matter of moving the mind and shifting it to other subjects—and it is best to focus on matters of Torah. For if a little light dispels much darkness, how much more so does a great deal of light.

Regarding your statement that your explanation of the shiurim you teach is insufficient: Since our Sages have said, "Who is wise? He who learns from every person," it would be appropriate for you to attend the shiurim given by the teachers and rabbis in your vicinity, and observe their method of explanation and delivery of the shiur in detail.

Regarding your mention of the pronunciation of the letters: It can be said that this is connected to your being nervous. When you strengthen your sense of bitachon in Hashem, who oversees each and every person with hashgacha pratis, there will be an improvement in this area as well. It would be appropriate for you to study *Shaar HaBitachon* in the sefer *Chovos HaLevavos*. Additionally, you should maintain the monthly Tehillim schedule (as Tehillim is divided for the days of the month) and recite it every day after morning davening. Every weekday, before morning davening, set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above.

Regarding your questions:
a) Why is the pregnancy not mentioned regarding Hevel, unlike with Kayin (Bereishis 4:1-2)?
The reason is that Hevel was already present during the conception of Kayin (*Bereishis Rabbah* 22:3).

b) The reason for the name Hevel, and why it is not stated [in the same way] as with Kayin?
It can be said that this is because he was merely an addition and secondary to the primary pregnancy, which was Kayin, and the Torah spared us from explicitly stating his lack of importance. A hint is sufficient in the word **"vatosof"** (and she added), which implies nothing more than an addition (see *Bereishis Rabbah* 61:4).

On behalf of the Rebbe,

Secretary

## Z'erev

B"H, 25 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yitzchak, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled, and in accordance with your request, it is being sent without waiting for its turn.

Based on what is explained in many places regarding the *nachas ruach* of the souls of the departed, it is understood that one should not engage in matters that would, G-d forbid, detract from the *chinuch* on the purity of holiness of many sons and daughters of Israel. On the contrary—one should increase efforts in this area, and this will increase the *nachas ruach* and the elevation of their souls. From this, it is understood regarding your holy work in the holy institution named after my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya*, Nasi of Israel, and regarding matters for the merit of the soul: one should include the study of Mishnayos in public—at the very least, the completion of the study in public—with the addition of some explanation suitable for the understanding of the listeners, and it is best to add a Chassidic concept appropriate to their understanding. And surely you will be able to recite *Kaddish D'Rabbanan* afterward. This study can be arranged before *davening* or after *davening*, in your specific case, in order to fulfill the number of *Kaddishim*.

It is also appropriate, as is customary in any case, to give a few coins to *tzedakah* every weekday before the morning *davening* for the merit of the soul, and likewise before the *Mincha* *davening* (even if it is a smaller amount than the aforementioned). It is understood that all of the above should be done *bli neder*.

Regarding what you wrote that you *daven* *Maariv* while it is still day—there are several reasons for leniency found in the books of the *poskim*, especially since you surely recite *Krias Shema* afterward at its proper time, and likewise *Sefirah*. However, regarding *Sefirah*, you will surely manage to count **only** after *tzeis hakochavim*, since the counting is done in private. Furthermore, there is hope that perhaps a few more of the residents of the *moshav* will do as you do because of this.

As a side note and a remark on the matter: if, as mentioned above, the *Sefirah* of the following day is also counted while it is still day, one should arrange to count again the next day—naturally without a *bracha*—at the time of *Shacharis*. In any case, there are those who count the same *Sefirah* at night and also during the day...

May Hashem, who repairs the breaches of His people Israel, gladden you and your brothers, may they live, with true joy and goodness, and may you bring good tidings in a revealed and manifest way.

With blessings for good tidings.
