## 770

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from after Pesach, I am certain that the promise of our Sages will be fulfilled for you—that whoever is granted goodness, it is for long, good days and years. And since you bring good news of visible goodness at the beginning of your letter, may you continue to bring good news regarding the other matters you wrote about in this letter and the previous one. This, of course, is also simply a result of increasing the *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah* and your success in this endeavor.

Regarding what you wrote—that there is a question that confuses you, for which you have not yet found an answer, and you are suffering from this doubt, etc.—and you are asking for sources and references where you might find the answer to your question:

The question is: What is the reason that the performance of *mitzvos* is required of us even in a situation and state where the matter involves difficulties and toil, to the point of being a *nisayon* (test)?

It is surprising that there is doubt or a question regarding such a simple matter. Let me explain: This doubt could only have a place in one of two scenarios: a) If the One who commanded the *mitzvah* had commanded it in an incomplete manner—meaning, He only gave the general principles and the details were missing, in which case there would be room for various doubts regarding those matters that were not specified. b) If the One who commanded the *mitzvah* could not have foreseen every possible situation and state in which the person commanded might find himself, and therefore it would be impossible to know if one is commanded to fulfill the directive even in that specific situation.

Since the foundation of our faith (and, incidentally, this is the foundation of other faiths as well, *lehavdil*) is that the One who commanded the *mitzvah* is the ultimate perfection, it is therefore evident in the *mitzvos* themselves, which were given in a clear manner. Furthermore, He is the One who knows the future, and in the perfection of His wisdom, He foresaw every possible situation and state in which the recipient of the command might find himself in the present and in the future—the near future and even the distant future. Therefore, the two aforementioned conditions certainly do not exist.

Consequently, one must find in the Torah of the One who commanded the *mitzvah* the manner and requirement for fulfilling the *mitzvah*, which has no limitations other than the one limitation: "And he shall live by them," etc. As explained by our Sages in many places (among them Yoma 85b), from this we learn that only *pikuach nefesh* (saving a life) overrides the matters of the Torah, and nothing else. Similarly, other limitations that exist regarding *mitzvos*—such as the *hiddur mitzvah* (beautification of a *mitzvah*) up to a third—are also explicitly explained in the Torah of the One who commanded the *mitzvah*, in such a way that there is no room for any doubt. With this, your doubt is also negated.

And since we have come from the festival of Pesach, the time of our freedom, may it be His will that you be freed from all limitations and matters that distract you from the *avodah* of the *Ribono shel Olam* with joy and a good heart.

At a time of *ratzon*, you should be mentioned at the *tziyon* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for whatever you are in need of.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

*[Nissan, 5720]*

## 7282

B”H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the honorable Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, who is occupied with communal needs, may he live,
Rabbi Sh. Z. [Zevin],

Peace and blessing!

Following a silence to which you are not accustomed, your letter from Motzaei Shabbos was received. I await further good news regarding the rabbinical position. I have written on this matter to the esteemed Chossid, etc., Rabbi Sh. D. Zislin, and likewise to my friend, the esteemed Chossid, etc., Rabbi A. Z. Slonim, as indicated in your letter. After all, the rabbinate in the Chabad shul in Tel Aviv was merely an internal matter... It is understood that my intention is not to complain about the past, but rather regarding the near future; it is worth striving as much as possible for the aforementioned rabbinate to have an official standing, in a way that also allows for influence beyond the confines of the shul, as mentioned above. Regarding the details of that matter, I am interested in knowing your esteemed opinion regarding a suitable candidate for the position of Rabbi in the Chabad shul in Tel Aviv.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning the writing of [the year] 5720, and your desire to find support from the fact that in some calendars the *kaf* in the middle is printed as a final *kaf* (*kaf peshuta*), from which one might argue *kal v’chomer* for the end of the word.

In my opinion, there is no *kal v’chomer* or *kal v’chomer* logic here, since the explanation for writing a *kaf peshuta* at the beginning or middle of a word—it is impossible that it is because of the concept of final letters. Perhaps the writer intended to rule out the substitution of the letter *nun* (*nun kefufa*), which in his handwriting looked similar to a *kaf kefufa*, and the like.

Similarly, regarding what you wrote that in some *maamarim* of *Chassidus* and letters of our Rebbes, the year 5720 is written with a *kaf peshuta* at the end—I believe I already commented on this in my letter to the question from Jerusalem (a copy of which was sent to you), that one should not bring proof from isolated cases. Especially since the custom of *Bnei Yisrael* is to use allusions and hints, etc. [For example, it is known regarding the *Hemshech* "Tiku" of 5650, which is cited in many places with a *nun peshuta*. And in several manuscripts and letters, *maamarim* from that year are mentioned under the name "Year of Rinnat"]. The issue at hand is standard, daily writing, regarding which, in my opinion, the proofs you write of in your letter fall away...

Regarding what you wrote about the customs of *hagbah*, etc.—as is apparent from your letter, they have already implemented this in the shul a few times, with the argument that this is the custom in the shul where the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, used to daven.

Now, even if initially your reasons for opposing a change in custom were perhaps correct, especially since the elders of *Anash* in previous generations were accustomed to this when they came to the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt, the problem now is: should one touch upon the point of *hiskashrus* that someone has to our Rebbes, even if it is expressed to an excessive degree?

One can connect this to the story of *Chazal* (*Sukkah* 32b, end of page): "He would be careful..." because "since it came from his mouth"—even though certainly the author of the ruling himself, Rav Kahana, did not insist that it specifically be two and one, but rather, since it came from his mouth, his student must be careful to act in accordance with his words. This is where the connection is highlighted, and all the more so in the present case, which is a practical matter. Furthermore, one who sees the change will be prompted to ask the reason and will receive the answer, that this is the custom of our Rebbes, etc., and as *Chazal* say, "until Chevron." As mentioned, the main point in all this is that to revert the custom now to how it was would weaken the position that one must strive to conduct oneself according to the customs of the shul of the Rebbe, my father-in-law.

With respect and blessing for good news,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7,283

B"H, 2 Iyar, 5720, Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Bicentennial Year of the Histalkus-Hillula
of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, involved in the needs of the community, R' Chananya Yosef, may he live,
Gabbai of the Beis Yosef-Chabad Synagogue in Jerusalem,
the Holy City,
may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily and in our days, Amen.

Shalom and Blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 27 Nissan, the month of Geulah, Erev Rosh Chodesh Ziv, in which you bring good tidings regarding the completion of the Shas, which is being studied publicly in the synagogue in the coming week.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the completion be marked by joy, enthusiasm, light, and radiance, as should the new beginning, in accordance with the text of the prayer: "to learn and to teach, to observe, to perform, and to fulfill, etc." May the conclusion of this prayer be fulfilled in each and every one: "that the Torah shall not depart from my mouth, nor from the mouth of my children, nor from the mouth of my children's children, from now and forever." And in their days and in our days, may we merit the fulfillment of the promise as written in the conclusion of that prayer and at the completion of the Shas: "Hashem will give strength to His people; Hashem will bless His people with peace," with the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu. At that time, there will be no jealousy or competition, etc., and the Jewish people will be great sages, knowing the hidden matters, etc.

Our Rebbeim, the Nesi'im, have already explained that the attainment of this ultimate goal depends upon our deeds and our avodah throughout the entire duration of the Golus, etc.

That despite the double and redoubled darkness of the night of Golus, we shall "recite the Shema" in this evening [service] until the dawn rises—the dawn of the true and complete Geulah, speedily and in our days, Amen.

With respect and with blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

#### ***7,283***

**R' Chananya Yosef:** Halperin. Another letter to him—above, Vol. 18, 6,776.

**With the coming of Moshiach:** See Rashi to Tehillim 29:11; Tanya, Chapter 36.

**There will be no:** Rambam at the conclusion of his Yad HaChazakah.

**Our Rebbeim have already explained:** Tanya, beginning of Chapter 37.

**Recite the Shema:** Meaning: Accept, know, and believe. The acknowledgement of the Unity and the faith, etc., upon which all the mitzvos of the Torah depend (Chinuch, Mitzvah 417, in abbreviated form).

**Dawn of the Geulah:** Beginning of the Jerusalem Talmud: R' Chiya Rabba said to R' Shimon ben Chalafta (the conclusion of the Shas), etc.: "For though I sit in darkness, Hashem is a light unto me."

## 784

784

B”H, 5 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

After a long hiatus, your letter from the beginning of the month of Iyar was received. At an auspicious time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

It is understandable that I am alarmed, in addition to being greatly surprised and bewildered, by the conclusion of your letter, in which you write that you have resigned from being [a mashpia], etc., though you continue to learn with three bochurim and one avreich, etc. Can it be believed that this is the way one utilizes all of one’s capacity, as is required in a person’s avodah—to be as one **ought** to be? As is understood from the statement of our Sages that the Holy One, blessed be He, did not create anything in His world in vain, from which it is understood—and it is also simple—that if one does not utilize all of one’s capacity, one disrupts the entirety of creation and its order. This is especially so according to what is explained in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov regarding the concept of Divine Providence, that every detail completes the supernal intent. From this it is understood that if a detail, Heaven forbid, fails to utilize its capacity, etc.—it is difficult to elaborate on such an alarming matter, especially for one who has merited to serve for some time as a mashpia for others in matters of Chassidus and its conduct (the foundation of which is joy and a good heart, and consequently, the greatest possible energy). In place of this, your "good" eye is [focused] on your own affairs and the affairs of others, and as mentioned, you are learning with... three bochurim and one avreich.

It is understood that there is surely room to write an excuse that so-and-so did not conduct himself as he ought, etc., but this does not exempt you at all from the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos. The fact that so-and-so is not conducting himself as he ought in his own affairs—and in general, the gates of excuses are never locked, even when the matter is difficult and absurd—still stands.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that immediately upon receiving this letter, you will increase your influence in your surroundings, and first and foremost in the Yeshiva..., in a manner of "spreading outward" (*u’fartzta*) in the literal and simple sense, without any pretexts. In addition to the obligation to increase every single day in the *u’fartzta* of that day, there should also be a rectification of the deficiency of the past, similar to what is explained in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, end of Chapter 9, "he was accustomed," etc., and "there is nothing that can stand before the will," even in the aforementioned matter.

With blessings for good tidings in all that has been said.

## 750

B"H, 5 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Iyar, in which you write some of your reasoning regarding your place of work in Chinuch al Taharat HaKodesh for the upcoming school year, and also mention the content of the sicha from 10 Shevat, the hillula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that one should not necessarily chase after greatness, etc.

Regarding the field of Chinuch, there is another point to add to the aforementioned one, which is also fundamental: it is very often difficult to gauge the future of a student and their potential. That is to say, it is entirely possible that even those who appear simple at first glance may, in the future, reveal talents or a capacity for perseverance and diligence such that they will succeed in their studies and conduct far more than those who are merely talented. Indeed, they may become the pride of the school and their teachers. As we have seen tangibly in all times, the magnitude of the impact of the power of perseverance—even when the talent was simple—and likewise, how exceptional talents have been revealed that were not anticipated at all from the outset. This is especially true in the school where you have worked until now, which, judging by your description, fits the statement of our Sages: "Be careful with the children of the poor, for from them will come Torah." Regarding this school in particular, you have a special responsibility and certainly a special inclination, for it is natural for a person to cherish the work of their hands.

From what has been said above, my opinion is understood: that you should continue with strong hope and confidence in the school where you have served in holiness until now. Surely, your dedication to this work will be the channel and vessel for additional success in your work and for additional blessing in your personal matters and in the matters of your family members, who, as you requested, will be mentioned at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in whose name the school is named and in whose spirit it is conducted.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
As per your request, the letter is being sent without waiting for its turn.

## 7288

B"H, 6 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the Avreich Meir, may he live,
Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 2nd of Iyar.

1) Regarding the recitation of Tachanun during Krias Shema al Hamitah on Motzaei Shabbos:

The instruction is understood from the recitation of Tachanun in Selichos on Motzaei Shabbos, which takes place after halachic midnight. From this, one can learn the answer to your question: it depends on whether the time for Krias Shema is before midnight or after it.

2) Regarding the repetition of the three words in Krias Shema:

The various opinions on this in the Shulchan Aruch and the Acharonim are well-known. It is surprising that you are asking from overseas; regarding the practical ruling, you should ask the elders of Anash, for *maaseh rav* (the actual practice of a great person) is the deciding factor.

It gave me pleasure to read in your letter about your activities within the framework of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, and surely you will influence your peers in this regard as well. May it be His will that through this, you will also be granted additional blessings from Hashem in your persistence and diligence in your studies of Nigleh and Chassidus, and in the performance of mitzvos with hidur.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## Zartzev

B"H, 9 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with the needs of the community, R' Yisrael, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

Following the letter on behalf of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 2nd of Iyar, the birthday of the Rebbe Maharash, as well as your previous letters. I believe I have already written that I would request that the special fund contribute up to one-third of the expenses for the farbrengens that have taken place, as well as regarding Lag B'Omer and the printing matters you mention in your letter of the 2nd of Iyar.

Regarding what you wrote about so-and-so—concerning his work in Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, I believe I have already written several times that it is difficult to give instructions from here regarding specific individuals, as the matter depends on many details.

In your letter, you mention that his work in the activities of the *pe'ilim* involves travel, and that at times this will detract from his ability to serve as *chazzan* and from the number of *Kaddishim* he recites. I have already written regarding such matters several times: it is obvious that *nachas ruach* and an *aliyah* for the soul cannot come through a deficiency in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*. Education on the basis of *taharas hakodesh* is a fundamental point in this, and the merit of the many depends on it (which is incomparable to the recitation of *Kaddish*). From this, it is understood that he should not diminish his holy work in education on the basis of *taharas hakodesh*; on the contrary, he should increase it.

In order that there be no lack (as far as possible) in the aforementioned, there is room for him to arrange for someone else to recite *Kaddish* at times when he is unable to do so himself, and in this way, his holy work will not be compromised. May it be His will that in this, too, the principle of "one *mitzvah* draws another *mitzvah*" will be fulfilled.

It is surprising that, apparently between the lines and from information received from other sources, the *shmurah* matzah campaign this year seems to have been more limited compared to previous years, even though, logically, the opposite should have been the case.

With blessings for good tidings in both general and personal matters.

From the funds that will be received from the special fund, please be kind enough to deliver one hundred and eighty lira to Rabbi Yisrael Hess, may he live, of Ra'anana, for the expenses of his activities in education on the basis of *taharas hakodesh*.

#### ***Zartzev***

**R' Yisrael, may he live:** Libov, Kfar Chabad. Additional letters to him—above 7,088, and in the references noted there.

## 6393

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Beis Rivkah Teachers’ Seminary
And the Administration of the Beis Rivkah School,
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 8 Iyar, in which you write regarding the scheduling of the upcoming summer vacation, noting several reasons for changing the arrangement that has been in place until now.

As you conclude in your letter, this matter and its details should be consulted upon in accordance with local conditions—that is, the circumstances of the students’ homes and their parents—and, of course, one must also take into account the arrangements in France regarding educational institutions of a similar nature that are based on *taharas hakodesh*.

The general points regarding this, although they cannot always be fully articulated, are that any reduction in vacation time from *limudei kodesh* is commendable; this is obvious and simple.

b) During times when there are no secular studies, the student is better able to absorb *limudei kodesh* with greater breadth and depth, since they are not occupied with other areas.

c) Another point in this regard is that it also emphasizes, in matters of education, the distinction between *kodesh* and *chol*, between light and darkness; that the former is a study for specific times, whereas the primary study is something additional to it, etc.

As mentioned above, this is presented as a general point. Regarding the practical application, while the above must be taken into account, it is essential to consider the aforementioned conditions.

With blessings for outstanding success in your *avodah* in the *kodesh* of educating the daughters of Israel, each of whom is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah.

## 7294

7294

B"H, Sunday, Parshas Emor, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the annual testimonial dinner of the Lubavitcher Yeshiva in Newark,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I send my greetings and blessing to all the honored guests and participants, shlita, in the annual dinner of the Lubavitcher Yeshiva in Newark. I hope that this endeavor will exceed all expectations in providing the necessary assistance—both spiritual and financial—through the special efforts of all the friends of the Yeshiva.

This year is a special *segulah* year for institutions of education *al taharas hakodesh*, combining *nigleh* and Chassidus.

It is the 200th year since the *histalkus-hilula* of the holy Baal Shem Tov (the first day of Shavuos, *zman matan toraseinu*), the founder of the general *Toras HaChassidus*, the spiritual "grandfather" of the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, and the founder of *Toras Chassidus Chabad*—may their merit protect us.

The first activity of the Baal Shem Tov, even before he was *niskaleh* (revealed), was as an assistant, teaching young children the holy letters of the *alef-beis*, *brachos* and *tefillos*, *amen yehei shmei rabba*, *barechu*, and *kedusha*. At the same time, he also raised great students and *geonim* in Torah and Chassidus, to illuminate the dark *galus* in these generations of *ikvesa d'meshicha*.

The Lubavitcher Yeshiva in Newark, like many other Lubavitcher *mosdos haTorah al taharas hakodesh*—may they increase—is a link in the golden chain that extends from the Baal Shem Tov. Here, the two fundamental points of the *shitas* of the Baal Shem Tov are united: *chinuch al taharas hakodesh* from a young age—from the *ketanim*—in such a way that they will subsequently become the true *gedolim*, those who carry out the instructions of "Great is Hashem and highly praised," by spreading the light of Torah and *mitzvos* upon the foundations of *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael*.

In order to realize this, however, there must first be the "to warn the adults regarding the children"—the adults, parents, *askanim*, and friends of the Yeshiva must provide the opportunity for the Yeshiva and the students to grow and ascend and become what they need to be: *neros leha'ir*, shining lights that illuminate their entire surroundings.

With a blessing for success in *gashmius* and *ruchnius*, and with respect,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7,297

B"H, 14 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday, in which you write regarding the will of Rabbi Yehuda HeChassid concerning the names of a bride and her mother-in-law.

It appears that the report you were told in the name of the Tzemach Tzedek is correct: since one of them has two names, then, in his holy language, there is no concern in the world whatsoever. See Responsa of the Tzemach Tzedek, Even HaEzer, Siman 143, and Piskei Dinim of the Tzemach Tzedek, Yoreh Deah, Siman 116.

2) It is understood that the second name must not be "forgotten" (nishtakea) in such a way that the names become identical. The definition of a name that has been "forgotten" is brought in the Tur and Shulchan Aruch and its commentaries, Siman 129.

And here, I have the duty and the privilege to urge you regarding the necessity of establishing fixed times for the study of the inner dimension of Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. If in all places and at all times this was a necessity, how much more so in our era and in these countries in particular—and especially as you stand before your wedding, the building of a home in Israel, an everlasting edifice.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 7,898

B"H, 15 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs, R' Yitzchak, may he live:

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter of 12 Iyar, along with the *pidyon nefesh* which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory:

1) Regarding your question at the end of Chapter 1 of *Tanya*: "And also the good character traits that are in the nature of all Jews, such as compassion and acts of kindness, come from it"—why did he not also include the trait of bashfulness?

The reason is that this is not **in the nature** [of a Jew], by birth. On the contrary, "Jews are the boldest of the nations," and [bashfulness] is acquired over time (*Nedarim* 20a, *Beitzah* 25b).

2) Regarding the statement earlier: "At the time he commits sins he is called a complete *rasha*, and if he later does *teshuvah* he is called a complete *tzaddik*"—what is his status before he has done *teshuvah*?

The *halacha* is decided in *nigleh* regarding those disqualified from testifying, and in *Chassidus* it is explained that sin creates a stain. Before he has done *teshuvah*, the stain remains in its place, and consequently, so does the status.

Regarding your news of your grandson, Shneur Zalman, may he live, reaching the age of *mitzvos*: May it be His will that from the age of thirteen for *mitzvos*, he should grow to the age of fifteen for *Gemara*, etc., as the *Mishnah* rules in *Avos*, Chapter 5.

With blessings for good tidings and with proper health,

**M. Schneerson**

***

**7,898**

**R' Yitzchak:** Dubov, Manchester. Additional letters to him appear above, 7,070, and in the notes referenced there.

**Did not also include the trait of bashfulness:** See also above, Vol. 6, 1,793, and the notes referenced there.

## 7,199

B"H, 15 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 10 Iyar, regarding your stuttering, and that you have been under the care of several doctors, but as of yet, it has not helped you.

Since specialists in this field have treatments that are at least helpful to a significant degree, you should inquire about a specialist in this field and turn to him. However, according to the statement of our Sages, that the conduit for receiving the blessings of Hashem is through the matters of Torah and mitzvos, it is understood and simple that you must increase your diligence and perseverance in the study of Torah and your meticulousness in the performance of mitzvos, through which the blessings of Hashem will be increased in the areas you require.

It should also be noted that in most cases, the matter of stuttering is connected to a lack of self-confidence and a fear of people. From this, it is understood that when you have the concept of "I have set Hashem before me always" engraved in your mind at all times—and that He, may He be blessed, is the essence of good and desires to bestow good upon His creations, and oversees each and every one with Divine Providence, as these matters are explained specifically in the teachings of Chassidus—this will diminish and weaken the undesirable symptoms of a lack of self-confidence and fear of people, as it is written, "Hashem is with me, I will not fear."

At an auspicious time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and may it be Hashem's will that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
It is appropriate that you have your tefillin checked to ensure they are kosher according to the law, and also that every weekday, before the morning davening, you set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

***

**7,199**

**In a lack of self-confidence:** See also above, letter 7,173, and the references in the notes there.

## 760

B"H, 16 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 2nd of Parshas Emor.

At an auspicious time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

Regarding your question as to whether one should act with a "strong hand," etc. — it is a well-known instruction of the Great Teacher [the Rambam] in Hilchos Deios to follow the middle path. However, the difficulty is that the doctors in the United States, especially regarding children, advise fulfilling their desires to the extreme. Yet, recently, even they have begun to question the validity of this approach. Since you are in need of the doctors' advice, it is understood that their opinion must be taken into account. However, you should first explain to them the aforementioned point regarding the "golden path"—the middle way—especially when you see undesirable results. After that, you should follow the doctors' instructions, but without being overly meticulous about it.

Since we are currently in the days between Pesach and Shavuos—a time favorable for the health of both body and soul—may your situation improve in all the matters you wrote about, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed; a true good, which is "good for Heaven, good for people, and good that produces fruit" (Kiddushin 40a).

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 761

B”H, Lag B’Omer, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Brownsville and East New York Women’s Association,
May Hashem grant them life,

Blessings and peace!

Your annual celebration, which will take place this coming Tuesday, two days after Lag B’Omer, will surely be imbued with the impression of this current, luminous day of Lag B’Omer.

Lag B’Omer reminds us of two significant moments, which are connected to this day and to one another.

Lag B’Omer underscores the vital necessity of studying and disseminating Torah with ahavas Yisrael and mesiras nefesh, as in the times of the great Tanna Rabbi Akiva and his students.

Lag B’Omer is also the day when one of the greatest of Rabbi Akiva’s students, the holy Tanna Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai, completed his shlichus in this world, beginning to reveal the inner light and secrets of the Torah through the holy sefer Zohar. Through Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai, the Ribono shel Olam opened a new wellspring of deeper Elokus understanding, of emunah and bitachon, to refresh and strengthen the Jewish people in a difficult time of galus.

In a few days, on the first day of Shavuos, Zman Matan Toraseinu, it will be two hundred years since the holy Baal Shem Tov completed his soul’s shlichus—to disseminate and make accessible to **all** Jews the inner light of Torah and mitzvos through Toras HaChassidus. The divine wellsprings that Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai opened for the select few, the Baal Shem Tov opened wide for everyone. Thereby, the Ribono shel Olam showed an even greater chesed to His chosen people in a most critical time of galus.

It is superfluous to emphasize that this time is a special segulah-time for every activity to disseminate Torah and mitzvos with yiras shamayim, ahavas Yisrael, and mesiras nefesh—which is, after all, the mission of the Lubavitcher mosdos and all those who are connected to them.

Upon you, all Jewish mothers and women, especially being connected with the Lubavitcher mosdos, lies a special duty, which is also just as great a zechus, to help carry out this divine intent and shlichus. May the Ribono shel Olam grant success to your work, in an increasing measure, in good health, free from worries and cares, with simcha and vitality, in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

With blessings for success.

## 722

B"H, Lag BaOmer, the Hillula of Rashbi, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the honorable Rabbi, the famous Gaon, wise in Torah and fear of Heaven,
Organizer and sharp-witted scholar,
G-d-fearing, a man of noble character, a man of many virtues, etc., etc.,
Rabbi Yitzchak Rachamim, shlita, Rishon LeZion,
Chief Rabbi

Peace and blessing!

In connection with the completion of two hundred years since the passing-Hillula of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory, on the first day of the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah (and not as those who err, who claim it is on the following day).

I am turning to your honor, shlita, with a suggestion—though it is surely unnecessary, as the matter has certainly already occurred to your honor—to arouse the honorable Rabbis, shlita, in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, to dedicate their talks on this auspicious day, or in close proximity to it, to the personality and teachings of the master of the Hillula, which are founded on the golden pillars of Ahavas Hashem, Ahavas HaTorah, and Ahavas Yisrael, all of which are one. And a word spoken in its time is good.

With great respect and with a blessing to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate to one such as yourself regarding the extra affection known to our Sephardic brethren for the inwardness of Torah since ancient times, and the teachings of Chassidus are indeed the inwardness of the Torah, the *neshamata d'oraita* (soul of the Torah). Although, of course, my intention in the aforementioned arousal is for Ashkenazim and Sephardim alike, as is known from the saying of the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and the Shulchan Aruch, a student of the student of the Baal Shem Tov, that the teachings of Chassidus are the inheritance of the entire nation.

## 744

B"H, 19 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

Regarding what you wrote about your personal situation, I will mention it once again at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

I believe I also mentioned to the esteemed Chossid... regarding him, when he was here, that the only reason I can find for the delay, etc., is that he is "pushing the hour" regarding this matter from the moment he began writing about it. Although it is only regarding "finding a lost object" that they said it comes through complete distraction, in matters of *parnassah* the situation is such that excessive exertion not only does not hasten [the result], but rather, etc. This is similar to what is explained at times in such cases: that although one must utilize the "garments of nature" in matters of *parnassah*—as part of the general needs of a person, and as it is written, "in all that you do" specifically—when one creates these garments beyond the necessary measure, not only does the extra length not assist, but on the contrary, it hinders rapid progress. And although you are correct in your letter that you have been raising this point for some years, I must say that from the very beginning there was excessive exertion and "pushing the hour." However, since a person is not held accountable for his distress, and in addition to this—and this is the main point—the merit of the public assists him, and first and foremost his lofty activities in the matters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, leader of Israel, my hope is strong that the strength of his trust in Hashem will increase his blessing and also hasten it.

May it be the will that this should be very soon, literally, and in a way that is good, visible, and revealed. And since we have just come from the bright day of Lag B'Omer, the *hillula* of Rashbi, whose conduct was "and strangers shall stand and pasture your flocks" (*Berachos 35b*), may it be the will that it should be the same regarding your matters—that is, that your *parnassah* should be with true abundance, and the majority of your time, energy, and talents should be dedicated and sanctified to the matters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

With blessings for truly good tidings, and with true joy, in the immediate future.

## 765

B"H, 19 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After the longest of intervals, your letter from Pesach Sheni was received. My hope is strong that despite the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the study of this day (printed in *Hayom Yom*: "It is never too late"), regarding the matter about which you write, you will stand guard with urgency so that it is carried out in practice, and specifically as our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, require—namely, that it should be in both places simultaneously a fortress of Chassidus, and even more than that: a place from which the matters of Chassidus will spread, and not merely a fortress and shield for those who are within them. This, too, stems from the requirement that "your springs shall spread outward," as flowing water is superior to water that is gathered and fortified in its place.

At a time of favor, please mention all those you write about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may his merit shield us, and may it be His will that you bring good tidings regarding this.

Especially as we find ourselves on the day after the bright day of Lag B'Omer, the hillula of Rashbi. It is said in the name of the Alter Rebbe that for souls as lofty as Rashbi, the Beis Hamikdash was never destroyed at all (*Maamar* "Eileh Shemos," by the great Tzaddik and Chassid, the Rav of Paritch, in his book *Palach HaRimon*, Shemos, page 7). The essence of this is that his task was to draw down the *penimiyus* (inner dimension) into revelation, and this is well understood.

With respect and blessings for good tidings.

## Zheshu

B"H, 19 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter from the 18th of Iyar.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all the matters you wrote about.

Regarding the fact that you did not mention the health of [Name]—may she live and be well—I hope this is a sign that her condition is improving.

Concerning what you wrote regarding the position in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), the arguments in its favor—to win souls for Chassidus, etc.—are well-taken.

Surely, for someone like you, it is unnecessary to elaborate that the situation in this entire area is completely different in Eretz Yisrael than it is here. Here, people are already accustomed to the fact that accepting a position in a certain institution does not constitute a stamp of approval for all the institution’s affairs. This is not the case in Eretz Yisrael, where, in addition to the issue of factionalism, there is also the fact that the opposite of the *ahavas achim* that existed at the time of the destruction—and was its cause—some 1,900 years ago, is still dancing [active]. Consequently, there is a concern that every issue will be magnified and even exaggerated, etc.

Furthermore—and this is also the main point, as I have answered to many regarding similar questions—when one does not relocate to a new country, and the leadership requires correction and improvement, then when one complains and demands changes regarding the leadership, etc., the responses (which are more or less justified) are that the "leaven in the dough" hinders, etc., and it appears like a mountain, etc. This is in addition to the fact that "the land of the nations is impure, and you are the few among the people of the land," etc.

However, when one relocates of his own volition—and especially to the palace of the King, the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He—then all the aforementioned justifications will not be accepted by the intellect, nor do they have any foothold. For the first question is: Who asked this of you, to come—without proper preparation—specifically to the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year, and which cannot tolerate matters that are contrary to His wisdom and will, etc.?

There is much more to elaborate on regarding all of the above, but my hope is strong that you can also elaborate on this direction yourself, and much more. Regarding your writing that I am "busy and occupied with *orthodoxische politik* (Orthodox politics)" and therefore the situation in other areas does not appear "klar" (clear), and one does not appreciate the "grosse meglichkeit" (great possibility) to act for Hashem and His Torah—I generally do not subscribe to the emphasis on "orthodoxische politik." For those who use this term intend it to mean the preservation and permeation of Torah and mitzvos, even into daily life. And it is incumbent upon **each and every one** of us to strive **as much as possible** until he identifies and **becomes one** with the aforementioned, and **only** this will be his worldview **in every single respect.** This is the point of the faith of **unity,** which is the foundational point of the faith of the Jewish people: "In **all** your ways **know Him**," that even in his eating and drinking, etc., he is connected with strength and courage and **does not** divert his mind, as explained in many places (see Tanya, end of Chapter 3).

Based on this, it is understood that this is not a deficiency or an obstacle to seeing the situation in other areas; on the contrary, **this is** the illuminating mirror to see them as they are in **true** reality—that is, as they appear to the truth of the Creator’s reality, and not to flesh-and-blood eyes that are biased by various matters and perhaps even personal interests. It is just that we have **not yet merited** to identify with the perspective called "orthodoxische politik." In the language of the Tanya, this is in the category of *eino gamur* (not complete). Of course, I do not mean the level of a *tzaddik she’eino gamur*, but rather that he is not complete on a lower level, below a *tzaddik she’eino gamur*, but in his own context, he is not complete and perfect. But despite this lack of completion and perfection, it is also clear that the situation and the difference between the work in the Diaspora and in Eretz Yisrael are as stated above, only with even more decisiveness and sharpness.

I would add that it is puzzling that you apparently do not see that the vast majority of the Jewish people are specifically in the Diaspora. Furthermore, the work here does not encounter the same obstacles and confusion as it does there, where everything is bound by the iron chains of organizations and various parties. Surely you also realize that the attitude toward someone who comes as a guest—especially from the United States—is not the same as the attitude when he accepts a position in an institution located there, and becomes a "servant to servants." I have said enough.

Regarding what you wrote at the end of your letter, the question is not so clear. If your intention is regarding the **Conservative movement**, then after the premise that the Jewish people who were misled or who erred in participating in it are to be pitied—a terrible and great pity, even those who stand at their head for reasons of livelihood and a good salary, etc., even though they know their responsibility and the punishment associated with it, etc.—this is not the case for the movement itself and its institutions. Their judgment is decided clearly and definitively in the Mishnah and Gemara, and up to the *Mishneh Torah*, *Hilchos Teshuvah*, Chapter 3, Halachah 8. This is not at all comparable to working in a Hillel institution, where the official line and goal of the matter is not to deny that the Torah is from Heaven, etc.

May it be His will that as we stand on the eve of the bright day of Lag B'Omer—whose theme is the connection and revelation of the inner dimension of Torah within the revealed dimension of Torah, as explained in Chassidus regarding the innovation of the Rashbi—it will affect every single one, within the entirety of the Jewish people, that the inner soul (which is connected to the inner dimension of Torah), which remained faithful to Him even at the time of sin and even in the case of the most insignificant person, will act in a revealed manner, in the way explained in Tanya, end of Chapter 19, to banish and push away the *Sitra Achra* and the *kelipos* so that they cannot touch even his garments, which are his thoughts, speech, and actions, etc. And even though it is human nature that "a novelty is beloved," it will act in accordance with the aforementioned and the ruling of our Sages that "whatever is more straightforward is better"—meaning the observance of Torah and mitzvos in public, as mentioned above, so that it will be recognizable in his garments of thought, speech, and action, until he serves as a living example, automatically and without any contemplation or deep analysis, as a person whose Judaism ("orthodoxische politik") is his very essence. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for good news in all the above [and it is understood that my intention is for open-hearted letters, and to dismiss all the "bewahrungen" (reservations) and notes that might prevent you from writing your innermost thoughts, etc.].

With blessings.

## 7,607

B"H, 20 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 6th of the month, in which you write regarding your son, may he live, arguing that he should study to obtain a matriculation certificate, etc., as if this were the only way for your son to be able to succeed in his future life.

It is astonishing, for since you are in a place like Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, you surely know that thousands of *avreichim*—may they increase—of your son’s age are in yeshivos in Eretz Yisrael, studying our holy Torah, which is also called *Toras Chaim* (the Torah of life), encompassing the life of this world and the World to Come together. They study with diligence and perseverance, and with inner confidence, joy, and goodness of heart. What increases my bewilderment even more is that you are surely aware of what has been printed in several newspapers in Eretz Yisrael regarding what is happening with the youth there and their conduct. The strongest fortification against the unusual winds blowing in the street is received precisely in these yeshivos, to the extent that among thousands of delinquent youth, not a single one is found among the yeshiva students who study Torah all day. Since the primary duty of parents regarding their children is to set them on a firm footing in life, without inner conflict or internal complications, and since various methods of education have been attempted recently, the dry statistics—as mentioned above, which have been publicized everywhere and similarly in other countries—have clarified the results in a **sharply** unequivocal manner, and this is easy to understand.

In other words, even if your son’s inclination were not toward the form of education he has chosen, it would be **your duty** to influence him to agree to it for at least a period of a few years. Now that, by the grace of the Almighty, you have been blessed with a son of good character and virtues who has chosen for himself the good, the beautiful, and the holy—to follow the aforementioned path and study accordingly—you should thank the Almighty for His blessing in this, and strengthen and encourage your son in this decision of his, in a manner of "increasing and continuing." And most certainly, He who is described as "He who sustains the entire world with His goodness, with grace, with kindness, and with mercy"—who sustains two and a half billion people—will provide his livelihood in its proper time. Your son, too, should study the Torah of the Creator and Guide of the world with warmth and enthusiasm, and this will add to the blessings of Hashem, as it is written: "If you walk in My statutes" [and as our Sages explain: "You shall be toiling in Torah"] etc., "then I will give your rains," etc., and all the blessings enumerated in the *parsha*.

With blessings for *nachas* that is Jewish and Chassidic from your son, may he live—which is the true *nachas*—and with health and goodness of heart from the aforementioned.

#### ***7,607***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 21, p. 388.

## 768

B"H, 20 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn

To the Organization of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in Kfar Chabad

It was with pleasure that I received your letter of the 17th of Iyar, in which you write regarding the shiur among the members concerning the study of the laws of Taharas HaMishpacha.

May it be the will of Hashem that this be in a good and auspicious hour. Fortunate is the portion of all those who exert themselves and assist in this, for this is one of the foundations of our holy Torah, the Torah of life. This is explained at length in many places, and it is also understood from the statement of our Sages that this mitzvah was given to the women of Israel, for through it they rectify the first sin, which is the source of all sins in the world, and the source of all that is not good in the world.

May it be the will of Hashem that your aforementioned activity serve as an example, so that the women of Israel in many, many places will see and do likewise. May this be done with tranquility, joy, and a good heart. May this also serve as a channel and vessel for an increase in the blessings of Hashem in all that they require in general, and specifically in the inner matter that, together with their husbands—may they live—they will raise all their offspring—may they live—to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 760

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the auspicious day of Lag B’Omer.

1) During a time of favor, I will mention your mother, may she live and be well, at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the success of her medical treatment. May it be His will that just as you have written this request, you will soon share good news regarding it. It is understood and simple that the more your mother, may she live and be well, strengthens her trust in Hashem—the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders—the more abundant and immediate the success will be.

2) Regarding what you wrote about the proposal to travel to the country of... etc.—the solution is in your hands. I mean that if you decide with the necessary firmness to spread traditional Judaism and its matters there—with the purpose and essence being practical action—without paying attention to the difficulties one encounters when wanting to act for the sake of our Torah, the Torah of life, and its mitzvos, then the proposal is correct and good. For as our Sages of blessed memory state, the role of a person and the purpose of his creation is to serve his Creator (Mishnah, end of Maseches Kiddushin). Furthermore, a great principle in the Torah is "Love your fellow as yourself." Just as one desires and yearns for himself to be among those of whom it is said, "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today," one must also strive for this regarding his fellow.

It is a well-known saying and instruction of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory, that the mitzvah of "Love your fellow as yourself" applies even to a Jewish man or woman whom one has never seen. And this is understood.

3) Since this year is a year of special significance—the bicentennial of the passing and hillula of the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory, one of the foundations of whose teachings is that love of Hashem, love of the Torah, and love of a fellow Jew are one—then an **added** measure of courage and effort must be invested in the aforementioned avodah. Just as one of the primary expressions of love for Hashem is love for His only child (each and every Jew), so too, conversely, one of the expressions and foundations of love for a fellow Jew is when one brings fellow Jews closer to our Father in Heaven, to His Torah, and to His mitzvos. And since we have been commanded to do this, then certainly and surely, He who fashions their hearts together and understands all their deeds provides the possibilities and the strengths to fulfill this task completely; it is only that in His goodness and kindness, He desires that we do this through free choice.

As you requested, this letter is being sent without waiting for the regular turn.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## Z'shi

[28 Iyar, 5720]

In response to your letter from the auspicious day of Lag B’Omer.

At an opportune time, I will mention your wife, may she live, once again at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your hearts’ desires for the good.

It is understood, and indeed simple, that your work in the Reshet school—which is named after my father-in-law, the Rebbe, at whose holy resting place you will be mentioned—serves as a channel and a vessel for increasing the blessings of Hashem in whatever you require, and specifically in the aforementioned matter. For the attribute of the Holy One, blessed be He, is "measure for measure," and even many times more so. "And you shall teach them to your children" refers to these students; "and you shall teach them to your children" in its literal sense.

However, it is also simple that the work of Hashem—which is the work of education, as per the instruction of our Sages on this matter—must be done with *mesiras nefesh*, diligence, and standing guard, without taking into account the confusion of the *yetzer*, whether the confusion comes from within or from without. If this is true in any place, how much more so in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, and in our generation, the footsteps of Moshiach. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all matters, both general and personal alike.

## 7111

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Mevarchim HaChodesh Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the activists and friends of the Beis Rivkah schools in general, and to the participants in the eighteenth annual banquet of the Beis Rivkah schools in particular,
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

This year, the annual banquet of Beis Rivkah is taking place the day after Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Sivan—the month of Kabbalas HaTorah—and a few days before the 200th yahrtzeit of the histalkus-hilula of the Baal Shem Tov z"l, on the first day of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah.

These two moments—Matan Torah and the histalkus of the Baal Shem Tov—have a special significance for the Beis Rivkah mosdos, their activists, and their friends, bearing in mind that in Torah in general, and in Toras HaChassidus in particular, the Jewish woman occupies a most important place.

At the time of Matan Torah, the Ribono shel Olam commanded Moshe Rabbeinu to address the women first and then the men ("Thus shall you say to the House of Yaakov"—this refers to the women—"and tell the Children of Yisrael"—the men). The Jewish woman and mother, as the *akeres habayis*, has the great responsibility and the great zechus to strengthen and secure the foundations of Torah and mitzvos in the Jewish home.

In the revelation and development of Toras HaChassidus and the Chassidic movement, too, the Jewish woman and mother has occupied a most important place, as is known to all who are familiar with the life and work of the founders of Chassidus and Chassidus Chabad. As a living example, it suffices to mention the story of Rochel, the grandmother of the Alter Rebbe, the founder of Chabad, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, as it is told in the second volume of the *Zichronos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the founder of the Beis Rivkah mosdos, which has just been published (in connection with the 200th yahrtzeit).

The shita of Chabad and the securing of the future of Klal Yisrael demand that Jewish daughters receive a thorough Jewish-Chassidic education, and the Beis Rivkah schools are the mosdos that carry out this intent.

All who help support and expand the Beis Rivkah mosdos therefore have a great share in *hafatzas hama'ayanos*—the spreading of the springs of Torah and mitzvos, illuminated with the inner light and vitality of Chassidus—which is also the preparation for the Geulah Shleimah v'Amitis through Moshiach Tzidkeinu. Every new effort in this direction opens new springs of Hashem’s blessings in everything one needs, in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

With blessings for besuros tovos and for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness,

**M. Schneerson**

## 612

By the Grace of Hashem, 25 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all the members of Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad everywhere,
And to the participants of the Fifth Annual Convention in particular,
May Hashem grant you life,

Blessings and peace!

On the occasion of the annual convention of Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, and through the medium of this gathering, I send my blessing to each and every one of you, with an inner prayer for the success of your work in all areas of your program, and especially for far-reaching achievements from the upcoming convention.

Yesterday we blessed the month of Sivan. The central point of this month is the Yom Tov of Shavuos, **Zman Matan Toraseinu** (the time of the giving of our Torah).

Hashem gave us a **Torah Temimah**, a **complete** Torah. As our Sages, of blessed memory, express it (everything that a veteran student will eventually innovate was already stated to Moshe at Sinai), everything that is accomplished in Torah throughout all generations was already given to Moshe Rabbeinu at Mount Sinai.

It goes without saying that this includes all parts of the holy Torah that have been revealed from generation to generation, especially **Pnimius HaTorah**, the inner light of the Torah, which was revealed to individuals through Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai—whose Yahrtzeit-Hilula is Lag B’Omer—and which was later spread widely among all Jews, beginning with the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory, whose Yahrtzeit-Hilula is on the first day of Shavuos, Zman Matan Toraseinu.

This year marks two hundred years since the Histalkus-Hilula of the Baal Shem Tov, and it also falls on the same day of the week—Wednesday, the luminous day of Maaseh Bereishis, when the luminaries began to shine from the heavens. As the Alter Rebbe, the founder of Chabad, says regarding this day: **Natlu HaMeoros** (the luminaries were taken) and **Nitlu HaMeoros** (the luminaries were hung/elevated). This means that on this day, the Baal Shem Tov completed his soul’s mission and his holy soul returned to the Creator, but at the same time, his light began to spread more strongly and broadly through his students and his students’ students. Every year on this day, new springs of his light open up, drawing from the deepest roots of his divine soul.

The revelation of Torah in general, and of Toras HaChassidus and Chassidus Chabad in particular, has a special significance for the Jewish woman. As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, emphasized many times, both in word and in writing, the especially important place that Jewish women in general, and N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in particular, occupy in Jewish life.

"Everything that is holy and precious to the divine Jewish people—the foundation of the Jewish home, the education of the children, the kashrus and holiness of the home, the holiness of Shabbos—all of this Hashem has given and entrusted to the Jewish woman. The woman who fulfills her duty and life-task in family life, in the management of the home, and in the education of the children according to Torah—of her it is said in the Torah: **Chachmos nashim ban'sa beisah** (The wisdom of women builds her home)—each of these wise women **builds** her home."

The women and daughters of Chabad have the special duty to stand in the front lines of every activity to strengthen Yiddishkeit in general, and the conduct of the home in particular.

Through the fact that each of you will build her own home, and help to raise up the homes of Jewish neighbors around you upon the eternal foundations of Torah and Mitzvos, permeated with the light and warmth of Chassidus, the entire **Beis Yisrael** is built. This prepares the ground for Moshiach Tzidkeinu, in accordance with the well-known letter of the Baal Shem Tov, that when **Yafutzu Mayanosecha Chutzah** will be fulfilled—when the springs of the Baal Shem Tov, his instructions, teachings, and ways, will be spread even "outside"—the Geulah Shleimah will come, through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

* * *

May Hashem bless your work, that you may carry it out with great success in all respects, and may He bring happiness to each one of you, together with your families, may they live, also in personal matters, in both material and spiritual respects alike.

With blessings for outstanding success and for good tidings.

## Z'shig

B"H, 26 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the eve of Wednesday, in which you write about what has occurred to you regarding a lack of vitality, thoughts of sadness, etc., and you ask for my opinion on this.

Now, all matters of our Torah—the Torah of life—are instructions for life (and from the affirmative you hear the negative, etc.). Since the inner dimension of the Torah is established in the holy Zohar (Part III, 152a) as being called the "soul of the Torah," it is understood that when there is a lack in the vitality of the soul, there is a lack in the vitality of all the matters of the body—which, in the analogy, are the 248 limbs and 365 sinews, meaning the matters of the 248 positive mitzvos and 365 negative mitzvos and the study of their halachos. It is also understood that the vitality of the soul in such a state is, so to speak, similar to the vitality of the soul during sleep. Even though this is sufficient to operate the digestive organs, it is not sufficient at all regarding matters of understanding, comprehension, and true feeling; it results only in vain imaginings and dreams—dreams of the type discussed in the holy Zohar [...] and explained in Tanya (Chapter 29). From the above, the remedy and advice for all that has been said is understood: an increase in the vitality of the soul, meaning:

Establishing fixed times for the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. This should be a daily commitment, with an increase on the holy Shabbos, which is "holy to Hashem," as explained in the writings of the Arizal regarding the study of the inner dimension of the Torah on Shabbos. May it be the will that this commitment be—as in the saying of our Rabbeinu HaZaken, the author of the Tanya (who decides in the hidden dimension of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (who decides in the revealed dimension of Torah)—a commitment not only in time, but also (and this is the essential part) a commitment in the soul; and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for good tidings in all that has been mentioned, and in the language of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
It would be appropriate to have your tefillin checked to ensure they are kosher according to the law, and likewise, that every weekday before the morning davening, you set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

## 7617

B"H, 26 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

After the longest of pauses, I received your letter of 21 Iyar with the good news that you have begun studying maamarim of Chassidus on Shabbos in the shuls of Yafo.

May it be Hashem’s will that you continue this with added strength and added vigor, as with all matters of Torah, mitzvos, and holiness, which we are commanded to elevate in sanctity. The commandment is constant—meaning, our actions must be in a state of constant ascent. This is especially true regarding the inner dimensions of Torah, as explained in the holy Zohar, where it is called the "soul of the Torah." Just as any addition to the soul—which in itself is simple —adds to all the 248 limbs and 365 sinews of the body, the parallel in Torah is understood. From this comes a definitive instruction: every effort and endeavor in this area is worthwhile. These days are days of auspiciousness, especially as we approach the time of the giving of our Torah on the first day of Shavuos, which is also the two-hundredth yahrtzeit of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov. With blessings to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness, and for good news regarding the above.

This is understood from the aforementioned, for no matter how much the measure of the limited increases, it is incomparable to that which is "exceedingly broad."

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 718

B"H, 28 Iyar, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, whose work is the work of Heaven, a man of energy, etc.,
Yisroel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the conclusion of Shabbos Mevarchim the month of Sivan, the third month, it was a pleasure for me to read the details regarding your holy work in the field of *chinuch al taharat hakodesh*. Certainly, you do not content yourself with this, for we are commanded to ascend in all matters of our Torah and *mitzvos*, and especially in the field of *chinuch*. Any addition in the education of a child or youth grows many times over as the student matures, and at times, it changes the entire course of their life, including their domestic life when they marry and build a Jewish home. Since the responsibility and the merit in this are so great, it is certain that special and immense powers are bestowed from Above, and this is easy to understand.

May it be His will that you carry out all that has been mentioned with joy and a good heart. According to the measure of the *Ribono shel Olam*, which is "measure for measure," but multiplied many times over, may you derive much true *nachas*—a Jewish, traditional, *Chassidishe* *nachas*—both from "and you shall teach them to your children" in its literal sense, and from "and you shall teach them to your children—these are the students."

My hope is strong that in connection with the upcoming *Chag HaShavuos*, the time of the giving of our Torah—which this year is also the two-hundredth *hillula* of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, and falls on the same day of the week, Wednesday, the first day of *Chag HaShavuos*, which, as our *Rebbe* the Alter Rebbe stated, is the day the luminaries were given and suspended—you will plan activities in this direction wherever your reach extends, and especially among those you influence, to establish study in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, which is the very essence of *Chassidus*, and to walk in the ways of his instructions and conduct.

With blessing, and in the language of my father-in-law, the *Rebbe*, to receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

## 720

*[Late Iyar, 5720]*

**Why, etc., does Hashem bring the Midrash, etc., regarding the attribute of judgment—**

Because the tzaddikim are similar to their Creator, and the Holy One, Blessed be He, also did so and wrote: "In the beginning **Elokim** created," etc.

**And this is also in Rashi’s commentary** [by way of remez, **and in Chassidic thought:** the beginning of the **Heh**—the world that was created with it]. And see Zohar Vol. III, 39a.

**But behold, etc., in Chapter 4—**

There, it is not speaking of priority in **creation**, but rather priority in the **human understanding**—that it is simpler to understand that one cannot comprehend the expansion from above, than it is to understand that one cannot comprehend the Tzimtzum.

**Note:** Perhaps they prophesied, and they did not know what they prophesied—for it is explained at times (similar to the above) that the beginning of the seven days of **construction** is the attribute of Chesed, because the essence and cause of creation, and likewise the cause of the Tzimtzum, is because it is the nature of the Good to do good, etc., and He also desires that it be within the capacity of the created beings, and therefore He contracts, etc. However, this is the **cause** of the matter, and not that He creates through this; and this is understood.

**There is a Midrash to the c o n t r a r y—**

There is not. There is a Midrash that **includes** both possibilities, as in Bereishis Rabbah (end of Chapter 12): If He creates with the attribute of mercy, etc., if He creates with the attribute of judgment, etc., but not the reverse.

***

The letter is to R' Dovber Baumgarten, and was written on the margin of his letter dated 19 Iyar 5720: We are currently studying Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah. He (R' Chaim Yehuda Levin) asks: Why, at the beginning of Chapter 5, does he bring the Midrash that initially it arose in the thought to create the world with the attribute of judgment, and He saw that the world could not endure, so He associated the attribute of mercy with it? Yet, as explained above in Chapter 4, on the contrary, the attribute of kindness was first, and that is the primary element, while the attribute of severity is secondary—as it says that just as it is impossible to understand His attribute of kindness and its expansion, so too is it impossible to understand His attribute of severity, etc. Especially since there is also a Midrash to the contrary, that initially it arose in the thought to create with the attribute of mercy, and He saw that the world could not endure, so He associated the attribute of judgment with it—and this Midrash would have been more correct.

The bolded words at the beginning of each section are a quotation of the language of the aforementioned question.

## 7,221

B"H, 1 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the avreich Chaim, may he live,
Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Thursday, in which you inquire about the nigun "Imati Kasi Mar" and ask regarding the source of the nigun.

As far as I am aware, the nigun is a Jerusalemite nigun, and it is not clear who composed it. Some years ago, several chareidim began singing it with these specific words because of the feeling that this nigun evoked in them. However, it is clear that this is not mandatory. If a G-d-fearing musician with deep feeling were to come along and invent a nigun more suited to the awakening of the soul and contemplation of the concept of "when the wellsprings spread outward, the Master will come," everyone is free to accept his opinion on the matter.

If your question pertains to the core concept of "when your wellsprings spread outward, the Master will come," these are the words of Melech HaMashiach himself, spoken in response to the Baal Shem Tov when he was in his chamber on high. This is as the Baal Shem Tov related in his Iggeres HaKodesh, which is printed in the book of one of his greatest disciples, the Ben Porat Yosef by Rabbi Yaakov Yosef of Polnoye. There can be no clearer instruction than this.

Regarding what you wrote—that you saw in a book that the study of Kabbalah and Pnimiyus HaTorah will hasten the days of Mashiach and the arrival of Mashiach—this is stated even more strongly in many places.* There are wondrous and even alarming statements regarding how the lack of this study prolongs the galus—the galus of the Bnei Yisrael and the Shechinah—and there is no need to elaborate on such an alarming matter.

It is my firm hope that you have a set time—and "that which is set does not cease"—for the study of Pnimiyus HaTorah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. Furthermore, you should increase in this, for we have been commanded to "increase in holiness."

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

*) For example: Rabbi Chaim Vital in his introduction to Shaar HaHakdamos.

## 722

B"H, 1 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is a great wonder that you do not mention anything regarding the activities for the bright day of Lag B'Omer and the festival of Shavuos (which are interconnected, beyond the general rule that Sefiras HaOmer is a preparation for the fiftieth day*). For it is explained in Chassidus that on Shavuos there was the giving of the Torah in a general sense, and a revelation of the inner dimensions of the Torah, akin to the giving of the Torah, occurred on Lag B'Omer. Furthermore, both are the yahrtzeit-hilula of those who opened a path and way for the study of the inner dimensions of the Torah: the Rashbi (for his generation and for the select few) and the Baal Shem Tov (for every single Jew, until his wellsprings spread outward, as in the well-known Iggeres HaKodesh of the Baal Shem Tov). May it be His will that you bring good news regarding the activities concerning the aforementioned, as well as regarding specific matters.

With the blessing in the language of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, to receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.
