## 7,263

B"H, 1 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, man of many accomplishments, R' Binyamin, may he live:

Shalom u'Bracha!

...Since everything is by Hashgacha Pratis, and as per the words of the Baal Shem Tov that we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that every matter a Jewish person sees or hears is an instruction in the avodah of Hashem, I interpret your writing to me as a reminder of my duty [relying on the Sages' teaching: "One only urges those who are already diligent"], to emphasize the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, his guidance, and his customs. This year is a year of segulah, the bicentennial year of the histalkus and hillula of the Baal Shem Tov, which falls on the same day of the week as this year’s calendar, on Wednesday, the festival of Shavuos. As our Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya (who decides in the nistar of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (who decides in the nigleh of Torah) states, it was on this day that the luminaries were taken—and given. It is certainly an opportune time to awaken every one of Bnei Yisrael, on the day of the hillula and the days preceding and following it, to the teachings of the master of the hillula, who sacrificed his life for the dissemination of this Torah. And as our Sages said, in a manner of "study that leads to action"—in his guidance and conduct, and even to the point of Chassidic living in daily life. Surely, for one such as you, there is no need to elaborate on this, and the entire writing is, as the Sages said, a matter of "urging the diligent."

Knowing your influence in your fine community and in several places in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, my hope is strong that you will utilize it as much as possible, and even more (for Torah governs and changes reality, to the extent that the Aron functions in a place that is beyond measure, despite its own dimensions being two and a half amos in length, etc.). There is a strength in propaganda that does not return empty, especially when the words come from the heart.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the above, and a person is obligated to speak in the language of his Rebbe (my father-in-law, the Rebbe) regarding the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

#### ***7,263***

**R' Binyamin:** Mendelsohn. Another letter to him—above, Vol. 6, 1,893.

## 7224

7224

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and learned, R' Shalom, may he live,

Shalom and blessing!

In response to your letter of 28 Iyar, in which you write regarding the affixing of a mezuzah.

There is a tradition among Chabad Chassidim, handed down from our Rebbes—I believe as far back as the Alter Rebbe—that we follow the *hiker tzir* (the pivot of the door hinge). This applies even in a case such as the one you describe, regarding a balcony (*balkan*) whose only entrance is through one of the rooms of the house. Regarding the question of how one would enter [if the door were closed], the response given was that one should climb through the roof. I believe that Rabbi Landau, may he live, of Bnei Brak, heard an explicit instruction regarding this from the Rebbe (Rashab), may his soul be bound in the bond of life.

Incidentally, in the *balkan* of the apartment of the Rebbe (Rayatz), may his soul be bound in the bond of life, the *hiker tzir* is on the inside of the room, and the mezuzah is affixed in the manner described above.

As is your custom, you do not mention anything regarding the *hafatzas hamaayanos* in your area. May it be the will [of Hashem] that you break this established pattern. The main thing is that you should disseminate and continue to disseminate, until [the wellsprings] reach even the "outside." This year, in particular, demands and requires additional effort in this regard, as it is the bicentennial year of the passing and *hillula* of the Baal Shem Tov, may his merit protect us, and this is understood.

With blessings for good tidings and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

#### ***7224***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 9, p. 259, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

**R' Shalom, may he live:** Rivkin, Seattle. Additional letters to him appear above, 7232, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

**Hiker tzir:** See also above, Vol. 18, 6775, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 725

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 29 Iyar.

At an auspicious time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

Regarding what you write about settling down in life, it is a simple matter that true happiness is found in building a home in Israel together with a *ben Torah* who has studied Torah in a *yeshiva* with *yiras shamayim*, as is explained in many places in the words of our Sages, of blessed memory...

Incidentally, regarding what you mention about financial hardship in connection with the matter of covering one’s hair—is it any wonder that one’s livelihood is strained? It is explained in the holy *Zohar* (Vol. 3, 126a) that when the matter of covering one’s hair by the mistress of the house is in order, one is blessed with everything: with blessings from above, with blessings from below, with wealth, and with children and grandchildren. Our Torah is a *Toras Chaim*—a Torah of life—providing instruction on how to conduct oneself in life, down to the details of daily living.

May it be the will of Hashem that as we approach the time of the giving of our Torah, from this point forward our Torah—which is *Torah Ohr*—will illuminate your path in life, and then your happiness will be true, from *nefesh* to *basar*.

With blessings for good news regarding the above and for a *chag sameach*.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 726

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in the needs of the community,
R' Shimshon HaLevi, may he live and be well,

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter of Wednesday, in which you inquire regarding the laws of milah.

Generally, regarding practical questions, one should consult a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah*. However, it is my duty and privilege to emphasize what is explained and explicit in the Torah Shebichtav and Torah Shebe'al Peh regarding the immense significance of entering into the covenant of our forefather Avraham—a covenant for which thirteen covenants were established, corresponding to the thirteen attributes of mercy. From this, it is understood, and it is also simple, that every detail in this matter touches upon both the spirituality of the soul and the matters of the body, and "whoever adds, they add to him."

Well-known are the words of Rabbeinu HaZaken, author of the Tanya (who decides the law in the hidden aspects of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (who decides the law in the revealed aspects of Torah), that the beginning of the entry of this holy soul is, etc., through the mitzvah of milah (see his Shulchan Aruch, Mahadura Basra, end of Siman 4), and that which is well-known requires no proof.

On this occasion, I have another holy duty, and also a privilege, to awaken you regarding the necessity of establishing set times for the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus, and especially for one whom Divine Providence has privileged to bring the children of Israel into the covenant of Avraham Avinu.

With respect and with blessings for good tidings, and in the language of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and with *pnimiyus*.

#### ***726***

**R' Shimshon:** Ellenberg, Salford.

## 7227

B"H, Days of Hagbalah, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the House of Yaakov (the women)
And to the Children of Israel (the men)
May they live, Hashem bless them

Greetings and blessings!

The days of Hagbalah—the preparation for Matan Torah—demand a special, deeper inner reflection on what Torah is.

The holy Torah is not a collection of laws for specific occasions; rather, it encompasses the person **entirely**, from their first moment to their last, and in every detail of their day-to-day life.

This is the inner meaning of Torah as *Toras Chaim* (a Torah of life).

Moreover, as our Sages of blessed memory explain, Torah encompasses **the entire creation**. They explain this with the analogy of an architect who, before building a structure, first creates a plan for every detail of the building. So too, Hashem first inscribed in the Torah **every** detail of creation, down to the lowest level in the *domem* (inanimate, material objects).

This leads to one of the fundamental principles of the general *Toras HaChassidus* of the Baal Shem Tov, according to his interpretation of the verse, *"L'olam Hashem devarcha nitzav bashamayim"* (Forever, Hashem, Your word stands in the heavens—*Yehi rakia*, etc.), as it is explained at length by the Alter Rebbe (author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch) in *Toras Chassidus Chabad*—specifically in *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*—

That everything—in the heavens above and down to the earth below, in all their details—exists only through the Divine word that created them, and creates and animates them constantly without cessation, every single moment.

From this follows the second fundamental principle—

That *Hashgacha Pratis*—the direct, individual Divine knowledge and supervision over every thing—applies to all details of creation, from man, the chosen of all creatures, down to the smallest component of the *domem*.

From this follows a further conclusion, which is also a fundamental principle in *Toras HaChassidus* and was especially emphasized by the Baal Shem Tov, although it is actually a ruling in the *Shulchan Aruch*—

That one must serve Hashem in, and with, all details, beginning with learning Torah and fulfilling the 613 *mitzvos*, down to the simplest occurrences and circumstances of daily life, and

That from everything around one, one must learn **Ahavas Hashem** and **Yiras Hashem**—the original sources from which a Jew draws the proper spirit to fulfill Torah and *mitzvos*, the *mitzvos-aseh* and *mitzvos lo-taaseh*, permeated with true *chayus*, and to fulfill them with *hiddur*.

Reflecting on all that has been mentioned above—reflecting with *hispaalus*, vitality, and brightness.

And in these auspicious days, on the eve of the day of Matan Torah, which is also the day of the *histalkus-hillula* of the Baal Shem Tov.

To bring this down into all the details of daily life, both in one's own life and in everything around oneself, in everything in the world, according to the expression:

**"Yafutzu mayanosecha chutzah"** (May your springs spread outward). That the springs of *Chassidus*, which is *Pnimiyus HaTorah*—the inwardness of the Torah—should spread and reach *chutzah*—even into the most external and distant details and affairs of creation as a whole,

This will also hasten the *Geulah HaAmitis VeHaShleimah* through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, when the entire creation will see and feel that **"Anochi Hashem Elokecha."**

With a wish for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, and a happy Yom Tov.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 7333

B”H, 14 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent, etc., Moreinu Harav R’ Sh.Y. (may he live)

Peace and blessing!

In response to your urgent letter of 12 Sivan, the completion of the days of payment for the festival of Shavuos, and therefore this response also comes urgently.

...Upon reviewing your letter, I saw that I have not yet answered what you wrote regarding "the tenth shall be holy" in the matter of exiting the pen. I omitted in my aforementioned letter the citation and reference to *Likutei HaShas* of the Arizal, tractate *Bechoros*. The text there, regarding our subject, states: "The tenth is holy and exits through the opening, etc., and understand this." Regarding your note on the law according to the revealed Torah (*nigleh*) that even in the pen it is holy: this is preceded by the fact that we find many such matters that are explained according to the inner dimension of Torah as the matter must be **ordered**. A simple example—a very general matter—is the explanation that all mitzvos must be performed with thought (*kavanah*), speech (blessing), and action (actual fulfillment of the mitzvah), even though for a large portion of mitzvos, *kavanah* is not required, and blessings do not invalidate the act.

I wrote this only as an "example," since in any case, *lechatchilah* (ideally), *kavanah* and a blessing are worthwhile. This is unlike exiting the pen, where one **could** have said that even *lechatchilah* it is not needed. But in truth, it is not so; on the contrary, **by Torah law** it is a mitzvah that they exit and that he counts them with a rod. And the main point—in my humble opinion—is that even *bedieved* (after the fact), in truth, it is not so according to the law of the revealed Torah, and the foundations are:

(a) In the *sugya* of *Bechoros* (58b and there), it is seemingly difficult to understand—for our Sages state simply that the tenth is holy in any case, even if he did not call it by name, etc., whereas regarding exiting the pen, they seek proofs and evidence. Seemingly, they are equivalent, etc.

(b) The words of the Rambam (*Hilchos Bechoros*, chapter 8, halacha 8), who writes the reason that the "count of the fit" exempts, which seemingly is only according to the initial assumption (*kasha d’kasha*) that an actual exit is required, as per the question of the *Lechem Mishneh*.

(c) The language of the commentators on the *Shas* there, and also on 59b, which implies that the "count of the fit" is similar to the principle that "whatever is fit for *belilah* (mixing)—exit—*belilah* does not invalidate it."

(d) And this is the main point: how can one say that in the absence of an exit from the pen it is holy entirely? When does the holiness take effect? For if he were to take the tenth out through a different door, it is not holy, because it is not joined to the nine that were counted. Furthermore, how is this different from death or exiting from the category of "living" entirely—from one who takes out a living animal through a different door?

All of the above is resolved if we say that the law is that if the tenth remained in the pen, it is a "tenth of tithe" only if it subsequently exits alive through that same door, for then it is clarified from the outset that it belongs to them. This is unlike if the tenth died in the pen, where they did not say in the *baraisa* that it is a "tenth of tithe," and as mentioned above, this is an example of exiting through a different door—that the nine that were counted are exempt only because of the "count of the fit." Therefore, Rashi (*Bechoros* 59b) combined the case of a dead animal with the tenth in the pen that exited through a different opening and wrote the reason that it is the "count of the fit." From this—regarding our matter—at the very least, as a clarification, the exit is necessary. And in the *Likutei HaShas* of the Arizal there, it brought me to the distinction—that it is impossible to say this regarding the counting of *Malchus*, for the entire matter happens by itself, similar to what is said regarding the ship of *Binah*, which is above the *seder hishtalshelus*, as I have written in the past.

Regarding what you wrote about *hagbahah* (lifting the Torah): it is somewhat surprising that it is not mentioned in the encyclopedia entry regarding the manner of *hagbahah* practiced in Chabad, where we place the *Sefer Torah* on the table after the *hagbahah* and before the *gelilah*. And see this new thing—that specifically the author of the *Aruch HaShulchan* confirms and praises this custom.

I was pleased to read in the signature of your letter regarding matters connected to the bicentennial year, etc., and your activities in this. My hope is strong, even though you do not mention it, that it was emphasized with the necessary force to negate the error as if the Baal Shem Tov, etc., were lenient regarding the performance of mitzvos with *hiddur* (beautification), etc. And one of the reasons I am writing this is that if it has not yet been emphasized as required, it is proper to do so at every opportunity, at least from here on out, for those who err are many, even if part of them err willingly, etc.

The talk you mention at the end of your letter—thank you for sending it here, and especially the speeches at the time of the *kinus*—for as of now, they have not reached me.

**M. Schneerson**

## 735

B"H, 17 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through your *mechutan*, the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing and learned, [Name] *shlita*, I received your request for a blessing and a *pidyon nefesh* on your behalf.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*. May it be His will that just as you brought this request, you will yourself bring good tidings regarding this matter.

This is especially relevant as we have just passed the two-hundredth *yahrzeit* (which occurred on the first day of the holiday of Shavuos) of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, *z"l*. It is well known what he taught regarding the verse, "If you see the donkey... you shall surely release it with him," [interpreting it as a directive] to serve Hashem with one's body and its affairs.

Moving from one subject to another related matter: I have already written many times regarding the great necessity to spread the *maayanos* (of the Baal Shem Tov—which is the teachings of Chassidus—until they reach even) *chutza* (the outside). Although your general conduct is one of *nichba el ha-keilim* (hiding oneself among the vessels), with all due respect, it is highly questionable whether the current time is appropriate for that. And even if one were to argue that it is, we have received instruction from the Baal Shem Tov himself, who in no way wished to reveal himself, etc., as is explained in his holy letters. And while who is one who would dare to compare himself to the Baal Shem Tov, *z"l*? Yet, the very fact that this was told to us implies that it is certainly not, Heaven forbid, merely a story or a waste of time, but rather an instruction and a *maaseh rav* (a significant precedent) for all who wish to follow in his footsteps, similar to the words of the Alter Rebbe in *Tanya*, Chapter 44; see there.

May it be His will that in this, too, you will bring good tidings, in accordance with the definition of the Sages of "true good"—good for Heaven, good for people, and good that produces the fruits of the "Tree of Life," the inner dimension of Torah which has been revealed in our generation through the teachings of Chassidus.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 736

B"H, 17 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 12 Sivan, the conclusion and final day of the *tashlumin* (make-up period) for the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah.

At a time of *ratzon* (divine favor), I will mention you and your wife, *tichye*, at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nebag"m, zya",* in accordance with the contents of your letter.

Regarding what you wrote about the change in your mood—that when you hear words of *hisorerus* (inspiration) it affects you deeply, but afterwards, etc.—the advice for this is well-known: one should immediately connect the *hisorerus* to an actual act of Torah study, the proper fulfillment of a *mitzvah*, or performing a *mitzvah* with *hiddur* (extra care). It is then much easier to sustain this *hisorerus*, since it has been brought into reality through some action. As is brought in the holy *sefarim*, this is the reason we find in many places that the prophet was commanded to perform an actual deed; the matter is understood.

Regarding what you wrote about your concerns for *parnassah* (livelihood), the advice of our Sages is well-known: to increase in *tzedakah* and to distribute it in many small portions. A propitious time for this is every weekday morning before *davening*, to set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*.

On this occasion, I wish to urge you regarding the necessity of establishing a regular study of *pnimiyus haTorah* (the inner dimension of Torah), which in our generation has been revealed through the teachings of Chassidus. If this was necessary in all places and at all times, it is all the more so in our era, and especially in Eretz Yisrael, *tizkeh l'shanim rabos*. This is particularly true as this year is the bicentennial of the *histalkus* and *hillula* of the Baal Shem Tov, a year of *segulah* (special potential) for the spreading of his wellsprings—which is the teachings of Chassidus—until they reach the *chutzah* (the outermost reaches).

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

P.S. It would be appropriate to have your *tefillin* checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in your home, to ensure they are all *kosher* according to *halacha*.

## 7 Sivan

After the longest of interruptions, your letter of 13 Sivan arrived, along with its enclosure. ## 739

B"H, 18 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After the longest of interruptions, your letter from Wednesday, requesting a blessing and a *pidyon nefesh*, was received.

At an opportune time, I will mention you at the holy *tziyun* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter, and may it be Hashem’s will that you bring good news regarding this.

Understandably, there is wonder and astonishment that you do not mention in your letter anything regarding your activities concerning the dissemination of Yiddishkeit in general, and the dissemination of the *maayanos* in particular—especially since this year is the bicentennial of the passing of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov. The words of his *Iggeres HaKodesh* are well-known: that when his *maayanos* spread outward, the Master (Mashiach) will come. Likewise, there is no mention of your participation in the activities of Beis Lubavitch; this, too, is a source of great wonder, especially after Divine Providence has privileged you with such great and internal closeness to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of Yisroel. May it be Hashem’s will that you bring good news regarding this as well.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 7640

## 770

B"H, 21 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Chaim Shalom, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 18th of Sivan. At an opportune time, your *pidyon nefesh* will be read at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding your question concerning translating the *Tze'enah U-Re'enah* into Lashon HaKodesh: In general, this is a correct endeavor. However, one must investigate whether others have already preceded you in this, and I do not necessarily mean a translation of the aforementioned work, but rather a book similar to it.

Since everything is governed by *hashgachah pratis*, I have the obligation and the privilege to awaken you to the necessity of setting fixed times for the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. If this was a necessity in all places and at all times, how much more so in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and especially in our current era. Moreover, this year is the bicentennial of the *histalkus* and *hillula* of the Baal Shem Tov—a year of *segulah* for the spreading of the *ma'ayanos*, which is the teachings of Chassidus, until they reach the outermost reaches.

Regarding what you wrote about an *avreich* who would come here to be in a Chabad framework for work and studies—there is no such framework here, as in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim the study is all day long. Furthermore, the Yeshiva is not currently accepting students of that nature.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

***

**R' Chaim Shalom:** Schwartz, Jerusalem.

## 7242

B"H, 22 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled, in which you ask about the matter of guarding one's eyes:

It is understood that this is not the place for such a discussion, nor is it necessary, as these matters are explained in the Chassidic texts of our Rebbes, Nesi’im, among them the *Kuntres HaAvodah* by the Rebbe Rashab, *nifshoi eden*, in addition to what is explained in *mussar* works. The same applies to the other senses. The general concept is also understood from the statement of our Sages that a blind person is considered as one who is dead; since looking at things in a forbidden manner is the opposite of the purpose for which the eyes were created, this is, *rachmana litzlan*, a temporary state of blindness, and even worse. There is no need to elaborate on such a simple matter.

It is my strong hope—even though you do not mention it—that you have set times for the study of Chassidus, as the great necessity for this is explained in the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* by the Rebbe Rashab, *nifshoi eden*, and it is also evident in practice. This is all the more true regarding a *bochur yeshiva*. This set time must, of course, be every day, with an increase on Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem, as explained in the writings of the Arizal.

It is appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked, and also that every weekday, before the morning *davening*, you set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*

#### ***7242***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 23, p. 363.

## 7343

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas V'zchartem Es Kol Mitzvos Hashem Va'asitem Otam, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch
For the Chag HaSiyum,
Montreal
May Hashem keep them alive

Peace and Blessing!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the Chag HaSiyum (graduation), although, naturally, a Siyum in Torah is connected with a new beginning and a transition from one level to a higher level. I hope that this will be the case for all the graduating students. It is certainly unnecessary to elaborate on this matter for students of a Lubavitcher Yeshiva.

Surely, the Chag HaSiyum will be under the impression of the 200th anniversary of the Histalkus-Hilula of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory, which took place on the first day of Shavuos, Zman Matan Toraseinu.

The Baal Shem Tov, z"l, demanded—and in matters of Torah, a demand is also a nesinas-koach, a special strength to carry out that demand—to fulfill Torah and mitzvos specifically with simcha, and to connect ahavas Hashem with ahavas Yisrael through ahavas HaTorah. From this, it is understood how great ahavas HaTorah must be, as it is the central point and the connecting force of the other two, such that through it, one achieves the highest level in avodas Hashem with simcha and a good heart.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant you all, and each one individually, success in ascending in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos, as mentioned above, permeated with the light, warmth, and vitality of Toras HaChassidus.

With blessings for success in both material and spiritual matters alike.

#### ***7343***

## 7446

B"H, 24 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 14/6, in which you write about your sons, may they live, who are not conducting themselves in the way of Torah, and that for this reason you have begun to fast, and you ask my opinion on this.

According to what is explained in the books of Chassidus, you should replace the fasting with giving to tzedakah. It would be very appropriate to find friends and acquaintances who will speak with your sons regarding the study of Torah and the observance of mitzvos. They should speak not just once, but several times, initially in pleasant ways but with the necessary firmness. Their words should come from the heart, for then they will enter the heart of the listener.

It is appropriate to have the tefillin of the men who are obligated to wear tefillin checked, and to ensure that the mezuzos in your home are all kosher according to the law. Likewise, you should maintain the good custom of the daughters of Israel to set aside tzedakah before lighting the candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

With blessings for good news.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
When you provide the names of those you write about in Lashon HaKodesh, along with their mother’s name (as is the custom when mentioning them in prayer), they will be mentioned at the holy resting place of the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever they may need.

In my secretariat, we do not write in French, which is why this response is in Lashon HaKodesh; however, you may write in French, as I am able to read that language.

You should ask the rabbi of your community whether you require a halachic permit regarding the aforementioned fast.

## Z'shma

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn

To the avreich engaged in tzedakah, Rabbi Emanuel, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the newspaper containing a series of articles regarding the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory, as well as other matters of Yiddishkeit.

It is understood that I was pleased to see the publication of matters concerning the Baal Shem Tov, his Torah, and his approach. It is my hope that this will be of mutual benefit—not only to the readers but also to the author, and this is well understood. I am certain you will also send the continuation of this series, and I thank you in advance.

As is customary among the children of Israel, I will offer a few comments on what has already been printed, as it is possible that these points may be relevant for the upcoming articles. Furthermore, in my opinion, there is room to consider printing the entire series as a separate booklet [naturally, with the necessary improvements and changes required when transitioning from articles in a newspaper to a standalone booklet].

These are my notes, written in haste. I will begin with a general comment: you cite various authors in the footnotes and, even more so, within the body of the article itself. Among them are some whose inclusion in a footnote is questionable (even if not everyone pays attention to the citations), and certainly so within the body of the text. This is especially true since, regarding the subjects you are writing about and citing, one should bring sources from those whose names and works are beyond any doubt. Surely, when you read through your articles again, you will understand to whom I am referring. In such cases, the doubt should be treated with stringency, as your readers come from various and diverse circles.

2) In the second chapter, at the end of the section regarding the Zohar: the transcription of the statement (Yerushalmi Sanhedrin 1:2), "It is enough that I and your Creator know your strength," requires correction.

3) In chapter four, regarding the chadarim, where you bring the memoirs of Solomon Maimon as testimony: it is well known that he is not reliable in such matters, as his hatred for these things caused him to distort many facts.

4) In chapter five: according to the letters printed in *HaTmim*, a person never met the Baal Shem Tov on Erev Shabbos, which is the opposite of what is written—that they studied together. Similarly, at the end of the aforementioned chapter, regarding the claim that the original handwriting of the Baal Shem Tov was preserved by his brother-in-law—my father-in-law, the Rebbe, already explained at length in his letter that the letters from the Genizah are copies, not the original handwriting.

5) Likewise, the beginning of the final section, 26, there: aside from the fact that the style is inappropriate, the content is also problematic. It is impossible to write that from the moment he was born (or specifically from age ten) he did not want to reveal anything about himself [in *Likkutei Dibburim* it says 26 years **in concealment**—this refers to the time from his birth* until he turned 26, followed by ten years of study, and thereafter 26 years in revelation].

All of the above is intended as encouragement, as the publication in the newspaper and the continuation of this work in the future are most worthwhile.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 7-Shamo

B"H, 26 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Friday.

Regarding what you wrote about your ailment, you should consult a specialist in the field, as many treatments and medicinal remedies have been developed in recent years, and surely there are those among them that are appropriate for you; and the Torah has granted the physician permission to heal.

As for your question regarding whether one should adopt the pronunciation used by our Sephardic brethren: you do not explain the reason for this sudden change, and regarding your reference to certain places that advocate for a different pronunciation—if there is no special reason for changing the pronunciation or the like, it is also recommended in this regard: "Do not forsake the custom of your ancestors," and "every river has its own course."

On this occasion, it is my duty (and privilege) to urge you regarding the absolute necessity of setting fixed times for the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus, especially since our Sephardic brethren have held fast to this study from time immemorial.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
It is proper that you have your tefillin checked to ensure they are kosher according to the law, and also that you observe the ancient ordinance to recite the daily portion of Tehillim every day after the morning prayers—as the Tehillim is divided for the days of the month.

## 7647

B"H, 29 Sivan, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
R' Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 27 Sivan along with the enclosure, and while at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I mentioned you in accordance with the contents of your letter.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the explanation in Likutei Torah, Bamidbar (15d), that there are four senses and not five—if one were to suggest that this is not a typographical error, it could be explained by the fact that it emphasizes here the *hitlabshus* (clothing) according to the temperament and nature, which is not the case with the sense of touch (see the commentary on foreign terms in Moreh Nevuchim, end of Part I, entry "Chush"; note also Ra'aya Mehemna—Zohar Vol. III, 229b—and its commentaries there).

Regarding your note on Likutei Torah, Parshas Shelach (49c), on the superiority of *Chochma* over *Gulgolta*—even though that which it draws and receives from *Mocha Stima'ah* passes through the *Gulgolta*, the **object** through which light passes or is even *mislabesh* (clothed) does not necessarily undergo a change because of it. This is similar to a screen through which sunlight passes, and the like.

With blessings for a *Shabbos* *tava* and a *chodsha* *tava*, the excellence of *Shabbos* and *Rosh Chodesh* combined.

## 750

B"H, 2 Tammuz, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Sivan, in which you write that your hope of finding the atmosphere to which you were accustomed in your home country has not been fulfilled, and how this has caused you disappointment, etc. — my hope is strong that you will not allow the *yetzer* to entice you with the aforementioned argument regarding the lack, *chas v'shalom*, of the feeling of *ahavah* to the necessary degree. Especially since the explanation for this is that when one is in a situation of danger, *chas v'shalom*, the situation compels that the aforementioned feeling be constantly revealed and active, as it is necessary to utilize it at every step and turn, for otherwise the consequences are extreme. This is not the case in a much more comfortable situation, where even when the aforementioned feeling is revealed, it is expressed in matters that are not vital; thus, other *kochot hanefesh* that are more active cover over the aforementioned feeling. The proof that this is so is in exceptional cases, such as at a wedding or a public *farbrengen* when people from other circles also attend; then, the special closeness between the people of this circle is expressed with greater intensity and strength.

Regarding what you wrote about studying in the seventh and eighth grades at the Reshet school — you do not write whether you need to pass examinations and the like, or if the delay is only due to the scheduling mismatch, as studies begin in Elul, and I advised you to study in the *yeshiva* until Rosh Hashanah. If that is the only obstacle, then a solution must be found, since studies in school leave enough free time for studies appropriate to the *yeshiva* curriculum, and indeed, the Reshet schools are to a significant extent a continuation of and preparation for the *yeshiva*.

Regarding what you wrote about your father’s financial situation, *shlita*, my hope is strong that in a short time the situation will improve and continue to get better, according to what is said, "little by little," etc. Surely your father knows, and also conducts himself accordingly, to set aside a few coins for *tzedakah* before the morning *davening* on weekdays.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

P.S.
My hope is that you are participating in the activities of *hafatzas hama'ayanos chutzah* within the framework of Atah and Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, and especially the statement of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe (printed at the beginning of the book *Torah Or*), that through the act of *tzedakah*, one's mind and heart become refined a thousand times over.

## Zeshna

B"H, 2 Tammuz, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Sivan.

At an auspicious time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter. May it be His will that just as you have written your request, you will also share good news regarding these matters.

Regarding your question as to whether there is a specific significance to a woman reciting chapters of Tehillim—

It is appropriate that you pray once a day to Hashem, the Creator and Guide of the world. Regarding the specific prayers to recite, you should consult with the Rav in your community, so that they may be suitable to your situation and level of knowledge.

It is understood and self-evident that the primary focus should be that your daily life is conducted in accordance with the instructions of our Torah—the Torah of life—and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them."

With blessings for good news regarding the matters you wrote about in your letter.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 7552

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, R' Yaakov, may he live:

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter of 27 Sivan: regarding what you wrote concerning the matter of the tablets, I had not written about this until now because it was still being clarified. Now, information has been received—and it appears to be well-verified—that the coating of the tablets differs from one factory to another; some are kosher and some are the opposite. From this, there are two conclusions: a) that in every location, one must investigate regarding the products of the factory being used there; b) since the coating can be made kosher, there is always room to approach the factory with a logical request that they produce the aforementioned in a way that is acceptable to all.

You do not mention in your letter anything regarding activities for the *hafatzas hama'ayanos*, especially in connection with the bicentennial year of the passing of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, z"l, and I do not know the reason for this. Since I received a clipping from a newspaper in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, suggesting that the *Chassidim* are supposedly not comfortable with the slogan of the bicentennial year, etc.—regarding a question of this nature that was addressed to me, I replied that the criterion in such matters is known based on the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, n"e (printed in *Hayom Yom*, 23 Sivan): one must examine the results that will come from the aforementioned activity, and from the failure to utilize the aforementioned slogan. In my opinion, it is clear that by publicizing the aforementioned slogan, there will certainly be additional members of *Bnei Yisrael* who will study the books of the Baal Shem Tov, his students, and his students' students—and this, too, is a significant matter. Especially since the study of their Torah is likely to lead also to action, in addition to a strengthening in all general matters of *Yiddishkeit*, which will certainly also increase through the aforementioned. Conversely, from the failure to utilize it, I do not see what will be gained. It is understood that all of the above is an addition to the essential point—that which is recounted from the Alter Rebbe, in the parable of the precious stone in the King's crown, which is ground down, etc., and poured, provided that there is at least a doubt, or a double doubt, that one drop will enter the mouth of the dying prince, and certainly [if he is] only ill. And *kal v'chomer* [it is understood].

May it be the will [of Hashem] that as we approach the days of the *Chag HaGeulah* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, all matters of *Chassidim* and *Chassidus* will be redeemed from all distracting matters, and the *ma'ayanos* of the Baal Shem Tov—which is the Torah of *Chassidus*—will spread until they reach the outermost reaches, and they will bring about the true and complete *Geulah* immediately.

With respect and with a blessing for the *Chag HaGeulah* and for good tidings in all the above.

## 753

B"H, 5 Tammuz, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letters from the 2nd of Tammuz and those preceding it.

It is my hope that after all the difficulties you mention, things will eventually work out, although it seems that this year, too, matters must be handled specifically in a miraculous way, since the time of anash is not available for such things [even though I have urged them time and again that, ultimately, it must be done through natural means].

Regarding what you wrote concerning specific instructions from here—in any event, some proposal must come from Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, since many important details and secondary matters are not known here. First and foremost, experience has shown that when something is done out of necessity, the result is commensurate with a matter of necessity.

Although it would be appropriate for there to be **joint** proposals resulting from **discussion and negotiation between them,** if this is impossible in any way, you should ask several of the activists to send their proposals separately, and you should certainly do the same, as you wrote—as soon as possible.

It is obvious that my intention is a proposal not only regarding yourself and your own place of work, but also regarding the other matters of the Reshet.

With blessings for Chag HaGeulah and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 754

B"H, 5th of Parshas Ali Be'er, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

200th Year of the Histalkus Hillula
of the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory
Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad, [Local] Branch...
May Hashem grant them life.

Blessing and Peace!

With the approach of the time when schooling for children concludes, and in connection with this, a change in the household routine and conduct also arrives.

I wish to hope that the work program of Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad is being prepared in good time, adapted to the aforementioned changes—both for those who are affiliated and active in the work, and for those N'shei U'Bnos Yisrael who are not yet aware of it, or are not aware of it to a sufficient degree.

For it is clearly evident that work performed according to a previously prepared program has greater success, both in the scope and in the depth of the work.

Coming from Rosh Chodesh Tammuz and finding ourselves a few days before the Chag HaGeulah—the Festival of Liberation—of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the leader of our generation, on the upcoming 12th-13th of Tammuz, this will surely add warmth and dedication to the work. This will further increase the success, as well as the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam in the personal matters of the members and their families, may they live and be well.

And may Hashem Yisbarach help that it should be in accordance with the instruction from the well-known Torah of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory, on the verse: "When you see the donkey" (*Ki tir'eh chamor*)—meaning, to observe the characteristics of the *chamor* (donkey), which represents the *chomer* (matter/the body)—and to reach the conclusion that "you shall surely help with him" (*azov ta'azov imo*)—to serve Hashem Yisbarach with the body and its affairs together.

And as explained at length in many places in the teachings of Chassidus Chabad, from our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe until my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the leader of our generation, this must be done *b'simcha u'v'tuv leivav*—with joy and a good heart.

With the wish for success in all of the above, and in anticipation of good tidings regarding this, and with the blessing of Chag HaGeulah,

**M. Schneerson**

## Z'shanu

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs, etc., Moreinu HaRav R' Sh. Y., may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha,

In response to your letter of 3 Tammuz, and addressing the first point first, etc.

Regarding your difficulty with what I wrote—that the tenth is holy even while it is in the pen—you argue that this only applies if it subsequently exits through the same opening, which clarifies the matter from the outset. You question: what difference does it make to us whether it exited, and where it exited, etc.?

One can answer with a logical premise (*sevara*), and one can answer with an explicit source.

The logical premise is simple: exiting through a different opening signifies that it belongs to a different "threshing floor" (*goren*). Moreover, it uproots the status even if, prior to this, it was considered part of the "appropriate count" (*minyan haraui*). Since this is the case regarding exiting through a [different] opening, the logic dictates that it is exactly the same regarding death; death also uproots it from this "threshing floor." How, then, could this lamb be sanctified simply because there are nine [others] in a *different* "threshing floor"? In other words, exiting—through a different opening—establishes the "threshing floor."

And there is no reason to distinguish in this between the ninth and the tenth.

Regarding your point that the *halacha* is that the tenth is holy even if it did not exit, etc.—in many matters, the rule is that the matter is clarified *retroactively* (*lemifrah*) in this manner or the reverse.

And as for the explicit source, as I noted in my previous letter [Rashi in manuscript, s.v. *minyan haraui* (Bechoros 59b), states that if it died or exited through a different opening, Rashi there says, "the tenth was not sanctified." And this is speaking of a case where there were only ten].

It is a great wonder that you cite a book (which I do not have at hand) that writes that this language of Rashi is imprecise, because in any case it is exempt since the tenth is holy—for it is explicitly stated in Rashi that it is *not* holy. Perhaps he saw the Rashi in manuscript but did not see the standard Rashi. It is similar in the commentary of the Ritva (Bava Metzia 6b, end of side b), which reads: "If he has ten sheep in the pen... it jumped... they are exempt from the *minyan haraui* for *maaser*, even though it did not exit," etc.

I was very pleased with the efforts regarding the situation of the Rabbinate in Ramat Gan. I look forward to hearing good news regarding this.

And truly, according to my perspective, this is for the benefit of the individual and also for the benefit of the many...

It is strange that in the public addresses in connection with the bicentennial year of the passing (*hillula*) of the Baal Shem Tov, I have not yet found that they proclaimed (and especially since, in my opinion, it requires special emphasis) that the Baal Shem Tov **added** light to Torah and *mitzvos*, and did not, Heaven forbid, diminish them in even a single detail, even though he emphasized the words of our Sages that "the Merciful One desires the heart."

With blessings for good news regarding the above, in both general and specific matters, and with the blessing of the Festival of Redemption—the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and our redemption together with him,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7557

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

As we stand in proximity to the days of 12 and 13 Tammuz, the Chag HaGeulah of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of our generation, who sacrificed his life for the dissemination of Torah in general and the dissemination of the wellsprings in particular, I cannot refrain from writing the following lines:

I have said that after having been here for some time—and it is impossible that this should not have left some impression, in accordance with the will and hopes of our Rebbes—upon their return and ascent to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, in general, and specifically to Kfar Chabad, which was founded and directed by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, they should immediately immerse themselves—with a sense of urgency and total dedication—in establishing, expanding, and deepening the activities of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in Kfar Chabad and its surroundings, with true enthusiasm and vitality. This is especially true since, even with physical eyes, one can see that the majority of the matters there need to be expanded many times over, and the only thing lacking is manpower.

To my regret, until now I have not received any news—not only regarding the aforementioned enthusiasm, but even regarding actions in the spirit of what was said. This is despite the fact that there is not a day that goes by without receiving letters regarding the lack of activity within the framework of Kfar Chabad in general, and within the framework of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad there in particular—both on-site and from travels and visits, etc., etc. Furthermore, in some of the aforementioned frameworks, they spoke about their participation in this, but it never came to fruition. Moreover, when taking into account that, in a good and auspicious hour, the time of each of their weddings is approaching, now is the time to utilize every possibility in the aforementioned matters, as this also serves as a foundation for building a home in Yisrael—a Chassidishe home. There is no need to elaborate on such a simple matter.

May it be the will of Hashem that, at the very least, immediately upon receiving this letter, the aforementioned will be rectified. As per the instruction of our Alter Rebbe in Iggeres HaTeshuvah, end of Chapter 9, "If one was accustomed to reading one page, he should read two pages, etc.," and they should also bring others who are in their vicinity and surroundings to engage in the aforementioned vital activities—activities of building specifically. I look forward to hearing good news.

With blessings for good news and with the blessing of Chag HaGeulah.

It is surely unnecessary to point out to someone like yourself the significance of the 12th and 13th of Tammuz, the festival of the liberation of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. It is my hope that you will also participate in person in the *farbrengens* of these days.

## 760

B”H, 11 Tammuz, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following up on my previous letter and in response to your questions:

It is understood, and indeed simple, that what you wrote regarding the other extreme (in a manner of lowliness and a falling of spirit concerning what one has done and accomplished until now) is also incorrect. As is well known, the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe: Just as one must know one’s own shortcomings, one must also know one’s own virtues. We see tangibly the great damage caused when one listens to the enticement of the *yetzer* along this line of bringing a person down from his true level—and this is a *maaseh rav* (a significant precedent). However, the lack of listening to its enticements does not mean one should grasp the other extreme, that "everything is within one's power and it is specifically upon you to finish the battle." This holds true even if it were clear that one would clarify that which needs to be clarified as much as is necessary, and that it would not affect the one clarifying or the environment at all. As written in my previous letter, the environment interprets many actions according to their perceived *hechsher* (validity/approval). Furthermore, *kal v’chomer*: since so-and-so provides a *hechsher*, it is certainly *l’chatchilah* and completely permissible for our environment, or on the contrary, that this is the maximum, etc.

This is explained even further according to the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the teaching of Chazal on the ways of the *kaluginker* (the cunning one). At first—today—he says, "Do **thus**." He agrees that he is an expert in his enticements, and he approaches everyone in the appropriate guise, magnifying his actions to the greatest extent. From this, it is understood that for a person who is "boiling" with *birurim* (clarifications), specifically of the lost and the cast-away, he first makes a calculation as strong as **iron** (*barzel*—which has the same *gematria* as **Amalek**), that the greatest salvation will come specifically through his work in this area, and there is no room for **doubt** (*safek*—which also has the *gematria* of *barzel* and *Amalek*). Moreover, only he is capable of doing this, and without him, *chas v’shalom*, there is no hope for the aforementioned *nitzotzos d’kedushah* (sparks of holiness). How great is the effect of these things—which are in the category of a bribe, and consequently, their effect is to conceal and hide even matters that are seen tangibly...

As we stand on the eve of the days of the *Chag HaGeulah*, 12 and 13 Tammuz, may it be the will of Hashem that each and every one of us be redeemed from all matters that cause confusion. Indeed, the greatest confusion comes not from a certain prohibition, but from a *safek issur* (doubtful prohibition) and a *s’fek s’feika* (a double doubt), and *kal v’chomer* (the rest is understood).

With blessings for good tidings and with the blessing of *Chag HaGeulah*.

## 7662

7662

B"H, 13 Tammuz, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-scholar, and diligent communal worker,
Rabbi Asher, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Following a very long hiatus, your letter of 8 Tammuz was received, in which you describe your holy activities in teaching and in education based on the purity of holiness.

It is my strong hope, even though you do not mention it specifically, that you are doing everything in your power to also disseminate the study of the necessary halachos among all circles and all ages. For we see tangibly how lacking the knowledge is precisely in these halachos—and not only regarding matters of custom, stringency, and the beautification of a mitzvah, but regarding the mitzvah itself. And this is not limited to Rabbinic mitzvos, but also [regarding Torah-mandated ones], and so on, to a most alarming degree. If in the time of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe they raised an outcry regarding the study of these halachos—as is evident from the introduction to the Alter Rebbe’s Shulchan Aruch—how much more so in our current era and in these countries. And this is obvious. In your location, it is even easier to effect change in this area. As the parable goes, sowing and planting in virgin soil does not require the labor and exertion of uprooting foreign vines, and so on.

As we approach these days of redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz, when the master of the redemption and the joy sacrificed himself for this very cause—even though, according to the way of nature, there appeared to be no room for success in the struggle against such a mighty regime—nevertheless, he accomplished his work, and in the end, they saw the finest fruits, and now we see the fruits of the fruits as well.

How much more so when one is in a land of freedom [...] and in a period when the hour demands it: come and act. May it be the will of Hashem that you utilize all the possibilities and strengths that have been granted to you to their fullest, and that you do so with joy and a glad heart—for this, too, will add to the success in practical terms.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7363

B"H, 14 Tammuz, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 9 Tammuz and the one preceding it, in which you write about the improvement in your health. May it be His will that you continue from good to even better, until you return to your full strength—both in the literal sense and in the sense of *eitan* (strength) as explained in the *maamar* "Maskil Le-Eitan Ha-Ezrachi" by our Alter Rebbe (printed in *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus*). May you utilize that strength solely for healthy and good matters, in the true sense of good: good for Heaven, good for people, and good that produces fruit.

Regarding what you wrote about your participation in the framework of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad: it should certainly be arranged in a way that does not affect your health. You should specifically discuss this with the doctor who knows your condition. If done this way, your participation will, on the contrary, add to your physical health as well, for "Yisrael are one nation on earth," and as is known, the interpretation of this is that they are the ones who draw down complete unity into the earth. And the Baal Shem Tov’s interpretation of the verse "When you see... you shall surely help him" is well known: to serve Hashem with the body and its affairs.

I am certain you will report on the *yemei ha-geulah* (days of redemption) in the necessary detail. May it be His will that this *hisorerus* (awakening) continues throughout all the days that follow, in accordance with the will and intent of the *baal ha-simcha* (the one celebrating the occasion), for "the body follows the head."

With blessings for good tidings, in true health and with joy and goodness of heart,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7665

B"H, 19 Tammuz, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter, in which you write about the impression and influence you received from your participation in the farbrengen here.

It is my hope that this influence will be lasting and will inspire you to increased diligence and perseverance in the study of our holy Torah, **Toras Chaim** (the Torah of life), and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, **"And he shall live by them."**

Since we are currently in the time of "Bein HaMetzarim" (the Three Weeks), during which we call to mind the destruction of our glorious Beis HaMikdash and the exile of our people, you surely know what the cause of the exile and destruction was. As we say in our prayers, "And because of our sins we were exiled from our land." This means that the purpose of these days is to rectify and nullify the causes that brought about the destruction. The path to this is **"Turn from evil and do good"** in your daily life, as well as in influencing your friends. And when one truly desires this, our Sages, of blessed memory, have said: **"There is nothing that can stand before the will."**

With blessings for success in the study of Torah with diligence and perseverance, and in the fulfillment of mitzvos with hiddur, with joy and a glad heart—and then you will surely be a source of much true nachas to your parents, may they live long.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 7667

7667

B"H, 22 Tammuz, 5720

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning the study of *Pnimiyus HaTorah* — it is understood and also simple that one is obligated (and privileged) to do so even before marriage. It is also understood that regarding the study of *Chassidus*, one must study it specifically from the books of those authors who possessed the study and *kabbalah* from person to person, reaching back to our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, the revealer of the teachings of *Chassidus*. And regarding the study of *Kabbalah*, it must be specifically according to what Rabbi Chaim Vital wrote in his introduction to *Shaar HaHakdamos*, and as is well known, the *halacha* follows the Arizal and his disciples. In this, the study of the aforementioned differs from the study of the revealed parts of Torah (*nigleh*). See *Zohar* Vol. I, 5a, and in many other places.

## 7668

## 770

B"H, 29 Tammuz, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 15 Tammuz, which reached me in due course, in which you write regarding the avreich... shya: It seems that his letter should first and foremost address the aforementioned point—that he should be more involved with people. This will be a good start for him to return to his former strength. And although, as our Sages have said, "all beginnings are difficult," and his return to mingling with people will seem difficult to him, he must force himself in this. Surely his friends will help him to do what is stated. However, since one must demand of a person according to his strength, it is understood that the intention here is not for an *atafcha* from one extreme to the other—to be involved with people for many hours every day—but rather step by step, with those circles with whom it will be easier for him to connect. This should be done with the intention and goal that his involvement will grow, until he feels comfortable without effort (*anstrengung*) in his speech and his interactions with them. It is also appropriate that he teach before some group, and as mentioned, this should be an easy study, without him feeling that it requires effort, but rather a small amount, proportionally.

Together with the aforementioned—and this is the main thing—the aforementioned must be strong in the knowledge (which corresponds to reality) that his current situation can be 100% rectified, provided it is done step by step. This is based on the fundamental point of *avodas Hashem* with joy and a good heart—an *avodah* that is in accordance with the statement "in all your ways," meaning in his eating, his drinking, etc., as explained in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*, section 231. As mentioned, it is close to saying that the aforementioned will see how close the matter is to him, etc. And since you have brought his question, you will surely not let go of him, and in the end, the avreich will thank you for your efforts in this, even if at first he does not express satisfaction.

My hope is strong that, even though you do not mention his participation in the *Chag HaGeulah*, he surely participated in it, and you will surely inform me at the next opportunity with the necessary details.

With respect and blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and for success in your holy work.

## 7171

B"H, Bein HaMetzarim, may they be transformed into joy without boundaries,
Brooklyn, N.Y.
5720

Rabbi Moshe, may he be known as Dr. Munk,
Shalom u’Bracha!

I received your letter regarding the seminary in Kfar Chabad in due time. My response has been delayed since then because not all matters were entirely clear, and as the Mishnah states, "If you have idled, many will idle." The clarification took much longer than I had anticipated. But just now, I have received word that in many points, matters there have already been arranged, and my hope is strong that the remaining points will be settled as well. The main thing is that the matter has been arranged according to your request, namely, the appointment of a special director. Mr. Shmuel, may he live, Chaper has been appointed to this position, and I hope that you are personally acquainted with him. From what I know of him through his letters, there is every prospect that, with the help of Hashem, he will succeed in his holy work of *chinuch* on *taharas hakodesh* in the seminary, in a manner of "increasing and continuing, increasing and illuminating."

Moving from one subject to another within the same theme: although for someone like yourself there is surely no need for a special appeal, yet since we have been commanded that "one does not urge except those who are already diligent," and *talmidei chachamim* require reinforcement, I will not refrain from expressing my strong hope once again that you, for your part, will assist in all matters of the seminary as much as possible, and even more. Based on the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which he would frequently repeat: when a Jew decides to undertake an act of *tzedakah* (whether literally or in spiritual matters), even if at the moment of the decision it is beyond his ability, Above they open for him a special channel and source so that he may fulfill his good resolution.

I will conclude as I began, with a request for your forgiveness for the delay of my letter until now.

With respect and blessing for good tidings,

I cannot refrain from mentioning on this occasion the opportune time in which we find ourselves, in the bicentennial year of the *histalkus-hilula* of our master, the Baal Shem Tov, founder of the general teachings of Chassidus. And although I do not know your attitude toward the aforementioned—and it seems that the Frankfurt education did not have any established attitude toward this at all, even though it is somewhat puzzling, since the *Baal Hafla'ah*, the *Ra'avad* of Frankfurt, was one of the greatest students of the Maggid, the successor of the Baal Shem Tov—nevertheless, my hope is strong that in our current era, there is no longer room for any point of opposition. For the deed is the main thing, and everyone admits that the teachings of Chassidus and its guidance increase *ahavas Hashem* and *yiras Hashem*, which are the foundation for the fulfillment of the 248 positive *mitzvos* and 365 negative *mitzvos*, as explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 4. See also Rambam, *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, beginning of Chapter 2, in his commentary there. It is also worth noting regarding the opposition during the time of the Baal Shem Tov, and the decree at that time, that it was specifically in a manner of "revealing the reason for the Torah and the *mitzvos*," and see *Eruvin* 35a, and it is understood. My hope is that in your environment, and in the place where your influence reaches, you will disseminate the matters of this Torah, and the merit of the many will assist you.

## 7272

B"H, 29 Tammuz, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 17 Tammuz—may it soon be transformed into joy and gladness—regarding your son, may he live and be well, and the manner of his future arrangements.

It seems to me that in our conversation, even though it was short in terms of time, I expressed my opinion that for the time being, he should not be sent away from home. Since, certainly, there will not be the same level of supervision for him elsewhere as is possible at home. However, at the same time, in order to avoid any issue of excessive pampering—and furthermore, and this is the main point, to strengthen his energy—you should provide him, in addition to his studies, with some form of communal activity where he will be the leader. For example, a group of children younger than him with whom he can study *limudei kodesh*, and the like. We see tangibly that success in such matters increases energy and independence. When his parents, may they live and be well, supervise this from close by, they will certainly be able to increase his responsibilities from time to time, so that he progresses more and more.

It is understood that any increase in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*—and indeed, in matters of goodness and holiness, no matter how good the situation may be, there is always room to add, since they are connected to the *Ribono shel Olam* who is infinite—adds to the blessing of *Hashem* in all that a person and his household require.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 7373

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs,
R' Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter and the enclosure, and the receipt is enclosed herewith.

When I was at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on the eve of Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, I mentioned you in accordance with the contents of your letter.

As we stand on Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av—which is as its name implies, that our Father in Heaven comforts each and every one of His children, "My son, My firstborn, Israel," and "You are children to Hashem your G-d"—in place of those events that transpired during these days and weeks, may it be His will that this be seen also with physical eyes, in a good, visible, and revealed manner: building in place of destruction, and "you shall spread out to the west and to the east and to the north and to the south" in place of the *bein ha-metzarim* (the period of distress), and may it be speedily in our days through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

Regarding your note on *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Pinchas* (77c, in the *shita* beginning "Be-Ohr"): You wrote "Be-Ohr Ein Sof," but seemingly it should be "Be-Ein Sof." The same could be said for the following line, but in many places, even *Ein Sof* is referred to as *Ohr Ein Sof* (see *Likutei Torah*, *Shir HaShirim* 8a, and elsewhere). This is because *Ein Sof* does not refer to His actual Essence and Being, for even that is "without beginning."

And regarding the precision of the Rama MiPano, it is brought and explained in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Pekudei* (7, bottom of column b).

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***7373***

**R' Ephraim Eliezer:** Yalles, Philadelphia. Additional letters to him appear above, 7230, and in the references noted there.

## 744

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5720.
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Bicentennial Year of the Histalkus Hillula
of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov,
The Vaad of Kfar Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be established
and under the leadership of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory,
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

As we stand at the beginning of Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av—which is as its name implies, for our Father in Heaven comforts every single one of the Bnei Yisrael, "My firstborn son is Yisrael" and "You are children to Hashem your G-d," in exchange for those matters that occurred during these days and weeks—may it be His will that all of this be seen also with physical eyes, in a visible and revealed good: building in place of destruction, and in a manner of "spreading out to the west, east, north, and south," in place of the "straits" (Bein HaMetzarim), speedily in our days through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

In continuation of the above, it has been arranged, with Hashem’s help, to receive a commitment from […], that if all the buildings in Kfar Chabad are completed and finished—that is, all the buildings for the Moroccans and all the buildings for the professionals (no fewer than six; and my hope is strong that they will succeed in adding to this with the appropriate efforts and with the help of our friends, may they live and be well), and all the housing buildings in Kfar Chabad (no fewer than forty) by the eve of Rosh Hashanah, which is approaching us and all of Yisrael for good, and in any event no later than the time of our rejoicing, the festival of Sukkos, which is also connected to the year that precedes it, as the verse states, "At the end of seven years," etc.—

He will donate to the fund of the Vaad of Kfar Chabad a sum of no less than five thousand Israeli liras.

May it be His will that the desire of Hashem will succeed in their hands, to establish and expand all the affairs of Kfar Chabad, both in quantity and in quality. The aforementioned building projects are included in this, as they are both quantity and quality together, and both physical and spiritual together. May they act in this with wondrous alacrity, as per the words of our Rabbeinu HaZaken in his Iggeres HaKodesh, and may they succeed.

This will also serve to expand and enlarge the channel and the vessels for receiving the blessings of the Creator of the world—

And its Leader—in all the affairs of Kfar Chabad and its residents, may they live and be well.

Until the fulfillment of the promise of "He who comforts Tzion and builds Yerushalayim," to redeem us with the true and complete Geulah.

With blessings for success in the above and for good tidings in all of this.

P.S.
Regarding the content of the letter, a fast, urgent message was sent. Surely they will respond by return mail.

In response to your inquiry via the esteemed chossid, involved in communal needs, R' Tzvi Shusterman, regarding your state of health and the doctor’s opinion:

In general, one should follow the instructions of two specialists in the field. Since you have written that both of their opinions concur regarding the necessity of the treatment, you should proceed.

Enclosed is a copy of my general letter for the past Shavuos, which is relevant for the entire year. From it, too, it is understood how good that is revealed and manifest should walk hand-in-hand with true good, and how every addition in the study of Torah—both the revealed aspects and Chassidus—adds to the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam in the manner mentioned above.

With blessings for good tidings and proper health,

**M. Schneerson**

## 760

B"H, 1 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Wednesday, Parshas Matos-Masei.

1) You heard a rumor in the name of, etc.

We are not responsible for rumors until they are verified by the source of the report or similar means. However, a matter similar to what you wrote is explicitly discussed in the holy Tanya, Igeres HaKodesh, Chapter 9: that the Sages did not say that Torah study is equivalent to acts of kindness except in their time, etc. The reason is explained there, and it is simple that this does not contradict the Mishnah cited in that very Igeres HaKodesh, since a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others takes precedence over Torah study (Moed Katan 9b, end of side a). And according to what is explained in Igeres HaKodesh, **now** this is the case.

2) Regarding your question on what is written in the Meiri (Kiddushin 30) concerning the efficacy of Torah study even for one who commits a transgression, whereas it is stated, "But to the wicked, Hashem says, etc."

The answer is understood according to the ruling of our Alter Rebbe in his Shulchan Aruch, Hilchos Talmud Torah, Chapter 4, Section 3, and in the Kuntres Acharon there.

3) Regarding the text of the song on Motzaei Shabbos, "Fortunate is he who saw his face (of Eliyahu HaNavi)," and you ask, how does one know that it is Eliyahu HaNavi?

There is a well-known witticism regarding this: one does not raise questions about a dream. The answer to this is along the lines of "the **words** of truth are recognizable," and it is obvious regarding the seeing of a face that it is established for the one who sees it with certainty that it is such-and-such a person. See Sanhedrin 102, 2b and in many places. And Vayikra Rabbah, Chapter 26:7: "And now that I, etc." In the case at hand regarding Eliyahu, it can also be said that it is according to what is written (Melachim II 1:8): "A hairy man, etc., and he said, 'It is Eliyahu the Tishbi.'"

4) Is it permitted to change from Ashkenaz tefillin to Sefard?

You should turn to a Rav who is a teacher of halacha; explain to him the reason for the change, and he will instruct you.

It is my hope that you have fixed times for the study of the inner dimension of Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus, and that you increase this from time to time, for we have been commanded to ascend in matters of holiness.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 7,627

B"H, 2 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 26th of Tammuz.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the matter of a shidduch, one must act in the natural way and in ways of modesty, and strengthen one’s trust in Hashem, who is the One who arranges matches and who oversees, with Divine Providence, every single person, that He will guide him in the way that is good before Him.
