## 7678

B"H, 2 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 5 Tammuz, along with the enclosed guidelines and plan for establishing a center for Chassidus.

It is understood that, in general, any matter involving the unification of those who tremble at the word of Hashem—and specifically regarding the dissemination of the wellsprings of the Baal Shem Tov, which is the very essence of the teachings of Chassidus—is most appropriate, and there is no need for any elaboration or explanation on this.

On the other hand, as I view the situation, for the establishment of the aforementioned center to be successful, it requires preparation in several areas. First and foremost, all those who are involved and striving in this matter must act with greater vigor, each in his own sphere, in a manner that is ever-increasing. Beyond the benefit and necessity of the matter itself, the work itself will prove to each of them the great utility and the impossibility of functioning without the establishment of the aforementioned center. For, regrettably, due to several reasons that are not the place to explain here, not everyone will recognize the benefit of the matter, and some will even oppose it, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

Because of my aforementioned view that the entire matter still requires organized preparation and a significant amount of time, I am not entering into the details and methods of the center about which you write, as it is not yet relevant in practice. However, several points in the plan require absolute change, and others are such that it is impossible to agree to them at all; yet, as mentioned, the time has not yet arrived to discuss the matter.

Consistent with the content and spirit of your letter, my hope is strong that you have fixed times for the study of the teachings of Chassidus every day, with an increase on the holy Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem. And in every place that your influence reaches, you are working in the aforementioned direction, for ultimately, the deed is the essential thing, even in the sphere of Chassidus—which is a part of our Torah—and one comes to know the deed through the study that precedes it, for "great is study, as it leads to action."

With respect and blessing.

## 779

B"H, 2 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn

To the General Committee of Kfar Chabad and the Spiritual Committee,
May they live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters and the report of 23 Tammuz, and to your questions:

1) It is understood and simple that, in addition to the specific buildings (the residential houses, the professional workshops, and the housing in Kfar Chabad) for which the General Committee is responsible for their prompt construction and completion, what I wrote regarding alacrity also applies to the buildings being constructed by Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, Beis Tikvah, etc. I did not mention this specifically in my previous letter because they are being built by their respective administrations, and surely the Village Committee will assist them if they request help. It is obvious that they would not hinder the aforementioned construction. It is understood that the fundraising and matters pertaining to this (the construction of Tomchei Temimim and Beis Tikvah) belong to the administrations of Tomchei Temimim and Beis Tikvah, as they have already received a general permit from the Kfar Chabad Committee long ago. Elaborating on such a simple matter is superfluous.

2) Regarding your writing that there is supposedly a lack of funds for the aforementioned, which is delaying the construction, etc. — after the investigation here, this report is puzzling; on the contrary. Surely you will inform me of the basis for this report.

3) Regarding your question about the authority of the Spiritual Committee — the doubt is puzzling. As its name implies, it is a committee concerning the **spiritual** state of Kfar Chabad: the rectification of this state, its improvement, and its enhancement. Even though, regrettably, for a long time you have not written about your activities in this regard, the lack of correspondence—and perhaps even a deficiency in action—does not change the responsibility incumbent upon you.

4) Regarding what was written about resignation — it is understood that this is not a solution or a rectification for any matter whatsoever, but rather a flight from the battlefield, a retreat from fulfilling the role that was assigned to you. There is only room for resignation in one of two cases: after one has fulfilled their duty completely and there is no longer a need for the committee, or, on the other hand, after one has exerted themselves in this **as much** as is required according to the Shulchan Aruch, with the greatest possible exertion and effort, and yet failed. Surely you recognize immediately that these two conditions have not even begun to be met, so what would be gained by resigning?!

5) Regarding a supervisory committee, as well as the details of the conduct of the General Committee — I have already written many times that in such matters, one should look at the conduct of similar settlements and moshavim in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established). In general, according to the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of our generation, "Love criticism," it is understood that a supervisory committee is desirable. However, I must add immediately that, judging by the results of the current General Committee's activities, it has succeeded in the village's affairs more than any of the committees that preceded it. Nevertheless, there is no one perfect except for the One, the Holy One, blessed be He, and therefore there is room for a supervisory committee.

As we stand in the month of Menachem Av, which is as its name implies—that our Father in Heaven comforts each and every one of His children, for "you are children to Hashem your G-d"—in place of those events that occurred during these days and weeks, may it be His will that all this be seen even with physical eyes, in goodness that is visible and revealed: building instead of destruction, and "you shall spread out to the west, and to the east, and to the north, and to the south" instead of the "narrow straits" (Bein HaMetzarim), speedily in our days through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and first and foremost in increasing alacrity in all the above, awaiting good news regarding all the above.

## 786

B"H, 2 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 10 Tammuz.

In general, it is a sound idea to hire an honest salesman so that you can utilize your talents in this area in a productive manner—good for the business and good for you as well. Furthermore, the fact that this is good for the business is a positive matter according to Torah, for the income must be utilized in a good way, in accordance with the instruction of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, in his teaching on the verse, "If you see the donkey... you shall surely release it with him" (Shemos 23:5)—to serve Hashem with one's body and its affairs. This applies not only to the portion that one gives directly to tzedakah, which, as our Alter Rebbe expresses it (Tanya, Chapter 34), "elevates with it all four parts," but also directly within the four parts themselves, according to the ruling of the Torah: "In all your ways, know Him," as explained at length in the Tur and Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, Siman 231. (See also Tanya, ibid.: "And beyond this, at the time of Torah study and tefillah, everything... ascends to Hashem.")

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 7-Shpa

B"H, 3 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Following a long hiatus, your letter was received on 12 Tammuz—the day of the redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and our own redemption—in which you reiterate several reasons and excuses as to why you do not increase your study of Chassidus, and express doubt as to whether you are suited for it, etc.

In such a case, one should examine the source of these doubts by observing their result: have they led to an increase in Torah and mitzvos, or, on the contrary, the opposite? See also the *Hayom Yom* for 23 Sivan regarding the test for this.

Regarding your writing as to whether you are suited for the study of Chassidus—the well-known adage of the Alter Rebbe, the author of the *Tanya* (the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah) and the *Shulchan Aruch* (the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah), is famous: that Chassidus is the inheritance of the entire Jewish people, and it depends on nothing but time.

Regarding your writing about the explanation that an individual’s mission is tested by the opposition and difficulties they encounter when attempting to fulfill it, and your question of how to clarify this when there is opposition to all the mitzvos—surely, in any event, it is not equal for all mitzvos, as is clearly evident.

In conclusion: "Fear G-d and keep His commandments, for this is the whole man." This applies to increasing the study of our holy Torah, both the revealed and Chassidus, and increasing the beauty in the performance of mitzvos. In a manner of "increasing and continuing," one naturally adds **light**, and many questions—which are darkness—are nullified from the outset.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

782

By the Grace of G-d
3 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi Yaakov Emanuel, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings,

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Monday and the one preceding it, as well as the continuation of the newspaper clippings. Regarding the comments on the previous articles:

In article 6, where you write about prophecy and that it is as if anyone can become a prophet, provided they prepare themselves—this is not the case according to the *Lechem Mishneh* at the beginning of chapter 2 of *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*. Rather, preparation is a necessary prerequisite, but after that, it depends on the Divine Will. See there, *Halacha 5*. Furthermore, this entire lengthy discussion—not only is it entirely irrelevant to the subject, but it is naturally superfluous, etc., especially regarding such a delicate matter as the one mentioned above—it will only stir up questions, etc.

In article 7, regarding the claim that R. G. of Kitov was the Chief Rabbi of Brody—that was R. Y. Y. Horowitz. R. G. "stood at the head of two *Batei Din*" out of the four that were there (at length, see R. G. Kitiver to Prof. Heschel, HUCA 23).

In article 8, regarding your writing about *Hashgacha Pratis*, see *Yahel Ohr* to *Tehillim* 36:7, where the Alter Rebbe brings proof from *Chullin* 61a—a proof from the *Nigleh* of Torah. (And in another place, I noted how the proof can be refuted by other statements of Chazal—see the book *Kovetz He'aros HaTemimim*, entry *Hashgacha*—unlike the aforementioned passage in *Chullin*).

In article 9, regarding the letter of the Baal Shem Tov to his student, the author of *Toldos Yaakov Yosef*—I believe this is the only letter in his own holy handwriting, and it was printed in *HaTamim* in facsimile.

There, regarding the well-known story of the rooster's crowing—it should be corrected according to what is printed in *Kuntres Toras HaChassidus*.

In article 10, at the end, regarding the "severed limb" that was cut off—it is worth noting the *Mishnah* in *Sanhedrin*, chapter 6, *Mishnah* 5.

In article 11, there are sharp expressions regarding the *misnagdim*. Considering that these matters are being printed and can be handled by anyone, without even entering into the question of whether these expressions are appropriate—in any case, it is not worthwhile for them to appear in print. Likewise, the entire lengthy discussion regarding bans (*cherem*), etc., is not worthwhile. Why revive and stir up forgotten matters, which, as the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, goes: those who brought about the aforementioned are already in the World of Truth and regret the entire matter with complete repentance.

In that same article: "A word for a *sela*." It is better to use the word "worth" in English. "V'k"l" (and so on)—it is more appropriate to use "easy."

There, regarding the sources for the Baal Shem Tov's interpretation of "G-d will seek the pursued"—it is from *Merchak Yavi Lachmo*, at a time when that is the opinion of most Torah commentators on the verse and the *Targum*.

In article 12, regarding why you brought from the *Kuzari* concerning movements during *davening* and not from other books—it is simple: because it is proven from there that the practice was so typical of the Jewish people that the *Kuzari* speaks of it specifically, unlike other books where one could interpret that only some individuals practiced it.

Regarding your writing about "he who exhales, exhales from within himself"—this is found in several books. When I noted that I could not find its source, I meant in the *Zohar*, where our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe cites it in *Tanya Kadisha*.

In articles 13-14, it is completely missing that the *hafatzas hamaayanos* must be specifically through the mode of understanding, as is precise in the language of the holy *Zohar*. See also the *sicha* enclosed, note 19.

At the end of article 14: "Pentecost!" What is lacking in the term *Shavuos* (see *Kiddushin* 70, end of side 1)?

[Regarding your writing as to whether one should say that R. Adam Baal Shem is R. Adam Luntz Baal Shem—since this does not appear in any of the lists or *Likutei Dibburim* to that effect, it seems almost certain that this is not the case.]

Some time ago, I wrote to someone regarding the behavior of several individuals and offices in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, where an internal exile has been brought there—that is, a feeling of inferiority before any non-Jew. When there is a choice, they prefer to quote a non-Jew rather than a Jew. And it seems that regarding this—religious or not religious—it is even in their writing.

And this also influences the readers, who will rely on a book whose author is on this side and not the opposite, etc.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, Shlita
Secretary

783

B"H, 3 Menachem Av, 5720

Brooklyn.

To the Avreich Chaim Zusha, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding your note on the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, concerning the case of "if one added honey to it, etc.," and why [the Gemara asks] "why [is it disqualified]?" and answers "because [it is not the way of the world to do so]"—seemingly, it should have stated more concisely: "One does not mix honey into it because [it is not the way of the world to do so]." ## 7,824

[3 Menachem Av, 5720]

Your letter, in which you write about your impressions during the days of the Pesach holiday and the farbrengen, etc., reached me with much delay.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that, as is the purpose of every farbrengen, its impression should be evident throughout the entire year, and extend into daily life in thought, speech, and action.

Regarding your question as to whether you will receive a response to your letter, and whether there will be closeness and favor, etc.:

The doubt and question regarding this is very surprising. This is the nature of Bnei Yisrael throughout their history (see Tanya, end of Chapter 1, and Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 12—that this is so from the perspective of the nefesh habehamis and the nefesh elokis). This is especially true according to what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus, beginning with its founder, the Baal Shem Tov, whose two-hundredth yahrtzeit/hillula we are in this year.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that it be "as water reflects the face to the face," and that the hiskashrus about which you write be in the known manner—that is, by studying those subjects in our Torah, Toras Chaim—through which Bnei Yisrael are united with one another and with the Ribono shel Olam, etc., as the holy Zohar states: Yisrael, the Torah, and the Kudsha Brich Hu are all one.

It is my hope that you are increasing your shiurim in the teachings of Chassidus, in addition to your shiurim in the nigleh of Torah, and in this, too, you fulfill the words of our Sages: "Great is study, for it leads to action."

## 765

## 7695

B"H, 4 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn

To the avreich Avraham Moshe, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Tammuz, in which you ask about the statement in Tanya, Chapter 29, that it is possible for a teshuvah not to have been accepted yet, versus the statement in Iggeres HaTeshuvah, Chapter 11, that there is no doubt or uncertainty in the world that Hashem is "abundant in forgiveness."

There is no contradiction here. For in Iggeres HaTeshuvah there, it concludes that there is a condition: before asking "forgive us," one must first ask "and return us in complete teshuvah before You." Since this is within a person's power—meaning, at that moment, to resolve that he will not return to folly, etc., which is the condition for the completeness of teshuvah—then there is no doubt at all that if he does so, Hashem is indeed "abundant in forgiveness."

From the style of your letter, I hope that you have fixed times for the study of Chassidus, and that you are increasing this on Shabbos, as written in the writings of the Arizal. This is in addition to the fact that this year is the bicentennial of the histalkus-hillula of the Baal Shem Tov, a year of special potential for spreading his wellsprings—which is the Torah of Chassidus—until they reach the "outside" as well...

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

**Avraham Moshe:** Greenberg, Bnei Brak. Additional letters to him appear in Vol. 18, 6995, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 7,827

B"H, 4 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rav, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' Shmuel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding the matter, I saw your honor’s article in *HaPardes* for the month of Menachem Av concerning the *bracha* of *HaMapil*. See *Eshel Avraham* (by the holy Gaon of Buchach) to *Orach Chaim* 231 and 239, where he discusses this at length. It is brought in brief in *Orchos Chaim HaChadash* 239.

On that same subject: The *Acharonim* on *Orach Chaim* 239 (the *Pri Megadim* and others) write that the *bracha* of *HaMapil* is a *mitzvah* dependent on a specific time (*zman grama*). This requires further study (*tzarich iyun gadol*), for if so, all the *Birchos HaShachar* would have the same status (see *Gemara Berachos* 60b and the *Rishonim* there, that they all come in one sequence). Yet, it is well known that women are obligated in *Birchos HaShachar*, and even in one of them specifically, as is known from the discussion regarding the *bracha* of *shelo asani* [goy/eved/ishah].

**7,827**

## 7,828

B"H, 5 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Moshe, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Following the longest of breaks, your letter of 2 Menachem Av was received. Regarding your question concerning setting a date for moving into your new home:

According to the well-known statement of our Sages, if it is possible to wait until the month of Elul—the month of mercy—rather than this month, that is the proper course. Our custom is to bring a Siddur, Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya into the home first, in addition to the custom (which I believe is common everywhere) of bringing bread and salt.

Regarding the affixing of the mezuzos, you should inquire about the custom in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) in such matters. Our custom **outside of Israel** is to affix them immediately upon moving in without a bracha. Then, on the thirtieth day, one removes a single mezuzah to check it (or to replace it with a more mehudar one) and reaffixes it with a bracha, with the intention of covering all the other mezuzos as well.

Regarding your writing about reciting the morning brachas in public—our custom is known to be to recite them at home, especially in our times, as there is often a significant amount of time between waking up and arriving at the beis medrash, and in the interim, it is impossible to avoid speaking words of Torah, etc.

At an opportune time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter. It is my hope that you will continue to share good news regarding your health and regarding the dissemination of Yiddishkeit and the dissemination of the wellsprings in particular. This is especially true as this year is the bicentennial of the passing and hilula of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory—a year of unique potential for disseminating his wellsprings, which is the Torah of Chassidus, until they reach even the outermost reaches. May you do this with joy and a glad heart.

With blessings for good news in all the aforementioned.

#### ***7,828***

**R' Moshe:** Heisler, Tel Aviv.

 See Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah 286:22.

## 757

B"H, 5 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 17 Tammuz—which reached me in due course—in which you write of the events of your life, and conclude that you are finally walking on the path of the King, King of the universe, according to the guidance of our Torah, the Torah of life, and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." You also mention that you were recently presented with a proposal for marriage, and you ask my opinion regarding the attitude of your parents toward this proposal, given that the young woman in question is from our brethren, the Sephardim of Morocco.

Since, as you write, she is a G-d-fearing woman and conducts herself as is fitting for a daughter of Israel—each of whom is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah—it has already been stated regarding this, "a woman who fears Hashem, she shall be praised." You should pursue this proposal until its successful completion in a good and auspicious hour. It is understood, and indeed simple, that there is no room for reservation or for erecting a barrier, Heaven forbid, between Ashkenazim and Sephardim, especially in these most recent years, when many have intermarried and are building their homes upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, happy in both material and spiritual matters.

Since for every matter and endeavor one requires the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam and Siyata Dishmaya, especially in a foundational matter such as this, you should increase your diligence and perseverance in the study of Torah. This should include a fixed time for the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. This is especially pertinent as this year is the bicentennial of the passing and Hillula of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, a year of special potential for the dissemination of his wellsprings, which are the teachings of Chassidus.

It is appropriate that you have your tefillin checked, and also that every weekday, before the morning davening, you set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

With blessings for good tidings in good health,

A. Quint

## 7191

B"H, 11 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn

Mr. Zvi, known as Dr. Harkavi,

Peace and blessing!

It has been a very long time since I have received any word from you. Although, according to *din*, we presume a Jewish person to be in a state of *chezkat kashrut*, and that every *shaliach* performs his mission—and the mission of every member of *Bnei Yisrael* is as the *Mishnah* states, "I was created to serve my Creator," through *Torah* and *mitzvos* and their dissemination—nonetheless, it would be pleasant for me to hear from you explicitly regarding this. This is especially so given that in this period, good news does not constitute the majority of the letters received.

Moving from one subject to a related one, I have been looking for news of your activities in disseminating the *maayanos* (the wellsprings of Chassidus) outward. This is particularly relevant since you sent me what was printed explicitly in a newspaper in *Eretz Yisrael* (may it be rebuilt and established), stating that after your visit here, you became a *Chassid*, or at the very least, are moving in that direction. Especially since, for the time being, there is no place for the opposition that existed in the past. The matter of the *maayanos* has become the inheritance of every member of *Bnei Yisrael*. Naturally, this also applies to the letters of opposition that were published in the early days of *Chassidus*, which recorded the reasons for the opposition and the concerns. After two hundred years, it is a *maaseh rav* (a proven fact) that there is no basis for those aforementioned concerns; and when the reason is nullified, the decree is nullified. You have the pen and the time in your hands, and you can—in addition to your activities in other areas—take an important part in the aforementioned dissemination through newspapers, etc. May it be His will that I receive good news regarding this, and from time to time, news of further progress in this area.

Enclosed is a newspaper clipping; surely the shipment has already been received.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

To preempt the argument that the time has already passed: in addition to the fundamental principle that the study (and dissemination) of *Torah* in all its parts is not a *mitzvah* that is time-bound, *Chai Elul* is the birthday of the *Baal Shem Tov* and the day of his revelation. This is according to the tradition in the family of my father-in-law, the *Rebbe*—person from person, back to the *Alter Rebbe*, who spoke face-to-face with the students of the *Baal Shem Tov* and his family.

## 762

B"H, 11 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning wedding arrangements: In general, I am not at all comfortable with the squandering of money on renting halls and the like—expenses that serve no purpose, not even a physical one. And although Chazal have spoken at length about the mitzvah of rejoicing with a bride and groom, and how everyone is obligated in this, we see clearly that the joy is actually greater when the wedding is not held in a formal hall that costs a fortune, but rather in a manner where simplicity is preferred. However, it is also understood that in every case, one must arrange the matter specifically in a pleasant manner and with the **full** agreement of both sides; in this, the opinion and wishes of the women must also be taken into account, and so on. And, of course, this is also understood from the *maamar* of *Chassidus* regarding exactly how one dances before the bride.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 7393

B"H, 11 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn

To the Kfar Chabad Committee,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters, in which you write that... and therefore you wish to make changes regarding this, etc.

Now, as a general rule, it is **not** the proper order or custom at all for every new committee to change all the matters decided upon by its predecessor. For if so, there is no place for orderly work or for the development of organized affairs. This is impossible in any matter of any kind, even if one were to say that there are the most important reasons, etc.

From this, my opinion regarding the content of your letter is understood: that there should **not** be any revolutions, confusion, etc., etc.

You should utilize your time and energy to establish the village and expand it in both quantity and quality, rather than focusing on revolutions. Especially in the aforementioned case—where there is no need for this **at all.** Rather, from now on, you should deliberate on any such proposals—if there are any—and decide what is appropriate for the matter and its details...

With blessings for good tidings regarding your success in the above.

## 734

B"H, 11 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your first letter since you traveled from here! And the great surprise and astonishment [at the delay] is understandable.

Regarding your question concerning your organization, it is understood that from here I can only provide guidance in general points, meaning:

That it should be in matters of Chabad, Chabad institutions, or Kfar Chabad in general, and in a manner that utilizes your talents. As to which of the aforementioned you should choose, you must contemplate this on the spot and consult with friends, for a person is close to himself and does not always see the situation as clearly as it is. May Hashem, who oversees each and every one with Divine Providence, guide you in what is truly good for you, both materially and spiritually.

Regarding what you wrote about setting the date for the wedding, it is understood that both sides must discuss this together. My opinion has been known since always, that delaying this for a long time is not desirable. The sooner, the better. May it be the will [of Hashem] that you decide at a good and auspicious time, and may it be with *mazal tov*, *mazal tov*.

Regarding your writing about reserving an apartment in Shikun Chabad — the question about this is also surprising, for it is certainly the right thing to do.

In response to your letter of the 19th of Tammuz, in which you write regarding the trip of your husband, Rabbi Shaya.

In other words, this is for their benefit as well, both materially and spiritually.

I hope that regarding the matter you wrote about previously, everything is in order, and may Hashem Yisbarach help that things should go from good to even better, and may you report good news.

## 7,397

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Avraham, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Following our conversation when you were here—which, naturally, gave me great satisfaction and pleasure—my hope is strong that you will not only continue to assist the second Kfar Chabad in the same way you helped the existing Kfar Chabad, but will do so with even greater effort, in accordance with the demands of the hour, which have also grown. Every person, and especially our brethren the Bnei Yisrael, of whom it is said, "You are called 'Adam' (man)," is commanded to ascend from level to level, in the language of the verse, "They go from strength to strength."

The command of our Torah, the Torah of life, is proof that this is not only possible, but that it also provides encouragement and empowerment.

I have delayed this letter until now because I thought that soon, perhaps, someone special could travel from here to assist specifically with the founding of the second Kfar Chabad. However, since for reasons beyond my control this possibility has not yet materialized, I did not want to delay the letter any further. I am certain that even without the arrival of a special person from here, it will be possible to proceed with the founding and construction of the village, and it is understood that at the first opportunity for someone to travel, they will not delay in coming.

As we discussed during our conversation some time ago, the site for the second Kfar Chabad has been determined. As they have already written to me, representatives of the various offices visited the site together with representatives of Anash. The area is, relatively speaking, in close proximity to the existing Kfar Chabad. For several reasons that we spoke about in our conversation, in my opinion, the second Kfar Chabad should be separate from the first, yet at the same time, not at a great distance, so that in the event that assistance is needed from one village to the other, they can easily do so.

My estimation, which borders on certainty, is that in the very near future—in addition to the settlers in the new Kfar Chabad from those already in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established—there will be a core group of settlers from abroad of no fewer than ten couples.

After the "birth pangs" pass, it is certain that many more will be added to them. It is understood that the news received from the first settlers will encourage and increase the number of those wishing to settle there. As I mentioned at the beginning of the letter, knowing your attitude toward the first Kfar Chabad and the attitude of our friends in the various offices—foremost among them a friend of the house of our Rebbes and a branch of the fathers' tree, Mr. Shazar, may he live and be well—my hope is strong that the project of the second Kfar Chabad will advance with swift steps and at a rapid pace.

I will conclude by expressing the hope that with the conclusion of this year—a year of special quality, the bicentennial year of the histalkus-hilula of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov—the beginning of the second village will already be clearly visible, and at an early stage. As we mentioned in our conversation, a certain sum is earmarked for the public affairs of this second Kfar Chabad. Even though, relative to the required amounts, it may only suffice for a portion of the budget, based on the statement of our Sages, "One only urges those who are already diligent," my hope is that this, too, will arouse an extra measure of diligence and speed in the activities. Now that the days of Bein HaMetzarim, the remembrance of the destruction, have passed—and as with all matters that are mentioned and acted upon year after year in the lives of the people of Bnei Yisrael, where the intent is not merely for remembrance but for action—here, too, the intent is to nullify the causes that led to the destruction and to increase in building, overcoming the boundaries and constraints (metzarim), in the manner of "And you shall spread out to the west and to the east, to the north and to the south."

With respect and blessing,

## 7398

By the Grace of Hashem, 15 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and accomplished individual, a man of noble character, a scion of a distinguished family, etc., R’ Shazar, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Mr. Herzfeld, may he live, surely conveyed to you the content of our conversation, which was long and detailed relative to the circumstances. Although I intended to write to you regarding what was discussed several weeks ago, the delay occurred from day to day due to the reason explained in the copy of my letter to Mr. Herzfeld. May it be the will of Hashem that the length of time taken in preparing the beginning will fulfill the obligation of spending time on the foundation and construction itself. From now on, the foundation of the second Kfar Chabad—or in your terminology, the third Kfar—should proceed at a rapid pace, in the language of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 21, "with wondrous alacrity." As I wrote to Mr. Herzfeld, it is my hope that in this auspicious year, the bicentennial of the passing and *hillula* of the Baal Shem Tov, the first stage of this village will already be seen in actuality.

There is another point regarding the timeliness of this matter, and it is a primary point: some of the candidates for settlement in the new village are about to get married or settle down in the very near future. Expediting the realization of the first stage will encourage them not to settle and become rooted elsewhere, as it would then be difficult to uproot them from one place and transplant them to the second.

Based on the general instruction in our Torah, the *Torah of Life*, that the many Torah and *mitzvos* Hashem gave to the Jewish people are not intended to confuse them, or in a way that one matter hinders another—on the contrary, "one *mitzvah* brings about another," as the *Mishnah* states regarding these two—my hope and certainty is that the efforts for the second village will not, G-d forbid, detract from the affairs of the first village. Conversely, the efforts for the first village will not hinder the affairs of the new village in the slightest. I am enclosing a copy of my letter to Kfar Chabad regarding this, and my hope is that in these matters, too, it will be as our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe said: "with wondrous alacrity." Since through *is'arusa d'lesata* (an awakening from below) comes *is'arusa d'le'eila* (an awakening from above), with the help of Hashem, everything will be with great success. Just as you merited to establish the first Kfar Chabad and succeeded in it, so too may you merit to succeed in the new Kfar Chabad, and from building to building in our Holy Land, both in spirituality and in physicality, until the fulfillment of the building of the House of Hashem—the building of the *Beis HaMikdash*, the House of the King, etc. (*Megillah* 27a)—through Mashiach Tzidkeinu in our true and complete redemption, with double comfort, and with joy and gladness without limitations.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above and your activities in this regard, in good health, joy, goodness of heart, and with outstanding success. I sign with appreciation, honor, and blessing.

***

I was told from the village that you participated in a gathering of historians and also delivered a lecture about the Baal Shem Tov, and afterward at a gathering of the Rav Kook Institute, etc., and that at the first gathering, [Name] also lectured, and some say he spoke about the Baal Shem Tov in his old manner and style. Of course, I do not know the accuracy of the rumor, but if it is true, I hope that you responded in an appropriate manner. Especially since, in addition to the tradition from Rebbe to Rebbe up to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the *geonius* (in its literal sense, in the *nigleh* of Torah) of the Baal Shem Tov—as our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe heard from his teacher, the Maggid—even a healthy mind confirms this truth. A healthy mind, even that of a simple person who has never visited any scientific institution and certainly has no honorary titles, but who has heard something about the Alter Rebbe’s estimation of the knowledge of Torah—the *nigleh* of Torah—which was for him a fundamental foundation and an immovable pillar like a rod of iron, would find it absolutely absurd and impossible that the Alter Rebbe would accept the authority, let alone the absolute authority, of someone who was not a *gaon* in the *nigleh* of Torah, a *gaon* according to the understanding and concepts of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe. Anyone who says otherwise and believes it proves that he has **no** concept of the worldview of the author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*. Furthermore, **he does not want to know** about his worldview, which he emphasized many times in writing and orally, in the *Shulchan Aruch* and in the printed *maamarim* of Chassidus, and those in manuscript which are also well-known.

My hope is that if there is a copy of your lectures, it will be sent here. Thank you in advance.

## 707

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the Bar Mitzvah celebration
in Azor, near Tel Aviv, may it be built and established,
May Hashem protect them and may they live in goodness,

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter, signed by the participants, with pleasure. During a time of favor, I mentioned you at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. May it be Hashem’s will that you share good news, and that you may be able to increase the dissemination of Yiddishkeit with proper health, tranquility, joy, and Chassidic vitality, as emphasized in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, whose two-hundredth yahrtzeit we commemorate each and every day of this auspicious year.

The intent of such a commemoration is that it be expressed in action, for that is the essential thing. This should not be limited to the "four cubits" of each individual, but rather in the widest possible environment, in accordance with the great principle of the Torah: "Love your fellow as yourself." This is especially true in light of the emphasis and the detailed explanation of this concept in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, and particularly in Chabad Chassidus, that love of a fellow Jew, love of the Torah, and love of Hashem are one and the same.

With respect and blessing for good news regarding all of the above.

## 7771

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the faculty of teachers,
And foremost among them, the director, R' Shmuel Chefer, may he live and be well,

Shalom u'Bracha!

I received with pleasure, in due time, the news regarding the graduation celebration, along with the details of the reports and lists, etc., and I thank you very much for this.

It is my hope that you emphasized to the students that the completion of a grade or a department is merely a preparation for a higher stage, and that in matters of Torah and mitzvos, every completion is a beginning. This is because Torah and mitzvos are infinite matters, as their source is in Hakadosh Baruch Hu, who has no end or limit. On the contrary, every ascent necessitates an increased push to ascend in holiness, with greater intensity and greater strength.

And surely you also emphasized that this year is a year of special significance—the bicentennial year of the passing of the Baal Shem Tov. This is especially true since, as is known, even before his revelation, he dedicated himself to the education and care of the children of the *cheder*, and he spoke at great length about the importance of education based on the purity of holiness.

At a time of favor, I mentioned everyone, collectively and individually, at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for outstanding success in your work and for everything needed, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good tidings and for great success,

## 7712

7712

By the Grace of Hashem, 15 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yosef, known as Dr. Goldschmidt
Shalom u’Bracha!

My reply to your previous letter has surely been received by now. I am writing to you now in connection with the preparations for the upcoming school year. Everything is by Hashgacha Pratis, and this includes the fact that these days I came across your article in English regarding the integration of the various communities (*mizug galuyos*) as it pertains to the field of education.

It is my firm hope that you will continue to assist the Chabad school institutions in every way within your power, in a manner of "increasing and ascending" as with all matters of holiness that we are commanded to elevate. I cannot refrain from expressing my gratitude to you—even though it may be superfluous, it serves as a spur, and "one only spurs those who are already spurred."

It is understood that this also includes the point that one should not be overly particular about formal credentials, etc. As I have emphasized several times: while you are certainly correct that the higher the level of knowledge and skill of the educator, the greater his influence on the students—and it goes without saying that I also urge those who listen to me to improve and pursue professional development in the field of teaching—on the other hand, no less important, and perhaps even more so, is the dedication and enthusiasm for the holy task: education on the purity of holiness.

In connection with your article, which emphasizes the value of an approach that is suited to the spirit and feelings of the students, and the need to encourage them and strengthen their spirits, etc., it is my firm hope that you have surely witnessed for yourself, through your shluchim, that the integration of children from different backgrounds in Chabad schools is carried out in the best and most pleasant manner, with the greatest activity, in addition to instilling a love for Torah and mitzvos without regard for the masses on the outside, and even the environment on the inside—a point which you also emphasize in your aforementioned article.

This is also one of the points of the Chabad approach, which has always emphasized this, and which is now expressed in the activities of the people of Chabad in all areas, and first and foremost in the field of education.

As mentioned above, it is my hope that your attitude would have been as described even without my letter, and this was only needed as a preference, in the style of the Baal HaTanya. My thanks in advance for all of the above.

With respect and blessing.

In due time, I received the text of the directive from the Ministry of Education to all schools regarding the bicentennial of the passing of the Baal Shem Tov, as well as the explanatory material. Since 18 Elul, according to the tradition passed down from generation to generation, is the birthday of the Baal Shem Tov, and it seems that the start of the upcoming school year will be around that time, it is my hope that this will have a continuation then as well, with special emphasis in the religious division, which Divine Providence has placed under your leadership. Although I do not know your personal background regarding the teachings of Chassidus, it seems you mentioned in our conversation that you are a product of Frankfurt. The Ra’avad of Frankfurt was the Baal HaHafla’ah, a student of the student of the Baal Shem Tov, and successor to the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid. In any event, it has long since been revealed that there was no basis for any concerns, and everyone admits that the teachings of Chassidus have infused a spirit of life into Judaism in all its branches, and all the more so in the observance of Torah and mitzvos with beauty, etc., as is known and famous to all.

**Mr... Goldschmidt:** Additional letters to him—above 7193, and in the notes referenced there.

**Baal HaHafla’ah:** See also above, letter 7171.

## 7003

15 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yitzchak Damiel
Greetings and blessings!

It has been a long time since I received a letter from you, though I do not know who is "indebted" to whom. The main thing is that the time in the interim has been utilized as much as possible, and it is my hope that this is indeed the case. You are surely aware of "my" slogan for this year, which is my hope and demand that everyone act with added energy and in every possible way to disseminate the wellsprings outward.

Regarding the question I have been asked—from where do I know that this year is a year of *segulah*, etc.—if at the beginning of the year there was doubt about this, now that several months have passed, the *maaseh rav* (the deed itself) speaks for itself. We see how the proclamation of the bicentennial year has found an echo and made an impression in various and diverse circles. And even though it is possible to find room for intellectual argument regarding the difficulty that the awakening in this regard has not come specifically from religious circles—or more accurately, not specifically from Chassidic circles, who have lived their lives in the spirit of the Baal Shem Tov’s teachings even in the years 199 and 198, etc., since his passing—the blame for this lies not with those to whom the call and proclamation are addressed, but with the aforementioned Chassidic circles themselves, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

It is understood that all of the above is intended also to awaken added energy in each and every one of us, and from your side as well—it is both understood and simple—to act in two ways: propaganda and study within your own circle, and exerting influence wherever your hand can reach, and establishing teachers of this Torah there as well.

To my regret, due to a lack of interest in the following point on the part of religious circles regarding the aforementioned call, they have thus far almost entirely failed to emphasize the absolute negation and absurdity of the well-known statement by some of the *maskilim*—that the Baal Shem Tov, his disciples, and his disciples' disciples, *z"l*, supposedly took lightly the actual performance of *mitzvos maasiyos*. This is especially tragic, as this error has claimed many victims.

On this occasion, I must acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your book *Al HaSaf*, which I have, of course, read **with interest.**

A general comment regarding your book—and it seems my perspective on this was not sufficiently highlighted in my letters of response to your circle of followers—is that the inner point of my response to their questions from that time, and likewise to the questions in your aforementioned book, is that **it is not true at all** that they do not believe. The matter is similar to one who says he does not believe in eating and drinking, yet eats and drinks three times every day. The proof of this is that it is human nature to absolutely accept conclusions whose authority is far less than the authority of various philosophical systems—and it goes without saying, far less than the authority of the faith of Israel—and to live according to these conclusions, even in matters that are a danger to life (for example, flying in an airplane). On the contrary, one looks at anyone who does not behave in such a manner as abnormal and not a member of civilized society. From this it is simple that such conclusions, for which the evidence is far more definitive than the aforementioned, are certainly accepted and define the entire person.

There is no wonder in the fact that a person deludes himself into saying he does not believe, when one considers the results he draws from this delusion, which in the vast majority of cases involve the removal of restrictions, both regarding "turning away from evil" and regarding "doing good." From this, the reason for the aforementioned delusion is understood—it is in order to make his life easier for himself and to "get rid of" the fulfillment of positive and negative *mitzvos*, and to live his life without any restraint.

It is understood that the matters mentioned are at the beginning of the deviation from the path, but after a time of behaving in such a manner, it conforms to human nature: habit becomes second nature, both regarding behavior and regarding the delusion. Because of the many times a person repeats to himself that he does not believe, he succeeds—*un er hot zich eingeshmuest* (and he has talked himself into it). The proof that this is nothing more than *eingeshmuest* is when a shocking event occurs that breaks through his external layers and touches his inner point; then he reveals to himself that he does believe. And if you wish to say so, the above is a transcription of what is explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 19.

And likewise in the *maamar* for the *yom hilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Basi L'Gani*, and in many other places.

It is somewhat surprising that in your book there is not even a *ka salka da'atach* (a passing thought) along these lines, and I have not found it in your letters to me until now.

In closing, as in the opening, it is my hope that you are publicizing and will continue to publicize regarding the Baal Shem Tov, his personality, his teachings, etc. I thank you in advance if you will send a copy here.

It is simple that the above is also for the purpose of conveying this to your followers.

With blessings for good tidings regarding the above, and likewise in all your other matters, and to each and every member of your household—may they live.

**M. Schneerson**

## 770

B"H, 21 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your question as to why certain prayers found in various books are not mentioned in the Chabad Siddur:

It is well known that the Alter Rebbe established the Chabad *nusach* to be suitable for every soul, as explained in *Shaar HaKollel* by Rabbi A.D. Lavut. It is widely known and documented therein that it includes only those matters and prayers that are applicable to all. This is in contrast to those that pertain to *mekubalim* and individuals of unique spiritual standing.

Presumably, you have a set time for learning the inner dimensions of Torah, which in our generation has been revealed through the teachings of Chassidus, with additional time dedicated on the holy Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem.

Regarding the question of *kashrus* that you wrote about — please turn to a *rav* and *moreh hora'ah* in your vicinity.

## 7707

B"H, 22 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, involved in communal needs, R' Gershon Mendel, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 4th and 16th of Menachem Av, along with the enclosed copy regarding the bicentennial year.

It would be worthwhile to revise the opening, as it currently implies that "from the day the Torah was given, the Jewish people were divided into two categories: Torah scholars and simple folk, and the Baal Shem Tov changed this." This suggests that for thousands of years and more—even in the days of Moshe Rabbeinu—the matter was not organized at all! The correction is simple: in the opening lines, it should state that prior to the revelation of the Baal Shem Tov, it was as mentioned above, etc.

## 7808

B"H, 22 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent communal worker, R' Chaim Zusia, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 4th and 7th of Menachem Av, as well as the previous ones.

I am surprised by your question, as I have already written to the esteemed R' Yona, may he live.

At a time of favor, I will mention you—and all those you write about—at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter. I will pray for your success in the matters you write about, provided that you proceed with joy, a good heart, and in a manner that is orderly and planned, as I have written many times.

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate on the fact that my opinion—based on the teachings of our Rebbes—is not at all favorable toward undisciplined conduct during a farbrengen, etc., as is brought in several of the Rebbes' holy sichos on this matter.

Furthermore, regarding the drinking of mashke, this is merely a secondary matter—and even then, one requires a blessing and Siyata Dishmaya to ensure that one follows the **straight** path, etc. I am writing this because unpleasant rumors have reached me regarding this. Some seem to excuse this behavior by claiming it is necessary to enable the speaking of words of hisorerus—this is the **opposite** of what is explained in the holy sichos of our Rebbes, and a word to the wise is sufficient. Things that are well-known require no proof. This is even worse than a "mitzvah performed through a transgression," for in this case, the transgression is clear, while the "mitzvah" is in need of scrutiny and investigation. May it be G-d's will that you bring good news regarding this as well.

As we are in the month of Menachem Av—which is as its name implies, for our Father in Heaven comforts each and every one of His children, the firstborn sons of Israel, for "you are children to Hashem your G-d"—may it be His will that in exchange for the events that occurred during these days and weeks, we will see this with physical eyes, in a revealed and manifest good: rebuilding in place of destruction, and in a manner of "spreading out to the west, east, north, and south," in place of the "narrow straits" (bein hametzarim), speedily in our days through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for good news in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

My hope is that the construction is continuing **in actuality**, with alacrity and in all three categories. May you continue in this manner (and it would be even better if there is an increase) until it is **completed** in deed and in truth. I trust that you will remain vigilant in this.

- It is obvious that regarding the second village, it must be specifically in the area that was allocated from the beginning (which was before the freeze), as it must be close to the current village, etc., etc.

## 709

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn

Mr. Shmuel, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 12 Tammuz, the day of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and our own redemption, which reached me in due time.

In it, you write of your work in the field of education and conclude with a question: should the undesirable conduct of the listeners prevent the teaching of the shiur, etc.? You fear that if you insist on the aforementioned and demand a change in conduct, they will turn you away empty-handed, or worse, etc.

First and foremost (and this is the essential point in such matters), our Sages have stated (Shabbos 55a): "It is revealed before You (Hashem), but to them, is it revealed?" In the present case, why should you suspect Bnei Yisrael, at a time when we are commanded to judge them favorably? It is a well-known adage of the Baal Shem Tov — this year being the bicentennial of his passing and hillula — that Bnei Yisrael are called *eretz chefetz* (a land of desire). Just as the most precious treasures are hidden in the earth, but one must uncover them, so too is it with every single Jew (see *Hayom Yom*, 17 Iyar). It is evident from your letter that, as of yet, no effort has even been made to change the aforementioned conduct.

To add to the above: I am aware of cases involving Bnei Yisrael abroad who are even less observant than those you describe, and yet, when the teacher requested that the conduct be appropriate for a specific subject, the students responded willingly. It is highly probable that this will be the case for you as well. Especially now, as you yourself write, there has been a change for the better in the general atmosphere in the aforementioned field.

It is understood that the first question will be: "What is different today that their conduct has suddenly changed?" But even this question has no place now, as we are at the beginning of a school year. Rather, the matter must be something that concerns you, and the words must come from the heart — for then they will enter the heart of the listener, and through pleasant ways, they will achieve their effect, **and the Name of Heaven will be sanctified.** This could be a good beginning, from which others will see and do likewise in other schools. This is not the case if the demand for change is never made.

In accordance with the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, as mentioned above, may it be Hashem’s will that you merit success in uncovering the treasure within the *eretz chefetz* of these students, and may you do so with joy and a glad heart.

Awaiting good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7th of Menachem Av

B"H, 28th of Menachem Av, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, along with the enclosure in which you write regarding the proposal of honors, and the question of who will be the *shoshvinin* to escort the *chassan* or the *kallah* to the *chuppah*.

It should be done as both sides agree upon, and it is best that neither the *chassan* nor the *kallah* involve themselves in the matter.

Regarding what you wrote about a *chuppah* under the open sky—since this is brought down in many places and there are several reasons for it, my hope is strong that everyone will agree to do it in the aforementioned manner, i.e., under the open sky. Even when the wedding takes place in a fully covered hall, the *chuppah* can be outside, adjacent to the hall, just as has already been done at many, many weddings here.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that they be blessed like the stars of the heavens (which is also one of the reasons for the aforementioned, and *kal v'chomer*).

And here, it is my duty (and privilege) to urge you regarding the necessity of establishing a regular *shiur* in the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. If in all times and in all places this was a necessity, how much more so in our era, and in these countries in particular.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned.

## Zayin-Tav-Yud-Alef

[28 Menachem Av, 5720]

I was distressed to learn that your health is not as it should be. Surely, a large part of this is due to nerves and thoughts, and a lack of avodah of Hashem specifically with simcha. Yet, according to the ruling of the Rambam—as cited in the Tur and Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chayim, siman 231, and in many other places—the avodah of the Ribono shel Olam is "in all your ways," including eating, drinking, walking, and so on.

I am surprised by you, for the root of this matter stems from a state of "smallness" in emunah, or as Chazal phrase it, "those of little faith." For emunah as it should be **compels** one to say that "according to the camel is the load"—meaning that the Ribono shel Olam does not give a person an avodah that is beyond their strength. Since maintaining a healthy and whole body is one of the "ways of Hashem," it is certain that the avodah itself does not, **in its own essence**, diminish one’s physical health. As for the fact that there are concealments and hidden obstacles—and at times it seems, and perhaps it is even true, that they are beyond the standard measure—it is already known what is explained in Tanya: that "reasons" (*ta'amim*) is plural, for there are two types of this, and two kinds of *nachas ruach*: whether through an avodah that involves no battle, or specifically through one that does. And even in battle, one must proceed "with a joyful march," as is known from the sicha of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. A spiritual battle is the same; it should not affect one's actual health, even if the matter itself is distressing.

May the Ribono shel Olam strengthen and fortify you, so that from a state of proper health you may fulfill your shlichus to spread the Torah of Chassidus and make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place in the lower worlds, even in that country, through the spreading of the wellsprings outward.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***Zayin-Tav-Yud-Alef***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 19, p. 525.

## 712

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Elul, the month of mercy, 5720
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Bicentennial Year of the Histalkus-Hillula
of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, z"l
The Organizing Committee, Kfar Chabad,
May Hashem grant them life.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the P"N, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, ztzk"l, nb"m, zy"a.

I am writing to offer a suggestion, with a preface: Leaving Eretz Yisrael, t"v, for abroad is permissible only in special cases, one of which is to prostrate oneself at the graves of tzaddikim (see Sdei Chemed, Vol. 1, Asifat Dinim, at the beginning, and Pe'at HaSadeh there). This is especially true regarding a tzaddik and Nasi to whom one was close, whose Torah one studies, and whose instructions and guidance one follows—or, at the very least, commits to doing so from this point forward.

The words of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, are well-known regarding the matter of hiskashrus, which is achieved through (as mentioned above) studying their Torah and fulfilling their guidance and takanos.

It is well-known and famous to what extent my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of Yisrael, sacrificed himself for the Torah of Chassidus in general, and for its dissemination in the broadest possible way and to the most diverse circles—all with love, and in the very "language" that they understand.

Therefore, each and every one of the participants in this trip must begin to implement the aforementioned before the trip actually commences. I refer to an increase in the study of Chassidus, and specifically in the study of the maamarim of the one who rests at the gravesite.

Regarding the women, this applies to them as well, or perhaps especially to them.

(See Hilchos Talmud Torah by the Alter Rebbe, end of Chapter 1: "Women are obligated to learn the laws that apply to them, etc., all positive mitzvos that are not time-bound, etc. And in their days, the sage would expound, etc., in a language that the women understand, etc." And surely, included in the positive mitzvos that are not time-bound are, first and foremost, the six mitzvos whose obligation is constant, never ceasing from a person for even a moment throughout their life. These are: 1) To believe in Hashem, 2) Not to believe in any other, 3) To unify Him, 4) To love Him, 5) To fear Him, 6) Not to stray after the thoughts of the heart and the sights of the eyes.

One arrives at these specifically through study—which in our times is the study of the Torah of Chassidus, as per the ruling of the Rambam in Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah, beginning of Chapter 2. And *maaseh rav*—the deed is the essential thing.)

Furthermore, each person should—without a vow—set aside a few coins for tzedakah every weekday morning for the institutions of the one who rests at the gravesite, to strengthen those institutions. Also, before the trip, they should visit—at least once—amongst the Bnei Yisrael in circles that, for the time being, are not yet fully connected in all their affairs, etc.—meaning, that in terms of proximity, they still bear the description of "the outside." During their visit, they should speak words of hisorerus in general, and specifically from the Torah of the one who rests at the gravesite.

Anyone who adds to any of the above is praiseworthy, as is understood.

During the trip, they should study in public the three daily portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—as is well-known according to the takanah of the one who rests at the gravesite. Likewise, they should study a shiur in his Torah—in a place that the hearts of the majority of the participants desire.

Surely, all the travelers will join in, along with the staff, who are also of the Bnei Yisrael.

May it be the will of Hashem that the trip be in a good and successful hour in all its details, and in its inner point—that through it, there will be an increase in the dissemination of Yudaism in general, and in the dissemination of the wellsprings outward in particular.

May they utilize their time here, in the style of our Sages, as is proper—with joy and a glad heart.

And may we merit soon the fulfillment of the promise of "in return and rest," that we shall all return in return and rest to our holy land through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, immediately.

Awaiting good tidings in all the above, and signing with a blessing of *Kesivah V'Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually—to each and every one, shlita.

**Menachem Schneerson**

P.S. This letter also serves as a response to the individual letters of several of the participants, shlita, in the aforementioned trip. Surely you will inform each of them of the above.

## 713

B”H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5720
Brooklyn

Mr. Schneur Zalman, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I was pleased to hear from the avreichim, may they live, who are traveling the country on behalf of the Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch, that they visited your camp in Burlington and your home, and delivered to me your gift—the book *Toldos HaRav MiLiadi*—along with your regards. Thank you very much.

It is my strong hope—especially based on the content of the conversation you had with them—that you not only remember the rock from which you were hewn, but that your way of life reflects this as well. This is of particular importance in these years, as each and every one of us is a "brand plucked from the fire." This is especially true regarding those circles of Torah and mitzvah-observant Jews upon whom the hand of Hashem, may we be spared, fell so heavily; they constitute the majority of our Jewish brethren who sacrificed their lives for the sanctification of Hashem’s name during the recent years, the years of the terrible war from 5700–5704. Yet, it is precisely in these most recent years that a strong awakening is being felt among the people of the United States to return to the sources of our Torah and its mitzvos, particularly among the youth. Therefore, every action in this regard—and all the more so a living example—is capable of bringing about important and significant results, even in quantity. Naturally, I would be pleased to hear good news regarding all of the above.

With special interest, I heard from the avreichim, may they live, that you possess, as an inheritance, a menorah belonging to our Rabbeinu HaZaken, according to your account. My thanks in advance if you would inform me of the veracity of these details, the history of how the menorah came into your possession, etc., and also if you have in your possession any manuscripts or similar items belonging to our Rabbeinu HaZaken or his descendants. In such matters, the more detail provided, the better.

With respect and blessing for a *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah*.

***

**713**
**Schneur Zalman:** Shapira, Burlington.

## 714

B”H, 1 Elul, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R’ Yisrael, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning the study schedule between Mincha and Maariv: While it is true that this is a propitious time for studying the inner dimensions of Torah with a minyan—specifically the Aggadah in the sefer *Ein Yaakov*, in which most of the secrets of the Torah are concealed and which atones for a person’s sins (*Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 23)—this does not preclude adding other studies as well. Indeed, during the year of mourning, the study of *Mishnayos*—the letters of which are [an acronym for] *neshamah*—is appropriate and follows every prayer, including Mincha.

## 7,315

B"H, 2 Elul, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After the longest of intervals, your letter from 27 Menachem Av, Erev Rosh Chodesh Elul—the month of mercy—has been received.

It is understood and self-evident that there is, Heaven forbid, no issue of distance or the like. I have already written many times to various members of anash, may they live, that sometimes, due to a multitude of matters, a response is delayed; one should not derive any distorted interpretations from this. My hope is that, in any case, from here on there will be no room for such concerns.

This is especially true in light of the Baal Shem Tov’s instruction regarding the matter of "serving Hashem with joy" and from a place of the strongest bitachon.

As we stand in the month of Elul, the month of mercy—the acronym for which is "and tzedakah shall be ours, for..." (Devarim 6:25; Mishnas Chassidim, Maseches Elul, at the beginning)—may it be the will that our avodah of Hashem be the avodah as explained by the holy Ohr HaChaim on the aforementioned verse: avodah out of love. And the ultimate love is not for the sake of any ulterior motive; see Kuntres HaAvodah, chapter 5, that love which is not dependent on anything—which stems from the yechidah—is effective even in asiyah, as the verse concludes: "to do."

And just as "as water reflects a face to a face," so too, from Above, it will be drawn down in a line of love and chesed, at which point the drawing down is without boundaries or Tzimtzum, reaching down to the lowest levels, in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

With blessings for good tidings and to be inscribed and sealed for good.

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7,315***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 19, p. 526, and completed based on the secretariat’s copy. See also letter 7,323 below.

## 7,516

7,516

B"H, 2 Elul, 5720
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your telegram, in which you write regarding the study of abridged versions of the Chumash.

The instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and his father, the Rebbe (Rashab) — of blessed memory, may their merit protect us — along with all the great leaders of Israel, is well-known regarding the absolute prohibition of this. From this, it is understood that my position is one of absolute opposition.

May it be the will of Hashem that He pour out a spirit from on high upon all those involved in the education of the children of Israel wherever they may be, including the individuals about whom you write, to recognize the truth of our Torah — the Torah of truth — which does not tolerate abbreviations or compromises, for it is a complete Torah. May every single son and daughter of Israel — for even one soul is an entire world — be educated in the purity of holiness, to raise students whom all who see them will recognize as the seed which Hashem has blessed.

With respect and with blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 717

B"H, 5 Elul, 5720
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your notification regarding your move into a new apartment:

May it be the will of Hashem that this change of place brings a change of fortune for the good and for blessing, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good tidings and to be inscribed and sealed for good.

The saying of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, regarding the "comfortable baal habayis" is well known—how this is a repulsive thing (the very description of it proves that it is not speaking of negating something explicitly forbidden), and this is the well-known "gemitlichkeit" (comfort-seeking), whose nature is like mud and deep mire, in which one sinks, Heaven forbid, lower and lower [while "within the permission" of the Torah—and consequently, what is there to regret or do teshuvah for?]. And according to the most distressing rumors, it seems that you and... and others have reached the "ultimate goal" [...] happy, B"H, with your lot in spirituality (in nigleh, in Chassidus, in the avodah of tefillah, etc.), and with your most vigorous activities in spreading the wellsprings regarding yourselves, others, and the entire environment. Yet, since a person must be a "walker" (one who progresses), you strive to add to all the comforts of the material body and its affairs—amidst an afternoon nap, and their sleep is sweet to them. Is it truly the case that the descent from a high roof to a deep pit is for the sake of this "ascent"?

## 718

B"H, 5 Elul, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished,
R' Moshe Yehuda, may he live, HaKohen

Since you do not mention anything regarding health matters, I hope that everything is in order for you and for every member of your household, may they live. Nevertheless, it is appropriate to follow the instruction in the beginning of Yoreh Deah — Siman 1, Seif 1 in the Rema (from the She'iltos, Parshas Beha'aloscha) — and inform me of this explicitly.

## 7619

B"H, 5 Elul, 5720
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs,
R' Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letters from the 1st and 3rd of Elul, the month of mercy.

Regarding your note on *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 10, that the 613 mitzvos were told to Moshe at Sinai is derived from Chazal:

Indeed, in Part I of *Tanya*, at the beginning of Chapter 20, this very statement is cited in the name of Chazal. See also the *Hoda’ah Rabbah* at the beginning of the *Tanya* regarding how the *Iggeres HaKodesh* was discovered, etc.

Regarding your writing at the conclusion of the second letter, "avodah temah" (complete service):

See also the *Tzava’as HaRivash* at its beginning, "avodah temah." I have noted in one of the *farbrengens* that this should be connected to the parameters of *avodah temah*, which completes the matter and requires no further service (*Yoma* 26a). This is the novelty in the *Tzava’ah*—for seemingly, the matter mentioned there is simple and cited in many places.

Regarding your mention of the holy *Ohr HaChaim* concerning *nefesh* and *ruach* :

See *Ginzei Nistaros*, Part I, page 70, regarding what the Baal Shem Tov said about the author of the *Ohr HaChaim*. The words of the Chida regarding the spread of the study of this book through the words of the Baal Shem Tov are well known (*Shem HaGedolim*, entry *Ohr HaChaim*).

With blessings for good tidings and to be inscribed and sealed for good.
